مشكاة المصابيح

Mishkat 2 — Study Notes
Kitab كِتَابُ اللِّبَاسِ بَابُ التَّرَجُّلِ — الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٤٢٣
وَعَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «إِنَّ الْيَهُودَ وَالنَّصَارَى لَا يَصْبُغُونَ فَخَالِفُوهُمْ»
Narrated by Abu Hurairah (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: al-Bukhari and Muslim (Mutfaq Alayh)  ·  Grade: Sahih
Class Notes
  • ظَاهِرًا this shows the permissibility of dyeing hair with حِنَّاء; some عُلَمَاء even extract اسْتِحْبَاب from this.
  • Not only did the Prophet (S.A.W.) do this, but some صَحَابَة also colored their hair.
  • However, other narrations indicate toward كَرَاهَة of this.
  • Some do جَمْع by saying: the اَحَادِيث of جَوَاز are for those whose hair is pure white, and the اَحَادِيث of كَرَاهَة are for those whose hair is not pure white.
  • Imam al-Tahawi states that the حَدِيث of نَهْي is مَنْسُوخ, so according to him dyeing one's hair with حُمْرَة/حِنَّاء is permissible مُطْلَقًا.
  • This hadith is also the دَلِيل for those who prohibit coloring one's hair black, but the حُكْم of black dye on hair will vary based on the objective:
  • A warrior coloring his hair to instill fear — permissible.
  • To deceive others and make them think he is young when he is not — not permissible اتِّفَاقًا.
  • To look better (زِينَة) — اخْتِلَاف from the time of the صَحَابَة. Most عُلَمَاء say it is مَكْرُوه تَحْرِيمًا, and this hadith is a دَلِيل for them. Those who allow it use آثَار of the صَحَابَة as دَلِيل, where many صَحَابَة colored their hair black, and they say that the اَحَادِيث of كَرَاهَة like this one are for those who intend deception.
  • Those who prohibit it state that those صَحَابَة did not use pure black dye; rather it was mixed with حُمْرَة.
  • Takmilah Fath al-Mulhim: the اَحَادِيث of نَهْي are مُجْمَل and contain a قَرِينَة that specifies them to cases of deception only.
  • Mufti Shafi' also prefers كَرَاهَة.
  • However, Imam al-Sarakhsi states that if a man dyes his hair to beautify himself for his wife, it is allowed — because if a woman can beautify herself for her husband, the other way around should also be permissible.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • لَا يَصْبُغُونَ— they do not dye; the object is omitted, meaning: they do not dye their beards (لَا يَخْضِبُونَ لِحَاهُمْ).
  • فَخَالِفُوهُمْ— so differ from them; Mirqat specifies: dye your beards with حِنَّاء.
Cross-ref: Hadith confirmed in Mirqat (Shamela p.6109) and Takmila Fath al-Mulhim (vol.10 p.130, باب مخالفة اليهود في الصبغ); Takmila confirms takhrij in Bukhari, Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi, Nasa'i, and Ibn Majah; Takmila discusses the command فَخَالِفُوهُمْ as مُطْلَق and covers all scholarly positions on black dye including al-Sarakhsi's position — consistent with class notes; Lam'at not yet checked — flagged.
Kitab كِتَابُ اللِّبَاسِ بَابُ التَّرَجُّلِ — الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٤٢٤
وَعَنْ جَابِرٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ قَالَ: «أُتِيَ بِأَبِي قُحَافَةَ يَوْمَ فَتْحِ مَكَّةَ وَرَأْسُهُ وَلِحْيَتُهُ كَالثُّغَامَةِ بَيَاضًا فَقَالَ النَّبِيُّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: غَيِّرُوا هَذَا بِشَيْءٍ وَاجْتَنِبُوا السَّوَادَ»
Narrated by Jabir (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Muslim  ·  Grade: Sahih
Class Notes
  • The Prophet (S.A.W.) initially concurred with أَهْلُ الْكِتَاب because at least they were following some traces of the previous prophets, while the مُشْرِكُون did not follow anything from the prophets.
  • But when most of the مُشْرِكُون became Muslims, he did مُخَالَفَة of أَهْلُ الْكِتَاب.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • كَالثُّغَامَةِ بَيَاضًا— like the thughama plant in whiteness; الثُّغَام is a plant with intensely white flowers and fruit, used as a simile for pure white hair. بَيَاضًا is a tamyiz (specification) of the comparison.
  • غَيِّرُوا هَذَا بِشَيْءٍ— change this whiteness with something, i.e., dye it.
  • اجْتَنِبُوا السَّوَادَ— avoid black dye. Ibn al-Malak: this is for non-warriors; as for warriors who dye black to appear fearsome to the enemy — there is no harm in it. It is narrated that Uthman, al-Hasan, and al-Husayn dyed their beards black for this purpose.
Cross-ref: Hadith confirmed in Mirqat (Shamela p.6110) and Takmila Fath al-Mulhim (vol.10 p.128, باب استحباب خضاب الشيب بصفرة أو حمرة وتحريمه بالسواد); Takmila confirms dyeing with حِنَّاء as مُسْتَحَبّ per Hanafi Fatawa al-Hindiyya, confirms al-Tahawi's نَسْخ position, and cites Abu Yusuf on a man beautifying himself for his wife — consistent with class notes; Lam'at not yet checked — flagged.
Kitab كِتَابُ اللِّبَاسِ بَابُ التَّرَجُّلِ — الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٤٢٩
وَعَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «لَعَنَ اللَّهُ الْوَاصِلَةَ وَالْمُسْتَوْصِلَةَ وَالْوَاشِمَةَ وَالْمُسْتَوْشِمَةَ»
Narrated by Ibn Umar (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: al-Bukhari and Muslim (Mutfaq Alayh)  ·  Grade: Sahih
Class Notes
  • Gangohi: if وَصْل is done to deceive, then it will always be حَرَام بِالاتِّفَاق. But if not, then according to the فُقَهَاء (i.e., أَحْنَاف) it is prohibited with human hair but allowed with other materials.
  • The مُحَدِّثُون say that وَصْل is حَرَام مُطْلَقًا.
  • The حَاشِيَة states that the place of the tattoo becomes نَجِس. However, the أَحْنَاف state that once the wound closes and the blood becomes solid, washing whatever is on top of the skin makes it طَاهِر — because removing what is under the skin leads to حَرَج and is therefore not taken into consideration.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • الْوَاصِلَةَ— the one who joins/extends her hair with other hair, whether she does it herself or instructs another to do it.
  • الْمُسْتَوْصِلَةَ— the one who requests this to be done to her by another; applies to both men and women.
  • الْوَاشِمَةَ— the one who does tattooing: piercing the skin with a needle until blood flows, then filling it with كُحْل, indigo, or lime so it turns green/blue.
  • الْمُسْتَوْشِمَةَ— the one who requests tattooing to be done to her. Al-Nawawi: this is حَرَام on both the doer and the one it is done to.
Cross-ref: Hadith confirmed in Mirqat (Shamela p.6119) and Takmila Fath al-Mulhim (vol.10 p.164, باب تحريم فعل الواصلة والمستوصلة); Takmila outlines four scholarly positions on وَصْل: (1) وصل بشعر آدمي — حَرَام مُطْلَقًا by إجماع; (2) وصل بشعر طاهر غير آدمي — جمهور say حرام, al-Layth says permissible with wool etc.; (3) Shafi'i: permissible with husband/master's permission; (4) Hanafi المختار (Nawawi cites): وصل بشعر الآدمي حَرَام, وصل بغيره جَائِز for a woman for زِينَة — consistent with Gangohi's position in class notes; Lam'at not yet checked — flagged.
Kitab كِتَابُ اللِّبَاسِ بَابُ التَّرَجُّلِ — الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٤٣٠
وَعَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ مَسْعُودٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ قَالَ: لَعَنَ اللَّهُ الْوَاشِمَاتِ وَالْمُسْتَوْشِمَاتِ وَالْمُتَنَمِّصَاتِ وَالْمُتَفَلِّجَاتِ لِلْحُسْنِ الْمُغَيِّرَاتِ خَلْقَ اللَّهِ فَجَاءَتْهُ امْرَأَةٌ فَقَالَتْ: إِنَّهُ بَلَغَنِي أَنَّكَ لَعَنْتَ كَيْتَ وَكَيْتَ فَقَالَ: مَا لِي لَا أَلْعَنُ مَنْ لَعَنَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ وَمَنْ هُوَ فِي كِتَابِ اللَّهِ فَقَالَتْ: لَقَدْ قَرَأْتُ مَا بَيْنَ اللَّوْحَيْنِ فَمَا وَجَدْتُ فِيهِ مَا تَقُولُ قَالَ: لَئِنْ كُنْتِ قَرَأْتِيهِ لَقَدْ وَجَدْتِيهِ أَمَا قَرَأْتِ: وَمَا آتَاكُمُ الرَّسُولُ فَخُذُوهُ وَمَا نَهَاكُمْ عَنْهُ فَانْتَهُوا قَالَتْ: بَلَى قَالَ: فَإِنَّهُ قَدْ نَهَى عَنْهُ
Narrated by Ibn Masud (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: al-Bukhari and Muslim (Mutfaq Alayh)  ·  Grade: Sahih
Class Notes
  • Other narrations mention النَّامِصَات and الْمُتَنَمِّصَات (both with ص — sad).
  • النَّامِصَات refers to those who pluck the hair of the face (of others).
  • الْمُتَنَمِّصَات refers to those who seek others to do that to them.
  • As for a woman removing her beard, mustache, or goatee if they begin to emerge — this is permissible according to the أَحْنَاف.
  • Women often do نَمْص in their eyebrows.
  • The general rule: anything a person does to their body, whether out of نِيَّة or for the purpose of زِينَة, in such a way that it permanently remains OR makes it seem as though they were born that way — this is prohibited, as it is deception.
  • As for what a woman does to beautify herself for her husband — such as applying حِنَّاء on her hands or reddening her lips — in a way that does not make it resemble her original creation, that is allowed.
  • As for cutting off an additional finger, that is permissible, because one is merely removing an عَيْب.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • الْمُتَنَمِّصَاتِ— those who request removal of facial hair using the منماص (tweezers/pincers); the one who performs it is called نامصة. Al-Nawawi: this is حَرَام except if a woman grows a beard or mustache.
  • الْمُتَفَلِّجَاتِ لِلْحُسْنِ— those who seek gaps (فَلَج) between their front teeth by filing them for beautification. Al-Nawawi: حَرَام if done for beauty; allowed if needed to treat a medical condition or tooth defect.
  • الْمُغَيِّرَاتِ خَلْقَ اللَّهِ— those who change Allah's creation; an adjectival description applying to all the acts mentioned above. The لام in لِلْحُسْنِ indicates the cause — showing the prohibition is specifically for what is done in pursuit of beauty.
Cross-ref: Hadith confirmed in Mirqat (Shamela p.6120) and Takmila Fath al-Mulhim (vol.10 pp.164–167, same باب); Takmila confirms الوَاشِمَة والمُسْتَوْشِمَة are حَرَام on both doer and recipient — النَّهْي is على التحريم; Takmila cites al-Nawawi that the النَّهْي is among the strongest دَلَالَات for prohibition, not merely تنزيه; Lam'at not yet checked — flagged.
Kitab كِتَابُ اللِّبَاسِ بَابُ التَّرَجُّلِ — الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٤٣٣
وَعَنْ أَنَسٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ قَالَ: نَهَى رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ أَنْ يَتَزَعْفَرَ الرَّجُلُ
Narrated by Anas (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: al-Bukhari and Muslim (Mutfaq Alayh)  ·  Grade: Sahih
Class Notes
  • Why is it impermissible? The majority of عُلَمَاء say it is due to the رَائِحَة (smell) — this is why, if a ثَوْب مُزَعْفَر is washed and the smell no longer emanates, they allow it.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • يَتَزَعْفَرَ— to use زَعْفَرَان (saffron) on his garment or body. Mirqat: this is عَادَةُ النِّسَاءِ (a woman's habit); a small amount is overlooked. Abu Isa (al-Tirmidhi): the كَرَاهَة is specifically for using it as طِيب (perfume). طِيبُ الرِّجَالِ مَا خَفِيَ لَوْنُهُ — a man's perfume is that which hides its color (scent without visible color).
Cross-ref: Hadith confirmed in Mirqat (Shamela p.6124, بَابُ التَّزَعْفُر) and Takmila Fath al-Mulhim (vol.10 p.127, بَابُ نَهْيِ الرَّجُلِ عَنِ التَّزَعْفُرِ); Takmila confirms most عُلَمَاء permit a washed saffron garment when nothing remains except the color — consistent with class notes on the smell being the operative cause; Lam'at not yet checked — flagged.
Kitab كِتَابُ اللِّبَاسِ بَابُ التَّرَجُّلِ — الفصل الثاني
حديث ٤٤٤١
وَعَنْ عَمَّارِ بْنِ يَاسِرٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ قَالَ: قَدِمْتُ عَلَى أَهْلِي مِنْ سَفَرٍ وَقَدْ تَشَقَّقَتْ يَدَايَ فَخَلَّقُونِي بِزَعْفَرَانٍ فَغَدَوْتُ عَلَى النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فَسَلَّمْتُ عَلَيْهِ فَلَمْ يَرُدَّ عَلَيَّ وَقَالَ: «اذْهَبْ فَاغْسِلْ هَذَا عَنْكَ»
Narrated by Ammar ibn Yasir (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Abu Dawud  ·  Grade: Hasan
Class Notes
  • It is likely that the زَعْفَرَان was applied for مُدَاوَاة (medical treatment of cracked hands from travel).
  • The Prophet (S.A.W.) still reprimanded him — either because the excuse wasn't clear to him, or because he disliked him coming out in public with it still applied.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • خَلَّقُونِي بِزَعْفَرَانٍ— they applied خَلُوق (a saffron-based perfume) into the cracks of his hands for مُدَاوَاة. Ibn al-Malak: the بِزَعْفَرَانٍ is either for emphasis or on the basis of تجريد.
  • فَلَمْ يَرُدَّ عَلَيَّ— He did not return the greeting. Mirqat: this is one of the strongest refutations against those who permit a small amount without excuse. Three possibilities given: (1) the excuse wasn't apparent to the Prophet (S.A.W.); (2) he disliked him coming out with it; (3) he disliked him keeping it on without washing it.
Cross-ref: Hadith confirmed in Mirqat (Shamela p.6132, بَابُ التَّرَجُّل الفصل الثاني); Takmila vol.10 covers this bab — page not yet pulled; Lam'at not yet checked — flagged.
Kitab كِتَابُ اللِّبَاسِ بَابُ التَّرَجُّلِ — الفصل الثاني
حديث ٤٤٤٢
وَعَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «طِيبُ الرِّجَالِ مَا ظَهَرَ رِيحُهُ وَخَفِيَ لَوْنُهُ وَطِيبُ النِّسَاءِ مَا ظَهَرَ لَوْنُهُ وَخَفِيَ رِيحُهُ»
Narrated by Abu Hurairah (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: al-Tirmidhi and al-Nasa'i  ·  Grade: Hasan
Class Notes
  • مَا ظَهَرَ لَوْنُهُ — if the مَطْلُوب of that طِيب is the color and not the smell.
  • A woman's طِيب being that which has color but not smell applies when she goes outside her house.
  • But when in the house with her husband, she can use any perfume she wants.
  • مَا خَفِيَ رِيحُهُ — it is still called طِيب because it does not mean it has no smell; it is possible that it does have a smell but the smell does not spread far.
  • زَيَّات is the one who sells oil. Here it means that his قِنَاع was like a cloth belonging to a زَيَّات because it was oily.
  • A person is supposed to maintain اعتدال — he should not become disheveled, but he should also not make تَزَيُّن his purpose.
  • This نَهْي is specifically for تَزَيُّن.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • طِيبُ الرِّجَالِ مَا ظَهَرَ رِيحُهُ وَخَفِيَ لَوْنُهُ— a man's perfume is that whose scent is apparent but whose color is hidden. Examples: rosewater, musk, amber, camphor.
  • طِيبُ النِّسَاءِ مَا ظَهَرَ لَوْنُهُ وَخَفِيَ رِيحُهُ— a woman's perfume is that whose color is apparent but whose scent is hidden. Mirqat (citing Sa'd in Sharh al-Sunna): this ruling is for when she goes out; when she is with her husband, she may use any perfume she wishes. Ibn Hajar: examples include زَعْفَرَان and حِنَّاء.
Cross-ref: Hadith confirmed in Mirqat (Shamela p.6133, بَابُ التَّرَجُّل الفصل الثاني); Mirqat cites Abu Musa al-Ash'ari narration — any woman who perfumes herself and walks past a gathering is like such-and-such (i.e., زَانِيَة); Takmila vol.10 — page not yet pulled; Lam'at not yet checked — flagged.
Kitab كِتَابُ اللِّبَاسِ بَابُ التَّرَجُّلِ — الفصل الثاني
حديث ٤٤٥٧
وَعَنْ عَمْرِو بْنِ شُعَيْبٍ عَنْ أَبِيهِ عَنْ جَدِّهِ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «لَا تَنْتِفُوا الشَّيْبَ فَإِنَّهُ نُورُ الْمُسْلِمِ مَنْ شَابَ شَيْبَةً فِي الْإِسْلَامِ كَتَبَ اللَّهُ لَهُ بِهَا حَسَنَةً وَكَفَّرَ عَنْهُ بِهَا خَطِيئَةً وَرَفَعَهُ بِهَا دَرَجَةً»
Narrated by Amr ibn Shu'ayb, from his father, from his grandfather  ·  Riwayah: Abu Dawud  ·  Grade: Hasan
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • لَا تَنْتِفُوا الشَّيْبَ— do not pluck the white hair. Mirqat (Mirak): most عُلَمَاء say it is مَكْرُوه to pluck grey hairs. Ibn al-Arabi: the نهي is for plucking specifically — not for dyeing — because plucking changes the creation from its root, unlike dyeing.
  • نُورُ الْمُسْلِمِ— the Muslim's light/dignity (وَقَار): it restrains the soul from desires and leads to صَالِح works which become نور in the grave and light ahead of him in the darkness of the Resurrection.
  • شَيْبَةً— a single white hair (one strand); the reward applies even for one hair grown in Islam.
Cross-ref: Hadith confirmed in Mirqat (Shamela p.6153, بَابُ التَّرَجُّل الفصل الثاني); placed here to show apparent contradiction with خضاب-encouraging hadiths — see hadith 4458 for discussion; Lam'at not yet checked — flagged.
Kitab كِتَابُ اللِّبَاسِ بَابُ التَّرَجُّلِ — الفصل الثاني
حديث ٤٤٥٨
وَعَنْ كَعْبِ بْنِ مُرَّةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ عَنْ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «مَنْ شَابَ شَيْبَةً فِي الْإِسْلَامِ كَانَتْ لَهُ نُورًا يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ»
Narrated by Ka'b ibn Murra (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: al-Tirmidhi and al-Nasa'i  ·  Grade: Sahih
Class Notes
  • This hadith and the previous one (4457) appear to contradict the other narrations which encourage خضاب.
  • As mentioned previously, al-Tahawi states that the اَحَادِيث of نَهْي are مَنْسُوخ.
  • Some do جَمْع by saying: if the hair is very white — like that of Abu Quhafa — then he should do خضاب; if not, then he should leave it.
  • Imam Muhammad also states that خضاب is جَائِز.
  • Some say the حُكْم of dyeing is specifically for when a person has a mix of black and white — so he should dye it so it doesn't look unsightly (مُسْتَبْشَع). But if the hair is fully white, he should leave it.
  • Some say that the encouragement to do خضاب is specifically for war.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • مَنْ شَابَ شَيْبَةً فِي الْإِسْلَامِ— whoever grows a single white hair while being Muslim.
  • نُورًا يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ— a light (ضِيَاء) and salvation from the darkness and hardships of the Day of Gathering. Mirqat: this is why Ali, Salama ibn al-Akwa', Ubayy ibn Ka'b, and many senior صَحَابَة did not dye — while al-Hasan, al-Husayn, and many others did, using the hadith of Abu Umama as دَلِيل.
Cross-ref: Hadith confirmed in Mirqat (Shamela p.6154, بَابُ التَّرَجُّل الفصل الثاني); Mirqat cites al-Tabari's جمع: خضاب is recommended when the grey is مُسْتَبْشَع (unsightly), otherwise not — but خضاب مُطْلَقًا is still better for مُخَالَفَة أَهْلِ الْكِتَاب — consistent with class notes; Lam'at not yet checked — flagged.
Kitab كِتَابُ اللِّبَاسِ بَابُ التَّرَجُّلِ — الفصل الثاني
حديث ٤٤٧٠
وَعَنْ ثَوْبَانَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ قَالَ: كَانَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ إِذَا سَافَرَ كَانَ آخِرُ عَهْدِهِ بِإِنْسَانٍ مِنْ أَهْلِهِ فَاطِمَةَ وَأَوَّلُ مَنْ يَدْخُلُ عَلَيْهَا فَاطِمَةَ فَقَدِمَ مِنْ غَزَاةٍ وَقَدْ عَلَّقَتْ مَسْحًا أَوْ سِتْرًا عَلَى بَابِهَا وَحَلَّتِ الْحَسَنَ وَالْحُسَيْنَ قُلْبَيْنِ مِنْ فِضَّةٍ فَقَدِمَ فَلَمْ يَدْخُلْ فَظَنَّتْ أَنَّ مَا مَنَعَهُ أَنْ يَدْخُلَ مَا رَأَى فَهَتَكَتِ السِّتْرَ وَفَكَّتِ الْقُلْبَيْنِ عَنِ الصَّبِيَّيْنِ وَقَطَعَتْهُ مِنْهُمَا فَانْطَلَقَا إِلَى رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ يَبْكِيَانِ فَأَخَذَهُ مِنْهُمَا فَقَالَ: «يَا ثَوْبَانُ اذْهَبْ بِهَذَا إِلَى فُلَانٍ إِنَّ هَؤُلَاءِ أَهْلِي أَكْرَهُ أَنْ يَأْكُلُوا طَيِّبَاتِهِمْ فِي حَيَاتِهِمُ الدُّنْيَا يَا ثَوْبَانُ اشْتَرِ لِفَاطِمَةَ قِلَادَةً مِنْ عَصْبٍ وَسُوَارَيْنِ مِنْ عَاجٍ»
Narrated by Thawban (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Ahmad and Abu Dawud  ·  Grade: Da'if
Class Notes
  • مَا رَأَى here refers to the سِتْر (curtain) and the قُلْبَيْن (silver bracelets).
  • They (al-Hasan and al-Husayn) were crying because what they had on them was taken away from them.
  • The meaning of "أَكْرَهُ أَنْ يَأْكُلُوا طَيِّبَاتِهِمْ": I prefer that my family has فَقر in this world so that they can have the طَيِّبَات of the آخرة.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • مَسْحًا أَوْ سِتْرًا— a mat/coarse cloth or a curtain at her door (أَوْ for doubt in the narrator). Mirqat: the curtain was for زِينَة (decoration); had it been for modesty/concealment, he would not have objected. It may also have had pictures (تَمَاثِيل) which caused the objection.
  • قُلْبَيْنِ مِنْ فِضَّةٍ— two silver bracelets (قُلْب = a single bracelet/bangle).
  • أَكْرَهُ أَنْ يَأْكُلُوا طَيِّبَاتِهِمْ فِي حَيَاتِهِمُ الدُّنْيَا— I dislike for them — as I dislike for myself — enjoying fine food, clothing, and luxuries in this life. Mirqat: he chose فَقر and spiritual discipline for them so their ranks in جَنَّة would be higher, and so they would not resemble those of whom Allah said: ﴿أَذْهَبْتُمْ طَيِّبَاتِكُمْ فِي حَيَاتِكُمُ الدُّنْيَا﴾ (Al-Ahqaf 46:20).
Cross-ref: Hadith confirmed in Mirqat (Shamela p.6169, بَابُ التَّرَجُّل الفصل الثاني); Mirqat cites al-Tibi and extensive commentary on the زينة vs modesty question regarding the curtain; Lam'at not yet checked — flagged.
Kitab كِتَابُ اللِّبَاسِ بَابُ التَّرَجُّلِ — الفصل الثاني
حديث ٤٤٧١
وَعَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «عَلَيْكُمْ بِالْإِثْمِدِ فَإِنَّهُ يَجْلُو الْبَصَرَ وَيُنْبِتُ الشَّعَرَ» وَزَعَمَ أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ كَانَ لَهُ مُكْحُلَةٌ يَكْتَحِلُ بِهَا عِنْدَ نَوْمِهِ ثَلَاثًا فِي كُلِّ عَيْنٍ
Narrated by Ibn Abbas (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: al-Tirmidhi  ·  Grade: Hasan
Class Notes
  • إثمد is a stone which is mainly black but has a reddish hue.
  • It is found abundantly in the Hijaz but the best quality of إثمد comes from أصفهان (Isfahan).
  • Some say that إثمد IS كُحْل itself; others say it is the stone from which كُحْل is made.
  • الشَّعَر here refers to the eyelashes (الهُدَب — what grows on the edge of the eyelid).
  • The كُحْل made from إثمد is still available today and is more expensive than normal كُحْل.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • الْإِثْمِدُ— a black stone with a reddish tinge used for كُحْل/eye application. Found in the Hijaz; best quality from Isfahan.
  • يَجْلُو الْبَصَرَ— improves vision and clears the sight (يُحْسِنُ النَّظَرَ), increases the light of the eye, and cleanses the pupil by repelling harmful matter descending from the head.
  • وَيُنْبِتُ الشَّعَرَ— grows the hair. Mirqat: الشَّعَر here = الهُدَب (the eyelashes that grow on the edges of the eyelids — أشفار العين). From Abu Asim and al-Tabari: إثمد is a grower of hair, remover of dirt (مَذْهَبَة لِلْقَذَى), and purifier of sight.
  • مُكْحُلَةٌ— a كُحْل applicator/case. The Prophet (S.A.W.) applied إثمد three times in each eye before sleeping.
Cross-ref: Hadith confirmed in Mirqat (Shamela p.6172, بَابُ التَّرَجُّل الفصل الثاني); Mirqat cites corroborating narrations from Abu Asim, al-Tabari, and Ibn Majah; Lam'at not yet checked — flagged.
Kitab كِتَابُ اللِّبَاسِ بَابُ التَّرَجُّلِ — الفصل الثاني
حديث ٤٤٧٣
وَعَنْ عَائِشَةَ: أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ نَهَى الرِّجَالَ وَالنِّسَاءَ عَنْ دُخُولِ الْحَمَّامَاتِ ثُمَّ رَخَّصَ لِلرِّجَالِ أَنْ يَدْخُلُوا بِالْمِيَازِرِ
Narrated by Aisha (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: al-Tirmidhi and Abu Dawud  ·  Grade: Hasan
Class Notes
  • The حَمَّام here refers to the public bathhouse, not the bathroom of a private home.
  • The رُخْصَة (concession) for men was conditional: they may enter only while wearing their مِيَازِر (lower garments).
  • Mulla Ali Qari: women were completely prohibited from الْحَمَّامَاتِ because they do not feel uncomfortable exposing their bodies to one another — and since that restraint is absent, entry is prohibited entirely.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • الْحَمَّامَاتُ— public bathhouses; from الحمّ (heat); spaces shared by multiple bathers.
  • رَخَّصَ— granted a concession/relaxation; from رخصة (dispensation from a general rule).
  • الْمِيَازِرُ— lower garments, waistcloths; singular مِئْزَر; covering from navel to knee.
Cross-ref: Hadith confirmed in Mirqat commentary on باب الترجل; Mirqat discusses the condition of the مئزر and cites the reason for women's complete prohibition as Mulla Ali Qari's explanation noted above; Lam'at not yet checked — flagged.
Kitab كِتَابُ اللِّبَاسِ بَابُ التَّرَجُّلِ — الفصل الثاني
حديث ٤٤٧٤
وَعَنْ أَبِي الْمَلِيحِ قَالَ: قَدِمَ عَلَى عَائِشَةَ نِسْوَةٌ مِنْ أَهْلِ حِمْصٍ فَقَالَتْ: مَنْ أَيْنَ أَنْتُنَّ؟ قُلْنَ: مِنَ الشَّامِ فَلَعَلَّكُنَّ مِنَ الْكُورَةِ الَّتِي تَدْخُلُ نِسَاؤُهَا الْحَمَّامَاتِ؟ قُلْنَ: بَلَى قَالَتْ: فَإِنِّي سَمِعْتُ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ يَقُولُ: «لَا تَخْلَعُ امْرَأَةٌ ثِيَابَهَا فِي غَيْرِ بَيْتِ زَوْجِهَا إِلَّا هَتَكَتِ السِّتْرَ بَيْنَهَا وَبَيْنَ رَبِّهَا»
Narrated by Abu al-Malih from Aisha (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: al-Tirmidhi and Abu Dawud  ·  Grade: Sahih
Class Notes
  • Mirqat: the reason is that a woman is commanded to cover her عَوْرَة from everyone except her husband, even in complete privacy (خُلْوَة).
  • There are two types of عَوْرَة: the عَوْرَة for which a person incurs sin by exposing it, and the عَوْرَة which حَيَاء demands be covered. For women, حَيَاء demands that their body be covered even when alone or with other women.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • لَا تَخْلَعُ ثِيَابَهَا— she should not remove her clothing; خلع = to strip off/remove entirely.
  • فِي غَيْرِ بَيْتِ زَوْجِهَا— outside her husband's home; the marital space is the only place where full uncovering is permissible.
  • هَتَكَتِ السِّتْرَ— she tears/rips the veil; from هتك = to tear; metaphor for destroying the shield of modesty between herself and her Lord.
Cross-ref: Hadith confirmed in Mirqat commentary; the explanation distinguishing the two types of عَوْرَة (sin-incurring vs. حَيَاء-demanded) is consistent with Mirqat's discussion; Lam'at not yet checked — flagged.
Kitab كِتَابُ اللِّبَاسِ بَابُ التَّصَاوِيرِ — الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٤٩٤
«أَشَدُّ النَّاسِ عَذَابًا يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ الَّذِينَ يُضَاهُونَ بِخَلْقِ اللَّهِ»
Narrated by Aisha (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: al-Bukhari and Muslim (Muttafaq Alayh)  ·  Grade: Sahih
Class Notes
  • Some scholars say this refers to those who actually attempt to rival Allah in the act of creation — trying to create a living being.
  • Ibn al-Malak: if one believes he can genuinely rival Allah's creative act, he is a كَافِر. If he doesn't hold that belief, then this hadith is taken as تَهْدِيد (severe warning/threat) — not a statement of تَكْفِير.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • يُضَاهُونَ— they rival/imitate; from مضاهاة = to emulate or compete with; applied here to imitating Allah's exclusive act of creation.
  • بِخَلْقِ اللَّهِ— in what Allah has created; the prefix بـ implies comparison and rivalry — they set their work alongside Allah's.
Cross-ref: Hadith confirmed in Mirqat (باب التصاوير); Ibn al-Malak's distinction between اعْتِقَادُ الْمُسَاوَاة (كُفْر) and mere act without such belief (تَهْدِيد) confirmed in Mirqat; consistent with class notes; Lam'at not yet checked — flagged.
Kitab كِتَابُ اللِّبَاسِ بَابُ التَّصَاوِيرِ — الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٤٩٨
وَعَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «مَنْ تَحَلَّمَ بِحُلُمٍ لَمْ يَرَهُ كُلِّفَ أَنْ يَعْقِدَ بَيْنَ شَعِيرَتَيْنِ وَلَنْ يَفْعَلَ وَمَنِ اسْتَمَعَ إِلَى حَدِيثِ قَوْمٍ وَهُمْ لَهُ كَارِهُونَ أَوْ يَفِرُّونَ مِنْهُ صُبَّ فِي أُذُنَيْهِ الْآنُكُ يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ وَمَنْ صَوَّرَ صُورَةً عُذِّبَ وَكُلِّفَ أَنْ يَنْفُخَ فِيهَا وَلَيْسَ بِنَافِخٍ»
Narrated by Ibn Abbas (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: al-Bukhari  ·  Grade: Sahih
Class Notes
  • Lying about a dream is worse than ordinary lying because it is lying about عِلْمُ الْغَيْبِ (unseen knowledge).
  • Also because رُؤْيَا (dream) is a جُزْء of نُبُوَّة — so he is effectively claiming that Allah showed him something which Allah did not show him.
  • يَفِرُّونَ مِنْهُ — they flee from him so that he does not hear their conversation.
  • The first and last punishments ظَاهِرًا imply that this person will be punished forever — but this appears to contradict the position of أَهْلُ السُّنَّةِ وَالْجَمَاعَةِ (that Muslim sinners do not receive eternal punishment).
  • Ibn Hajar's response: الْمُرَاد is زَجْر شَدِيد — threatening them with the punishment of a كَافِر (خُلُود in the fire) as a severe deterrent. الظَّاهِر (literal sense of eternity) is not the intended meaning; this is a rhetorical emphasis known in classical Arabic rhetoric, paralleled in Nawawi's explanation in Sharh Muslim that such threats of eternal punishment for Muslim sinners are تَغْلِيظ (exaggerated severity) for deterrence.
  • All the previous أَحَادِيث in this section have زَجْر against pictures, collectively showing that pictures of ذَوِي الْأَرْوَاحِ (animate beings) are مَمْنُوع, and the majority of فُقَهَاء agree.
  • Many narrations from the صَحَابَة (R.A.) and تَابِعِينَ also prohibit this.
  • The claim that النَّهْي against pictures was only to prevent idol worship — and thus is no longer applicable since the aversion to idol worship is already firm — is incorrect. الْعِلَّة stated in the أَحَادِيث is مُضَاهَاةُ خَلْقِ اللَّهِ, which still applies today.
  • مَذَاهِب on image-making: Nawawi (R.A.) — making pictures of living beings is حَرَام, أَشَدُّ تَحْرِيمٍ, whether مُمْتَهَن (degraded) or not, whether on cloth or coin; pictures of trees and things without رُوح are permissible; pictures on degraded objects like carpets (stepped on) are allowed; no distinction between 2D and 3D; this is the position of Abu Hanifah (R.A.), al-Shafi'i (R.A.), Ahmad (R.A.), al-Thawri, and others.
  • Among the الْمَالِكِيَّة: the مُجْمَعٌ عَلَيْهِ position is the حُرْمَة of 3D images; there is اخْتِلَاف on 2D.
  • Ibn Baz: this (regarding video/photography) is مَحَلُّ النَّظَر and I do تَوَقُّف due to the severe warnings against صُوَر.
  • If الْعِلَّة is مُضَاهَاةٌ بِخَلْقِ اللَّهِ, then why restrict الْحُرْمَة to ذَوِي الْأَرْوَاحِ? — Mufti Shafi' (R.A.): things without رُوح — while created by Allah just like those with رُوح — involve some human contribution (like planting a seed); in contrast, humans have absolutely no involvement in creating life within an animal or human, hence the special prohibition.
  • Regarding video: other عُلَمَاء do not accept the قِيَاس on a mirror because a video can be paused and rewound while a mirror cannot.
  • Nardasheer (backgammon): its حُرْمَة is مَنْصُوصٌ عَلَيْهِ (explicitly stated in hadith). If gambling is removed, الْعِلَّة for prohibition is disputed; the most defensible الْعِلَّة is that the game pieces are historically related to idols used in worship.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • تَحَلَّمَ— fabricated/invented a dream; claimed to have seen a dream which he did not see; from حلم (dream) with تفعّل indicating feigning/pretending.
  • شَعِيرَتَيْنِ— two barley grains; the punishment is to be tasked with tying a knot between them — an impossible task symbolizing endless futile torment.
  • الْآنُكُ— molten lead; poured into the ears of the eavesdropper on the Day of Judgment as a fitting punishment.
  • مَنْ صَوَّرَ صُورَةً— whoever makes an image (of a living being); tasked with blowing life into it, which he can never do — showing the futility and gravity of claiming rivalry with Allah's creation.
Cross-ref: Hadith confirmed in Mirqat (باب التصاوير, الفصل الأول); Mirqat discusses the three punishments and the question of خُلُود in context of زَجْر; Ibn Hajar's تَغْلِيظ explanation confirmed in Mirqat citing Nawawi; the fuller فِقْهِي discussion on مَذَاهِب (Nawawi, Abu Hanifah, Mufti Shafi') aligns with Mirqat and class notes; Lam'at not yet checked — flagged.
Kitab كِتَابُ الطِّبِّ وَالرُّقَى بَابُ الأَدْوِيَةِ وَالتَّدَاوِي — الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٥١٣
عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «مَا أَنْزَلَ اللَّهُ دَاءً إِلَّا أَنْزَلَ لَهُ دَوَاءً»
Narrated by Abu Hurairah (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: al-Bukhari  ·  Grade: Sahih
Translation
"Allah has not sent down a disease except that He has also sent down its cure."
Class Notes
  • The treatments mentioned by Rasulullah (S.A.W.) are known as الطِّبُّ النَّبَوِيّ.
  • What is the حَيْثِيَّة (status/nature) of these treatments?
  • Some عُلَمَاء state that the medicines mentioned by Rasulullah (S.A.W.) are not part of the شَرِيعَة which Allah has commanded us to follow — such as Ibn Khaldun: لَيْسَ مِنَ الْوَحْيِ شَيْءٌ (these are not from وَحْي, but from habit and experience).
  • Others like Ibn Qayyim state that his treatments are not like those of ordinary doctors — because his treatments are مُتَيَقَّنٌ فِيهِ since they come from وَحْي and نُبُوَّة.
  • Mufti Taqi: both احْتِمَالَان are possible; but what we can say is that any medicine which is ثَابِت and صَحِيح from the Prophet (S.A.W.) is not خِلَافُ الْوَاقِع, and these medicines are not part of شَرِيعَة, so following them is not obligatory. Even if his statement is not direct وَحْي, if it were خِلَافُ الْوَاقِع then وَحْي would have come to correct it.
  • We can say that the treatments mentioned by Rasulullah (S.A.W.) are not part of شَرِيعَة or رِسَالَة — they are not among those things mandatory on everyone in every place and time; there is no sin in not using them, and a person will not be considered as leaving the شَرِيعَة.
  • These أَحَادِيث motivate and encourage both the sick and the doctors.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • دَاءً— illness/disease; from الداء = any harmful bodily ailment; the indefinite form (نكرة) in سياق النفي indicates comprehensiveness.
  • إِلَّا أَنْزَلَ لَهُ دَوَاءً— except that He sent down for it a cure; the parallel use of أَنْزَلَ for both داء and دواء emphasizes divine origin and pairing of illness with remedy.
  • دَوَاءً— cure/medicine/remedy; from الدواء; existence of a cure is certain even when it remains unknown to humans.
Cross-ref: Hadith confirmed in Mirqat (بَابُ الأَدْوِيَةِ وَالتَّدَاوِي, الفصل الأول); Mirqat discusses the حَيْثِيَّة of الطِّبُّ النَّبَوِيّ and records the debate between Ibn Khaldun's position (not from وَحْي) and Ibn Qayyim's position (مُتَيَقَّنٌ فِيهِ); Mufti Taqi's reconciliation (both احْتِمَالَان valid; any ثَابِت treatment is not خِلَافُ الْوَاقِع) consistent with class notes; Lam'at not yet checked — flagged.
Kitab كِتَابُ الطِّبِّ وَالرُّقَى بَابُ الأَدْوِيَةِ وَالتَّدَاوِي — الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٥١٤
وَعَنْ جَابِرٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «لِكُلِّ دَاءٍ دَوَاءٌ فَإِذَا أُصِيبَ دَوَاءُ الدَّاءِ بَرَأَ بِإِذْنِ اللَّهِ عَزَّ وَجَلَّ»
Narrated by Jabir (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Muslim  ·  Grade: Sahih
Translation
"For every disease there is a cure; so when the cure of a disease is correctly applied, it heals by the permission of Allah the Almighty."
Class Notes
  • Objection: there are many diseases which people take medicines for but are not cured.
  • Answer (القاضي عياض): not being cured is due to not knowing the correct treatments and method of treatment — not due to the absence of any cure. Similarly, when doctors say a disease has no cure, that is because they do not know what the cure is, not that no cure exists at all.
  • Nawawi: this hadith shows اسْتِحْبَاب of taking medicine when sick; this is the مَذْهَب of خَلَف and سَلَف; it does رَدّ on those who deny and reject مُدَاوَاة — specifically the extremists among الصُّوفِيَّة.
  • The extremists say: everything is based on قَدَر so there is no benefit in taking any treatment.
  • Response: we do not claim that دَوَاء is مُؤَثِّر in itself — rather it has its effect through the permission of Allah; مُدَاوَاة is also part of قَدَر, just as making دُعَاء and refraining from putting oneself in harm are also part of قَدَر; the existence of قَدَر does not negate these concepts.
  • Is the عُمُوم of this hadith completely مُطْلَق? Some عُلَمَاء state that it is مَخْصُوصٌ عَنْهُ الْبَعْض — like al-Khattabi and Ibn Arabi.
  • Ibn Abi Jamrah al-Andalusi (d. 699 A.H.): saying it is مَخْصُوصٌ عَنْهُ الْبَعْض is a clear mistake — because that opinion is based on تَجْرِبَة, not on وَحْي. How can we prefer doctors' experience over the one about whom وَمَا يَنْطِقُ عَنِ الْهَوَى (Al-Najm 53:3) was said?
  • Mufti Taqi: both احْتِمَالَان have no problem — it is very common for Arabs to use كُلّ in the meaning of أَكْثَر; but what Ibn Abi Jamrah said is also correct, because just because doctors say something is not beneficial for a certain disease does not mean that what Rasulullah (S.A.W.) stated is incorrect — their statement reflects the limits of their تَجْرِبَة and knowledge, not the non-existence of the cure; the Prophet's (S.A.W.) word, grounded in وَحْي, is not negated by the limits of human medical knowledge.
  • Gangohi: this (the hadith) does not mean that medicine is always beneficial in all amounts and methods — rather, to use it for all diseases it needs to be given based on the مِزَاج of the مَرِيض; the amounts might vary; one might need to give other medicines alongside to bring the effect properly.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • لِكُلِّ دَاءٍ دَوَاءٌ— for every disease there is a cure; whether كُلّ is مُطْلَق (absolute) or means أَكْثَر (most) is a point of scholarly debate — see notes above.
  • أُصِيبَ دَوَاءُ الدَّاءِ— when the cure of the disease is hit/matched precisely; من الإصابة = to hit the mark exactly; cure requires correct identification of the disease and the right remedy.
  • بَرَأَ— was cured / recovered; the cure is conditional on both correct application and Allah's permission (بِإِذْنِ اللَّهِ).
  • بِإِذْنِ اللَّهِ عَزَّ وَجَلَّ— by the permission of Allah the Mighty and Majestic; the medicine is not an independent cause — its effect is entirely through Allah's will, refuting those who treat medicine as مُؤَثِّر in itself.
Cross-ref: Hadith confirmed in Mirqat (بَابُ الأَدْوِيَةِ وَالتَّدَاوِي, الفصل الأول); Mirqat records القاضي عياض's answer to the objection and Nawawi's position on اسْتِحْبَاب of مُدَاوَاة; the رَدّ on the extremists of الصُّوفِيَّة and the قَدَر argument confirmed in Mirqat; Ibn Abi Jamrah's argument on عُمُوم vs. Khattabi/Ibn Arabi's تَخْصِيص position both noted in Mirqat; Gangohi's note on مِزَاج-dependent application consistent with classical طِبّ principles; Lam'at not yet checked — flagged.
Kitab كِتَابُ الطِّبِّ وَالرُّقَى بَابُ الأَدْوِيَةِ وَالتَّدَاوِي — الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٥١٦
وَعَنْ جَابِرٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ قَالَ: رُمِيَ أَبِي يَوْمَ الْأَحْزَابِ عَلَى أَكْحَلِهِ فَكَوَاهُ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ
Narrated by Jabir (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Muslim  ·  Grade: Sahih
Translation
My father was struck on his cephalic vein (vein in the middle of the hand) on the Day of Ahzaab, and the Messenger of Allah (S.A.W.) cauterized him.
Class Notes
  • The عُلَمَاء have various ways to do جَمْع between the أَحَادِيث which prohibit الْكَيّ (cauterization) and those which permit it — see حَاشِيَة 3 for the full discussion of جَمْع opinions.
  • Rasulullah (S.A.W.) did not like الْكَيّ because of its extreme pain — sometimes the ضَرَر is more than the نَفْع; so النَّهْي against it is إِرْشَادِيّ/تَنْزِيهِيّ (by way of guidance and discouragement), not تَحْرِيمِيّ.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • رُمِيَ— was struck/hit (by an arrow); passive form; Jabir's (R.A.) father was wounded during the Battle of the Confederates (غَزْوَة الْأَحْزَاب, 5 A.H.).
  • أَكْحَلُهُ— his cephalic vein (الأكحل); the prominent vein of the forearm/elbow, historically used for bloodletting and targeted in serious wounds.
  • فَكَوَاهُ— and he cauterized him; from الكيّ = cauterization using a heated instrument; used here to seal the wound and prevent further blood loss or infection.
Cross-ref: Hadith confirmed in Mirqat (بَابُ الأَدْوِيَةِ وَالتَّدَاوِي, الفصل الأول); Mirqat discusses the جَمْع between الكيّ prohibiting and permitting أَحَادِيث; the النَّهْي being إِرْشَادِيّ/تَنْزِيهِيّ (not تَحْرِيمِيّ) due to the extreme pain and risk of ضَرَر outweighing نَفْع confirmed in Mirqat — consistent with class notes; حَاشِيَة 3 contains further detail on جَمْع positions; Lam'at not yet checked — flagged.
Kitab كِتَابُ الطِّبِّ وَالرُّقَى بَابُ الأَدْوِيَةِ وَالتَّدَاوِي — الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٥٢٠
عَنْ أَبِي سَعِيدٍ الْخُدْرِيِّ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ أَنَّ رَجُلًا أَتَى النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فَقَالَ: أَخِي اسْتَطْلَقَ بَطْنُهُ. فَقَالَ: «اسْقِهِ عَسَلًا». فَسَقَاهُ ثُمَّ جَاءَ فَقَالَ: سَقَيْتُهُ فَلَمْ يَزِدْهُ إِلَّا اسْتِطْلَاقًا. فَقَالَ ذَلِكَ ثَلَاثَ مَرَّاتٍ. ثُمَّ جَاءَ الرَّابِعَةَ فَقَالَ: «اسْقِهِ عَسَلًا». فَقَالَ: لَقَدْ سَقَيْتُهُ فَلَمْ يَزِدْهُ إِلَّا اسْتِطْلَاقًا. فَقَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «صَدَقَ اللَّهُ وَكَذَبَ بَطْنُ أَخِيكَ». فَسَقَاهُ فَبَرَأَ
Narrated by Abu Sa'id al-Khudri (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: al-Bukhari & Muslim  ·  Grade: Muttafaq Alayh
Translation
A man came to the Prophet (S.A.W.) and said: "My brother's stomach has become loose." The Messenger of Allah (S.A.W.) said: "Give him honey to drink." He gave it to him, then came back and said: "I gave it to him but it only increased his looseness." This happened three times. Then he came the fourth time and he said: "Give him honey to drink." He said: "I have given it to him but it only increased his looseness." The Messenger of Allah (S.A.W.) said: "Allah spoke the truth and your brother's stomach lied." He gave him honey again and he was cured.
Class Notes
  • صَدَقَ اللَّهُ is إِشَارَة to the آية فِيهِ شِفَاءٌ لِلنَّاسِ (Surah al-Nahl, 16:69) — Allah declared honey a cure, and this hadith is a practical demonstration of that truth.
  • Apparent objection: how could the Prophet (S.A.W.) keep prescribing honey when it apparently worsened the اسْتِطْلَاق? Answer: disease differs person to person; what worsens one may cure another.
  • Why did honey initially increase اسْتِطْلَاق? — the honey was removing harmful toxins from the بَطْن, which temporarily increased the اسْتِطْلَاق, but in doing so it cleansed and ultimately fixed the بَطْن — the person and his brother did not realise this process was happening.
  • صَدَقَ اللَّهُ وَكَذَبَ بَطْنُ أَخِيكَ — Allah is truthful; honey is indeed a cure; the reason it appeared not to work was the abundance of toxins; the بَطْن's resistance was not evidence against the cure.
  • Rasulullah (S.A.W.) continued prescribing honey with full confidence, knowing it would fix the بَطْن in the end.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • اسْتَطْلَقَ بَطْنُهُ— his stomach became loose; اسْتِطْلَاق = looseness of the bowels (diarrhea).
  • اسْقِهِ عَسَلًا— give him honey to drink; command form addressed to the brother.
  • فَلَمْ يَزِدْهُ إِلَّا اسْتِطْلَاقًا— it did nothing but increase his looseness; apparent worsening due to the honey expelling toxins.
  • صَدَقَ اللَّهُ— Allah spoke the truth; إِشَارَة to Quran 16:69 (فِيهِ شِفَاءٌ لِلنَّاسِ).
  • كَذَبَ بَطْنُ أَخِيكَ— your brother's بَطْن "lied" (i.e., its apparent resistance was misleading); the honey was working beneath the surface by purging toxins.
  • فَبَرَأَ— and he was cured.
Cross-ref: Hadith confirmed in Mirqat (بَابُ الأَدْوِيَةِ وَالتَّدَاوِي, الفصل الأول); إِشَارَة to Quran 16:69 noted in Mirqat; the explanation of temporary worsening as toxin purging discussed in Mirqat commentary; Lam'at not yet checked — flagged.
Kitab كِتَابُ الطِّبِّ وَالرُّقَى بَابُ الأَدْوِيَةِ وَالتَّدَاوِي — الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٥٢٢
وَعَنْ أُمِّ قَيْسٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهَا قَالَتْ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «لَا تُعَذِّبُوا صِبْيَانَكُمْ بِالْغَمْزِ مِنَ الْعُذْرَةِ عَلَيْكُمْ بِالْقُسْطِ»
Narrated by Umm Qais (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: al-Bukhari & Muslim  ·  Grade: Muttafaq Alayh
Translation
"Do not torture your children by squeezing for uvulitis — you must use costus (الْقُسْط)."
Class Notes
  • Previously, people thought that by squeezing (الْغَمْز) the inflamed tonsils/uvula (الْعُذْرَة), blood or pus would come out and the child would be treated — the Prophet (S.A.W.) forbade this painful and ineffective practice and prescribed الْقُسْط instead.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • لَا تُعَذِّبُوا— do not torture/cause pain; النَّهْي here is تَحْرِيمِيّ or تَنْزِيهِيّ depending on the degree of harm inflicted.
  • صِبْيَانَكُمْ— your children; young ones whose uvula or throat is affected.
  • الْغَمْزِ— pressing/squeezing; the folk practice of pressing the uvula or inflamed tonsils with fingers to release blood or pus.
  • الْعُذْرَةِ— tonsil inflammation / uvulitis; a condition causing throat pain, swelling, and difficulty swallowing in children; also refers to the uvula itself in some usages.
  • عَلَيْكُمْ بِالْقُسْطِ— you must use الْقُسْط; prescriptive command; الْقُسْط = costus root (Indian/sea costus), a principal remedy of Prophetic medicine.
Cross-ref: Hadith confirmed in Mirqat (بَابُ الأَدْوِيَةِ وَالتَّدَاوِي, الفصل الأول); الْغَمْز as folk Arab practice and الْعُذْرَة as uvulitis/tonsillitis confirmed in Mirqat; see Hadith 4523 (Umm Qais, longer version) for further detail on الْقُسْط and its seven cures; Lam'at not yet checked — flagged.
Kitab كِتَابُ الطِّبِّ وَالرُّقَى بَابُ الأَدْوِيَةِ وَالتَّدَاوِي — الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٥٢٣
وَعَنْ أُمِّ قَيْسٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهَا قَالَتْ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «عَلَى مَ تَدْغَرْنَ أَوْلَادَكُنَّ بِهَذَا الْعِلَاقِ؟ عَلَيْكُنَّ بِهَذَا الْعُودِ الْهِنْدِيِّ فَإِنَّ فِيهِ سَبْعَةَ أَشْفِيَةٍ مِنْهَا ذَاتُ الْجَنْبِ يُسْعَطُ مِنَ الْعُذْرَةِ وَيُلَدُّ مِنْ ذَاتِ الْجَنْبِ»
Narrated by Umm Qais (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: al-Bukhari & Muslim  ·  Grade: Muttafaq Alayh
Translation
"Why do you press your children's throats in this manner? You must use this Indian wood (costus), for indeed it contains seven cures — among them pleurisy. It is used as nasal drops for uvulitis and placed in the side of the mouth for pleurisy."
Class Notes
  • Some عُلَمَاء say the number سَبْعَة (seven) here is for تَكْثِير (indicating a large/abundant number) rather than تَحْدِيد (specifying an exact count of seven remedies).
  • الْقُسْط = wooden pieces of roots or trunk from a tree normally found in India; a highly prized root used extensively in Prophetic medicine.
  • Transported by sea traders, it is also called الْقُسْطُ الْبَحْرِيّ (the sea-brought costus).
  • Some عُلَمَاء say ذَاتُ الْجَنْبِ in this hadith refers specifically to pleurisy (inflammation of the lining of the lungs).
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • تَدْغَرْنَ— you press/push (plural feminine); from الدَّغْر = pressing on the palate or throat; the act of pushing the child's uvula upward with the fingers.
  • الْعِلَاقِ— this pressing practice; the folk method of treating الْعُذْرَة by manual pressure on the throat.
  • الْعُودِ الْهِنْدِيِّ— Indian wood/root; = الْقُسْط (costus); from the Indian subcontinent, transported by sea = الْقُسْطُ الْبَحْرِيّ.
  • سَبْعَةَ أَشْفِيَةٍ— seven cures/remedies; some عُلَمَاء say سَبْعَة here is for تَكْثِير (a large number) not تَحْدِيد (an exact count of seven).
  • ذَاتُ الْجَنْبِ— literally "the one of the side"; the ailment affecting the side/chest; some عُلَمَاء say it refers to pleurisy (inflammation of the pleural lining of the lungs).
  • يُسْعَطُ— it is administered as nasal drops; from السَّعُوط = medicine introduced through the nose; prescribed for الْعُذْرَة.
  • يُلَدُّ— it is placed in the side of the mouth; from اللَّدُود = medicine given from the cheek/side of the mouth; prescribed for ذَاتُ الْجَنْبِ.
Cross-ref: Hadith confirmed in Mirqat (بَابُ الأَدْوِيَةِ وَالتَّدَاوِي, الفصل الأول); سَبْعَة as تَكْثِير vs. تَحْدِيد discussion confirmed in Mirqat; الْقُسْط = الْعُودُ الْهِنْدِيّ and الْقُسْطُ الْبَحْرِيّ etymology confirmed; ذَاتُ الْجَنْبِ as pleurisy noted in Mirqat; see Hadith 4522 for the shorter version of this incident; Lam'at not yet checked — flagged.
Kitab كِتَابُ الطِّبِّ وَالرُّقَى بَابُ الأَدْوِيَةِ وَالتَّدَاوِي — الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٥٢٤
الْحُمَّى مِنْ فَيْحِ جَهَنَّمَ فَأَبْرِدُوهَا بِالْمَاءِ
Narrated by Aisha (R.A.) and Rafi' ibn Khadij (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: al-Bukhari and Muslim (Muttafaq Alayh)  ·  Grade: Sahih
Translation
"Fever is from the breath/blaze of Hell, so cool it with water."
Class Notes
  • Mufti Taqi: there is another possibility not mentioned by the shurrah, but it is not بَعِيد — that sickness is the punishment for the evil a person has committed.
  • A person has been given the punishment in this دُنْيَا as if it is part of the punishment of the fire, but it has been given to him early, and so he is saved from the punishment in the آخِرَة.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • الْحُمَّى— fever; a rise in the body's heat. Here its spiritual origin is described as being from the breath/heat of Hellfire.
  • فَيْحِ جَهَنَّمَ— the breath/blaze of Hell; فَيْح = intense exhalation of heat; used either as a spiritual reality or as a simile for the intensity of fever's heat.
  • فَأَبْرِدُوهَا بِالْمَاءِ— so cool it with water; إبراد = lowering the heat; indicates the use of cold water as treatment for fever.
Cross-ref: Muttafaq Alayh confirmed; Mufti Taqi's interpretation (sickness as early punishment substituting for آخِرَة punishment) not yet located to specific page in Takmila — flagged; Mirqat and Lam'at pages not yet pulled — flagged.
Kitab كِتَابُ الطِّبِّ وَالرُّقَى بَابُ الأَدْوِيَةِ وَالتَّدَاوِي — الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٥٢٥
رَخَّصَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فِي الرُّقْيَةِ مِنَ الْعَيْنِ وَالْحُمَّةِ وَالنَّمْلَةِ
Narrated by Anas ibn Malik (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Muslim  ·  Grade: Sahih
Translation
"The Messenger of Allah (S.A.W.) gave permission (رُخْصَة) for رُقْيَة from the evil eye, the scorpion sting, and the نَمْلَة."
Class Notes
  • There was a time when رُقْيَة was not allowed; this hadith establishes the رُخْصَة permitting it.
  • الْعَيْن refers to the pain/affliction of the eye — i.e., the evil eye.
  • الْحُمَّة refers to the sting of a scorpion, though it can also be applied to snakebite.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • رَخَّصَ— gave permission/concession (رُخْصَة); implies that رُقْيَة had previously been prohibited or restricted, and this hadith lifts that restriction for specific conditions.
  • الْعَيْنِ— the evil eye; the harm caused by an admiring or envious gaze directed at another person.
  • الْحُمَّةِ— the sting/venom, primarily of a scorpion; can also encompass snakebite by extension.
  • النَّمْلَةِ— lit. "ant"; in medical usage: small blisters or pustules that appear on the skin; another meaning is a sickness that afflicts the skin without penetrating it.
Cross-ref: Confirmed in Muslim; Mirqat and Lam'at pages not yet pulled — flagged.
Kitab كِتَابُ الطِّبِّ وَالرُّقَى بَابُ الأَدْوِيَةِ وَالتَّدَاوِي — الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٥٢٧
وَعَنْ أُمِّ سَلَمَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهَا أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ رَأَى فِي بَيْتِهَا جَارِيَةً فِي وَجْهِهَا سَفْعَةٌ فَقَالَ: «اسْتَرْقُوا لَهَا فَإِنَّ بِهَا النَّظْرَةَ»
Narrated by Umm Salama (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: al-Bukhari and Muslim (Muttafaq Alayh)  ·  Grade: Sahih
Translation
"The Prophet (S.A.W.) saw a girl in her home whose face had a سَفْعَة — meaning a yellowish discoloration — and he said: 'Seek رُقْيَة for her, for she has been afflicted by the evil eye (النَّظْرَة).'"
Class Notes
  • Some explain سَفْعَة (with سين فاء عين تاء مربوطة) as صُفْرَة (yellowness), some as سَوَاد (blackness), and some as حُمْرَة (redness).
  • The result is that parts of her face were not their normal skin color — whatever the exact nature of the discoloration.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • سَفْعَةٌ— discoloration on the face; scholars differ on its exact color: some say صُفْرَة (yellowness), some سَوَاد (blackness), some حُمْرَة (redness); the overall meaning is an abnormal color in part of her face departing from her natural complexion.
  • اسْتَرْقُوا لَهَا— seek رُقْيَة for her; i.e., request someone to perform رُقْيَة on her behalf.
  • النَّظْرَةَ— the evil glance/gaze; a synonym of الْعَيْن; the harm caused by a harmful or admiring look.
Cross-ref: Confirmed as Muttafaq Alayh; Mirqat and Lam'at pages not yet pulled — flagged.
Kitab كِتَابُ الطِّبِّ وَالرُّقَى بَابُ الأَدْوِيَةِ وَالتَّدَاوِي — الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٥٢٩
اعْرِضُوا عَلَيَّ رُقَاكُمْ لَا بَأْسَ بِالرُّقَى مَا لَمْ يَكُنْ فِيهِ شِرْكٌ
Narrated by Auf ibn Malik al-Ashja'i (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Muslim  ·  Grade: Sahih
Translation
"Present your رُقَى to me. There is no harm in رُقَى so long as they do not contain شِرْك."
Class Notes
  • Mufti Taqi: this hadith is the أَصْل (foundation) of this bab.
  • This is why it is prohibited to use a رُقْيَة whose meaning is not known — because it is possible it contains some form of شِرْك.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • اعْرِضُوا عَلَيَّ رُقَاكُمْ— present your رُقَى to me for inspection/approval; the command was to vet the incantations being used in pre-Islamic practice.
  • لَا بَأْسَ بِالرُّقَى— there is no harm/objection in رُقَى; لَا بَأْس indicates permissibility after a prior restriction.
  • مَا لَمْ يَكُنْ فِيهِ شِرْكٌ— as long as it does not contain شِرْك; this is the decisive condition. If the رُقْيَة's meaning is unknown, it cannot be verified to be free of شِرْك — hence the prohibition on using unfamiliar رُقَى.
Cross-ref: Confirmed in Muslim; Mufti Taqi's commentary noted from Takmila Fath al-Mulhim — exact page not yet pulled, flagged; Mirqat and Lam'at pages not yet pulled — flagged.
Kitab كِتَابُ الطِّبِّ وَالرُّقَى بَابُ الأَدْوِيَةِ وَالتَّدَاوِي — الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٥٣٠
الْعَيْنُ حَقٌّ فَلَوْ كَانَ شَيْءٌ سَابَقَ الْقَدَرَ سَبَقَتْهُ الْعَيْنُ وَإِذَا اسْتُغْسِلْتُمْ فَاغْسِلُوا
Narrated by Ibn Abbas (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Muslim  ·  Grade: Sahih
Translation
"The evil eye is real. If anything were to outstrip divine decree, the evil eye would. And if you are asked to wash (for the afflicted), then wash."
Class Notes
  • إِصَابَةُ الْعَيْنِ — a man sees and looks with amazement/admiration at something he likes in another person, so the مَنْظُور إِلَيْه is harmed due to the evil glance of the نَاظِر and his إِعْجَاب.
  • After the effect of عَيْن takes place: the نَاظِر is called عَائِن; the مَنْظُور إِلَيْه is called مَعْيُون.
  • فَلَوْ كَانَ شَيْءٌ سَابِقٌ — the effect of عَيْن is very strong and real, but it still operates within the bounds of قَدَر.
  • How does عَيْن have effect? Just as a person's face and emotions can change when people look at them, similarly a person's صِحَّة can be affected by another's amazed gaze — by the إِجْرَاء of Allah, with the actual مُؤَثِّر being the رُوح of the نَاظِر.
  • Al-Maziri: the concept of غَسْل and using that water for the مَعْيُون cannot be understood through عَقْل, so it also cannot be rejected on the basis of عَقْل.
  • This غَسْل is only effective if the مَعْيُون believes in the method.
  • Mufti Taqi: this method of غَسْل is only after the effect of عَيْن has already occurred. As for when a person thinks he may cause عَيْن at the time of looking, he should say لَا حَوْلَ وَلَا قُوَّةَ إِلَّا بِاللَّهِ.
  • Also, if هَلَاك or destruction of a limb is feared from the عَيْن, this غَسْل becomes وَاجِب upon the عَائِن.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • الْعَيْنُ حَقٌّ— the evil eye is a reality; حَقّ here = an established and real phenomenon, not a metaphor or superstition.
  • سَابَقَ الْقَدَرَ— outstripped/preceded divine decree; a hypothetical condition — meaning even in such an impossible scenario, the evil eye would be the most potent force, showing how powerful and real it is.
  • اسْتُغْسِلْتُمْ— you are asked/requested to wash; the عَائِن (the one who caused the عَيْن) performs غَسْل (washing) and the water is then used to treat the مَعْيُون.
  • فَاغْسِلُوا— then wash; a command to the عَائِن to comply when asked; the method is established by نَصّ and its mechanism is beyond عَقْل — making it both undeniable and irrefutable by reason.
Cross-ref: Confirmed in Muslim; Mufti Taqi and al-Maziri's commentary from Takmila Fath al-Mulhim — exact pages not yet pulled, flagged; Mirqat and Lam'at pages not yet pulled — flagged.
Kitab كِتَابُ الطِّبِّ وَالرُّقَى بَابُ الأَدْوِيَةِ وَالتَّدَاوِي — الفصل الثاني
حديث ٤٥٣١
قَالُوا: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ أَفَنَتَدَاوَى؟ قَالَ: «نَعَمْ يَا عِبَادَ اللَّهِ تَدَاوَوْا فَإِنَّ اللَّهَ لَمْ يَضَعْ دَاءً إِلَّا وَضَعَ لَهُ شِفَاءً غَيْرَ دَاءٍ وَاحِدٍ الْهَرَمُ»
Narrated by Usama ibn Sharik (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Ahmad, al-Tirmidhi, Abu Dawud  ·  Grade: Sahih
Translation
"They said: O Messenger of Allah, shall we seek treatment? He said: 'Yes, O servants of Allah, seek treatment. For Allah has not created a disease except that He created a cure for it — except for one disease: old age.'"
Class Notes
  • Gangohi: this hadith is for إِبَاحَة (permissibility) and تَخْيِير (choice) — not وُجُوب (obligation).
  • تَوَكُّل is of different types:
  • Type 1 — تَوَكُّل that goes against a نَصّ, such as jumping off a cliff, drinking poison, or refusing to eat. This is against the آية: وَلَا تُلْقُوا بِأَيْدِيكُمْ إِلَى التَّهْلُكَةِ (2:195). This type is حَرَام.
  • Type 2 — Leaving those things in which there is غَالِبُ الظَّنّ that they are a سَبَب, such as taking medicine. This is the highest level of تَوَكُّل. Based on this, not taking medicine is more virtuous than taking it.
  • Type 3 — Leaving that which there is no غَالِبُ الظَّنّ that it is a سَبَب. This is the lowest level of تَوَكُّل.
  • Based on this, the أَحَادِيث where Rasulullah (S.A.W.) commands taking medicine are for إِبَاحَة, not اسْتِحْبَاب.
  • Not taking medicine is the highest level of تَوَكُّل, but taking it does not go against أَصْلُ التَّوَكُّل.
  • There is no وُجُوب of taking or giving medication, so it is جَائِز to remove a person from a ventilator if their chances of recovery are not high.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • أَفَنَتَدَاوَى— shall we seek medical treatment? The hamza + fa indicates they sought confirmation/permission from the Prophet (S.A.W.).
  • تَدَاوَوْا— seek treatment; a command, but Gangohi clarifies this is for إباحة not وجوب.
  • الْهَرَمُ— old age/senility; the one "disease" Allah has not created a cure for, as it is the natural termination of life itself.
Cross-ref: Confirmed in Ahmad, Tirmidhi, and Abu Dawud; Gangohi's commentary on تَوَكُّل types noted from class; Mirqat and Lam'at pages not yet pulled — flagged.
Kitab كِتَابُ الطِّبِّ وَالرُّقَى بَابُ الأَدْوِيَةِ وَالتَّدَاوِي — الفصل الثاني
حديث ٤٥٣٢
لَا تُكْرِهُوا مَرْضَاكُمْ عَلَى الطَّعَامِ فَإِنَّ اللَّهَ يُطْعِمُهُمْ وَيَسْقِيهِمْ
Narrated by Uqba ibn Amir (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: al-Tirmidhi and Ibn Majah  ·  Grade: Hasan Gharib
Translation
"Do not force your sick to eat, for Allah gives them food and drink."
Class Notes
  • Gangohi: the meaning is that Allah will put something in place of their food and drink — not that He literally feeds them and gives them drink.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • لَا تُكْرِهُوا— do not force/compel; إكراه = compelling against one's will.
  • مَرْضَاكُمْ— your sick people; pl. of مَرِيض.
  • يُطْعِمُهُمْ وَيَسْقِيهِمْ— He feeds them and gives them drink; Gangohi: means Allah compensates/substitutes for the food and drink they are not consuming — not a literal divine feeding, but that their body's needs are fulfilled through Allah's إجراء without forced intake.
Cross-ref: Confirmed in Tirmidhi and Ibn Majah; Mirqat and Lam'at pages not yet pulled — flagged.
Kitab كِتَابُ الطِّبِّ وَالرُّقَى بَابُ الأَدْوِيَةِ وَالتَّدَاوِي — الفصل الثاني
حديث ٤٥٣٦
عَنْ أَسْمَاءَ بِنْتِ عُمَيْسٍ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ سَأَلَهَا: «بِمَ تَسْتَمْشِينَ؟» قَالَتْ: بِالشُّبْرُمِ قَالَ: «حَارٌّ جَارٌّ» قَالَتْ: ثُمَّ اسْتَمْشَيْتُ بِالسَّنَا فَقَالَ النَّبِيُّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «لَوْ أَنَّ شَيْئًا كَانَ فِيهِ الشِّفَاءُ مِنَ الْمَوْتِ لَكَانَ فِي السَّنَا»
Narrated by Asma' bint Umais (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: al-Tirmidhi and Ibn Majah  ·  Grade: Hasan Gharib
Translation
"The Prophet (S.A.W.) asked Asma' bint Umais (R.A.): 'What do you use as a laxative?' She said: 'شُبْرُم.' He said: 'It is intensely hot (حَارّ جَارّ).' She said: 'Then I used سَنَا.' The Prophet (S.A.W.) said: 'If anything contained a cure from death, it would be سَنَا.'"
Class Notes
  • حَارٌّ — this plant (شُبْرُم) has a lot of heat.
  • What is جَارٌّ? Some explain it as إِتْبَاع — a rhyming echo word used for تَأْكِيد of the previous word, similar to رُوٹِی بُوٹِی (roti boti) or چَائے شَائے (chai shai) in Urdu.
  • Gangohi: saying that جَارّ is used as إِتْبَاع is not correct. Rather, it means that شُبْرُم pulls out and expels substances that the person did not even intend to expel. The best quality of this plant is found in Makkah.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • بِمَ تَسْتَمْشِينَ— what do you use as a laxative/purgative? اسْتِمْشَاء = using something to induce bowel movement; lit. "to make oneself walk/move."
  • الشُّبْرُمُ— a plant (spurge/Euphorbia); a powerful purgative plant known for its intense heat.
  • حَارٌّ جَارٌّ— intensely hot; حَارّ = hot; جَارّ: (1) some say إِتْبَاع — a rhyming echo word for emphasis; (2) Gangohi says it means "one that pulls/drags out" — شُبْرُم expels more substances from the body than the person intended.
  • السَّنَا— senna; a medicinal plant praised by the Prophet (S.A.W.) as the closest thing to a cure for death — indicating its exceptional healing properties.
Cross-ref: Confirmed in Tirmidhi and Ibn Majah (Hasan Gharib); Gangohi's distinction on جَارّ noted from class; Mirqat and Lam'at pages not yet pulled — flagged.
Kitab كِتَابُ الطِّبِّ وَالرُّقَى بَابُ الأَدْوِيَةِ وَالتَّدَاوِي — الفصل الثاني
حديث ٤٥٣٧
إِنَّ اللَّهَ أَنْزَلَ الدَّاءَ وَالدَّوَاءَ وَجَعَلَ لِكُلِّ دَاءٍ دَوَاءً فَتَدَاوُوا وَلَا تَتَدَاوَوْا بِحَرَامٍ
Narrated by Abu al-Darda' (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Abu Dawud  ·  Grade: Da'if (al-Albani)
Translation
"Indeed Allah has sent down the disease and the cure, and He has made a cure for every disease — so seek treatment, but do not seek treatment with anything forbidden."
Class Notes
  • The أَحْنَاف state: التَّدَاوِي بِالْمُحَرَّم is حَرَام, unless a حَاذِق (skilled/expert) doctor states that there is no other حَلَال medicine available for that condition.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • أَنْزَلَ الدَّاءَ وَالدَّوَاءَ— He sent down the disease and the cure; both paired together to show that Allah is the source of both, and neither occurs outside of His will.
  • لَا تَتَدَاوَوْا بِحَرَامٍ— do not seek treatment with what is forbidden; the Ahnaf apply this absolutely — except when a حَاذِق doctor certifies no حَلَال alternative exists.
Cross-ref: Confirmed in Abu Dawud; graded Da'if by al-Albani; Ahnaf position on تداوي بالمحرم consistent with established فِقْه; Mirqat and Lam'at pages not yet pulled — flagged.
Kitab كِتَابُ الطِّبِّ وَالرُّقَى بَابُ الأَدْوِيَةِ وَالتَّدَاوِي — الفصل الثاني
حديث ٤٥٣٩
مَا كَانَ أَحَدٌ يَشْتَكِي إِلَى رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ وَجَعًا فِي رَأْسِهِ إِلَّا قَالَ: «احْتَجِمْ» وَلَا وَجَعًا فِي رِجْلَيْهِ إِلَّا قَالَ: «اخْتَضِبْهُمَا»
Narrated by Salma, the Prophet's servant (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Abu Dawud  ·  Grade: Sahih
Translation
"Whenever anyone came to the Messenger of Allah (S.A.W.) complaining of pain in his head, he would say: 'Get cupped.' And whenever someone complained of pain in his feet, he would say: 'Apply henna to them both.'"
Class Notes
  • Mirqat: the hadith is عَامّ for both men and women, but men should limit the حِنَّاء to the soles of their feet; they should not apply it to their fingers or the top of their feet, so as to refrain from تَشَبُّه بِالنِّسَاء.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • يَشْتَكِي— complains of; reports pain to someone; اشتكاء = voicing one's ailment.
  • احْتَجِمْ— get cupped; perform حِجَامَة (wet cupping therapy); prescribed for head pain.
  • اخْتَضِبْهُمَا— apply henna to them both (the two feet); خِضَاب with حِنَّاء on the feet as a remedy for leg pain. Mirqat: the command is general but men must restrict application to the soles only, avoiding fingers and top of feet due to تَشَبُّه بِالنِّسَاء.
Cross-ref: Confirmed in Abu Dawud (Sahih); Mirqat's ruling on men restricting hinna to soles noted; Lam'at page not yet pulled — flagged.
Kitab كِتَابُ الطِّبِّ وَالرُّقَى بَابُ الأَدْوِيَةِ وَالتَّدَاوِي — الفصل الثاني
حديث ٤٥٤١
مَنْ أَهْرَاقَ مِنْ هَذِهِ الدِّمَاءِ فَلَا يَضُرُّهُ أَنْ لَا يَتَدَاوَى بِشَيْءٍ لِشَيْءٍ
Narrated by Abu Kabsha al-Anmari (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Abu Dawud and Ibn Majah  ·  Grade: not yet fully graded (al-Albani)
Translation
"Whoever lets this blood (i.e., performs cupping), it will not harm him not to seek any other treatment for anything."
Class Notes
  • I.e., after performing حِجَامَة, it will not harm him to not take any other medicine — indicating the comprehensiveness of cupping as a treatment.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • أَهْرَاقَ مِنْ هَذِهِ الدِّمَاءِ— let/shed this blood; إِهْرَاقَة الدَّم = drawing out blood through حِجَامَة (cupping); "these bloods" refers to the blood drawn through the cupping procedure.
  • فَلَا يَضُرُّهُ أَنْ لَا يَتَدَاوَى بِشَيْءٍ لِشَيْءٍ— it will not harm him not to seek treatment with anything for anything; indicates cupping is sufficiently comprehensive that no further treatment is needed.
Cross-ref: Confirmed in Abu Dawud and Ibn Majah; Mirqat and Lam'at pages not yet pulled — flagged.
Kitab كِتَابُ الطِّبِّ وَالرُّقَى بَابُ الأَدْوِيَةِ وَالتَّدَاوِي — الفصل الثاني
حديث ٤٥٤٢
احْتَجَمَ عَلَى وَرِكِهِ مِنْ وَثْءٍ كَانَ بِهِ
Narrated by Jabir (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Abu Dawud  ·  Grade: not yet fully graded (al-Albani)
Translation
"He (the Prophet S.A.W.) had himself cupped on his thigh/hip for a contusion he had suffered."
Class Notes
  • Another meaning of وَثْء/النَّمْلَة (in the context of this bab) is a sickness that afflicts the skin without penetrating it.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • الْوَرِكُ— the hip/thigh region; the area above the thigh and below the waist.
  • وَثْءٌ— a contusion or bruise caused by a blow, without breaking the skin; also used for strain/sprain. The shurrah note another meaning in this context: a condition that afflicts the surface of the skin without penetrating into it.
Cross-ref: Confirmed in Abu Dawud; Mirqat and Lam'at pages not yet pulled — flagged.
Kitab كِتَابُ الطِّبِّ وَالرُّقَى بَابُ الأَدْوِيَةِ وَالتَّدَاوِي — الفصل الثاني
حديث ٤٥٥٥
وَعَنْ عِيسَى بْنِ حَمْزَةَ قَالَ: دَخَلْتُ عَلَى عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ عُكَيْمٍ وَبِهِ حُمْرَةٌ فَقُلْتُ: أَلَا تُعَلِّقُ تَمِيمَةً؟ فَقَالَ: نَعُوذُ بِاللَّهِ مِنْ ذَلِكَ قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «مَنْ تَعَلَّقَ شَيْئًا وُكِلَ إِلَيْهِ»
Narrated by 'Isa ibn Hamza from Abdullah ibn Ukaim (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Abu Dawud  ·  Grade: Hasan
Translation
"'Isa ibn Hamza said: I visited Abdullah ibn Ukaim who was suffering from a skin redness (humra). I said: 'Will you not hang an amulet?' He said: 'I seek refuge in Allah from that! The Messenger of Allah (S.A.W.) said: Whoever attaches himself to something will be left to it.'"
Class Notes
  • Al-Tibi: perhaps he (Abdullah ibn Ukaim (R.A.)) said أَعُوذُ بِاللَّهِ because he was from the مُتَوَكِّلُون and he adhered to the highest level of تَوَكُّل.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • حُمْرَةٌ— a skin ailment marked by redness; some identify it as erysipelas (a bacterial skin infection causing redness and swelling).
  • تَمِيمَةً— an amulet/charm; something hung on the body for protection or cure; prohibited when relied upon independently of Allah.
  • مَنْ تَعَلَّقَ شَيْئًا وُكِلَ إِلَيْهِ— whoever attaches/hangs himself to something will be entrusted/left to it; meaning Allah withdraws His direct care and the person is left dependent on that object — hence the complete ineffectiveness and prohibition of amulets.
Cross-ref: Confirmed in Abu Dawud; al-Tibi's commentary on Abdullah ibn Ukaim's تَوَكُّل noted from class; Mirqat and Lam'at pages not yet pulled — flagged.
Kitab كِتَابُ الطِّبِّ وَالرُّقَى بَابُ الأَدْوِيَةِ وَالتَّدَاوِي — الفصل الثاني
حديث ٤٥٦١
وَعَنْ أَبِي أُمَامَةَ بْنِ سَهْلِ بْنِ حُنَيْفٍ قَالَ: رَأَى عَامِرُ بْنُ رَبِيعَةَ سَهْلَ بْنَ حُنَيْفٍ يَغْتَسِلُ فَقَالَ: وَاللَّهِ مَا رَأَيْتُ كَالْيَوْمِ وَلَا جِلْدَ مُخَبَّأَةٍ قَالَ: فَلُبِطَ سَهْلٌ فَأَتَى رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فَقِيلَ لَهُ: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ هَلْ لَكَ فِي سَهْلِ بْنِ حُنَيْفٍ؟ وَاللَّهِ مَا يَرْفَعُ رَأْسَهُ فَقَالَ: «هَلْ تَتَّهِمُونَ لَهُ أَحَدًا؟» فَقَالُوا: نَتَّهِمُ عَامِرَ بْنَ رَبِيعَةَ قَالَ: فَدَعَا رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ عَامِرًا فَتُغُلِّظَ عَلَيْهِ وَقَالَ: «عَلَامَ يَقْتُلُ أَحَدُكُمْ أَخَاهُ؟ أَلَا بَرَّكْتَ؟ اغْتَسِلْ لَهُ» فَغَسَلَ لَهُ عَامِرٌ وَجْهَهُ وَيَدَيْهِ وَمِرْفَقَيْهِ وَرُكْبَتَيْهِ وَأَطْرَافَ رِجْلَيْهِ وَدَاخِلَةَ إِزَارِهِ فِي قَدَحٍ ثُمَّ صُبَّ عَلَيْهِ فَرَاحَ مَعَ النَّاسِ لَيْسَ لَهُ بَأْسٌ
Narrated by Abu Umama ibn Sahl ibn Hunayf (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Sharh al-Sunna (al-Baghawi) and Malik  ·  Grade: Sahih
Translation
"Amir ibn Rabi'a (R.A.) saw Sahl ibn Hunayf (R.A.) bathing and said: 'By Allah, I have never seen anything like today — not even the skin of a secluded girl!' Sahl then suddenly collapsed. The Prophet (S.A.W.) was told: 'O Messenger of Allah, what is the matter with Sahl ibn Hunayf? By Allah, he cannot even lift his head.' He said: 'Whom do you suspect?' They said: 'Amir ibn Rabi'a.' So the Prophet (S.A.W.) called Amir and reprimanded him, saying: 'Why does one of you kill his brother? Why did you not say بَارَكَ اللَّهُ? Wash for him.' So Amir washed his face, hands, elbows, knees, the ends of his feet, and the inner fold of his lower garment into a bowl — then it was poured over Sahl, and he walked with the people with no ailment."
Class Notes
  • Some of Sahl's (R.A.) body was exposed since he was taking a bath — which is how Amir ibn Rabi'a (R.A.) saw his skin and was struck by amazement.
  • Mirqat: this hadith shows that the عَائِن has a choice — he can choose whether to afflict the person or not — otherwise Rasulullah (S.A.W.) would not have reprimanded him.
  • This is further indicated by the words أَلَا بَرَّكْتَ — i.e., why did you not say بَارَكَ اللَّهُ when you saw him? The reprimand shows that he had an alternative.
  • Qadi Iyad: when you know that a person causes a lot of عَيْن, you should avoid him.
  • The قَاضِي should order him to stay in his house; and if he is فَقِير, he should be given رِزْق to the extent of his need — because his ضَرَر is greater than the ضَرَر of garlic and onions in the مَسْجِد, which themselves carry prohibitions.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • وَلَا جِلْدَ مُخَبَّأَةٍ— nor the skin of a secluded/sheltered girl; مُخَبَّأَة = a girl kept in seclusion/purdah whose skin has not been exposed to sun or harsh conditions; used as the ultimate standard of beauty and softness of skin.
  • فَلُبِطَ سَهْلٌ— Sahl suddenly collapsed; لُبِطَ = was struck down suddenly, fell without control.
  • أَلَا بَرَّكْتَ— why did you not say بَارَكَ اللَّهُ? i.e., why did you not invoke Allah's blessing when you saw him? This is the prescribed preventive — the reprimand confirms the عَائِن had a choice and is culpable for not saying it.
  • دَاخِلَةَ إِزَارِهِ— the inner/lower fold of his lower garment (إِزَار); washed as part of the غَسْل procedure for عَيْن and then the water poured over the مَعْيُون.
Cross-ref: Confirmed in Sharh al-Sunna (al-Baghawi) and مُوَطَّأ Malik (Sahih); Mirqat's point on the عَائِن having choice and culpability noted; Qadi Iyad's ruling on confining the aa'in confirmed — Mirqat and Lam'at page numbers not yet pulled, flagged.
Kitab كِتَابُ الطِّبِّ وَالرُّقَى بَابُ الْفَأْلِ وَالطِّيَرَةِ — الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٥٧٥
لَا طِيَرَةَ وَخَيْرُهَا الْفَأْلُ قَالُوا: وَمَا الْفَأْلُ؟ قَالَ: «الْكَلِمَةُ الصَّالِحَةُ يَسْمَعُهَا أَحَدُكُمْ»
Narrated by Abu Huraira (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: al-Bukhari and Muslim (Muttafaq Alayh)  ·  Grade: Sahih
Translation
"'There is no (power in) evil omens, and the best of (what they associated with it) is the فَأْل.' They asked: 'What is فَأْل?' He said: 'A good word that one of you hears.'"
Class Notes
  • فَأْل = تَيَامُن (taking a good omen). It is sometimes also used for تَشَاؤُم (bad omen), but تَيَامُن is the more common usage and is the مُرَاد here.
  • The أَصْل of تَطَيُّر in the time of جَاهِلِيَّة: people would rely on birds to determine good or bad omens before embarking on something.
  • If a bird flew to the right, they would consider it a good omen (تَيَامُن) and proceed. This bird was called بَارِح (with big ح).
  • If a bird flew to the left, they would consider it a bad omen (تَشَاؤُم) and abandon their action. This bird was called سَانِح.
  • So the original meaning of تَطَيُّر covers both تَشَاؤُم and تَيَامُن with birds, but it then became commonly used for any تَشَاؤُم even without birds.
  • لَا means تَطَيُّر has no تَأْثِير — it has no real effect.
  • Kirmani: the إِضَافَة in خَيْرُهَا is not إِضَافَة جُزْئِيَّة (which would imply طِيَرَة has two types: good and bad); rather it is إِضَافَة لِلْبَيَان.
  • Ibn Hajar: the إِضَافَة is حَقِيقِيَّة — because the Arabs would do تَطَيُّر for both good and bad omens, so the two-type reading is valid.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • لَا طِيَرَةَ— there is no (power/effect in) evil omens; لَا here is لَا النَّافِيَة لِلْجِنْسِ, negating all forms of تَطَيُّر categorically; meaning it has no real تَأْثِير.
  • الْفَأْلُ— a good omen; taking a positive interpretation from something one sees or hears; the opposite of تَشَاؤُم. Its أَصْل was specific to birds, then extended to any sign.
  • الْكَلِمَةُ الصَّالِحَةُ— a good/wholesome word; defined by the Prophet (S.A.W.) as the meaning of فَأْل — something positive a person hears that lifts his spirits and gives him hope.
  • خَيْرُهَا الْفَأْلُ— "the best of it (طِيَرَة) is فَأْل"; the إِضَافَة here is disputed: Kirmani says إِضَافَة لِلْبَيَان (طِيَرَة = فَأْل, one thing clarified by another); Ibn Hajar says إِضَافَة حَقِيقِيَّة (طِيَرَة has two types — good and bad — and فَأْل is the good type).
Cross-ref: Confirmed as Muttafaq Alayh; Kirmani vs. Ibn Hajar debate on إِضَافَة noted; Mirqat and Lam'at pages not yet pulled — flagged.
Kitab كِتَابُ الطِّبِّ وَالرُّقَى بَابُ الْفَأْلِ وَالطِّيَرَةِ — الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٥٧٦
لَا عَدْوَى وَلَا طِيَرَةَ وَلَا هَامَةَ وَلَا صَفَرَ وَفِرَّ مِنَ الْمَجْذُومِ كَمَا تَفِرُّ مِنَ الْأَسَدِ
Narrated by Abu Huraira (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: al-Bukhari  ·  Grade: Sahih
Translation
"There is no contagion (in itself), no evil omen, no hama, and no safar. And flee from the leper as you would flee from a lion."
Class Notes
  • The مَشْهُور opinion mentioned here is that the أَصْل of this hadith is نَفْيُ الْعَدْوَى — negating the idea that diseases spread by themselves.
  • The only reason Rasulullah (S.A.W.) told us to flee from a leper is so that if the healthy person becomes sick after interacting with the sick person, he does not think he became sick because of the عَدْوَى of the disease — so the أَمْر was actually meant to remove the possibility of اعتقاد فاسد.
  • Mufti Taqi: if it is established medically that germs of one sick body can transfer to another body, this does not contradict نَفْيُ الْعَدْوَى — because the مَنْفِيّ is the عَدْوَى being مُؤَثِّر حَقِيقِي by itself without Allah. There is no doubt that this اعتقاد is كُفْر and شِرْك.
  • As for believing that the transferral of germs can be a سَبَب for ضَرَر — just as other harmful things are considered سَبَب — and that all of this is subject to the will of Allah and His decree, such that if Allah does not will it, the germs will not transfer, or they will transfer but not cause sickness — this is a valid اعتقاد.
  • And since the norm for certain sicknesses is to transfer from one body to another, like جُذَام and طَاعُون, Rasulullah (S.A.W.) told people not to mix with them due to اختيار الأسباب.
  • Utilizing these أسباب does not go against تَوَكُّل, as long as the person recognizes that these أسباب are not مُؤَثِّر حَقِيقِي — similar to how wearing a jacket in the cold does not contradict تَوَكُّل.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • لَا عَدْوَى— there is no contagion (in itself); نَفْيُ الْعَدْوَى = negation of the pre-Islamic and incorrect belief that diseases spread by their own power, independently of Allah's will.
  • لَا هَامَةَ— no هَامَة; a pre-Islamic superstition that the spirit of a murdered person became an owl (هَامَة) crying at the grave of the deceased until blood was taken in revenge.
  • لَا صَفَرَ— no صَفَر; disputed meanings: (1) the month of صَفَر was considered inauspicious; (2) a disease believed to reside in the belly causing pain (worms); (3) a snakebite to the abdomen. All such beliefs are negated.
  • الْمَجْذُومِ— the leper; one afflicted with جُذَام (leprosy); fleeing from him is commanded not because the disease has independent power to spread, but as اختيار الأسباب without attributing مُؤَثِّر حَقِيقِي to the disease itself.
  • كَمَا تَفِرُّ مِنَ الْأَسَدِ— as you flee from a lion; the simile emphasizes urgency and shows that the caution is real and practical — not superstitious fear, but سَبَب-based avoidance within the framework of تَوَكُّل.
Cross-ref: Confirmed in al-Bukhari (Sahih); Mufti Taqi's reconciliation of نَفْيُ الْعَدْوَى with medical germ theory noted from Takmila Fath al-Mulhim — exact page not yet pulled, flagged; Mirqat and Lam'at pages not yet pulled — flagged.
Kitab كِتَابُ الطِّبِّ وَالرُّقَى بَابُ الْفَأْلِ وَالطِّيَرَةِ — الفصل الثاني
حديث ٤٥٨١
عَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ قَالَ: كَانَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ يَتَفَاءَلُ وَلَا يَتَطَيَّرُ وَكَانَ يُحِبُّ الِاسْمَ الْحَسَنَ
Narrated by Ibn Abbas (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Sharh al-Sunna (al-Baghawi)
Translation
"He (S.A.W.) would take good omens and would not take evil omens, and he loved a beautiful name."
Class Notes
  • He would take good omens (فَأْل) and would not take bad omens (طِيَرَة).
  • He loved a beautiful name (الِاسْمَ الْحَسَنَ), because a good name can be a source of فَأْل.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • يَتَفَاءَلُ— takes a فَأْل (good omen); to interpret something seen or heard as a positive sign; a habitual practice of the Prophet (S.A.W.).
  • يَتَطَيَّرُ— takes a bad omen (طِيَرَة); originally from observing birds as omens; negated here — the Prophet (S.A.W.) explicitly did not do this.
  • الِاسْمَ الْحَسَنَ— a beautiful/pleasing name; loved by the Prophet (S.A.W.) because a good name carries positive meaning and can naturally serve as a source of فَأْل.
Cross-ref: Narrated via Sharh al-Sunna (al-Baghawi); Mirqat and Lam'at pages not yet pulled — flagged.
Kitab كِتَابُ الطِّبِّ وَالرُّقَى بَابُ الْفَأْلِ وَالطِّيَرَةِ — الفصل الثاني
حديث ٤٥٨٢
وَعَنْ قَطَنِ بْنِ قَبِيصَةَ عَنْ أَبِيهِ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «الْعِيَافَةُ وَالطَّرْقُ وَالطِّيَرَةُ مِنَ الْجِبْتِ»
Narrated by Qabisa (R.A.) (via his son Qatan ibn Qabisa)  ·  Riwayah: Abu Dawud
Translation
"الْعِيَافَةُ, الطَّرْقُ, and الطِّيَرَةُ are from الْجِبْتِ."
Class Notes
  • The teacher connected this hadith to the Quran آية (4:51): أَلَمْ تَرَ إِلَى الَّذِينَ أُوتُوا نَصِيبًا مِنَ الْكِتَابِ يُؤْمِنُونَ بِالْجِبْتِ وَالطَّاغُوتِ.
  • These three things (الْعِيَافَةُ, الطَّرْقُ, الطِّيَرَةُ) are from what شَيْطَان commands people to do through وَسْوَسَة.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • الْعِيَافَةُ— augury from birds; determining omens by observing the direction, flight, or sounds of birds; a pre-Islamic Arab practice condemned in Islam.
  • الطَّرْقُ— divination by drawing lines in sand or casting/striking pebbles on the ground; a form of كَهَانَة (soothsaying).
  • الطِّيَرَةُ— evil omens; taking bad signs from birds, sounds, or events; negated throughout this bab.
  • الْجِبْتُ— everything followed or worshipped besides Allah; encompasses سِحْر (magic), divination, false deities; referenced in the Quran (4:51) where the People of the Book are censured for believing in الْجِبْت وَالطَّاغُوت.
Cross-ref: Narrated in Abu Dawud; connection to Quran (4:51) noted by teacher; Mirqat and Lam'at pages not yet pulled — flagged.
Kitab كِتَابُ الطِّبِّ وَالرُّقَى بَابُ الْفَأْلِ وَالطِّيَرَةِ — الفصل الثاني
حديث ٤٥٨٤
وَعَنْ جَابِرٍ أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ أَخَذَ بِيَدِ مَجْذُومٍ فَوَضَعَهَا مَعَهُ فِي الْقَصْعَةِ وَقَالَ: «كُلْ ثِقَةً بِاللَّهِ وَتَوَكُّلًا عَلَيْهِ»
Narrated by Jabir ibn Abdullah (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Ibn Majah
Translation
"The Prophet (S.A.W.) took the hand of a leper and placed it with his own in the bowl, saying: 'Eat, with trust in Allah and reliance upon Him.'"
Class Notes
  • This action of the Prophet (S.A.W.) shows that عَدْوَى (contagion) is not a مُؤَثِّر حَقِيقِيّ — diseases do not spread by their own inherent power independently of Allah's will.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • مَجْذُومٍ— a person afflicted with جُذَام (leprosy); from جَذَمَ (to cut off), as the disease erodes the extremities.
  • الْقَصْعَةُ— a wide communal bowl or dish used for eating; the shared bowl makes the Prophet's act of eating with the leper especially demonstrative.
  • ثِقَةً بِاللَّهِ— with trust in Allah; complete confidence that Allah alone controls benefit and harm; functions as حَال or تَعْلِيل for the act of eating together.
  • تَوَكُّلًا عَلَيْهِ— with reliance upon Him; absolute dependence on Allah; paired with ثِقَة to show this was an act of spiritual trust, not recklessness, since عَدْوَى has no independent power.
Cross-ref: Narrated in Ibn Majah; connects to 4576 (نَفْيُ الْعَدْوَى and مُؤَثِّر حَقِيقِيّ discussion); Mirqat and Lam'at pages not yet pulled — flagged.
