Kitab كِتَابُ الطِّبِّ وَالرُّقَى بَابُ الْفَأْلِ وَالطِّيَرَةِ — الفصل الثاني
حديث ٤٥٨٦
وَعَنْ أَنَسٍ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ كَانَ يُعْجِبُهُ إِذَا خَرَجَ لِحَاجَةٍ أَنْ يَسْمَعَ: يَا رَاشِدُ يَا نَجِيحُ
Narrated by Anas ibn Malik (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: al-Tirmidhi
Translation
"He (S.A.W.) would be pleased, when setting out for a need, to hear: 'O Rashid! O Najeeh!'"
Class Notes
  • From يَا رَاشِدُ (one who is rightly guided, who does not go astray) — he would take the فَأْل that he would not lose his path.
  • From يَا نَجِيحُ (one who succeeds in achieving his goal) — he would take the فَأْل that his needs are fulfilled, because that is نَجَاح (success).
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • كَانَ يُعْجِبُهُ— it used to please him / he was delighted by it; from عَجَبَ; indicates this was a regular, habitual response of the Prophet (S.A.W.).
  • يَا رَاشِدُ— O Rightly-guided one!; from رُشْد (being on the correct path, not straying); the Prophet (S.A.W.) took from this name the فَأْل that his journey would be guided and on course.
  • يَا نَجِيحُ— O Successful one!; from نَجَاح (achieving one's goals, succeeding in one's mission); the Prophet (S.A.W.) took from this name the فَأْل that his needs would be fulfilled and his mission would succeed.
Cross-ref: Narrated in al-Tirmidhi; illustrates the practice of فَأْل from good names, consistent with hadith 4581 (Ibn Abbas); Mirqat and Lam'at pages not yet pulled — flagged.
Kitab كِتَابُ الطِّبِّ وَالرُّقَى بَابُ الْفَأْلِ وَالطِّيَرَةِ — الفصل الثاني
حديث ٤٥٨٨
وَعَنْ أَنَسٍ قَالَ: قَالَ رَجُلٌ: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ إِنَّا كُنَّا فِي دَارٍ كَثُرَ فِيهَا عَدَدُنَا وَأَمْوَالُنَا فَتَحَوَّلْنَا إِلَى دَارٍ قَلَّ فِيهَا عَدَدُنَا وَأَمْوَالُنَا فَقَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «ذَرُوهَا ذَمِيمَةً»
Narrated by Anas ibn Malik (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Abu Dawud  ·  Grade: Hasan
Translation
A man said: "O Messenger of Allah, we were in a house in which our numbers and wealth were great; then we moved to another house in which our numbers and wealth decreased." The Messenger of Allah (S.A.W.) said: "Leave it — it is blameworthy (ذَمِيمَةً)."
Class Notes
  • ذَرُوهَا = leave it, i.e., move away from it.
  • Khattabi (Ma'alim al-Sunan, on Abu Dawud 3924): إِنَّمَا أَمَرَهُمْ بِالتَّحَوُّلِ عَنْهَا إِبْطَالاً لِمَا وَقَعَ فِي نُفُوسِهِمْ مِنْ أَنَّ الْمَكْرُوهَ إِنَّمَا أَصَابَهُمْ بِسَبَبِ السُّكْنَى فِي تِلْكَ الدَّارِ — "He only commanded them to move from it in order to nullify what had settled in their hearts — that the harm only befell them because of their residing in that house." [Verify complete text from Ma'alim al-Sunan]
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • تَحَوَّلْنَا— we moved/transferred our residence; from حَوَّلَ (to transfer, to change); a deliberate relocation to a new house.
  • ذَرُوهَا— leave it; abandon it; plural imperative from ذَرَ (to leave, to let be); the Prophet's command to vacate that house and not remain.
  • ذَمِيمَةً— blameworthy; reprehensible; condemned; حَال (circumstantial description) — leave it in a state of being blameworthy; from ذَمَّ (to blame, to censure). The wisdom: not to affirm that the house caused harm, but to remove the superstition from the hearts — as explained by Khattabi.
Cross-ref: Narrated in Abu Dawud (3924), graded Hasan; Khattabi's commentary in Ma'alim al-Sunan noted — full text and exact page reference not yet pulled, flagged; Mirqat and Lam'at pages not yet pulled — flagged.
Kitab كِتَابُ الطِّبِّ وَالرُّقَى بَابُ الْكَهَانَةِ — الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٥٩١
عَنْ مُعَاوِيَةَ بْنِ الْحَكَمِ قَالَ: قُلْتُ: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ، أُمُورًا كُنَّا نَصْنَعُهَا فِي الْجَاهِلِيَّةِ: كُنَّا نَأْتِي الْكُهَّانَ، قَالَ: «فَلَا تَأْتُوا الْكُهَّانَ»، قُلْتُ: كُنَّا نَتَطَيَّرُ، قَالَ: «ذَلِكَ شَيْءٌ يَجِدُهُ أَحَدُكُمْ فِي نَفْسِهِ فَلَا يَصُدَّنَّكُمْ»، قُلْتُ: وَمِنَّا رِجَالٌ يَخُطُّونَ، قَالَ: «كَانَ نَبِيٌّ مِنَ الْأَنْبِيَاءِ يَخُطُّ، فَمَنْ وَافَقَ خَطَّهُ فَذَاكَ»
Narrated by Mu'awiyah ibn al-Hakam (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Muslim
Translation
I asked: "O Messenger of Allah, about things we used to do in the days of ignorance: we used to visit soothsayers (كُهَّان)." He said: "Do not visit the soothsayers." I said: "We used to take omens (نَتَطَيَّرُ)." He said: "That is something one of you finds within himself — do not let it deter you." I said: "And among us there are men who draw lines (يَخُطُّونَ)." He said: "There was a prophet among the prophets who used to draw lines — whoever matches his lines, then so be it."
Class Notes
  • Another definition of كَاهِن: the one who informs about unseen matters (الَّذِي يُخْبِرُ عَنِ الْمُغَيَّبَاتِ).
  • Qadi Iyad — كَهَانَة was of three types among the Arabs:
    • (1) A person has a جِنّ companion who eavesdrops on the conversations of the angels in the heavens and relays them to the كَاهِن — this type ended with the sending of Rasulullah (S.A.W.) as a prophet.
    • (2) Reporting on events taking place in the world that are hidden from the person — this type still exists, though such information is sometimes right and sometimes wrong.
    • (3) A faculty (قُوَّة) that Allah grants to certain people, resembling astronomical inference — most of it is falsehood (كَذِب). Part of this category is عَرَّاف.
  • عَرَّاف: one who draws inferences from external signs and circumstances and claims these point to meaningful conclusions. This too falls under كَهَانَة — Shariah has prohibited listening to, believing in, and acting upon what such persons say.
  • Regarding خُطُوط (drawing lines in the ground): this was a miraculous gift (مُعْجِزَة) bestowed on certain prophets. The statement «كَانَ نَبِيٌّ مِنَ الْأَنْبِيَاءِ يَخُطُّ، فَمَنْ وَافَقَ خَطَّهُ فَذَاكَ» is a تَعْلِيقٌ بِالْمُحَال (conditioning permission on the impossible) — since no one today can know how those prophets drew their lines or verify correspondence with them, the practice is not permissible at all.
  • What are these خُطُوط in practice? They refer to the forms of علم الرَّمْل (geomancy): practitioners would draw lines in sand and, by their arrangement, claim to derive information. Ibn Hajar: «لَا يُصَرَّحُ بِالنَّهْيِ عَنِ الِاشْتِغَالِ بِالْخَطِّ لِنِسْبَتِهِ لِبَعْضِ الْأَنْبِيَاءِ» — the prohibition is inferred: since permission is conditioned on matching the prophet's lines (الأشكال التي لأهل علم الرمل), and this is impossible to verify, علم الرمل is prohibited. [Fath al-Mulhim, Vol. 4, p. 64]
  • Haji Khalifa (كَشْفُ الظُّنُونِ) on عَرَّاف: هُوَ عِلْمٌ يُعْرَفُ بِالاسْتِدْلَالِ عَلَى أَحْوَالِ الْمَسْأَلَةِ وَأَكْثَرُ هَذَا الْفَنِّ أُمُورٌ مَبْنِيَّةٌ عَلَى التَّجَارُبِ — "It is a science by which one draws inferences concerning the circumstances of the matter at hand; and most of this discipline consists of matters built upon experiential observation."
  • Mirqat — distinction between كَاهِن and عَرَّاف: A كَاهِن claims knowledge of future events and hidden unseen matters. An عَرَّاف claims to locate lost objects or predict specific situational outcomes — he is a predictor of particulars rather than a claimant of future/unseen knowledge broadly.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • كُهَّان— pl. of كَاهِن; soothsayers; those who claim knowledge of the unseen, typically through alleged جِنّ assistance or eavesdropping on the heavens.
  • نَتَطَيَّرُ— we used to take omens (طِيَرَة); originally from watching the flight direction of birds (طَيْر) to predict outcomes; refers to any act of drawing bad omens from chance occurrences.
  • يَخُطُّونَ— they draw lines; from خَطَّ (to trace/draw a line); here: the practice of علم الرَّمْل (geomancy) — drawing lines in sand to derive information from their arrangement.
  • فَمَنْ وَافَقَ خَطَّهُ فَذَاكَ— whoever matches his (that prophet's) lines, then so be it. Khattabi: said by way of زَجْر (deterrence), since no one can match a prophet's miraculous lines. Ibn Hajar: a تَعْلِيقٌ بِالْمُحَال — conditional permission tied to an impossible condition, effectively a prohibition.
Cross-ref: Muslim 537 (full version also includes the prayer incident, Najashi story, and slave-girl/أَيْنَ اللَّهُ episode); Fath al-Mulhim Vol. 4, pp. 41–69; see class 4574 (طِيَرَة).
Kitab كِتَابُ الطِّبِّ وَالرُّقَى بَابُ الْكَهَانَةِ — الفصل الثاني
حديث ٤٥٩٨
عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «مَنْ أَتَى كَاهِنًا فَصَدَّقَهُ بِمَا يَقُولُ، أَوْ أَتَى امْرَأَتَهُ حَائِضًا، أَوْ أَتَى امْرَأَتَهُ مِنْ دُبُرِهَا، فَقَدْ بَرِئَ مِمَّا أُنْزِلَ عَلَى مُحَمَّدٍ»
Narrated by Abu Hurayrah (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Ahmad, Abu Dawud  ·  Grade: Sahih
Translation
"Whoever visits a soothsayer and believes what he says, or approaches his wife while she is menstruating, or approaches his wife from her back passage — he has dissociated himself from what was revealed to Muhammad (S.A.W.)."
Class Notes
  • فَقَدْ بَرِئَ مِمَّا أُنْزِلَ عَلَى مُحَمَّدٍ — "has dissociated himself from what was revealed to Muhammad." Scholars hold this is either:
    • تَهْدِيد (tahdiid) — a severe hyperbolic warning, not a declaration of literal disbelief; used to stress the extreme gravity of these acts.
    • OR it applies specifically in the case of اسْتِحْلَال (istihlaal) — when the person considers such acts to be permissible, which would constitute disbelief.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • فَصَدَّقَهُ— and he believed/affirmed him; accepted what the soothsayer said as true; from صَدَّقَ (to deem truthful, to believe).
  • بَرِئَ مِمَّا أُنْزِلَ عَلَى مُحَمَّدٍ— has dissociated himself from what was revealed to Muhammad; a severe expression of condemnation; either تَهْدِيد (hyperbolic warning) or describes the state of one who commits these acts while considering them permissible (اسْتِحْلَال).
Cross-ref: Cf. class 4591 (prohibition of visiting soothsayers); Ahmad and Abu Dawud; Tirmidhi on visiting kahin.
Kitab كِتَابُ الرُّؤْيَا الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٦٠٥
عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «لَمْ يَبْقَ مِنَ النُّبُوَّةِ إِلَّا الْمُبَشِّرَاتُ»، قَالُوا: وَمَا الْمُبَشِّرَاتُ؟ قَالَ: «الرُّؤْيَا الصَّالِحَةُ»، وَزَادَ مَالِكٌ بِرِوَايَةِ عَطَاءِ بْنِ يَسَارٍ: «يَرَاهَا الرَّجُلُ الْمُسْلِمُ أَوْ تُرَى لَهُ»
Narrated by Abu Hurayrah (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Bukhari; Malik adds via 'Ata' ibn Yasar  ·  Grade: Sahih
Translation
"Nothing remains of prophethood except the مُبَشِّرَات (good tidings)." They asked: "What are the مُبَشِّرَات?" He said: "The righteous dream (الرُّؤْيَا الصَّالِحَةُ)." Malik adds via the narration of 'Ata' ibn Yasar: "which a Muslim man sees, or which is shown to him."
Class Notes
  • Toorbishti: The أَلِف of تَأْنِيث (ـا) was placed in رُؤْيَا in place of the taa' الْتَأْنِيث (ـة) of رُؤْيَة — in order to distinguish between what a person sees while asleep (رُؤْيَا) and what he sees while awake (رُؤْيَة).
  • Qurtubi: Sometimes رُؤْيَا is used in the meaning of رُؤْيَة (waking vision), as in the Quranic ayah: ﴿وَمَا جَعَلْنَا الرُّؤْيَا الَّتِي أَرَيْنَاكَ إِلَّا فِتْنَةً لِلنَّاسِ﴾ (17:60).
  • What is the true nature (حَقِيقَة) of رُؤْيَا? — Maaziri:
    • Many statements have been made on this question. Non-Muslims have put forward many unreliable (مُنْكَر) positions, because they attempted to understand something that cannot be grasped through reason alone — so their views became confused.
    • The sound position, held by the Ahl al-Sunnah wa'l-Jama'ah, is: Allah creates in the heart of a sleeping person certain convictions (اعْتِقَادَات), just as He creates such convictions in the waking mind. These convictions sometimes come from Allah (and are truthful) and sometimes come from Shaytan (and are false or distressing).
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • الْمُبَشِّرَاتُ— the glad tidings; things that bring good news; from بَشَّرَ (to give glad tidings); here: pious dreams that bring comfort or good news to a believer, as a remnant of the blessings of prophethood.
  • الرُّؤْيَا الصَّالِحَةُ— the righteous/good dream; رُؤْيَا (with أَلِف of تَأْنِيث ـا) specifically denotes sleep-visions, distinguished from رُؤْيَة (with taa' marbutah ـة) which is waking vision — per Toorbishti. الصَّالِحَة: good, wholesome — the dream of a righteous Muslim.
  • يَرَاهَا أَوْ تُرَى لَهُ— he sees it himself, or it is shown to him (i.e., another person sees the good dream on his behalf and reports it to him).
Cross-ref: Bukhari (Kitab al-Ta'bir); Malik's Muwatta (via 'Ata' ibn Yasar); Qurtubi's تَفْسِير on ﴿وَمَا جَعَلْنَا الرُّؤْيَا﴾ (17:60).
Kitab كِتَابُ الرُّؤْيَا الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٦٠٧
الرُّؤْيَا الصَّالِحَةُ جُزْءٌ مِنْ سِتَّةٍ وَأَرْبَعِينَ جُزْءًا مِنَ النُّبُوَّةِ
Narrated by Anas ibn Malik (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Bukhari, Muslim (Muttafaq Alayh)
Translation
"A righteous dream is one forty-sixth part of prophethood."
Class Notes
  • نُبُوَّة consists of many things, among which is إِخْبَارٌ بِمَا سَيَكُونُ (informing of what will happen) or informing of matters of the past that only Allah or one whom He informs can know. A true dream which a believer sees can sometimes contain this aspect of نُبُوَّة.
  • However, this does not make the person a prophet, nor can his dream itself be called نُبُوَّة — because نُبُوَّة has ended in its entirety with the death of Rasulullah (S.A.W.). Having a جُزْء (part) of something does not necessitate having the whole.
  • Knowledge of غَيْب is of three types:
    • (1) اسْتِيعَاب — knowledge of all past, present, and future — this belongs to Allah alone.
    • (2) Receiving خَبَر from Allah through وَحْي — this was for the prophets.
    • (3) Knowing غَيْب through a true dream — this is what remains for the believers.
  • Mufti Taqi: there is no way any longer to know قَطْعًا (with certainty) whether a dream is صَالِحَة or not.
  • Why specifically 46? The most well-known narration gives the number 46. Many scholars do تَوَقُّف (withhold judgment) on the reason behind it. Others say: the first 6 months of the prophethood of Rasulullah (S.A.W.) consisted mainly of dreams (وَحْيُ الرُّؤْيَا). If the total 23 years of نُبُوَّة is divided by those 6 months, the result is 46 parts — this is the mashhur opinion on the reason.
  • Objections raised against this opinion (e.g., how was this division established? What about the dreams Rasulullah (S.A.W.) saw later?). Answer: in the first 6 months dreams were the primary (غَالِب) form of وَحْي; after that the primary form changed, though he still continued to see dreams.
  • Ibn Hajar counted all the different numbers mentioned across the various narrations — arriving at 15 different numbers. Some of these are not ثَابِت, and some of the 15 وُجُوه are not talking about dreams at all but about something else. The most famous are 46 and 70.
  • Tabari: the difference in numbers depends on the person seeing the dream — the true dream of a righteous person (صَالِح) is 1 out of 46, while the true dream of a فَاسِق could be 1 out of 70. Those scholars who do تَوَقُّف on the reason for the number 46 also do تَوَقُّف on the وَجْهُ الْجَمْع between the different numbers.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • الرُّؤْيَا الصَّالِحَةُ— the righteous/good dream; seen during sleep; from Allah, not Shaytan — as opposed to حُلْم which is from Shaytan.
  • جُزْءٌ مِنْ سِتَّةٍ وَأَرْبَعِينَ جُزْءًا— one part out of forty-six parts; meaning the good dream shares one attribute of نُبُوَّة (prophetic knowledge of the unseen/future) but does not constitute نُبُوَّة in itself.
  • مِنَ النُّبُوَّةِ— of prophethood; i.e., it shares one fraction of the aspects of نُبُوَّة. نُبُوَّة itself has ended with Rasulullah (S.A.W.) — possessing a part does not entail possessing the whole.
Cross-ref: Muttafaq Alayh; see class 4605 (الرُّؤْيَا الصَّالِحَة = what remains of نُبُوَّة); class 4611 (الرُّؤْيَا الصَّالِحَة مِنَ اللَّهِ).
Kitab كِتَابُ الرُّؤْيَا الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٦٠٨
«مَنْ رَآنِي فِي الْمَنَامِ فَقَدْ رَآنِي فَإِنَّ الشَّيْطَانَ لَا يَتَمَثَّلُ فِي صُورَتِي»
Narrated by Abu Hurayrah (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Bukhari, Muslim (Muttafaq Alayh)
Translation
"Whoever sees me in a dream has truly seen me, for Shaytan cannot appear in my form."
Class Notes
  • What does it mean to "see the Prophet (S.A.W.)"? Two positions among scholars:
    • (1) Ibn Seereen, Bukhari, and Qadi Iyad: He sees Rasulullah (S.A.W.) in his actual form and known description as established in the ahadith — only then is it a true dream of him.
    • (2) It is not a condition (شَرْط) that he sees him in his known description; even if he sees him without his established appearance, it is still a valid ru'ya of him — as long as the person feels (with certainty) that it is him.
  • Did the person actually see the very person (ذَات) of Rasulullah (S.A.W.)? Two opinions:
    • (1) He sees the مِثَال (representation/likeness) of him — not his actual ذَات.
    • (2) He sees his actual ذَات in reality.
  • Can a person use a statement made by Rasulullah (S.A.W.) in a dream as a حُجَّة شَرْعِيَّة? No. However, if whatever he commands does not clash with the established أَحْكَام الشَّرِيعَة, he should do it out of أَدَب.
    • This hadith establishes that the رُؤْيَا is صَحِيح — it does not establish that every word heard in the dream is صَحِيح.
    • There is a high likelihood of mishearing, misremembering, forgetting, and then substituting something else in its place.
    • Even though Shaytan cannot take the shape of Rasulullah (S.A.W.), he can still put things into a person's imagination (خَيَال) — so the content heard in the dream can be affected.
    • Therefore a dream of Rasulullah (S.A.W.) cannot be used to override other حُجَجُ الشَّرِيعَة.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • فِي الْمَنَامِ— in sleep/during a dream; الْمَنَام = sleep, place/time of sleeping.
  • لَا يَتَمَثَّلُ— cannot appear/manifest; from تَمَثَّلَ (to take the form of, to appear in the likeness of); Shaytan is incapable of assuming the صُورَة (form) of Rasulullah (S.A.W.).
  • فِي صُورَتِي— in my form; meaning the specific physical appearance and description of Rasulullah (S.A.W.) known from the ahadith. Scholars differ on whether the dream is valid even when he does not appear in this known description.
Cross-ref: Muttafaq Alayh; see class 4610 (فَسَيَرَانِي فِي الْيَقَظَةِ — second related narration); Ibn Seereen's position referenced in Mirqat.
Kitab كِتَابُ الرُّؤْيَا الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٦١٠
«مَنْ رَآنِي فِي الْمَنَامِ فَسَيَرَانِي فِي الْيَقَظَةِ وَلَا يَتَمَثَّلُ الشَّيْطَانُ بِي»
Narrated by Abu Hurayrah (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Bukhari, Muslim (Muttafaq Alayh)
Translation
"Whoever sees me in a dream will see me in wakefulness — and Shaytan cannot appear as me."
Class Notes
  • The 2nd opinion mentioned in the حَاشِيَة (that فَسَيَرَانِي فِي الْيَقَظَةِ means he will see him in the آخِرَة) is weak (ضَعِيف) — because seeing Rasulullah (S.A.W.) in the آخِرَة is not exclusive to those who saw him in a dream; all believers will see him.
  • 3rd opinion: he will see the تَفْسِير and interpretation/fulfilment of what he saw in his dream — i.e., it will be realized in his waking life.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • فَسَيَرَانِي فِي الْيَقَظَةِ— he will see me in wakefulness (يَقَظَة); three interpretations: (1) he will actually see the Prophet in his lifetime (for companions); (2) he will see him in the آخِرَة (considered weak — not exclusive to dreamers); (3) he will see the تَفْسِير and fulfillment of the dream realized in real life.
  • لَا يَتَمَثَّلُ الشَّيْطَانُ بِي— Shaytan cannot take on my form/appearance; same principle as class 4608 but phrased differently (بِي instead of فِي صُورَتِي).
Cross-ref: Muttafaq Alayh; cf. class 4608 (فَقَدْ رَآنِي — first narration on same topic); the حَاشِيَة opinions discussed here build on class 4608's notes.
Kitab كِتَابُ الرُّؤْيَا الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٦١١
الرُّؤْيَا الصَّالِحَةُ مِنَ اللَّهِ وَالْحُلْمُ مِنَ الشَّيْطَانِ، فَإِذَا رَأَى أَحَدُكُمْ مَا يُحِبُّ فَلَا يُحَدِّثْ بِهِ إِلَّا مَنْ يُحِبُّ، وَإِذَا رَأَى مَا يَكْرَهُ فَلْيَتَعَوَّذْ بِاللَّهِ مِنْ شَرِّهَا وَمِنْ شَرِّ الشَّيْطَانِ، وَلْيَتْفُلْ ثَلَاثًا، وَلَا يُحَدِّثْ بِهَا أَحَدًا فَإِنَّهَا لَنْ تَضُرَّهُ
Narrated by Abu Qatadah (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Bukhari, Muslim (Muttafaq Alayh)
Translation
"A righteous dream is from Allah and a bad dream (حُلْم) is from Shaytan. When one of you sees something he loves, let him not recount it except to one he loves. And when he sees something he dislikes, let him seek refuge in Allah from its evil and from the evil of Shaytan, let him spit (وَلْيَتْفُلْ) three times, and let him not tell anyone about it — for it will not harm him."
Class Notes
  • Nawawi — six adab for whoever sees a bad dream (all established in the ahadith):
    1. تَعَوُّذ from the evil of the dream itself
    2. تَعَوُّذ from the evil of Shaytan
    3. Dry spit (تَفْل) to the left
    4. Do not inform anyone
    5. Turn onto the other side of the body
    6. Get up and pray
  • Qurtubi — حُلْم (bad dream) was attributed to Shaytan because it is placed by Shaytan in order to put fear into the one who sees it. Even though Allah is the one who creates it, Shaytan is its سَبَب (cause) — so it is attributed to him. This is the same as how وَسْوَاس is attributed to Shaytan even though the actual وَسَاوِس are created by Allah; he is merely the سَبَب.
  • Mufti Taqi — prefers Qurtubi's explanation over the opinion that حُلْم is attributed to Shaytan merely out of أَدَب with Allah (i.e., to avoid attributing something displeasing to Allah) — though that consideration is a factor as well.
  • Nawawi — the wisdom (حِكْمَة) behind not narrating a bad dream to anyone: the person might interpret/explain it in a way that is مَكْرُوه based on its apparent form (صُورَة ظَاهِرَة), even though the dream is open to other interpretations (مُحْتَمَل) — and then it actually turns out the way it was explained. This is based on the opinion that dreams are realized according to the first interpretation given.
  • Bukhari's position: dreams are realized in accordance with the first explanation — but only if the مُعَبِّر (interpreter) is correct. If he is mistaken, the dream will not happen as he described.
  • Based on Bukhari's opinion: the wisdom behind not narrating the bad dream is that an evil interpretation from the interpreter will increase the grief, anxiety, and fear of the one who saw it.
  • Wisdom behind only telling good dreams to those you love: clear on the first opinion (to avoid bad interpretation). On Bukhari's opinion: telling a good dream to indifferent people increases أَوْهَام (assumptions) in the heart and removes the happiness derived from the dream.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • الْحُلْمُ— the bad dream; from حَلَمَ; as opposed to رُؤْيَا (good dream). Attributed to Shaytan because he is its سَبَب — placing fear into the heart of the sleeping person — even though the actual creation is by Allah.
  • وَلْيَتْفُلْ ثَلَاثًا— and let him spit three times; تَفْل = a dry or light spit, not a full expectorant; done to the left as a gesture of تَحْقِير (contempt) toward Shaytan and إِعْرَاض (turning away) from the bad dream.
  • فَإِنَّهَا لَنْ تَضُرَّهُ— for it will not harm him; the promise that following these adab removes the harm of a bad dream entirely.
Cross-ref: Muttafaq Alayh; class 4612 (Jabir's narration with فَلْيَبْصُقْ vs. فَلْيَنْفُثْ); Nawawi's six adab noted from Mirqat.
Kitab كِتَابُ الرُّؤْيَا الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٦١٢
«إِذَا رَأَى أَحَدُكُمُ الرُّؤْيَا يَكْرَهُهَا فَلْيَبْصُقْ عَنْ يَسَارِهِ ثَلَاثًا، وَلْيَسْتَعِذْ بِاللَّهِ مِنَ الشَّيْطَانِ ثَلَاثًا، وَلْيَتَحَوَّلْ عَنْ جَنْبِهِ الَّذِي كَانَ عَلَيْهِ»
Narrated by Jabir (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Muslim  ·  Grade: Sahih
Translation
"When one of you sees a dream he dislikes, let him spit three times to his left, seek refuge in Allah from Shaytan three times, and turn from the side he was lying on."
Class Notes
  • Another narration has فَلْيَنْفُثْ in place of فَلْيَبْصُقْ. نَفْث = نَفْخ (blowing) accompanied by both ريق (saliva) and رِيح (breath) — i.e., a light exhale with moisture, less than a full spit.
  • Ulama prefer the narration with يَبْصُق (to spit) because it conveys more تَحْقِير (contempt/belittling) of Shaytan and more إِعْرَاض (turning away) from the bad dream.
  • Ibn Hajar: the instruction to turn to the other side of the body is for تَفَاؤُل (taking a good omen), so that the bad dreams stop coming.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • فَلْيَبْصُقْ— let him spit; a full spit to the left, preferred over فَلْيَنْفُثْ (blowing with saliva) for its greater expression of تَحْقِير (contempt) toward Shaytan.
  • نَفْث— a light exhale with moisture; نَفْخ (blowing) combined with ريق (saliva) and رِيح (breath); lighter than a full spit (بَصْق).
  • وَلْيَتَحَوَّلْ عَنْ جَنْبِهِ— and let him turn from his side; from تَحَوَّلَ (to shift, to change position). Ibn Hajar: the wisdom is تَفَاؤُل — taking a good omen by the change of position, which helps the bad dream stop recurring.
Cross-ref: Muslim; cf. class 4611 (Abu Qatadah — وَلْيَتْفُلْ; Nawawi's six adab); فَلْيَنْفُثْ vs. فَلْيَبْصُقْ variant discussed here.
Kitab كِتَابُ الرُّؤْيَا الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٦١٣
«إِذَا اقْتَرَبَ الزَّمَانُ لَمْ يَكَدْ يَكْذِبُ رُؤْيَا الْمُؤْمِنِ، وَرُؤْيَا الْمُؤْمِنِ جُزْءٌ مِنْ سِتَّةٍ وَأَرْبَعِينَ جُزْءًا مِنَ النُّبُوَّةِ، وَمَا كَانَ مِنَ النُّبُوَّةِ فَإِنَّهُ لَا يَكْذِبُ»
Narrated by Abu Hurayrah (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Bukhari, Muslim (Muttafaq Alayh)
Translation
"When time draws near, a believer's dream will hardly be false. And a believer's dream is one forty-sixth part of prophethood. And what pertains to prophethood cannot be false."
Class Notes
  • اقْتَرَبَ الزَّمَانُ — three interpretations:
    • (1) The end of times, when هَرَج (widespread chaos and killing) will become rampant. People at that time will need reminders. In the past, when people needed reminders, Allah would send a prophet — but since نُبُوَّة has ended, Allah will give true dreams to the believers in place of prophets.
    • (2) Refers to the people who will live with 'Isa (A.S.) when complete peace prevails on earth (Qurtubi).
    • (3) The hours of the day will pass by quickly (i.e., time will feel compressed and short).
  • Qurtubi — regarding this era of peace with 'Isa (A.S.): the people of that time would love to see شَاكِل (chains/shackles) on their ankles in dreams, because shackles on the ankles restrict the feet — indicating that they will never move toward anything contrary to the شَرِيعَة. This is therefore a praiseworthy dream for them.
  • Qadi Iyad — the reason people would dislike seeing chains/shackles on the NECK in dreams: the كُفَّار are described in the Quran as having shackles on their necks (الْأَغْلَال فِي الْأَعْنَاقِ). Therefore such a dream denotes كُفْر, بِدْعَة, or شَهَادَةُ الزُّورِ (false testimony). Some scholars also say it denotes a bad wife.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • إِذَا اقْتَرَبَ الزَّمَانُ— when time draws near; three interpretations: (1) approach of the end of times with widespread هَرَج; (2) the era of 'Isa (A.S.); (3) shortening of time/days passing quickly.
  • لَمْ يَكَدْ يَكْذِبُ— can hardly be false; كَادَ (negative: لَمْ يَكَدْ) = barely, almost not; meaning the dreams of believers in that era will almost never be wrong — their truthfulness increases as نُبُوَّة comes closer to its full realization.
  • وَمَا كَانَ مِنَ النُّبُوَّةِ فَإِنَّهُ لَا يَكْذِبُ— and what pertains to prophethood does not lie; the basis for the truthfulness of the righteous dream: since it shares the nature of نُبُوَّة, and نُبُوَّة is incapable of falsehood, such dreams are intrinsically true.
  • الشَّاكِل / الْأَغْلَال— شَاكِل = chains/shackles on the ankles (feet); Qurtubi: praiseworthy in dreams — restraint from sin. الْأَغْلَال = heavy shackles on the neck; Qadi Iyad: disliked in dreams — associated with كُفْر, بِدْعَة, or شَهَادَةُ الزُّوْر.
Cross-ref: Muttafaq Alayh; cf. class 4607 (جُزْءٌ مِنْ ٤٦ — same ratio, different context); Quranic reference for أَغْلَال فِي الْأَعْنَاقِ: e.g., Yasin 36:8.
Kitab كِتَابُ الرُّؤْيَا الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٦١٤
وَعَنْ أُمِّ الْعَلَاءِ قَالَتْ: رُئِيَ لِي عُثْمَانُ بْنُ مَظْعُونٍ فِي الْمَنَامِ وَعَيْنٌ تَجْرِي، فَأَخْبَرْتُ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ ﷺ، فَقَالَ: «ذَاكَ عَمَلُهُ»
Narrated by Umm al-ʿAlāʾ (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Bukhārī  ·  Grade: Ṣaḥīḥ
Translation
In a dream, ʿUthmān ibn Maz'ūn appeared to me with a flowing spring beside him. I informed the Messenger of Allāh ﷺ about this, and he said: "That is his deeds [flowing on]."
Class Notes
  • ʿUthmān ibn Maz'ūn (R.A.) was among the first of the Muhājirīn to pass away in Madinah.
  • Mirqāt: because he died as a مُرَابِط (one stationed in جِهَاد/defence of the faith), his deeds continue to flow and he continues receiving reward even after death — hence the flowing spring represents his ongoing ثَوَاب.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • رُئِيَ لِي— it appeared to me (in a dream); literally "was shown to me" — passive construction indicating it was a true vision given to her.
  • عَيْنٌ تَجْرِي— a flowing spring; metaphor for deeds that continue to flow and generate reward without ceasing.
  • ذَاكَ عَمَلُهُ— that is his deeds [flowing on]; the spring = his ongoing صَدَقَة جَارِيَة and the ثَوَاب of رِبَاط continuing after death.
Cross-ref: Bukhārī (kitāb al-manāqib); cf. class 4613 on dreams of the believers; concept of الصَّدَقَةُ الْجَارِيَةُ continuing after death.
Kitab كِتَابُ الرُّؤْيَا الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٦١٦
وَعَنْ أَنَسٍ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ ﷺ قَالَ: «رَأَيْتُ ذَاتَ لَيْلَةٍ فِيمَا يَرَى النَّائِمُ كَأَنَّنَا فِي دَارِ عُقْبَةَ بْنِ رَافِعٍ، فَأُتِينَا بِرُطَبٍ مِنْ رُطَبِ ابْنِ طَابٍ، فَأَوَّلْتُهَا الرِّفْعَةَ لَنَا فِي الدُّنْيَا وَالْعَاقِبَةَ لَنَا فِي الْآخِرَةِ وَأَنَّ دِينَنَا قَدْ طَابَ»
Narrated by Anas ibn Mālik (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Muslim  ·  Grade: Ṣaḥīḥ
Translation
The Prophet ﷺ said: "One night I saw in a dream — as a sleeping person sees — that we were in the house of ʿUqbah ibn Rāfi', and we were brought fresh dates (رُطَب) of the type known as Ibn Ṭāb. I interpreted this as: elevation for us in this world, a good outcome for us in the Hereafter, and that our religion has become pure and wholesome."
Class Notes
  • رُطَب ابن طاب: dates attributed to a man from Madinah called Ibn Ṭāb; the name became a category name for other fine dates and fruits as well.
  • The Prophet ﷺ interpreted رُطَب as the دِين because both are حُلْو (sweet) and سَهْل (easy/accessible).
  • Mufti Taqi: The fact that Rasulullāh ﷺ was initially uncertain whether the dream indicated Yamāma or Ḥajar shows that تَعْبِير (dream interpretation) is an اِجْتِهَادِيّ matter — based on personal reasoning — unless it is grounded in وَحْي.
  • Q: If the dreams of prophets are وَحْي, how could Rasulullāh ﷺ be uncertain about his interpretation? A: The dream itself — showing a location with date palms — was قَطْعِي (certain; from وَحْي, and it came to pass). However, which specific place (Yamāma or Ḥajar) was not specified in the dream; Rasulullāh's identification of the location was his own اجْتِهَاد and ظَنّ, not part of the وَحْي.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • فِيمَا يَرَى النَّائِمُ— in what a sleeping person sees; a clarifying phrase confirming this was a dream-vision, not a waking experience.
  • رُطَب— fresh ripe dates; at the soft, sweet stage before drying.
  • ابْنُ طَابٍ— a man from Madinah after whom this variety of dates was named; the name also became applied more broadly to fine fruit.
  • فَأَوَّلْتُهَا— I interpreted it; from أَوَّلَ (to interpret, especially a dream or ambiguous text).
  • الرِّفْعَةَ— elevation; high rank and honour.
  • الْعَاقِبَةَ لَنَا— the good ultimate outcome belongs to us; the final result of the Hereafter will be in our favour.
  • قَدْ طَابَ— has become pure and good; from طَابَ = to be pure, pleasant, wholesome.
Cross-ref: Muslim (كِتَاب الرُّؤْيَا); cf. class 4618 (another dream of the Prophet ﷺ with interpretation); Mufti Taqi's principle: تَعْبِير is اجتهاد unless based on وحي.
Kitab كِتَابُ الرُّؤْيَا الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٦١٨
وَعَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ: «بَيْنَا أَنَا نَائِمٌ رَأَيْتُ فِي يَدَيَّ سِوَارَيْنِ مِنْ ذَهَبٍ فَأَهَمَّنِي شَأْنُهُمَا، فَأُوحِيَ إِلَيَّ فِي الْمَنَامِ أَنِ انْفُخْ فِيهِمَا، فَنَفَخْتُ فَطَارَا، فَأَوَّلْتُهُمَا كَذَّابَيْنِ يَخْرُجَانِ بَعْدِي: أَحَدُهُمَا الْعَنْسِيُّ صَاحِبُ صَنْعَاءَ، وَالْآخَرُ مُسَيْلِمَةُ صَاحِبُ الْيَمَامَةِ»
Narrated by Abū Hurayrah (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Bukhārī, Muslim (Muttafaq ʿAlayh)  ·  Grade: Ṣaḥīḥ
Translation
The Messenger of Allāh ﷺ said: "While I was sleeping, I saw in my hands two gold bracelets, and they greatly distressed me. I was then inspired (أُوحِيَ) in the dream to blow into them, so I blew and they flew away. I interpreted them as two great liars who would emerge after me: one of them al-ʿAnsī, the master of Ṣanʿāʾ, and the other Musaylima, the master of Yamāma."
Class Notes
  • كِبْرَانِي (i.e. أَهَمَّنِي): the bracelets distressed him because ذَهَب is حِلْيَةُ النِّسَاءِ — gold is adornment for women; men are not permitted to wear it. So the dream itself was troubling.
  • Ibn Ḥajar: the two bracelets being blown away (فَطَارَا) is an إِشَارَة to the حَقَارَة (contemptibility and insignificance) of their affair — things that are blown away are weak and without substance.
  • Musaylima = Musaylama ibn Thumāma al-Ḥanafī, who claimed prophethood. He was killed during the caliphate of Abū Bakr (R.A.) by Waḥshī ibn Ḥarb — the same man who had previously killed Ḥamza (R.A.).
  • Muhallab: كِذْب = وَضْعُ الشَّيْءِ فِي غَيْرِ مَحَلِّهِ — placing something where it does not belong. The two bracelets on his hands = not their proper place (men cannot wear gold) = two who would falsely claim نُبُوَّة, which was never meant for them. Additionally: ذَهَب → ذَهَاب (going away) — they will come and then go (i.e., be defeated).
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • سِوَارَيْنِ— two bracelets (dual of سِوَار); a piece of jewellery worn on the wrist, associated with women.
  • أَهَمَّنِي— distressed me greatly / caused me anxiety; من الهَمّ (anxiety, worry).
  • أُوحِيَ إِلَيَّ— I was inspired; وَحْي came to me — even within the dream, indicating it was a true prophetic vision.
  • انْفُخْ فِيهِمَا— blow into them! (command form of نَفَخَ = to blow).
  • فَطَارَا— so they flew away (dual verb from طَارَ = to fly); symbol of the evanescence and humiliation of the two false claimants.
  • كَذَّابَيْنِ— two arch-liars (dual of كَذَّاب, intensive form); emphasising the magnitude of their falsehood.
  • الْعَنْسِيُّ— al-Aswad al-ʿAnsī, the false prophet of Yemen (Ṣanʿāʾ); killed near the end of the Prophet's ﷺ life.
Cross-ref: Muttafaq ʿAlayh; cf. class 4616 (dream interpretation as اجتهاد); class 4621 (dream realized by first interpretation); accounts of ridda wars in Sīrah/history.
Kitab كِتَابُ الرُّؤْيَا الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٦٢٠
وَعَنْ سَمُرَةَ بْنِ جُنْدُبٍ قَالَ: كَانَ النَّبِيُّ ﷺ إِذَا صَلَّى أَقْبَلَ عَلَيْنَا بِوَجْهِهِ فَقَالَ: «مَنْ رَأَى مِنْكُمُ اللَّيْلَةَ رُؤْيَا؟» فَإِنْ رَأَى أَحَدٌ قَصَّهَا فَيَقُولُ: مَا شَاءَ اللَّهُ. فَسَأَلَنَا يَوْمًا فَقَالَ: «هَلْ رَأَى مِنْكُمْ أَحَدٌ رُؤْيَا؟» قُلْنَا: لَا. قَالَ: «لَكِنِّي رَأَيْتُ اللَّيْلَةَ رَجُلَيْنِ أَتَيَانِي فَأَخَذَا بِيَدَيَّ فَأَخْرَجَانِي إِلَى أَرْضٍ مُقَدَّسَةٍ، فَإِذَا رَجُلٌ جَالِسٌ وَرَجُلٌ قَائِمٌ بِيَدِهِ كَلُّوبٌ مِنْ حَدِيدٍ يُدْخِلُهُ فِي شِدْقِهِ فَيَشُقُّهُ حَتَّى يَبْلُغَ قَفَاهُ ثُمَّ يَفْعَلُ بِشِدْقِهِ الْآخَرِ مِثْلَ ذَلِكَ وَيَلْتَئِمُ شِدْقُهُ هَذَا فَيَعُودُ فَيَصْنَعُ مِثْلَهُ. ثُمَّ أَتَيْنَا عَلَى رَجُلٍ مُضْطَجِعٍ عَلَى قَفَاهُ وَرَجُلٌ قَائِمٌ عَلَى رَأْسِهِ بِفِهْرٍ أَوْ صَخْرَةٍ يَشْدَخُ بِهَا رَأْسَهُ فَإِذَا ضَرَبَهُ تَدَهْدَهَ الْحَجَرُ فَانْطَلَقَ إِلَيْهِ لِيَأْخُذَهُ فَلَا يَرْجِعُ إِلَى هَذَا حَتَّى يَلْتَئِمَ رَأْسُهُ وَعَادَ رَأْسُهُ كَمَا كَانَ فَعَادَ إِلَيْهِ فَضَرَبَهُ. ثُمَّ أَتَيْنَا إِلَى ثَقْبٍ مِثْلِ التَّنُّورِ أَعْلَاهُ ضَيِّقٌ وَأَسْفَلَهُ وَاسِعٌ تَتَوَقَّدُ تَحْتَهُ نَارٌ فَإِذَا ارْتَفَعَتِ ارْتَفَعُوا حَتَّى كَادَ أَنْ يَخْرُجُوا مِنْهَا وَإِذَا خَمَدَتْ رَجَعُوا فِيهَا وَفِيهَا رِجَالٌ وَنِسَاءٌ عُرَاةٌ. ثُمَّ أَتَيْنَا عَلَى نَهَرٍ مِنْ دَمٍ فِيهِ رَجُلٌ قَائِمٌ عَلَى وَسْطِ النَّهَرِ وَعَلَى شَطِّ النَّهَرِ رَجُلٌ بَيْنَ يَدَيْهِ حِجَارَةٌ فَأَقْبَلَ الرَّجُلُ الَّذِي فِي النَّهَرِ فَإِذَا أَرَادَ أَنْ يَخْرُجَ رَمَى الرَّجُلُ بِحَجَرٍ فِي فِيهِ فَرَدَّهُ حَيْثُ كَانَ فَجَعَلَ كُلَّمَا جَاءَ لِيَخْرُجَ رَمَى فِي فِيهِ بِحَجَرٍ فَيَرْجِعُ كَمَا كَانَ. ثُمَّ انْتَهَيْنَا إِلَى رَوْضَةٍ خَضْرَاءَ فِيهَا شَجَرَةٌ عَظِيمَةٌ وَفِي أَصْلِهَا شَيْخٌ وَصِبْيَانٌ وَإِذَا رَجُلٌ قَرِيبٌ مِنَ الشَّجَرَةِ بَيْنَ يَدَيْهِ نَارٌ يُوقِدُهَا فَصَعِدَا بِيَ الشَّجَرَةَ فَأَدْخَلَانِي دَارًا أَوْسَطَ الشَّجَرَةِ لَمْ أَرَ قَطُّ أَحْسَنَ مِنْهَا فِيهَا رِجَالٌ شُيُوخٌ وَشَبَابٌ وَنِسَاءٌ وَصِبْيَانٌ ثُمَّ أَخْرَجَانِي فَصَعِدَا بِيَ الشَّجَرَةَ فَأَدْخَلَانِي دَارًا هِيَ أَحْسَنُ وَأَفْضَلُ مِنْهَا فِيهَا شُيُوخٌ وَشَبَابٌ. فَقُلْتُ لَهُمَا: إِنَّكُمَا قَدْ طَوَّفْتُمَانِي اللَّيْلَةَ فَأَخْبِرَانِي عَمَّا رَأَيْتُ. قَالَا: نَعَمْ، أَمَّا الرَّجُلُ الَّذِي رَأَيْتَهُ يُشَقُّ شِدْقُهُ فَكَذَّابٌ يُحَدِّثُ بِالْكَذْبَةِ فَتُحْمَلُ عَنْهُ حَتَّى تَبْلُغَ الْآفَاقَ فَيُصْنَعُ بِهِ مَا تَرَى إِلَى يَوْمِ الْقِيَامَةِ. وَالَّذِي رَأَيْتَهُ يُشْدَخُ رَأْسُهُ فَرَجُلٌ عَلَّمَهُ اللَّهُ الْقُرْآنَ فَنَامَ عَنْهُ بِاللَّيْلِ وَلَمْ يَعْمَلْ بِمَا فِيهِ بِالنَّهَارِ يُفْعَلُ بِهِ مَا رَأَيْتَ إِلَى يَوْمِ الْقِيَامَةِ. وَالَّذِي رَأَيْتَهُ فِي الثَّقْبِ فَهُمُ الزُّنَاةُ. وَالَّذِي رَأَيْتَهُ فِي النَّهَرِ آكِلُ الرِّبَا. وَالشَّيْخُ الَّذِي رَأَيْتَهُ فِي أَصْلِ الشَّجَرَةِ إِبْرَاهِيمُ وَالصِّبْيَانُ حَوْلَهُ فَأَوْلَادُ النَّاسِ. وَالَّذِي يُوقِدُ النَّارَ مَالِكٌ خَازِنُ النَّارِ. وَالدَّارُ الْأُولَى الَّتِي دَخَلْتَ دَارُ عَامَّةِ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ وَأَمَّا هَذِهِ الدَّارُ فَدَارُ الشُّهَدَاءِ. وَأَنَا جِبْرِيلُ وَهَذَا مِيكَائِيلُ. فَارْفَعْ رَأْسَكَ. فَرَفَعْتُ رَأْسِي فَإِذَا فَوْقِي مِثْلُ السَّحَابِ. وَفِي رِوَايَةٍ: مِثْلُ الرَّبَابَةِ الْبَيْضَاءِ. قَالَا: ذَلِكَ مَنْزِلُكَ. قُلْتُ: دَعَانِي أَدْخُلْ مَنْزِلِي. قَالَا: إِنَّهُ بَقِيَ لَكَ عُمُرٌ لَمْ تَسْتَكْمِلْهُ فَلَوِ اسْتَكْمَلْتَهُ أَتَيْتَ مَنْزِلَكَ»
Narrated by Samura ibn Jundub (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Bukhārī  ·  Grade: Ṣaḥīḥ
Translation
Whenever the Prophet ﷺ finished صَلَاة, he would turn to face us and ask: "Who among you saw a dream last night?" If someone had, they would relate it and he would say: «مَا شَاءَ اللَّهُ». One day he asked: "Has any of you seen a dream?" We said: No. He said: "But I saw last night: two men came to me, took me by my hands and brought me out to a sacred land. There I saw a man sitting while another stood over him with an iron hook (كَلُّوب), which he drove into his cheek and tore it open until it reached the back of his neck; then did the same to his other cheek, while the first would heal up and he would repeat the process. Then we came to a man lying on his back with another standing over his head with a boulder or smooth stone, smashing his head with it. Whenever he struck him, the stone rolled away; the striker chased after it, and by the time he returned the head had healed as before — then he struck it again. Then we came to a pit like an oven (تَنُّور), narrow at the top and wide at the bottom, with fire blazing beneath it. When the flames rose, those inside rose with them until they nearly escaped; when the flames subsided, they fell back in — inside were naked men and women. Then we came to a river of blood, in which a man stood in the middle, while on the bank stood a man with stones before him. Every time the man in the river tried to come out, the man on the bank threw a stone into his mouth and drove him back — and every time he tried to emerge, a stone was thrown into his mouth and he returned to where he had been. Then we arrived at a lush green garden containing a great tree, at whose base sat an old man with children around him, while nearby a man was kindling a fire. They climbed me up the tree and led me into a house in its midst — the finest house I had ever seen — filled with old men, young men, women, and children. Then they took me out and climbed further, leading me into a house even finer and more excellent, filled with old men and young men. I said to them: 'You have shown me much tonight; now tell me what I saw.' They said: 'Yes. The man whose cheek was being torn apart is a liar who spreads a lie that reaches to the horizons — this is done to him until the Day of Judgement. The man whose head was being smashed is one whom Allāh taught the Qurʾān, yet he slept through the night (neglecting its recitation) and did not act on its teachings by day — this is done to him until the Day of Judgement. Those in the pit are the fornicators. The man in the river is one who consumed usury (رِبَا). The old man at the base of the tree is Ibrāhīm (عليه السلام), and the children around him are the children of people (who died young). The man kindling the fire is Mālik, the keeper of Hell. The first house you entered is the abode of the generality of the believers, and the upper house is the abode of the martyrs. I am Jibrīl, and this is Mīkāʾīl. Now raise your head.' I raised my head and above me was something like clouds — in another narration: like a white cloud. They said: 'That is your dwelling.' I said: 'Let me enter my dwelling.' They said: 'There remains for you a lifespan you have not yet completed; had you completed it, you would have entered your dwelling.'"
Class Notes
  • Mirqāt: "when he finished صَلَاة" — this refers to صَلَاةُ الصُّبْح (the Fajr prayer); the Prophet ﷺ would turn to his companions after Fajr to ask about dreams.
  • All of the scenes shown in this dream will take place in the عَالَمُ الْبَرْزَخ (the intermediate realm between death and resurrection).
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • كَلُّوبٌ مِنْ حَدِيدٍ— an iron hook; an instrument used to tear or pierce flesh.
  • شِدْق— the cheek / corner of the mouth (dual: شِدْقَانِ); the site of punishment for the liar.
  • قَفَا— the back of the neck/head; the hook is driven through to the back, symbolising the extent of the lie's spread.
  • يَلْتَئِمُ— heals up / closes back together; the wound seals so the punishment can be repeated eternally.
  • فِهْر— a smooth rounded stone (used for grinding); here used to smash the head of one who neglected the Qurʾān.
  • يَشْدَخُ— to crush/smash (a head); شَدَخَ = to shatter something soft with force.
  • تَدَهْدَهَ— rolled away (the stone rolls down after the blow, giving the head time to heal).
  • ثَقْبٌ / التَّنُّور— a pit/hole shaped like a تَنُّور (clay oven): narrow at the top, wide at the bottom — a shape from which there is no easy escape.
  • تَتَوَقَّدُ— blazing / burning intensely; the fire beneath the pit drives the sinners up but the narrow top prevents escape.
  • الرَّبَابَةُ الْبَيْضَاءُ— a white cloud (specifically thin, bright white cloud); the Prophet's ﷺ dwelling in Paradise was shown as this.
  • طَوَّفْتُمَانِي— you have taken me on a tour / shown me around (from طَوَّفَ = to take someone around); the Prophet ﷺ acknowledges the comprehensive journey.
Cross-ref: Bukhārī (kitāb al-taʿbīr); cf. class 4614 (dream with flowing spring); عَالَمُ الْبَرْزَخ — cf. relevant آيَات on punishment of the grave; Ibrāhīm (A.S.) receiving souls of children: cf. barzakh literature.
Kitab كِتَابُ الرُّؤْيَا الفصل الثاني
حديث ٤٦٢١
وَعَنْ أَبِي رَزِينٍ الْعُقَيْلِيِّ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ: «الرُّؤْيَا عَلَى رِجْلِ طَائِرٍ مَا لَمْ تُعَبَّرْ، فَإِذَا عُبِّرَتْ وَقَعَتْ، وَلَا تَقُصُّهَا إِلَّا عَلَى وَادٍّ أَوْ ذِي رَأْيٍ»
Narrated by Abū Razīn al-ʿUqaylī (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Tirmidhī, Abū Dāwūd  ·  Grade: Ḥasan
Translation
The Messenger of Allāh ﷺ said: "A dream rests on the leg of a bird as long as it has not been interpreted; but once it is interpreted, it occurs. So do not relate your dream except to one who loves you or to one of sound judgment."
Class Notes
  • This hadith supports the position that a dream will be realized in accordance with its first interpretation — i.e., تَعْبِير brings about وُقُوع (occurrence). Other ahadith support the opposite view (that it occurs regardless of interpretation), but they are not cited here.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • عَلَى رِجْلِ طَائِرٍ— on the leg of a bird; an Arabic idiom meaning suspended / not yet settled — just as a bird can fly off from its perch, the dream can go either way until it is interpreted.
  • مَا لَمْ تُعَبَّرْ— as long as it has not been interpreted; تَعْبِير = interpreting a dream (crossing from symbol to meaning).
  • فَإِذَا عُبِّرَتْ وَقَعَتْ— once it is interpreted, it occurs; the dream lands (like the bird) and manifests in reality.
  • وَادٍّ— one who loves you (from وِدّ = affection); so the interpretation is given with care and goodwill, not carelessly or with envy.
  • ذِي رَأْيٍ— one of sound judgment and knowledge; a person qualified to interpret dreams correctly.
Cross-ref: Tirmidhī, Abū Dāwūd; cf. class 4612 (لَا يَقُصُّهَا إِلَّا عَلَى وَادٍّ — same instruction); class 4616 and 4618 (Prophetic dream interpretation as اجتهاد).
Kitab كِتَابُ الرُّؤْيَا الفصل الثاني
حديث ٤٦٢٢
وَعَنْ عَائِشَةَ أَنَّهَا سَأَلَتِ النَّبِيَّ ﷺ عَنْ وَرَقَةَ، فَقَالَ: «رَأَيْتُهُ فِي الْمَنَامِ وَعَلَيْهِ ثِيَابُ بَيَاضٍ، وَلَوْ كَانَ مِنْ أَهْلِ النَّارِ لَكَانَ عَلَيْهِ لِبَاسٌ غَيْرُ ذَلِكَ»
Narrated by ʿĀʾishah (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Aḥmad, Tirmidhī  ·  Grade: ضَعِيف (Albānī)
Translation
ʿĀʾishah asked the Prophet ﷺ about Waraqah, and he said: "I saw him in a dream wearing white garments. Had he been of the people of the Fire, he would have been wearing something other than that."
Class Notes
  • Mawlānā Zakariyyā: there is اِخْتِلَاف (scholarly disagreement) on whether Waraqah ibn Nawfal is considered Muslim.
    • The ظَاهِر (apparent meaning) of this hadith and the hadith of وَحْي (where he accepted the truth of the Prophet's message) together indicate that he was Muslim.
    • Qasṭallānī: he accepted the truth of prophethood even before the da'wa formally began — similar to Buḥayrā the monk. There is therefore نَظَر (scholarly scrutiny) in calling him a صَحَابِيّ.
    • Bulqīnī inclines toward him being Muslim.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • وَرَقَةَ— Waraqah ibn Nawfal ibn Asad; Khadījah's cousin, a حَنِيف scholar of the earlier scriptures who confirmed the Prophet's ﷺ prophethood at the onset of وَحْي.
  • ثِيَابُ بَيَاضٍ— white garments; in Islamic eschatology, white clothing is associated with the people of Paradise.
  • لِبَاسٌ غَيْرُ ذَلِكَ— a garment other than that; an allusion to the dark or fiery clothing associated with the people of the Fire.
Cross-ref: Aḥmad, Tirmidhī; Sīrah: hadith of وَحْي (first revelation and Waraqah's response in Bukhārī); cf. class 4614 (dream showing state of the deceased).
Kitab كِتَابُ الرُّؤْيَا الفصل الثالث
حديث ٤٦٢٣
وَعَنْ أَبِي خُزَيْمَةَ قَالَ: قُلْتُ: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ، رَأَيْتُ كَأَنِّي أَسْجُدُ عَلَى جَبْهَتِكَ، فَوَضَعَ النَّبِيُّ ﷺ جَبْهَتَهُ بِالْأَرْضِ ثُمَّ قَالَ: «صَدَقَتْ رُؤْيَاكَ»
Narrated by Abū Khuzayma (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Sharḥ al-Sunna  ·  Grade: See notes
Translation
"I said: O Messenger of Allāh, I saw in a dream that I was making سَجْدَة on your forehead. The Prophet ﷺ then placed his forehead on the ground and said: 'Your dream has proven true.'"
Class Notes
  • Muẓharī: this is تَصْرِيح (explicit confirmation) that if someone sees a good dream — one containing an act of طَاعَة (obedience to Allāh) — they should strive to make it come true in real life. The Prophet ﷺ himself realized the dream by placing his forehead on the ground.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • أَبُو خُزَيْمَةَ— Abū Khuzayma al-Anṣārī (R.A.); known as Dhū al-Shahādatayn — one whose testimony was counted as equal to two witnesses by the Prophet ﷺ.
  • أَسْجُدُ عَلَى جَبْهَتِكَ— that I was making سَجْدَة on your forehead; the dream symbol of prostrating on the Prophet's forehead = proximity, devotion, and honour.
  • صَدَقَتْ رُؤْيَاكَ— your dream has proven true / has been fulfilled; the Prophet ﷺ realised the dream immediately by placing his forehead on the ground.
Cross-ref: Sharḥ al-Sunna; manāqib of Abū Khuzayma (Dhū al-Shahādatayn); cf. class 4621 on acting upon dream interpretation.
Kitab كِتَابُ الرُّؤْيَا الفصل الثالث
حديث ٤٦٢٦
وَعَنْ أَبِي سَعِيدٍ الْخُدْرِيِّ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ: «أَصْدَقُ الرُّؤْيَا بِالْأَسْحَارِ»
Narrated by Abū Saʿīd al-Khudrī (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Tirmidhī, Dārimī  ·  Grade: ضَعِيف (Albānī)
Translation
The Messenger of Allāh ﷺ said: "The truest dreams are those seen at the time of سَحَر (pre-dawn)."
Class Notes
  • Suyūṭī: lying about dreams is worse than lying about what one sees while awake — for two reasons:
    • (1) It constitutes lying against Allāh (since true dreams are from Allāh, falsely claiming a dream is attributing a falsehood to Him).
    • (2) It is falsely claiming a portion of نُبُوَّة (prophethood), since a true dream is جُزْءٌ مِنَ النُّبُوَّةِ — and claiming it without truth is making a false claim to that share of prophetic inheritance.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • أَصْدَقُ— the most truthful / most accurate (elative of صَادِق); indicating that dreams at this time are most likely to be رُؤْيَا صَادِقَة (true, prophetic dreams).
  • بِالْأَسْحَارِ— at the time of سَحَر; the period of pre-dawn (roughly the last third of the night before Fajr). A time of divine proximity and بَرَكَة.
Cross-ref: Tirmidhī, Dārimī; cf. class 4613 (رُؤْيَا الْمُؤْمِنِ جُزْءٌ مِنَ النُّبُوَّة — basis for Suyūṭī's second point); class 4612 (seeing bad dream — what to do).
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ السَّلَامِ — الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٦٢٧
وَعَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ: «خَلَقَ اللَّهُ آدَمَ وَطُولُهُ سِتُّونَ ذِرَاعًا، ثُمَّ قَالَ: اذْهَبْ فَسَلِّمْ عَلَى أُولَئِكَ مِنَ الْمَلَائِكَةِ، فَاسْتَمِعْ مَا يُحَيُّونَكَ، تَحِيَّتُكَ وَتَحِيَّةُ ذُرِّيَّتِكَ. فَقَالَ: السَّلَامُ عَلَيْكُمْ. فَقَالُوا: السَّلَامُ عَلَيْكَ وَرَحْمَةُ اللَّهِ. فَزَادُوهُ وَرَحْمَةُ اللَّهِ. فَكُلُّ مَنْ يَدْخُلُ الْجَنَّةَ عَلَى صُورَةِ آدَمَ، فَلَمْ يَزَلِ الْخَلْقُ يَنْقُصُ حَتَّى الْآنَ»
Narrated by Abū Hurayrah (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Bukhārī, Muslim (Muttafaq ʿAlayh)  ·  Grade: Ṣaḥīḥ
Translation
Allāh created Ādam with a height of sixty cubits. He then said: "Go and give السَّلَام to those angels seated over there, and listen to how they greet you — for that will be your greeting and the greeting of your progeny." Ādam said: السَّلَامُ عَلَيْكُمْ. They replied: السَّلَامُ عَلَيْكَ وَرَحْمَةُ اللَّهِ — adding وَرَحْمَةُ اللَّهِ to what he said. Everyone who enters جَنَّة will be in the form of Ādam. Creation has continuously been decreasing from then until now.
Class Notes
  • Mirqāt: this hadith shows the جَوَاز of saying السَّلَامُ عَلَيْكُمْ in response to someone's سَلَام — since the angels used this form in response to Ādam's سَلَام. However, the جُمْهُور hold that it is better (أَفْضَل) to say وَعَلَيْكُمُ السَّلَامُ.
  • It is also possible that the angels had themselves intended to initiate the سَلَام, but Ādam said it first — as commonly happens among people. Hence they responded with the full السَّلَامُ عَلَيْكَ and additionally added وَرَحْمَةُ اللَّهِ.
  • The شَرْط (condition) for a valid سَلَام response: the response must come after the initial سَلَام, not simultaneously. If two people give سَلَام at the exact same time, each is obligated to give a separate جَوَاب of the other's سَلَام.
  • The more مُعْتَمَد عَلَيْهِ opinion: سِتُّونَ ذِرَاعًا refers to the average human ذِرَاع of our time, not Ādam's own arm-length — giving 60 cubits ≈ 28 metres / 90 feet.
  • Objections raised against the 60-cubit height:
    • Fossils and archaeology show no evidence of humans this tall.
    • The ruins of Thamūd are constructed for people of average size.
    • It is biologically implausible for a body to function at that size.
    • If creation has been continuously decreasing, why has human height remained stable over the last hundred years?
  • Responses:
    • Science and archaeology are not قَطْعِي (definitive); they cannot categorically disprove the hadith.
    • There is no قَطْعِي proof that the ruins attributed to Thamūd are the only structures they ever built; furthermore, the identification of those specific ruins with Thamūd is itself based on إسرائيليات.
    • Mufti Muntasir Zamān outlines three approaches scholars take when أَحَادِيث appear to conflict with science: (1) تَرْجِيح (preferring one over the other); (2) جَمْع by تَأْوِيل (harmonising via reinterpretation); (3) تَوَقُّف (suspending judgment).
    • تَرْجِيح path: Ibn Farrā and Mufti Yūnus Jawnpūrī prefer the scientific evidence and hold that the figure of sixty ذِرَاع is not correct.
    • تَأْوِيل path (Mufti Taqī, quoted by Kashmīrī): Ādam was sixty ذِرَاع in جَنَّة; when he descended to دُنْيَا his height became normal. On this reading, لَمْ يَزَلِ الْخَلْقُ يَنْقُصُ means: since Ādam descended, humans have always been born نَاقِص relative to sixty ذِرَاع — i.e., لَمْ يَزَلْ يُولَدُ نَاقِصًا. This تَأْوِيل is further supported by hadith 4624, in which the description of Ibrāhīm (A.S.) implies a stature greater than ordinary.
    • Other تَأْوِيلَات for لَمْ يَزَلِ يَنْقُصُ: (1) نُقْصَان in spirituality, not in physical height; (2) نُقْصَان in health as a person ages; (3) a person's rate of growth decreases with age — the increase from age 5 to 15 is proportionally greater than from 15 to 25; (4) نُقْصَان in length of lifespan.
    • Mufti Jawnpūrī raises a chain-criticism: there is وَهْم (error) in this رِوَايَة — some say there is تَفَرُّد (isolation) in the رِوَايَة; others attribute the وَهْم to Abū Hurayrah (R.A.) himself; others suggest he may have taken it from إسرائيليات; and others attribute the وَهْم to Hammām ibn Munabbih.
    • Response to Mufti Jawnpūrī: these narrations are from الصَّحِيحَيْن (Bukhārī and Muslim), and the أُمَّة has agreed upon their authenticity — a chain-criticism that contradicts this consensus cannot be accepted.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • وَطُولُهُ سِتُّونَ ذِرَاعًا— and his height was sixty cubits; ذِرَاع = the distance from the elbow to the tip of the middle finger; scholars differ on whether this refers to Ādam's own arm or the standard human ذِرَاع.
  • اذْهَبْ فَسَلِّمْ— go and give سَلَام; a divine command to Ādam establishing the سَلَام as the official greeting of his entire progeny.
  • مَا يُحَيُّونَكَ— how they greet you; from حَيَّا = to greet / to wish life upon someone; the angels' response becomes the model greeting.
  • تَحِيَّتُكَ وَتَحِيَّةُ ذُرِّيَّتِكَ— your greeting and the greeting of your offspring; the سَلَام is legislated for all of Ādam's descendants until the Day of Judgement.
  • فَزَادُوهُ وَرَحْمَةُ اللَّهِ— they added "and the mercy of Allāh" to his سَلَام; the angels' response exceeded what Ādam initiated, and adding وَرَحْمَةُ اللَّهِ in the response is the سُنَّة.
  • عَلَى صُورَةِ آدَمَ— in the form of Ādam; every person entering جَنَّة will be restored to the original perfected form of humanity — the sixty-cubit stature.
  • لَمْ يَزَلِ الْخَلْقُ يَنْقُصُ— creation has continuously been in a state of decrease; scholars differ on what is decreasing — physical height, spirituality, lifespan, or rate of growth.
Cross-ref: Muttafaq ʿAlayh (Bukhārī 3326, Muslim 2841); cf. class 4624 (size description of Ibrāhīm A.S. — supports Mufti Taqī's تَأْوِيل); Mufti Taqī's جَنَّة/دُنْيَا تَأْوِيل quoted by Kashmīrī; Mufti Muntasir Zamān's three scholarly paths on أَحَادِيث vs. science.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ السَّلَامِ — الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٦٢٩
وَعَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ: «خَمْسٌ تَجِبُ لِلْمُسْلِمِ عَلَى أَخِيهِ: رَدُّ السَّلَامِ، وَتَشْمِيتُ الْعَاطِسِ، وَإِجَابَةُ الدَّعْوَةِ، وَعِيَادَةُ الْمَرِيضِ، وَاتِّبَاعُ الْجَنَائِزِ»
Narrated by Abū Hurayrah (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Muslim  ·  Grade: Ṣaḥīḥ
Translation
The Messenger of Allāh ﷺ said: "Five things are due from a Muslim to his brother: responding to السَّلَام, blessing the one who sneezes (تَشْمِيت), accepting the invitation, visiting the sick, and following the جَنَازَة."
Class Notes
  • عِيَادَةُ الْمَرِيضِ (visiting the sick):
    • Nawawi: عِيَادَةُ الْمَرِيضِ is سُنَّة — for anyone, whether you know the person or not.
    • Bukhārī does جَزْم that it is وَاجِب (by using the word تَجِبُ in the hadith text itself).
    • Ibn Baṭṭāl does تَوْجِيه of Bukhārī's position: it is وَاجِبٌ عَلَى الْكِفَايَةِ (a collective obligation).
    • The جُمْهُور hold that it is سُنَّة.
  • رَدُّ السَّلَامِ (responding to سَلَام):
    • Nawawi: Ibn ʿAbd al-Barr transmits that there is إجماع that initiating سَلَام is سُنَّة and responding to it is فَرْض (وَاجِب).
    • If the مُسَلَّم عَلَيْهِ (person being greeted) is a single individual, saying السَّلَامُ عَلَيْكُمْ (plural) is sufficient — it includes the angels accompanying him.
    • Mufti Taqī (quoting Ḥaḍrat Thānawī): responding to سَلَام is وَاجِب, but making it audible to the other person (إِسْمَاع) is مُسْتَحَبّ.
  • تَشْمِيتُ الْعَاطِسِ (blessing the one who sneezes):
    • Is تَشْمِيت وَاجِب or سُنَّة?
      • Nawawi: سُنَّةٌ عَلَى الْكِفَايَةِ.
      • Some Shāfiʿīs: فَرْضُ عَيْن.
      • Aḥnāf and most Ḥanābila: وَاجِبٌ عَلَى الْكِفَايَةِ.
    • تَشْمِيت is only وَاجِب if the عَاطِس (sneezer) says الْحَمْدُ لِلَّهِ; if he does not say it, تَشْمِيت is not required.
    • تَشْمِيت is not required for a كَافِر; however, one should make دُعَاء for his هِدَايَة.
    • If a person sneezes multiple times: it is سُنَّة to do تَشْمِيت each time up to three sneezes. After three, one has a choice — تَشْمِيت is no longer required.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • خَمْسٌ تَجِبُ— five things are due / obligatory; تَجِبُ = it becomes binding. The use of this verb gave Bukhārī grounds to argue for وُجُوب; the جُمْهُور read it as expressing strong سُنَّة or وَاجِبٌ عَلَى الْكِفَايَةِ.
  • رَدُّ السَّلَامِ— returning the سَلَام; the obligation of response is by إجماع according to Ibn ʿAbd al-Barr, while initiating السَّلَام is سُنَّة.
  • تَشْمِيتُ الْعَاطِسِ— blessing the one who sneezes (saying يَرْحَمُكَ اللَّهُ); from شَمَّتَ = to wish well upon someone. Only required if the عَاطِس first says الْحَمْدُ لِلَّهِ.
  • إِجَابَةُ الدَّعْوَةِ— accepting the invitation; responding to a Muslim's invitation to a gathering or meal.
  • عِيَادَةُ الْمَرِيضِ— visiting the sick; from عَادَ يَعُودُ = to return / to visit. Whether this is فَرْضُ كِفَايَة or سُنَّة is a matter of خِلَاف.
  • اتِّبَاعُ الْجَنَائِزِ— following the funeral procession; walking with the جَنَازَة to the burial. Separate فِقْه discussion applies to this right.
Cross-ref: Muslim 2162; Bukhārī (chapter on عيادة المريض, using تَجِبُ in the text); cf. class 4627 (سَلَام etiquette); Ibn Baṭṭāl's تَوْجِيه of Bukhārī's اِسْتِدْلَال; Ibn ʿAbd al-Barr's إجماع on رد السلام.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ السَّلَامِ — الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٦٣١
وَعَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ: «يُسَلِّمُ الصَّغِيرُ عَلَى الْكَبِيرِ، وَالْمَارُّ عَلَى الْقَاعِدِ، وَالْقَلِيلُ عَلَى الْكَثِيرِ». وَفِي رِوَايَةٍ لِمُسْلِمٍ: «وَالرَّاكِبُ عَلَى الْمَاشِي».
Narrated by Abū Hurayrah (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Muttafaq ʿAlayh  ·  Grade: Ṣaḥīḥ
Translation
"The younger greets the elder, the passer-by greets the one sitting, and the smaller group greets the larger group." And in a narration of Muslim: "and the rider greets the one walking."
Class Notes
  • This hadith is part of the آدَاب of السَّلَام — it lays down the order of who should initiate the greeting.
  • The principle: the one in the higher / superior position gives السَّلَام first, out of تَوَاضُع. The رَاكِب (rider), being elevated, greets the مَاشِي (one on foot) — humbling himself and guarding against كِبْر.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • يُسَلِّمُ— initiates the greeting; gives the السَّلَام first.
  • الصَّغِيرُ عَلَى الْكَبِيرِ— al-Suyūṭī (in Mirqat): it is a command to honour the elder (تَوْقِير) and to humble oneself (تَوَاضُع) before him.
  • الْمَارُّ عَلَى الْقَاعِدِ / الْقَلِيلُ عَلَى الْكَثِيرِ— Mirqat: these carry the same meaning as الصَّغِير and الْكَبِير.
  • الرَّاكِبُ عَلَى الْمَاشِي— Mirqat: تَوَاضُعًا — since Allah elevated the rider by the mount, lest he think himself better than the one on foot; al-Ṭībī: also لِلْإِيذَانِ بِالسَّلَامَةِ (announcing safety) and removing fear. (Muslim's wording; Mirqat lists it as a separate hadith, ٤٦٣٢.)
Cross-ref: Muttafaq ʿAlayh (Bukhārī 6231/6234, Muslim 2160); «الرَّاكِبُ عَلَى الْمَاشِي» is Muslim's wording. Verified in Mirqat ٤٦٣٢–٤٦٣٣ (بَابُ السَّلَامِ, الفصل الأول — Shamela 8176, page-ids 6400–6401): al-Suyūṭī (تَوْقِير/تَوَاضُع), al-Māwardī & al-Ṭībī on the حِكْمَة of the order, and Nawawī — the newcomer (الْوَارِد) upon a seated group greets first regardless of age or number. cf. class 4629, 4633.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ السَّلَامِ — الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٦٣٣
وَعَنْ أَنَسٍ أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ ﷺ مَرَّ عَلَى غِلْمَانٍ فَسَلَّمَ عَلَيْهِمْ. مُتَّفَقٌ عَلَيْهِ.
Narrated by Anas (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Muttafaq ʿAlayh  ·  Grade: Ṣaḥīḥ
Translation
The Messenger of Allah ﷺ passed by some boys and greeted them.
Class Notes
  • This shows the جَوَاز of elders initiating السَّلَام to children.
  • It is also to teach the children the importance of السَّلَام — training them in its آدَاب from a young age.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • غِلْمَان— Mirqat: (with كَسْرَة on the غ) the plural of غُلَام, meaning صَبِيّ (boy) or مَمْلُوك (slave).
  • فَسَلَّمَ عَلَيْهِمْ— Mirqat: تَوَاضُعًا (out of humility); and because he ﷺ was passing by (مَارّ) and they were many.
  • — (Nawawī, in Mirqat)— استِحْبَاب of greeting all people, even discerning children (الصِّبْيَان الْمُمَيِّزِين); a manifestation of his ﷺ تَوَاضُع and his complete شَفَقَة on all the worlds.
Cross-ref: Muttafaq ʿAlayh (Bukhārī 6247, Muslim 2168) — the Mishkāt/Mirqat wording is غِلْمَان and the action is the Prophet's ﷺ own (the Bukhārī 6247 narration where Anas does it citing the Prophet's practice is a parallel). Verified in Mirqat ٤٦٣٤ (بَابُ السَّلَامِ, الفصل الأول — Shamela 8176, page-ids 6402–6403): Nawawī — استحباب of greeting all, even discerning children, showing his ﷺ تواضع and شفقة. cf. class 4631.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ السَّلَامِ — الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٦٣٤
وَعَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ ﷺ قَالَ: «لَا تَبْدَؤُوا الْيَهُودَ وَلَا النَّصَارَى بِالسَّلَامِ، فَإِذَا لَقِيتُمْ أَحَدَهُمْ فِي طَرِيقٍ فَاضْطَرُّوهُ إِلَى أَضْيَقِهِ». رَوَاهُ مُسْلِمٌ.
Narrated by Abū Hurayrah (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Muslim  ·  Grade: Ṣaḥīḥ
Translation
"Do not be the first to greet the Jews or the Christians with the السَّلَام; and when you meet one of them on a road, force him to its narrowest part."
Class Notes
  • There are two separate discussions regarding السَّلَام with non-Muslims:
    • إِنْشَاءُ السَّلَام — initiating the السَّلَام.
    • رَدُّ السَّلَام — responding to it after they have initiated.
    This hadith pertains to the first (initiating).
  • The جُمْهُور take this hadith and prohibit إِنْشَاءُ السَّلَام to non-Muslims; some allow it.
  • This is when the Muslim has no حَاجَة to the ذِمِّيّ; but if he does have a need, then there is no problem.
  • The main thing is that this differs with place, time, and culture.
  • Qadi Iyad: the last part (فَاضْطَرُّوهُ إِلَى أَضْيَقِهِ) means that if there is a narrow road, you should not move aside — out of your way — to make space for them out of honour and اِحْتِرَام.
  • Qurtubi also takes this understanding. This is better than the opinion in the حَاشِيَة, because that (forcing them into the tightest spot) is hurting others for no reason.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • لَا تَبْدَؤُوا ... بِالسَّلَامِ— Mirqat: do not initiate the السَّلَام; because initiating it is إِعْزَاز (honouring) of the one greeted, and honouring them is not permitted.
  • فَاضْطَرُّوهُ— Mirqat: أَلْجِئُوهُ — compel / force him.
  • إِلَى أَضْيَقِهِ— to the narrowest of the road (he keeps to the wall, or is told to move from the middle to an edge), جَزَاءً وِفَاقًا. But Mirqat: the narrowing must not be such that he falls into a وَهْدَة (pit); and if the road is free of crowding, there is no harm. Mirqat calls it a قَتْل مَعْنَوِيّ (symbolic humiliation), since their literal قَتْل was lifted by the jizya.
Cross-ref: Muslim 2167 (also Aḥmad, Abū Dāwūd, Tirmidhī); Nawawī: initiating their salam is حَرَام (the نَهْي is لِلتَّحْرِيم); Qadi Iyad relates some who permit it for ضَرُورَة/حَاجَة (ʿAlqama, al-Nakhaʿī). Verified in Mirqat ٤٦٣٥ (بَابُ السَّلَامِ, الفصل الأول — Shamela 8176, page-id 6404): فاضطروه = أَلْجِئُوه; the narrowing must not push him into a وَهْدَة, and no harm if the road is uncrowded; a قَتْل مَعْنَوِيّ. cf. class 4638.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ السَّلَامِ — الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٦٣٨
وَعَنْ أُسَامَةَ بْنِ زَيْدٍ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ ﷺ مَرَّ بِمَجْلِسٍ فِيهِ أَخْلَاطٌ مِنَ الْمُسْلِمِينَ وَالْمُشْرِكِينَ عَبَدَةِ الْأَوْثَانِ وَالْيَهُودِ، فَسَلَّمَ عَلَيْهِمُ النَّبِيُّ ﷺ. مُتَّفَقٌ عَلَيْهِ.
Narrated by Usāmah ibn Zayd (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Muttafaq ʿAlayh  ·  Grade: Ṣaḥīḥ
Translation
The Prophet ﷺ passed by a gathering in which there was a mixture of Muslims, idol-worshipping polytheists, and Jews, and the Prophet ﷺ greeted them.
Class Notes
  • Gangohi: he gave السَّلَام to them intending the Muslims in the gathering.
  • This is how a person should act if he is forced to give السَّلَام to a ذِمِّيّ — intend the Muslims present.
  • And if there are no Muslims there, then he should intend the حَفَظَة angels and the other angels.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • مَجْلِسٌ فِيهِ أَخْلَاطٌ— Mirqat: أَخْلَاط (فَتْحَة on the hamza) = plural of خِلْط (what is mixed); a mixed, intermingled assembly.
  • عَبَدَةِ الْأَوْثَانِ— worshippers of idols (أَوْثَان); Mirqat: عَطْف بَيَان / بَدَل for الْمُشْرِكِينَ. The Jews are termed مشركين either for their saying «عُزَيْرٌ ابْنُ اللَّهِ» or by تَغْلِيب.
  • فَسَلَّمَ عَلَيْهِمْ— Mirqat (Nawawī): when one passes a group containing Muslims (or a Muslim) and a كَافِر, the سُنَّة is to greet intending the Muslims; likewise, when writing to a مُشْرِك one writes as the Prophet ﷺ wrote to Heraclius: «سَلَامٌ عَلَى مَنِ اتَّبَعَ الْهُدَى».
Cross-ref: Muttafaq ʿAlayh (Bukhārī 6254, Muslim 1798 — abridged to the السَّلَام portion). Verified in Mirqat ٤٦٣٩ (بَابُ السَّلَامِ, الفصل الأول — Shamela 8176, page-id 6408): Nawawī confirms the class point — greet a mixed gathering intending the Muslims; the same principle governs writing to a non-Muslim (the Heraclius letter «سلام على من اتبع الهدى» — cf. class 4655). Gangohi's نِيَّة point and the حَفَظَة-angels option are consistent. cf. class 4634.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ السَّلَامِ — الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٦٣٩
وَعَنْ أَبِي سَعِيدٍ الْخُدْرِيِّ عَنِ النَّبِيِّ ﷺ قَالَ: «إِيَّاكُمْ وَالْجُلُوسَ عَلَى الطُّرُقَاتِ». قَالُوا: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ مَا لَنَا مِنْ مَجَالِسِنَا بُدٌّ نَتَحَدَّثُ فِيهَا. قَالَ: «فَإِذَا أَبَيْتُمْ إِلَّا الْمَجَالِسَ فَأَعْطُوا الطَّرِيقَ حَقَّهُ». قَالُوا: وَمَا حَقُّ الطَّرِيقِ؟ قَالَ: «غَضُّ الْبَصَرِ، وَكَفُّ الْأَذَى، وَرَدُّ السَّلَامِ، وَالْأَمْرُ بِالْمَعْرُوفِ، وَالنَّهْيُ عَنِ الْمُنْكَرِ». مُتَّفَقٌ عَلَيْهِ.
Narrated by Abū Saʿīd al-Khudrī (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Muttafaq ʿAlayh  ·  Grade: Ṣaḥīḥ
Translation
"Beware of sitting on the roads." They said: "O Messenger of Allah, we have no alternative to our gatherings, in which we talk." He said: "If you insist on the gatherings, then give the road its due right." They said: "And what is the right of the road?" He said: "Lowering the gaze, restraining harm, returning the السَّلَام, enjoining good, and forbidding evil."
Class Notes
  • The Sahaba's reply مَا لَنَا مِنْ مَجَالِسِنَا بُدٌّ نَتَحَدَّثُ فِيهَا means: ضَرُورَة has forced us to sit and speak here, because we have no other space in which to talk.
  • So the Prophet ﷺ did not forbid it absolutely, but commanded giving the road its حَقّ — among which is رَدُّ السَّلَام (which is why this hadith sits in بَابُ السَّلَامِ).
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • إِيَّاكُمْ وَالْجُلُوسَ عَلَى الطُّرُقَاتِ— beware of / avoid sitting on the roads (الطُّرُقَات = plural of الطُّرُق, plural of الطَّرِيق).
  • مَا لَنَا ... بُدٌّ— Mirqat (al-Ṭībī): مَا لَنَا فِرَاقٌ مِنْهَا — we cannot separate from these gatherings; ضَرُورَة compels us to them, لَا مَنْدُوحَةَ لَنَا (we have no alternative).
  • غَضُّ الْبَصَرِ— Mirqat: restraining the gaze from the مُحَرَّم and from people's عَوْرَات.
  • كَفُّ الْأَذَى— Mirqat: refraining from harming passersby — e.g. by التَّضْيِيق (crowding the road) and the like.
Cross-ref: Muttafaq ʿAlayh (Bukhārī 2465, Muslim 2121). Verified in Mirqat ٤٦٤٠ (بَابُ السَّلَامِ, الفصل الأول — Shamela 8176, page-id 6409): al-Ṭībī confirms the ضَرُورَة reading (مَا لَنَا فِرَاقٌ مِنْهَا … لَا مَنْدُوحَةَ); رَدُّ السَّلَام (to the Muslims) is counted among حَقُّ الطَّرِيق, which is why this hadith sits in بَابُ السَّلَامِ.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ السَّلَامِ — الفصل الثاني
حديث ٤٦٤٤
وَعَنْ عِمْرَانَ بْنِ حُصَيْنٍ قَالَ: جَاءَ رَجُلٌ إِلَى النَّبِيِّ ﷺ فَقَالَ: السَّلَامُ عَلَيْكُمْ. فَرَدَّ عَلَيْهِ ثُمَّ جَلَسَ، فَقَالَ النَّبِيُّ ﷺ: «عَشْرٌ». ثُمَّ جَاءَ آخَرُ فَقَالَ: السَّلَامُ عَلَيْكُمْ وَرَحْمَةُ اللَّهِ. فَرَدَّ عَلَيْهِ فَجَلَسَ، فَقَالَ: «عِشْرُونَ». ثُمَّ جَاءَ آخَرُ فَقَالَ: السَّلَامُ عَلَيْكُمْ وَرَحْمَةُ اللَّهِ وَبَرَكَاتُهُ. فَرَدَّ عَلَيْهِ فَجَلَسَ، فَقَالَ: «ثَلَاثُونَ». رَوَاهُ أَبُو دَاوُدَ وَالتِّرْمِذِيُّ.
Narrated by ʿImrān ibn Ḥuṣayn (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Abū Dāwūd, Tirmidhī  ·  Grade: Ḥasan
Translation
A man came to the Prophet ﷺ and said: «السَّلَامُ عَلَيْكُمْ». He returned it and the man sat, and the Prophet ﷺ said: "Ten." Then another came and said: «السَّلَامُ عَلَيْكُمْ وَرَحْمَةُ اللَّهِ», and he said: "Twenty." Then another came and said: «السَّلَامُ عَلَيْكُمْ وَرَحْمَةُ اللَّهِ وَبَرَكَاتُهُ», and he said: "Thirty."
Class Notes
  • Munziri: there are two narrators in this hadith who are لَا يُحْتَجُّ بِهِ (not relied upon as proof).
  • Ad-Durr al-Mukhtār: it is not recommended to increase in السَّلَام beyond وَبَرَكَاتُهُ.
  • There are narrations from the صَحَابَة which indicate that one should not say more than وَبَرَكَاتُهُ. Ibn Abbas (R.A.) says السَّلَام ends at بَرَكَة.
  • Aisha (R.A.): in Tabarani, she was conveyed السَّلَام from Jibreel (A.S.); when she responded she wanted to increase beyond وَبَرَكَاتُهُ, but Rasulullah ﷺ stopped her.
  • There are also ahadith that show one may increase beyond وَبَرَكَاتُهُ, but these ahadith are ضَعِيف.
  • Ibn Hajar, after mentioning the ahadith showing one may add beyond وَبَرَكَاتُهُ, states: these ahadith are ضَعِيف, but if you combine all of them they gain some strength — so it is understood that it is مَشْرُوع to add more than وَبَرَكَاتُهُ.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • عَشْرٌ / عِشْرُونَ / ثَلَاثُونَ— Mirqat: عَشْرٌ = لَهُ عَشْرُ حَسَنَاتٍ (ten حَسَنَات for him, or written/established for him); each fuller phrase of the greeting adds another ten.
  • السَّلَامُ عَلَيْكُمْ (بِضَمِيرِ الْجَمْعِ)— Mirqat: the plural pronoun (كُمْ), even when greeting a single person, is either for تَعْظِيم or to include those (companions / angels) who are with him.
  • وَبَرَكَاتُهُ— "and His blessings"; the final phrase of the full السَّلَام. The خِلَاف is over whether one may add anything beyond it.
  • لَا يُحْتَجُّ بِهِ— (a narrator) by whom proof is not established; whose narration is not relied upon.
Cross-ref: Abū Dāwūd 5195, Tirmidhī 2689 (Ḥasan); Munziri weakens two narrators; ad-Durr al-Mukhtār & Ibn Abbas (R.A.): do not exceed وَبَرَكَاتُهُ; Aisha (R.A.) / Tabarani (Jibreel's salam) supports the limit; Ibn Hajar: the addition-reports are individually ضَعِيف but collectively gain قُوَّة, so adding beyond وَبَرَكَاتُهُ is مَشْرُوع. Verified in Mirqat ٤٦٤٤ (بَابُ السَّلَامِ, الفصل الثاني — Shamela 8176, page-ids 6413–6414): عَشْرٌ = لَهُ عَشْرُ حَسَنَاتٍ; the plural pronoun in السلام عليكم (even for one) is for تَعْظِيم or to include those with him.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ السَّلَامِ — الفصل الثاني
حديث ٤٦٤٨
وَعَنْ عَمْرِو بْنِ شُعَيْبٍ عَنْ أَبِيهِ عَنْ جَدِّهِ أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ ﷺ قَالَ: «لَيْسَ مِنَّا مَنْ تَشَبَّهَ بِغَيْرِنَا، لَا تَشَبَّهُوا بِالْيَهُودِ وَلَا بِالنَّصَارَى، فَإِنَّ تَسْلِيمَ الْيَهُودِ الْإِشَارَةُ بِالْأَصَابِعِ، وَتَسْلِيمَ النَّصَارَى الْإِشَارَةُ بِالْأَكُفِّ». رَوَاهُ التِّرْمِذِيُّ.
Narrated by ʿAmr ibn Shuʿayb, from his father, from his grandfather (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Tirmidhī  ·  Grade: ضَعِيف إِسْنَاد (Tirmidhī) / Ḥasan (al-Qārī)
Translation
"He is not of us who imitates other than us. Do not imitate the Jews or the Christians, for the greeting of the Jews is gesturing with the fingers, and the greeting of the Christians is gesturing with the palms."
Class Notes
  • Bayhaqi: the مُرَاد here can be that sufficing on الْإِشَارَة without تَسْلِيم (verbal salam) is مَكْرُوه.
  • Nawawi: sufficing on الْإِشَارَة while being able to speak is مَكْرُوه; but if a person combines both (the verbal salam and the gesture), then it is the best of سُنَّة.
  • Ibn Hajar: the نَهْي from السَّلَام بِالْإِشَارَة is for those who can give السَّلَام verbally. So if someone is occupied such that he cannot speak, then الْإِشَارَة is permissible — e.g. if he is far away, or if he is addressing a deaf person.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • لَيْسَ مِنَّا مَنْ تَشَبَّهَ بِغَيْرِنَا— Mirqat: لَيْسَ مِنَّا = not of أَهْلِ طَرِيقَتِنَا (our way / those who observe following us); بِغَيْرِنَا = those not of our مِلَّة.
  • لَا تَشَبَّهُوا— Mirqat: (with one of the two تاء's elided) = لَا تَتَشَبَّهُوا — do not imitate; the extra لَا (لَا بِالنَّصَارَى) is added for emphasis.
  • الْإِشَارَةُ بِالْأَكُفِّ— gesturing with the palms; أَكُفّ (فَتْحَة then ضَمَّة) = plural of كَفّ. Mirqat: perhaps they sufficed with the two gestures without uttering the لَفْظ of السَّلَام — which is the سُنَّة of Adam and the prophets and أَوْلِيَاء among his descendants.
Cross-ref: Tirmidhī 2695 (Tirmidhī: ضَعِيفُ الإسناد). Verified in Mirqat ٤٦٤٩ (بَابُ السَّلَامِ, الفصل الثاني — Shamela 8176, page-id 6419): al-Qārī holds the mu'tamad is that عَمْرو بن شُعَيب عن أبيه عن جدّه is ḤASAN (Suyūṭī attributes it to Ibn ʿAmr), so the ruling stands; the نَهْي of تَشَبُّه is عَلَى الْكَرَاهَة (not تَحْرِيم); combining the verbal salam with the gesture is permissible (Asmāʾ bint Yazīd — the Prophet ﷺ waved his hand while also greeting). Bayhaqi & Nawawi: sufficing on الْإِشَارَة while able to speak is مَكْرُوه, combining both is أَفْضَل; Ibn Hajar: الْإِشَارَة is permissible when speech is impossible (distance, or a deaf addressee).
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ السَّلَامِ — الفصل الثاني
حديث ٤٦٥٠
وَعَنْ قَتَادَةَ قَالَ: قَالَ النَّبِيُّ ﷺ: «إِذَا دَخَلْتُمْ بَيْتًا فَسَلِّمُوا عَلَى أَهْلِهِ، وَإِذَا خَرَجْتُمْ فَأَوْدِعُوا أَهْلَهُ بِسَلَامٍ». رَوَاهُ الْبَيْهَقِيُّ فِي شُعَبِ الْإِيمَانِ مُرْسَلًا.
Narrated by Qatādah (مُرْسَل — a Tābiʿī)  ·  Riwayah: Bayhaqī, Shuʿab al-Īmān  ·  Grade: Mursal
Translation
"When you enter a house, greet its people; and when you leave, bid its people farewell with a سَلَام."
Class Notes
  • Responding to the السَّلَام of farewell (the parting salam) is مُسْتَحَبّ, because it is for دُعَاء — since it is not a تَحِيَّة (greeting of arrival), it is not included under the آية from which the وُجُوب (of responding) is taken: «وَإِذَا حُيِّيتُمْ بِتَحِيَّةٍ فَحَيُّوا بِأَحْسَنَ مِنْهَا أَوْ رُدُّوهَا» (an-Nisāʾ 4:86).
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • فَأَوْدِعُوا أَهْلَهُ بِسَلَامٍ— Mirqat: الْإِيدَاع here = التَّوْدِيع (bidding farewell, from الوَدَاع) — leave them accompanied by a سَلَام. al-Ṭībī: make the سَلَام a وَدِيعَة (deposit) with them, so that you return and reclaim it — وَدَائِع are reclaimed — as a تَفَاؤُل (good omen) for safety and meeting again.
  • جَوَابُ هَذَا السَّلَامِ مُسْتَحَبّ— Mirqat: responding to this (parting) salam is مُسْتَحَبّ, because it is دُعَاء and وَدَاع, not a سَلَامُ تَحِيَّة — so it does not fall under the command of an-Nisāʾ 4:86 from which وُجُوب is derived.
Cross-ref: Bayhaqī, Shuʿab al-Īmān (مُرْسَل; the مُرْسَل is حُجَّة per the جُمْهُور, per Mirqat). Verified in Mirqat ٤٦٥١ (بَابُ السَّلَامِ, الفصل الثاني — Shamela 8176, page-id 6422): the مُسْتَحَبّ / دُعَاء / not-a-تَحِيَّة point (basis: an-Nisāʾ 4:86) is Mirqat's own commentary, and al-Ṭībī's وَدِيعَة تَفَاؤُل. NOTE: the «إِذَا انْتَهَى أَحَدُكُمْ إِلَى الْمَجْلِسِ» hadith (Abū Dāwūd 5208 / Tirmidhī 2706, Abū Hurayrah) is a SEPARATE narration that Mirqat references as appearing elsewhere — it was placed here in error in Session 14 and is now corrected to the Qatādah hadith the class notes actually comment on.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ السَّلَامِ — الفصل الثاني
حديث ٤٦٥٢
وَعَنْ جَابِرٍ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ: «السَّلَامُ قَبْلَ الْكَلَامِ». رَوَاهُ التِّرْمِذِيُّ وَقَالَ: هَذَا حَدِيثٌ مُنْكَرٌ.
Narrated by Jābir (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Tirmidhī  ·  Grade: Munkar (ضَعِيف)
Translation
"The السَّلَام comes before speech."
Class Notes
  • Mullā ʿAlī al-Qārī: this is because السَّلَام is a تَحِيَّة — something one begins with. So if it occurs after كَلَام (speech), it is no longer functioning as a تَحِيَّة, and its purpose is lost.
  • Mirqat's analogy: it is like تَحِيَّةُ الْمَسْجِد, which comes before sitting — if you sit first, its point is gone (يَفُوتُ).
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • السَّلَامُ قَبْلَ الْكَلَامِ— the greeting precedes speech; one gives السَّلَام first, then speaks.
  • تَحِيَّة— a greeting of honour with which one opens; Mirqat: السَّلَام is a تَحِيَّة that is forfeited (يَفُوتُ) if speech begins before it, like تَحِيَّةُ الْمَسْجِد before sitting.
  • مُنْكَر— (grading) a report standing alone through a weak narrator; Tirmidhī himself graded this hadith مُنْكَر.
Cross-ref: Tirmidhī (graded by Tirmidhī himself as مُنْكَر); verified in Mirqat ٤٦٥٣ (بَابُ السَّلَامِ, الفصل الثاني — Shamela 8176, page-id 6424): السَّلَام = a تَحِيَّة opened with, lost if speech precedes it, with the analogy to تَحِيَّةُ الْمَسْجِد; al-Qudāʿī from Anas: «السَّلَامُ تَحِيَّةٌ لِمِلَّتِنَا وَأَمَانٌ لِذِمَّتِنَا».
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ السَّلَامِ — الفصل الثاني
حديث ٤٦٥٥
وَعَنْ أَبِي الْعَلَاءِ بْنِ الْحَضْرَمِيِّ أَنَّ الْعَلَاءَ الْحَضْرَمِيَّ كَانَ عَامِلَ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ ﷺ، وَكَانَ إِذَا كَتَبَ إِلَيْهِ بَدَأَ بِنَفْسِهِ. رَوَاهُ أَبُو دَاوُدَ.
Narrated by Abū al-ʿAlāʾ ibn al-Ḥaḍramī (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Abū Dāwūd  ·  Grade: ضَعِيف
Translation
al-ʿAlāʾ al-Ḥaḍramī was the agent (ʿāmil) of the Messenger of Allah ﷺ, and when he wrote to him he would begin with himself.
Class Notes
  • He would begin by mentioning who the letter is from — i.e. himself, the sender — before the السَّلَام.
  • Mirqat: supported by Tabarani from Nuʿmān ibn Bashīr (مَرْفُوع): «إِذَا كَتَبَ أَحَدُكُمْ إِلَى أَحَدٍ فَلْيَبْدَأْ بِنَفْسِهِ» — when one of you writes to someone, let him begin with himself. cf. the Prophet's ﷺ own letters (من محمد رسول الله … سلام على من اتبع الهدى).
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • عَامِل— agent / administrative deputy (governor); al-ʿAlāʾ was the Prophet's ﷺ عَامِل over Bahrain.
  • بَدَأَ بِنَفْسِهِ— he began with himself; i.e. wrote his own (the sender's) name first, then the recipient, then the السَّلَام.
Cross-ref: Abū Dāwūd 5134 (ضَعِيف); verified in Mirqat ٤٦٥٦ (بَابُ السَّلَامِ, الفصل الثاني — Shamela 8176, page-id 6428): a نُسْخَة has «وَعَنِ ابْنِ الْعَلَاءِ»; reinforced by Tabarani (Nuʿmān ibn Bashīr, مَرْفُوع) «إذا كتب أحدكم إلى أحد فليبدأ بنفسه». cf. class 4652.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ السَّلَامِ — الفصل الثاني
حديث ٤٦٥٧
وَعَنْ زَيْدِ بْنِ ثَابِتٍ قَالَ: دَخَلْتُ عَلَى النَّبِيِّ ﷺ وَبَيْنَ يَدَيْهِ كَاتِبٌ، فَسَمِعْتُهُ يَقُولُ: «ضَعِ الْقَلَمَ عَلَى أُذُنِكَ، فَإِنَّهُ أَذْكَرُ لِلْمَآلِ». رَوَاهُ التِّرْمِذِيُّ وَقَالَ: هَذَا حَدِيثٌ غَرِيبٌ، وَفِي إِسْنَادِهِ ضَعْفٌ.
Narrated by Zayd ibn Thābit (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Tirmidhī  ·  Grade: غَرِيب (ضَعِيف إِسْنَاد)
Translation
I entered upon the Prophet ﷺ while a scribe was before him, and I heard him ﷺ say: "Place the pen on your ear, for it is more reminding لِلْمَآل."
Class Notes
  • لِلْمَآلِ is how it is written in the نُسَخ of the Maṣābīḥ and the Mishkāt; but in Tirmidhī (and al-Jāmiʿ al-Ṣaghīr) the wording is لِلْمُمْلِي instead.
