  • Mullā ʿAlī al-Qārī: لِلْمُمْلِي is probably the correct (الصَّحِيح) wording, and لِلْمَآلِ is a تَصْحِيف (scribal corruption) of it — supported by the riwayah أَذْكَرُ لَكَ (Ibn ʿAsākir from Anas).
  • The حِكْمَة behind لِلْمُمْلِي: placing the pen on the ear is closer to remembering its place (أَقْرَبُ تَذَكُّرًا لِمَوْضِعِهِ) and easier and faster to grab (أَيْسَرُ مَحَلًّا لِتَنَاوُلِهِ) — unlike putting it elsewhere, where retrieving it quickly may be difficult.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • كَاتِب— a scribe; one writing down dictation.
  • لِلْمَآلِ— "for the outcome / end-result"; the reading found in the نُسَخ of the Mishkāt and Maṣābīḥ. Mullā ʿAlī al-Qārī holds it to be a تَصْحِيف.
  • لِلْمُمْلِي— "for the one dictating"; the مُمْلِي is the one dictating to the scribe. This is the Tirmidhī reading, which al-Qārī considers correct: the pen on the ear is a quicker reminder of its place for the dictator.
  • أَذْكَرُ— more reminding; more conducive to remembering.
Cross-ref: Tirmidhī 2714 (Tirmidhī: غَرِيب, with ضَعْف in the إِسْنَاد); verified in Mirqat ٤٦٥٨ (بَابُ السَّلَامِ, الفصل الثاني — Shamela 8176, page-id 6431): the Mishkāt/Maṣābīḥ nusakh read لِلْمَآلِ, while Tirmidhī / al-Jāmiʿ al-Ṣaghīr read لِلْمُمْلِي — which al-Qārī deems الصَّحِيح (لِلْمَآلِ a تَصْحِيف), the حِكْمَة being quicker recall and retrieval of the pen; Ibn ʿAsākir from Anas «أَذْكَرُ لَكَ» supports it. cf. class 4655.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ السَّلَامِ — الفصل الثاني
حديث ٤٦٥٩
وَعَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ: «إِذَا انْتَهَى أَحَدُكُمْ إِلَى الْمَجْلِسِ فَلْيُسَلِّمْ، فَإِذَا أَرَادَ أَنْ يَقُومَ فَلْيُسَلِّمْ، فَلَيْسَتِ الْأُولَى بِأَحَقَّ مِنَ الْآخِرَةِ». رَوَاهُ أَبُو دَاوُدَ وَالتِّرْمِذِيُّ.
Narrated by Abū Hurayrah (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Abū Dāwūd 5208 / Tirmidhī 2706  ·  Grade: Ḥasan
Translation
"When one of you reaches a gathering, let him give the سَلَام; and when he wishes to rise (to leave), let him give the سَلَام — for the first is not more deserving than the last."
Class Notes
  • The ظَاهِر of this hadith — as Ṭībī states, quoting Nawawi — is that responding to this سَلَام is وَاجِب: the الْجَمَاعَة must answer the سَلَام of the one leaving when he gives it.
  • But Qāḍī Ḥusayn holds it is only مُسْتَحَبّ, because the جَوَاب is only وَاجِب when the سَلَام is for تَحِيَّة (greeting upon meeting); this سَلَام is for اِنْصِرَاف (leaving), not تَحِيَّة.
  • Shāshī rejects this: the سَلَام upon leaving is سُنَّة just as the سَلَام upon arriving is سُنَّة — so responding to the سَلَام of leaving should be وَاجِب just as responding to the سَلَام of arrival is وَاجِب.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • اِنْتَهَى— reached / arrived at (أَتَى، وَصَلَ).
  • فَلَيْسَتِ الْأُولَى بِأَحَقَّ مِنَ الْآخِرَةِ— the first سَلَام (on arriving) is not more deserving than the last (on departing); both are equally established.
Cross-ref: Abū Dāwūd 5208 / Tirmidhī 2706 (حَسَن). Verified in Mirqat (بَابُ السَّلَامِ, الفصل الثاني — Shamela 8176): carries the full discussion verbatim — Ṭībī quotes Nawawi that the ظَاهِر makes the جَمَاعَة's reply to the departure سَلَام وَاجِب; Qāḍī Ḥusayn (with Abū Saʿīd al-Mutawallī) makes it مُسْتَحَبّ since جَوَاب is only وَاجِب for تَحِيَّة, not اِنْصِرَاف; Shāshī rejects this and holds the reply وَاجِب, the departure سَلَام being سُنَّة like the arrival سَلَام. Lamʿāt not yet checked.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ السَّلَامِ — الفصل الثالث
حديث ٤٦٦٤
وَعَنْ جَابِرٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ قَالَ: أَتَى رَجُلٌ النَّبِيَّ ﷺ فَقَالَ: لِفُلَانٍ فِي حَائِطِي عَذْقٌ، وَإِنَّهُ قَدْ آذَانِي مَكَانُ عَذْقِهِ، فَأَرْسَلَ النَّبِيُّ ﷺ: أَنْ بِعْنِي عَذْقَكَ، قَالَ: لَا، قَالَ: فَهَبْ لِي، قَالَ: لَا، قَالَ: فَبِعْنِيهِ بِعَذْقٍ فِي الْجَنَّةِ، فَقَالَ: لَا، فَقَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ: «مَا رَأَيْتُ الَّذِي هُوَ أَبْخَلُ مِنْكَ إِلَّا الَّذِي يَبْخَلُ بِالسَّلَامِ». رَوَاهُ أَحْمَدُ وَالْبَيْهَقِيُّ فِي شُعَبِ الْإِيمَانِ.
Narrated by Jābir (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Aḥmad, al-Bayhaqī (Shuʿab al-Īmān)
Translation
A man came to the Prophet (S.A.W.) and said, "So-and-so has a date-palm (عَذْق) in my orchard, and the position of his palm harms me." So the Prophet (S.A.W.) sent word: "Sell me your palm" — he said, "No." "Then gift it to me" — he said, "No." "Then sell it to me for a palm in Jannah" — he said, "No." So the Messenger of Allah (S.A.W.) said, "I have not seen anyone more miserly than you, except the one who is miserly with the سَلَام."
Class Notes
  • The Prophet's (S.A.W.) offer to buy, take, or exchange the date-palm (عَذْق) was not a binding legal ruling (حُكْم شَرْعِيّ) — it was only a request made by way of intercession (شَفَاعَة), not a command (أَمْر).
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • عَذْق— a date-palm (نَخْلَة).
  • حَائِط— a walled orchard/garden (بُسْتَان مُحَدَّق بِالْحِيطَان).
  • آذَانِي— it caused me harm/annoyance (جَعَلَنِي فِي الْأَذَى).
Cross-ref: Aḥmad, al-Bayhaqī (Shuʿab al-Īmān). Verified in Mirqat (بَابُ السَّلَامِ، الفصل الثالث — Shamela 8176): the Prophet's (S.A.W.) سَوْم (offer to purchase) was «شَفَاعَةً مِنْهُ لَا آمِرًا» — interceding, not commanding — which also indicates the palm-owner was a Muslim. Lamʿāt not yet checked.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ الِاسْتِئْذَانِ — الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٦٦٦
وَعَنْ أَبِي سَعِيدٍ الْخُدْرِيِّ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ قَالَ: كُنْتُ فِي مَجْلِسٍ مِنْ مَجَالِسِ الْأَنْصَارِ، إِذْ جَاءَ أَبُو مُوسَى كَأَنَّهُ مَذْعُورٌ، فَقَالَ: اسْتَأْذَنْتُ عَلَى عُمَرَ ثَلَاثًا فَلَمْ يُؤْذَنْ لِي فَرَجَعْتُ، فَقَالَ: مَا مَنَعَكَ؟ قُلْتُ: اسْتَأْذَنْتُ ثَلَاثًا فَلَمْ يُؤْذَنْ لِي فَرَجَعْتُ، وَقَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ: «إِذَا اسْتَأْذَنَ أَحَدُكُمْ ثَلَاثًا فَلَمْ يُؤْذَنْ لَهُ فَلْيَرْجِعْ»، فَقَالَ: وَاللَّهِ لَتُقِيمَنَّ عَلَيْهِ بِبَيِّنَةٍ، أَمِنْكُمْ أَحَدٌ سَمِعَهُ مِنَ النَّبِيِّ ﷺ؟ فَقَالَ أُبَيُّ بْنُ كَعْبٍ: وَاللَّهِ لَا يَقُومُ مَعَكَ إِلَّا أَصْغَرُ الْقَوْمِ، فَكُنْتُ أَصْغَرَ الْقَوْمِ، فَقُمْتُ مَعَهُ، فَأَخْبَرْتُ عُمَرَ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ ﷺ قَالَ ذَلِكَ. مُتَّفَقٌ عَلَيْهِ.
Narrated by Abū Saʿīd al-Khudrī (R.A.) — about Abū Mūsā al-Ashʿarī (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Muttafaq ʿAlayh (Bukhārī 6245)
Translation
I was in one of the gatherings of the Anṣār when Abū Mūsā (R.A.) came as if alarmed and said, "I sought permission from ʿUmar (R.A.) three times and was not granted it, so I returned." ʿUmar (R.A.) asked, "What kept you back?" He said, "I sought permission three times and was not answered, so I returned — for the Messenger of Allah (S.A.W.) said: 'When one of you seeks permission three times and is not answered, let him return.'" ʿUmar (R.A.) said, "By Allah, you shall bring me proof of this!" ... Ubayy ibn Kaʿb (R.A.) said, "By Allah, none will stand with you but the youngest of the people." I was the youngest, so I stood with him and informed ʿUmar (R.A.) that the Prophet (S.A.W.) had indeed said it.
Class Notes
  • More than one reason is given for why ʿUmar (R.A.) did not answer Abū Mūsā (R.A.): he was occupied with something; or he wished to discipline and teach him (تَأْدِيب) — having heard that Abū Mūsā (R.A.) used to do this while he was governor of Kūfah; and it is possible both were the case at once — there is no contradiction (مُنَافَاة) between the two reasons.
  • Not answering after three times is a proof (دَلِيل) of the absence of permission (عَدَمُ الْإِذْن), so the visitor should return.
  • If the host is occupied or does not answer for some reason, the visitor (زَائِر) should not feel offended or angry — he has no right to force permission; it may be the host is not yet ready to receive him.
  • This hadith shows that the سَلَام should be given before seeking permission (اِسْتِئْذَان); some hold the opposite, but the clear narrations that follow show the سَلَام comes before the اِسْتِئْذَان.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • مَذْعُور— alarmed, frightened (خَائِف فَزِع).
  • اِسْتِئْذَان— seeking permission (طَلَبُ الْإِذْن).
  • بَيِّنَة— proof; a witness (شَاهِد).
Cross-ref: Muttafaq ʿAlayh (Bukhārī 6245, matn verified on sunnah.com). Verified in Mirqat (بَابُ الِاسْتِئْذَانِ، الفصل الأول — Shamela 8176, page-id 6445, printed as ٤٦٦٧): the three اِسْتِئْذَان = announcing presence, allowing thought, and final decision. Lamʿāt not yet checked.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ الِاسْتِئْذَانِ — الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٦٦٧
وَعَنِ ابْنِ مَسْعُودٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ ﷺ قَالَ لَهُ: «إِذْنُكَ عَلَيَّ أَنْ يُرْفَعَ الْحِجَابُ، وَأَنْ تَسْمَعَ سِوَادِي حَتَّى أَنْهَاكَ». رَوَاهُ مُسْلِمٌ.
Narrated by ʿAbdullāh ibn Masʿūd (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Muslim 2169
Translation
The Prophet (S.A.W.) said to him: "The sign of your permission (to enter) upon me is that the curtain (حِجَاب) is raised and that you hear my private speech (سِوَاد) — until I forbid you."
Class Notes
  • I.e. when you see that my curtain (حِجَاب) is lifted, you automatically have permission to enter.
  • This permission was only for Ibn Masʿūd (R.A.). Just because Ibn Masʿūd (R.A.) had this privilege with Rasulullah (S.A.W.) does not mean that we have this privilege with anyone we wish.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • إِذْنُكَ— the sign of your permission (عَلَامَةُ الْإِذْن).
  • الْحِجَاب— the curtain/screen (السِّتَارَة).
  • سِوَادِي— my private, low speech that indicates my presence in the house (سِرِّي وَكَلَامِي الْخَفِيّ الدَّالّ عَلَى كَوْنِي فِي الْبَيْت).
  • أَنْهَاكَ— I forbid you (from entering) (أَمْنَعُكَ عَنِ الدُّخُول).
Cross-ref: Muslim 2169 (matn verified on sunnah.com). Verified in Mirqat (بَابُ الِاسْتِئْذَانِ، الفصل الأول — Shamela 8176): a great virtue and honour for Ibn Masʿūd (R.A.) due to his extensive service and constant companionship. Lamʿāt not yet checked.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ الِاسْتِئْذَانِ — الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٦٦٨
وَعَنْ جَابِرٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ قَالَ: أَتَيْتُ النَّبِيَّ ﷺ فِي دَيْنٍ كَانَ عَلَى أَبِي، فَدَقَقْتُ الْبَابَ، فَقَالَ: «مَنْ ذَا؟» فَقُلْتُ: أَنَا، فَقَالَ: «أَنَا أَنَا!» كَأَنَّهُ كَرِهَهَا. مُتَّفَقٌ عَلَيْهِ.
Narrated by Jābir (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Muttafaq ʿAlayh (Bukhārī 6250)
Translation
I came to the Prophet (S.A.W.) regarding a debt owed by my father, and I knocked on the door. He said, "Who is this?" I said, "It is I (أَنَا)." He said, "I! I!" — as though he disliked it.
Class Notes
  • Replying "أَنَا (it is I)" is not proper, because it carries no benefit (فَائِدَة): the listener will not know who is seeking permission; and even if he recognizes the person's voice, this statement is so short that he still cannot ascertain who is speaking.
  • It also carries an implication of arrogance (إِيهَامُ الْكِبْر).
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • دَقَقْتُ الْبَابَ— I knocked on the door (gently, like tapping with the fingertips, as is the manner of thoughtful people).
  • مَنْ ذَا— who is this (knocking)?
  • أَنَا أَنَا— the repetition expresses disapproval; saying only "أَنَا" removes no ambiguity — one should identify oneself by name.
Cross-ref: Muttafaq ʿAlayh (Bukhārī 6250 / Muslim 2155, matn verified on sunnah.com). Verified in Mirqat (بَابُ الِاسْتِئْذَانِ، الفصل الأول — Shamela 8176, page-id 6447, printed ٤٦٦٩). Lamʿāt not yet checked.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ الِاسْتِئْذَانِ — الفصل الثالث
حديث ٤٦٧٥
وَعَنْ جَابِرٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ: «لَا تَأْذَنُوا لِمَنْ لَمْ يَبْدَأْ بِالسَّلَامِ». رَوَاهُ الْبَيْهَقِيُّ فِي شُعَبِ الْإِيمَانِ وَالضِّيَاءُ.
Narrated by Jābir (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: al-Bayhaqī (Shuʿab al-Īmān), al-Ḍiyāʾ
Translation
"Do not grant permission (to enter) to one who does not begin with the سَلَام."
Class Notes
  • This too shows that the سَلَام should be given first (before seeking permission).
  • Giving the سَلَام first applies only when verbal seeking of permission (اِسْتِئْذَان) is possible; if they cannot hear you through the door, then the سَلَام is not necessary.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • لَا تَأْذَنُوا— do not grant permission (whether to enter, or for food: بِالدُّخُولِ أَوْ لِلطَّعَام).
  • لَمْ يَبْدَأْ بِالسَّلَامِ— did not begin with the سَلَام (either the سَلَام of seeking permission or the سَلَام of meeting: بِسَلَامِ الْإِذْنِ أَوْ بِسَلَامِ الْمُلَاقَاة).
Cross-ref: al-Bayhaqī (Shuʿab al-Īmān), al-Ḍiyāʾ. Verified in Mirqat (بَابُ الِاسْتِئْذَانِ، الفصل الثالث — the last hadith of the bab, Shamela 8176): prior narrations strengthen its meaning (سَبَقَ أَحَادِيثُ تُقَوِّيهِ). Lamʿāt not yet checked.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ الْمُصَافَحَةِ وَالْمُعَانَقَةِ — الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٦٧٦
وَعَنْ قَتَادَةَ قَالَ: قُلْتُ لِأَنَسٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ: أَكَانَتِ الْمُصَافَحَةُ فِي أَصْحَابِ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ ﷺ؟ قَالَ: نَعَمْ. رَوَاهُ الْبُخَارِيُّ.
Narrated by Qatādah — from Anas (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Bukhārī 6263
Translation
Qatādah said: I asked Anas (R.A.), "Was the handshake (مُصَافَحَة) practiced among the companions of the Messenger of Allah (S.A.W.)?" He said, "Yes."
Class Notes
  • The handshake (مُصَافَحَة) is a سُنَّة مُسْتَحَبَّة according to everyone (Nawawi).
  • Ibn Ḥajar: the non-mahram woman (أَجْنَبِيَّة) and the beardless youth of beautiful appearance (أَمْرَد حَسَن) are excluded from the generality (عُمُوم) of the مُصَافَحَة.
  • Mullā Ṣafwān: the prohibition (نَهْي) regarding women is general (عَامّ), but with the أَمْرَد it depends on the person — whether he feels safe from desire (شَهْوَة) or not.
  • Performing the مُصَافَحَة after the صَلَاة is neither مُسْتَحَبّ nor established in the Sharīʿah (ثَابِت شَرْعًا).
  • If someone does it to you, it is better to avoid it — but with wisdom (حِكْمَة).
  • The main problem with this (after-ṣalāh) مُصَافَحَة is the belief that it is a سُنَّة (اِعْتِقَادُ السُّنِّيَّة). If that belief is absent, then it is fine — as long as the person does not feel that it is binding on him.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • الْمُصَافَحَة— joining the palm of one hand to the palm of the other (إِلْصَاقُ صَفْحَةِ الْكَفِّ بِالْكَفّ).
Cross-ref: Bukhārī 6263 (matn verified on sunnah.com). Verified in Mirqat (بَابُ الْمُصَافَحَةِ وَالْمُعَانَقَةِ، الفصل الأول — Shamela 8176, page-id 6458). Lamʿāt not yet checked.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ الْمُصَافَحَةِ وَالْمُعَانَقَةِ — الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٦٧٧
وَعَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ قَالَ: قَبَّلَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ الْحَسَنَ بْنَ عَلِيٍّ وَعِنْدَهُ الْأَقْرَعُ بْنُ حَابِسٍ التَّمِيمِيُّ جَالِسًا، فَقَالَ الْأَقْرَعُ: إِنَّ لِي عَشَرَةً مِنَ الْوَلَدِ مَا قَبَّلْتُ مِنْهُمْ أَحَدًا، فَنَظَرَ إِلَيْهِ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ ثُمَّ قَالَ: «مَنْ لَا يَرْحَمُ لَا يُرْحَمُ». مُتَّفَقٌ عَلَيْهِ.
Narrated by Abū Hurayrah (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Muttafaq ʿAlayh (Bukhārī 5997)
Translation
The Messenger of Allah (S.A.W.) kissed al-Ḥasan ibn ʿAlī (R.A.) while al-Aqraʿ ibn Ḥābis al-Tamīmī was sitting nearby. Al-Aqraʿ said, "I have ten children and I have never kissed any one of them." The Messenger of Allah (S.A.W.) looked at him, then said, "Whoever does not show mercy is not shown mercy."
Class Notes
  • This hadith (about kissing — تَقْبِيل) is mentioned in this bab because many hadith books add التَّقْبِيل to the title of the bab (بَابُ الْمُصَافَحَةِ وَالْمُعَانَقَةِ وَالتَّقْبِيل).
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • قَبَّلَ— kissed.
  • مَنْ لَا يَرْحَمُ لَا يُرْحَمُ— whoever does not show mercy is not shown mercy.
Cross-ref: Muttafaq ʿAlayh (Bukhārī 5997, matn verified on sunnah.com — in بَابُ رَحْمَةِ الْوَلَدِ وَتَقْبِيلِهِ وَمُعَانَقَتِهِ). Verified in Mirqat (الفصل الأول — Shamela 8176). Lamʿāt not yet checked.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ الْمُصَافَحَةِ وَالْمُعَانَقَةِ — الفصل الثاني
حديث ٤٦٧٨
وَعَنِ الْبَرَاءِ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ: «مَا مِنْ مُسْلِمَيْنِ يَلْتَقِيَانِ فَيَتَصَافَحَانِ إِلَّا غُفِرَ لَهُمَا قَبْلَ أَنْ يَتَفَرَّقَا». رَوَاهُ أَبُو دَاوُدَ وَالتِّرْمِذِيُّ وَابْنُ مَاجَهْ.
Narrated by al-Barāʾ ibn ʿĀzib (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Abū Dāwūd 5212, Tirmidhī, Ibn Mājah
Translation
"There are no two Muslims who meet and shake hands except that they are forgiven before they part."
Class Notes
  • "Before they part" (يَتَفَرَّقَا) can refer either to the parting of their bodies (تَفَرُّق بِالْأَبْدَان), or to the separating of the handshake itself (تَفَرُّق الْمُصَافَحَة).
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • يَلْتَقِيَانِ— they meet one another.
  • يَتَصَافَحَانِ— they shake hands.
  • يَتَفَرَّقَا— they part / separate from one another.
Cross-ref: Abū Dāwūd 5212 (wording يَفْتَرِقَا), Tirmidhī, Ibn Mājah (matn verified on sunnah.com). Verified in Mirqat (الفصل الثاني — Shamela 8176). Lamʿāt not yet checked.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ الْمُصَافَحَةِ وَالْمُعَانَقَةِ — الفصل الثاني
حديث ٤٦٨١
وَعَنْ عَائِشَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهَا قَالَتْ: قَدِمَ زَيْدُ بْنُ حَارِثَةَ الْمَدِينَةَ وَرَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ فِي بَيْتِي، فَأَتَاهُ فَقَرَعَ الْبَابَ، فَقَامَ إِلَيْهِ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ عُرْيَانًا يَجُرُّ ثَوْبَهُ، وَاللَّهِ مَا رَأَيْتُهُ عُرْيَانًا قَبْلَهُ وَلَا بَعْدَهُ، فَاعْتَنَقَهُ وَقَبَّلَهُ. رَوَاهُ التِّرْمِذِيُّ.
Narrated by ʿĀʾishah (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Tirmidhī 2732 (Ḥasan غَرِيب)
Translation
Zayd ibn Ḥārithah (R.A.) arrived in Madīnah while the Messenger of Allah (S.A.W.) was in my house. He came and knocked at the door, and the Messenger of Allah (S.A.W.) rose to him uncovered (عُرْيَان), dragging his garment — by Allah, I never saw him uncovered before it or after it — and he embraced him and kissed him.
Class Notes
  • I.e. from his navel (سُرَّة) upward was uncovered; either his upper garment (رِدَاء) slipped off because of the haste with which he rose, or he had put it on but not properly/fully.
  • The hadith shows the legitimacy (مَشْرُوعِيَّة) of kissing (تَقْبِيل) and embracing (مُعَانَقَة).
  • Badāʾiʿ [al-Ṣanāʾiʿ]: embracing (مُعَانَقَة) is disliked (مَكْرُوه) only when done in a way that leads to desire (شَهْوَة), or when done without clothing; but when done out of honour (إِكْرَام) it is fine. As for kissing (تَقْبِيل) on the hand or the head: if it is with شَهْوَة it is not allowed, but if there is no fear of شَهْوَة it is allowed.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • عُرْيَانًا— uncovered (his upper garment having slipped).
  • يَجُرُّ ثَوْبَهُ— dragging his garment.
  • اعْتَنَقَهُ— he embraced him.
  • قَبَّلَهُ— he kissed him.
Cross-ref: Tirmidhī 2732, Ḥasan غَرِيب (matn verified on sunnah.com). Verified in Mirqat (الفصل الثاني — Shamela 8176). Lamʿāt not yet checked.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ الْمُصَافَحَةِ وَالْمُعَانَقَةِ — الفصل الثاني
حديث ٤٦٨٢
وَعَنْ أَبِي ذَرٍّ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ قَالَ: مَا لَقِيتُهُ قَطُّ إِلَّا صَافَحَنِي، وَبَعَثَ إِلَيَّ ذَاتَ يَوْمٍ وَلَمْ أَكُنْ فِي أَهْلِي، فَلَمَّا جِئْتُ أُخْبِرْتُ، فَأَتَيْتُهُ وَهُوَ عَلَى سَرِيرٍ، فَالْتَزَمَنِي، فَكَانَتْ تِلْكَ أَجْوَدَ وَأَجْوَدَ. رَوَاهُ أَبُو دَاوُدَ.
Narrated by Abū Dharr (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Abū Dāwūd 5214
Translation
I never met him (S.A.W.) but he shook my hand. One day he sent for me and I was not at home; when I came I was informed, so I came to him while he was on a couch (سَرِير), and he embraced me — and that was better and better.
Class Notes
  • سَرِير refers to a structure made for lying down upon.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • سَرِير— a bed/couch; a structure meant for lying upon.
  • الْتَزَمَنِي— he embraced me.
  • صَافَحَنِي— he shook hands with me.
Cross-ref: Abū Dāwūd 5214 (matn verified on sunnah.com). Verified in Mirqat (الفصل الثاني — Shamela 8176). Lamʿāt not yet checked.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ الْمُصَافَحَةِ وَالْمُعَانَقَةِ — الفصل الثاني
حديث ٤٦٨٣
وَعَنْ عِكْرِمَةَ بْنِ أَبِي جَهْلٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ ﷺ قَالَ لَهُ حِينَ قَدِمَ عَلَيْهِ: «مَرْحَبًا بِالرَّاكِبِ الْمُهَاجِرِ». رَوَاهُ التِّرْمِذِيُّ.
Narrated by ʿIkrimah ibn Abī Jahl (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Tirmidhī
Translation
The Prophet (S.A.W.) said to him when he arrived: "Welcome to the migrating rider (الرَّاكِب الْمُهَاجِر)."
Class Notes
  • Gangohi: مُهَاجِر here refers to the one who left his home (تَارِكٌ لِبَيْتِهِ), because the technical هِجْرَة (هِجْرَة اِصْطِلَاحِيَّة) no longer remained after the conquest.
  • Shaykh Zakariyyā: he was called مُهَاجِر because he came from Yemen — which was still a land of disbelief (دَارُ كُفْر) — to Makkah, which was a land of Islam (دَارُ إِسْلَام); on this understanding the هِجْرَة can be taken in its literal (حَقِيقِيّ) meaning. (The principle "no هِجْرَة after the conquest" — لَا هِجْرَةَ بَعْدَ الْفَتْح — applies specifically to Makkah; migration from a land of disbelief to a land of Islam remains.)
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • مَرْحَبًا— welcome.
  • الرَّاكِب— the rider.
  • الْمُهَاجِر— the migrant: to Allah and His Messenger, or from a land of war to a land of Islam (إِلَى اللَّهِ وَرَسُولِهِ، أَوْ مِنْ دَارِ الْحَرْبِ إِلَى دَارِ الْإِسْلَام).
Cross-ref: Tirmidhī. Verified in Mirqat (الفصل الثاني — Shamela 8176): الْمُهَاجِر = «إِلَى اللَّهِ وَرَسُولِهِ، أَوْ مِنْ دَارِ الْحَرْبِ إِلَى دَارِ الْإِسْلَام», with لَا هِجْرَةَ بَعْدَ الْفَتْح being Makkah-specific. Lamʿāt not yet checked.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ الْمُصَافَحَةِ وَالْمُعَانَقَةِ — الفصل الثاني
حديث ٤٦٨٧
وَعَنْ زَارِعٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ — وَكَانَ فِي وَفْدِ عَبْدِ الْقَيْسِ — قَالَ: لَمَّا قَدِمْنَا الْمَدِينَةَ، فَجَعَلْنَا نَتَبَادَرُ مِنْ رَوَاحِلِنَا فَنُقَبِّلُ يَدَ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ ﷺ وَرِجْلَهُ. رَوَاهُ أَبُو دَاوُدَ.
Narrated by Zāriʿ (R.A.) — of the ʿAbd al-Qays delegation  ·  Riwayah: Abū Dāwūd 5225
Translation
When we arrived in Madīnah, we hastened down from our mounts (رَوَاحِل) and began kissing the hand and the foot of the Messenger of Allah (S.A.W.).
Class Notes
  • Kissing the feet has the same ruling (حُكْم) as kissing the hand — but bowing (اِنْحِنَاء) must be avoided.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • نَتَبَادَرُ— we hastened (to dismount).
  • رَوَاحِلِنَا— our riding-mounts.
  • نُقَبِّلُ— we kiss.
Cross-ref: Abū Dāwūd 5225 (matn verified on sunnah.com — in بَابُ قُبْلَةِ الرِّجْل). Verified in Mirqat (الفصل الثاني — Shamela 8176, printed ٤٦٨٨). Lamʿāt not yet checked.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ الْمُصَافَحَةِ وَالْمُعَانَقَةِ — الفصل الثالث
حديث ٤٦٩٣
وَعَنِ الْبَرَاءِ بْنِ عَازِبٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ: «مَنْ صَلَّى أَرْبَعًا وَدَعَا قَبْلَ الْهَاجِرَةِ، فَكَأَنَّمَا صَلَّاهُنَّ فِي لَيْلَةِ الْقَدْرِ، وَالْمُسْلِمَانِ إِذَا تَصَافَحَا لَمْ يَبْقَ ذَنْبٌ إِلَّا سَقَطَ». رَوَاهُ الْبَيْهَقِيُّ فِي شُعَبِ الْإِيمَانِ.
Narrated by al-Barāʾ ibn ʿĀzib (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: al-Bayhaqī (Shuʿab al-Īmān)
Translation
"Whoever prays four (رَكْعَة) and supplicates before midday (الْهَاجِرَة) — it is as though he prayed them on Laylat al-Qadr; and when two Muslims shake hands, no sin remains but it falls away."
Class Notes
  • The reason this carries such great reward is that he worshipped his Lord voluntarily during the heat — at a time when people are resting or are in heedlessness (غَفْلَة).
  • A narration in Tirmidhī: «مِنْ تَمَامِ التَّحِيَّةِ الْأَخْذُ بِالْيَدِ» (part of completing the greeting is taking the hand). From this narration, some عُلَمَاء — especially Mubārakpūrī — state that مُصَافَحَة with one hand is سُنَّة and أَفْضَل.
  • Gangohi: the أَلِف لَام in «الْيَد» is for the genus (جِنْس), so oneness (i.e. using only one hand — وَحْدَة) cannot be proven from this hadith.
  • The truth (حَقّ) is that the مُصَافَحَة of Rasulullah (S.A.W.) is established (ثَابِت) both with one hand and with two hands; but since مُصَافَحَة with one hand was the emblem (شِعَار) of the Europeans, it should be avoided.
  • However, one hand being the شِعَار of the Europeans can change with time and place — nowadays most Arabs do it with one hand.
  • Durr al-Mukhtār (al-Ḥaṣkafī) says the سُنَّة is to do مُصَافَحَة with both hands.
  • Ḥanafī فِقْه books generally give preference (تَرْجِيح) to [doing it with two] hands, while some other مَذَاهِب do not give تَرْجِيح between one and two.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • أَرْبَعًا— i.e. the Ḍuḥā prayer (صَلَاةُ الضُّحَى).
  • الْهَاجِرَة— before midday (قَبْلَ نِصْفِ النَّهَار), the time of intense heat (وَقْتُ اشْتِدَادِ الْحَرّ); also used for noon (الظَّهِيرَة).
  • لَمْ يَبْقَ ذَنْبٌ إِلَّا سَقَطَ— "ذَنْب" here means rancour and malice (غِلّ وَشَحْنَاء); it falls away. Ṭībī: sin is put in place of rancour/malice because it is caused by them.
Cross-ref: al-Bayhaqī (Shuʿab al-Īmān). Verified in Mirqat (بَابُ الْمُصَافَحَةِ وَالْمُعَانَقَةِ، الفصل الثالث — Shamela 8176, page-id 6482, printed ٤٦٩٤): «أَرْبَعًا» = Ḍuḥā, «الْهَاجِرَة» = before noon at peak heat, the great reward being because he worshipped voluntarily bearing the heat «فِي وَقْتِ الْغَفْلَةِ وَزَمَانِ الِاسْتِرَاحَةِ»; «ذَنْب» = غِلّ وشحناء. The «مِنْ تَمَامِ التَّحِيَّةِ الْأَخْذُ بِالْيَدِ» one-hand-vs-two-hand discussion is from the class (Tirmidhī narration + Mubārakpūrī / Gangohi / Durr al-Mukhtār), not Mirqat's commentary on this hadith. Lamʿāt not yet checked.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ الْقِيَامِ — الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٦٩٥
وَعَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا عَنِ النَّبِيِّ ﷺ قَالَ: «لَا يُقِيمُ الرَّجُلُ الرَّجُلَ مِنْ مَجْلِسِهِ ثُمَّ يَجْلِسُ فِيهِ، وَلَكِنْ تَفَسَّحُوا وَتَوَسَّعُوا». مُتَّفَقٌ عَلَيْهِ.
Narrated by Ibn ʿUmar (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Muttafaq ʿAlayh
Translation
"A man must not make another man get up from his seat and then sit in it; rather, make room and spread out for one another."
Class Notes
  • Telling someone to get up and give you his spot is impermissible. (Nawawi: this prohibition is for تَحْرِيم — whoever precedes others to a permissible spot (مَوْضِع مُبَاح) is more entitled to it, and it is حَرَام for another to make him get up.)
  • As for if they willingly give up the spot without you asking, then you are allowed to take it.
  • But some Ṣaḥābah would refrain from taking this type of spot as well — Ibn ʿUmar (R.A.), if a man got up from his seat for him, would not sit in it.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • لَا يُقِيمُ— must not make (someone) get up (from الْإِقَامَة).
  • مِنْ مَجْلِسِهِ— from his place which he preceded others to — a permissible spot (مَوْضِع مُبَاح).
  • تَفَسَّحُوا وَتَوَسَّعُوا— make room and spread out for one another (do not crowd; move closer so the gathering widens) — cf. al-Mujādila 11.
Cross-ref: Muttafaq ʿAlayh. Verified in Mirqat (بَابُ الْقِيَامِ، الفصل الأول — Shamela 8176, page-id 6486, printed ٤٦٩٦): Nawawi — prohibition for تَحْرِيم; al-Qārī's بَحْث on the teaching/fatwā-spot exception (a رِيَاء concern); «كَانَ ابْنُ عُمَرَ إِذَا قَامَ لَهُ رَجُلٌ عَنْ مَجْلِسِهِ لَمْ يَجْلِسْ فِيهِ». Lamʿāt not yet checked.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ الْقِيَامِ — الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٦٩٦
وَعَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ ﷺ قَالَ: «مَنْ قَامَ مِنْ مَجْلِسِهِ ثُمَّ رَجَعَ إِلَيْهِ فَهُوَ أَحَقُّ بِهِ». رَوَاهُ مُسْلِمٌ.
Narrated by Abū Hurayrah (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Muslim
Translation
"Whoever gets up from his seat then returns to it is more entitled to it."
Class Notes
  • Durr al-Mukhtār (al-Ḥaṣkafī): it is possible to qualify (تَقْيِيد) the principle that every part of the مَسْجِد is permissible for sitting (كَوْنُ كُلِّ الْمَسْجِدِ مُبَاحًا لِلْجُلُوس) — such that his right to the spot holds only if he leaves intending to return; if he does not leave with the intention (نِيَّة) of returning, his exclusive right lapses.
  • Mufti Taqi: this [right to reclaim the spot] is only for someone who leaves for a short while. So what people do — leaving their rugs in the مَسْجِد after Maghrib in order to reserve that spot for ʿIshāʾ — is not permissible.
  • And if a person gets up from the gathering willingly and gives you the space, then you may sit there, based on «تَفَسَّحُوا فِي الْمَجَالِس».
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • مَنْ قَامَ مِنْ مَجْلِسِهِ— whoever gets up from his seat (intending to return to it soon — مُرِيدًا لِلرُّجُوعِ إِلَيْهِ قَرِيبًا).
  • فَهُوَ أَحَقُّ بِهِ— he is more entitled to it (only for that one sitting/صَلَاة — Nawawi).
Cross-ref: Muslim. The Durr al-Mukhtār point is verified consistent with Mirqat (بَابُ الْقِيَامِ، الفصل الأول — Shamela 8176, page-id 6487, printed ٤٦٩٧): Ibn al-Malak — if he leaves a خُمْرَة/rug etc. his right remains; al-Qārī — «وَالظَّاهِرُ أَنَّهُ إِذَا لَمْ يَتْرُكْ فِيهِ شَيْئًا بَطَلَ اخْتِصَاصُهُ رُجُوعًا لِلْمُبَاحِ إِلَى أَصْلِهِ»; the right holds only for that one sitting. Lamʿāt not yet checked.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ الْقِيَامِ — الفصل الثاني
حديث ٤٦٩٧
وَعَنْ أَنَسِ بْنِ مَالِكٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ قَالَ: «لَمْ يَكُنْ شَخْصٌ أَحَبَّ إِلَيْهِمْ مِنْ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ ﷺ، وَكَانُوا إِذَا رَأَوْهُ لَمْ يَقُومُوا، لِمَا يَعْلَمُونَ مِنْ كَرَاهِيَتِهِ لِذَلِكَ». رَوَاهُ التِّرْمِذِيُّ وَقَالَ: هَذَا حَدِيثٌ حَسَنٌ صَحِيحٌ.
Narrated by Anas ibn Mālik (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Tirmidhī (Ḥasan Ṣaḥīḥ)
Translation
"There was no person more beloved to them than the Messenger of Allah (S.A.W.); yet when they saw him they would not stand up, because they knew his dislike of that."
Class Notes
  • This is a دَلِيل of the مَنْع (prohibition) side regarding standing for someone out of تَعْظِيم: the Ṣaḥābah did not stand for the Prophet (S.A.W.) — the most beloved of all people to them — because they knew he disliked it.
  • Response of the مُجَوِّزِين (those who permit): merely that Rasulullah (S.A.W.) did not do or want something does not by itself prove its impermissibility (عَدَمُ الْجَوَاز). (The same response applies to hadith 4699.)
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • لَمْ يَقُومُوا— they would not stand up (for him upon seeing him).
  • كَرَاهِيَتِهِ— his dislike (of being stood up for).
Cross-ref: Tirmidhī (Ḥasan Ṣaḥīḥ). Verified in Mirqat (بَابُ الْقِيَامِ، الفصل الثاني — Shamela 8176, page-id 6488, printed ٤٦٩٨). Cited as دَلِيل of مَنْع; cf. hadith 4698. Lamʿāt not yet checked.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ الْقِيَامِ — الفصل الثاني
حديث ٤٦٩٨
وَعَنْ مُعَاوِيَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ: «مَنْ سَرَّهُ أَنْ يَتَمَثَّلَ لَهُ الرِّجَالُ قِيَامًا فَلْيَتَبَوَّأْ مَقْعَدَهُ مِنَ النَّارِ». رَوَاهُ التِّرْمِذِيُّ وَأَبُو دَاوُدَ.
Narrated by Muʿāwiyah (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Tirmidhī, Abū Dāwūd (also Aḥmad)
Translation
"Whoever is pleased that men stand before him (in attendance) — let him take his seat in the Fire."
Class Notes
  • I.e. he likes that people remain standing in front of him, like statues, out of so-called أَدَب. This is part of a longer incident: Muʿāwiyah (R.A.) came out, and ʿAbdullāh ibn ʿĀmir stood up while ʿAbdullāh ibn al-Zubayr (R.A.) remained sitting, so Muʿāwiyah (R.A.) related this hadith.
  • The types of standing for someone:
  • 1. The leader is sitting and the others remain standing for him for the entire majlis — forbidden (مَمْنُوع) by إِجْمَاع (the proof being this very hadith 4698), because this is the habit of the arrogant (الْمُتَكَبِّرِين).
  • 2. People stand for someone arriving, and they have to stand because of his arrogance (he thinks he is above the people in the majlis, so they must stand for him) — forbidden (مَمْنُوع) by اِتِّفَاق.
  • 3. Standing for one who arrives (قَادِم) who does not himself feel arrogance over those standing, but there is a fear that he may develop thoughts of arrogance — this is مَكْرُوه.
  • 4. Standing for a قَادِم out of happiness (فَرَح), or to congratulate someone for a blessing (نِعْمَة) he received, or for someone afflicted by a calamity to console him — this is مَنْدُوب.
  • 5. Standing for one who arrives out of honouring him (إِكْرَام), even though he does not want you to stand for him — this has اِخْتِلَاف among the عُلَمَاء:
  •   • Permission (جَوَاز): Ṭabarī, Ṭaḥāwī, Bayhaqī, Nawawi, Ibn Baṭṭāl, and Khaṭṭābī. Nawawi has a رِسَالَة on this.
  •   • Prohibition (مَنْع): Ibn al-Ḥājj (he has a refutation of Nawawi's رِسَالَة).
  •   • Ṭūrbishtī and Ibn Ḥajar mention both sides without clear تَرْجِيح, but the ظَاهِر is that [Ibn Ḥajar] inclines toward مَنْع.
  •   • Daleel of مَنْع: hadith 4697 and hadith 4698.   Daleel of جَوَاز: hadith 4694 and hadith 4688. Both sides respond to the other's evidence:
  •   Responses of the مَانِعِين (against the مُجَوِّزِين):
  •     a. hadith 4694 («قُومُوا إِلَى سَيِّدِكُمْ») means "stand to assist your master" (قُومُوا إِلَى إِعَانَةِ سَيِّدِكُمْ) — because Saʿd (R.A.) was injured; had it been for تَعْظِيم he would have said «لِسَيِّدِكُمْ» (for your master), not «إِلَى سَيِّدِكُمْ» (towards your master).
  •     b. hadith 4688 was for joy (فَرَح), so it falls under the 4th type of standing (which is مَنْدُوب).
  •   Responses of the مُجَوِّزِين (against the مَانِعِين):
  •     a. hadith 4697 — merely that Rasulullah (S.A.W.) did not do something does not prove عَدَمُ الْجَوَاز (the same response applies to hadith 4699).
  •     b. hadith 4698 refers to the first type from the earlier breakdown, and Muʿāwiyah (R.A.) acted on it out of caution (اِحْتِيَاط).
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • يَتَمَثَّلَ لَهُ الرِّجَالُ قِيَامًا— that men stand erect (يَنْتَصِب) before him, standing in attendance for his service and his exaltation (تَعْظِيم).
  • فَلْيَتَبَوَّأْ مَقْعَدَهُ مِنَ النَّارِ— let him prepare/take his seat in the Fire; the wording is a command but the meaning is a threat (لَفْظُهُ الْأَمْرُ وَمَعْنَاهُ الْخَبَرُ).
Cross-ref: Tirmidhī, Abū Dāwūd (also Aḥmad). Verified in Mirqat (بَابُ الْقِيَامِ، الفصل الثاني — Shamela 8176, page-id 6490, printed ٤٦٩٩): the وَعِيد is for one who takes the path of تَكَبُّر (the قَرِينَة being his سُرُور at the مُثُول); if they stand on their own for ثَوَاب or out of تَوَاضُع, no harm; Khaṭṭābī (via Bayhaqī, Shuʿab) — the meaning is that he commands/obligates it out of كِبْر and فَخْر; the Saʿd hadith shows standing for a virtuous leader / just ruler / one's teacher is مُسْتَحَبّ; Bayhaqī — standing on the way of البِرّ والإكرام is fine (Anṣār for Saʿd, Ṭalḥah for Kaʿb ibn Mālik), but the one stood-for must not desire it. The 5-types breakdown and the مَنْع/جَوَاز دَلِيل discussion are from the class. Lamʿāt not yet checked.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ الْقِيَامِ — الفصل الثاني
حديث ٤٧٠٠
وَعَنْ سَعِيدِ بْنِ أَبِي الْحَسَنِ قَالَ: جَاءَنَا أَبُو بَكْرَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ فِي شَهَادَةٍ، فَقَامَ لَهُ رَجُلٌ مِنْ مَجْلِسِهِ، فَأَبَى أَنْ يَجْلِسَ فِيهِ، وَقَالَ: إِنَّ النَّبِيَّ ﷺ نَهَى عَنْ ذَا، وَنَهَى النَّبِيُّ ﷺ أَنْ يَمْسَحَ الرَّجُلُ يَدَهُ بِثَوْبِ مَنْ لَمْ يَكْسُهُ. رَوَاهُ أَبُو دَاوُدَ.
Narrated by Saʿīd ibn Abī al-Ḥasan — about Abū Bakrah (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Abū Dāwūd
Translation
Abū Bakrah (R.A.) came to us to give a testimony (شَهَادَة), and a man got up from his seat for him, but he refused to sit in it and said: "The Prophet (S.A.W.) forbade this, and the Prophet (S.A.W.) forbade a man to wipe his hand on the garment (ثَوْب) of one whom he did not clothe."
Class Notes
  • «فِي شَهَادَةٍ» means لِأَدَاءِ الشَّهَادَة — i.e. he came to give/perform a testimony.
  • ثَوْب can mean a garment/dress or a handkerchief (مِنْدِيل) — Ṭībī: the intended meaning is the إِزَار, مِنْدِيل and the like. The prohibition: do not wipe your hand (when soiled with food) on the garment of someone you did not clothe — i.e. a نَهْي against using another's property without his permission/authority.
  • MAQ's (Mullā ʿAlī al-Qārī) أَظْهَر is that if the owner of the garment (صَاحِبُ الثَّوْب) is content with it, then it is fine to wipe your hands on his ثَوْب.
  • Likewise, if a person gets up from the gathering willingly (بِطِيبِ خَاطِر) and gives you the space, then you may sit there — based on «تَفَسَّحُوا فِي الْمَجَالِسِ» (al-Mujādila 11).
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • فِي شَهَادَةٍ— to give a testimony (لِأَدَاءِ شَهَادَةٍ كَانَتْ عِنْدَهُ).
  • فَأَبَى— he refused (to sit in the vacated seat).
  • بِثَوْبِ مَنْ لَمْ يَكْسُهُ— on the garment of one whom he did not clothe; Ṭībī: ثَوْب here = إِزَار / مِنْدِيل etc.
Cross-ref: Abū Dāwūd (Aḥmad agrees on the latter prohibition). Verified in Mirqat (بَابُ الْقِيَامِ، الفصل الثاني — Shamela 8176, page-id 6492, printed ٤٧٠١): Muẓhir — wipe on your own مِنْدِيل or that of your slave/son, not an أَجْنَبِيّ's; al-Qārī — «الْأَظْهَرُ أَنَّ صَاحِبَ الثَّوْبِ إِذَا كَانَ رَاضِيًا يَجُوزُ … وَكَذَلِكَ إِذَا عَلِمَ أَنَّ الشَّخْصَ قَامَ عَنِ الْمَجْلِسِ بِطِيبِ خَاطِرٍ فَلَا بَأْسَ بِجُلُوسِهِ». Lamʿāt not yet checked.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ الْقِيَامِ — الفصل الثالث
حديث ٤٧٠٤
وَعَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ قَالَ: «كَانَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ يَجْلِسُ مَعَنَا فِي الْمَسْجِدِ يُحَدِّثُنَا، فَإِذَا قَامَ قُمْنَا قِيَامًا حَتَّى نَرَاهُ قَدْ دَخَلَ بَعْضَ بُيُوتِ أَزْوَاجِهِ».
Narrated by Abū Hurayrah (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: الفصل الثالث
Translation
"The Messenger of Allah (S.A.W.) used to sit with us in the مَسْجِد narrating to us, and when he stood up we too would stand — remaining standing until we saw him enter one of the houses of his wives."
Class Notes
  • This is cited by the مُجَوِّزِين (those who permit standing). The response of the مَانِعِين (prohibition side) is that they would stand because the gathering had broken up (لِانْفِضَاضِ الْمَجْلِس), not out of تَعْظِيم.
  • This is because: if they would not stand up for him when he came (مُقْبِلًا), why would they stand up for him when he was leaving (مُدْبِرًا)? — a reasonable تَوْجِيه. (cf. hadith 4697: they did not stand for him knowing his dislike of it.)
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • فَإِذَا قَامَ قُمْنَا— when he stood we would stand — for the breaking-up of the gathering (لِانْفِضَاضِ الْمَجْلِس), not for تَعْظِيم.
  • قِيَامًا— an extended standing (وُقُوفًا مُمْتَدًّا), until they saw him enter his house.
Cross-ref: Mishkāt — الفصل الثالث. Verified in Mirqat (بَابُ الْقِيَامِ، الفصل الثالث — Shamela 8176, page-id 6496, printed ٤٧٠٥): «أَيْ لِانْفِضَاضِ الْمَجْلِسِ لَا لِلتَّعْظِيمِ؛ لِأَنَّهُمْ مَا كَانُوا يَقُومُونَ لَهُ مُقْبِلًا فَكَيْفَ يَقُومُونَ لَهُ مُدْبِرًا؟» — they perhaps waited in hope he might need something or return to sit, then dispersed. Lamʿāt not yet checked.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ الْجُلُوسِ وَالنَّوْمِ وَالْمَشْيِ — الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٧٠٩
وَعَنْ جَابِرٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ ﷺ قَالَ: «لَا يَسْتَلْقِيَنَّ أَحَدُكُمْ ثُمَّ يَضَعُ إِحْدَى رِجْلَيْهِ عَلَى الْأُخْرَى». رَوَاهُ مُسْلِمٌ.
Narrated by Jābir (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Muslim
Translation
"None of you should lie on his back and then place one of his legs over the other."
Class Notes
  • There is an apparent conflict: this hadith (ḥadīth النَّهْي) prohibits lying on the back with one leg over the other, yet another hadith (ḥadīth الْفِعْل) reports the Prophet (S.A.W.) doing it. How to reconcile them (جَمْع):
  • Ṭaḥāwī: the prohibition hadith is abrogated (مَنْسُوخ) — but to claim نَسْخ you need a دَلِيل [showing which came later].
  • Khaṭṭābī: the نَهْي is understood (مَحْمُول) to be the case where there is a fear of exposing the عَوْرَة (كَشْف الْعَوْرَة) — e.g. when wearing [only] an إِزَار; so the نَهْي is when كَشْف الْعَوْرَة is feared, and the فِعْل hadith is when there is no such fear.
  • Muẓhirī: the نَهْي is for the specific type of اِسْتِلْقَاء that risks كَشْف الْعَوْرَة, while the فِعْل hadith is about the اِسْتِلْقَاء that carries no such risk. [In plain terms: lying with one leg over the other is fine if wearing pants (سَرَاوِيل) or a very long إِزَار; but with a normal-sized إِزَار it exposes the عَوْرَة, so it is impermissible.]
  • Mufti Taqi: this ruling is based on the fear of كَشْف الْعَوْرَة, so it does not apply to someone wearing pants. Alternatively, the نَهْي may be due to قُبْح al-manẓar (the unseemly sight, since the shape of the عَوْرَة is outlined) — and on that understanding the نَهْي would apply even to pants.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • لَا يَسْتَلْقِيَنَّ— none of you should lie on his back (الاسْتِلْقَاء = lying flat on the back).
  • يَضَعُ إِحْدَى رِجْلَيْهِ عَلَى الْأُخْرَى— places one of his legs over the other.
Cross-ref: Muslim. Verified in Mirqat (بَابُ الْجُلُوسِ وَالنَّوْمِ وَالْمَشْيِ، الفصل الأول — Shamela 8176, page-id 6502, printed ٤٧١٠). The جَمْع (Ṭaḥāwī / Khaṭṭābī / Muẓhirī) reconciles this نَهْي with the فِعْل hadith (the Prophet ﷺ reclining thus, in Bukhārī). Lamʿāt not yet checked.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ الْجُلُوسِ وَالنَّوْمِ وَالْمَشْيِ — الفصل الثاني
حديث ٤٧١٥
وَعَنْ أَبِي قَتَادَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ ﷺ كَانَ إِذَا عَرَّسَ بِلَيْلٍ اضْطَجَعَ عَلَى شِقِّهِ الْأَيْمَنِ، وَإِذَا عَرَّسَ قُبَيْلَ الصُّبْحِ نَصَبَ ذِرَاعَهُ وَوَضَعَ رَأْسَهُ عَلَى كَفِّهِ. رَوَاهُ فِي شَرْحِ السُّنَّةِ.
Narrated by Abū Qatādah (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Sharḥ al-Sunnah
Translation
When he (S.A.W.) halted [on a journey] to rest at night, he would lie on his right side; and when he halted just before dawn, he would prop up his forearm and rest his head on his palm.
Class Notes
  • Near dawn he would prop up his forearm and rest his head on his palm so that he would not fall into a long sleep and miss the Fajr — a precaution (اِحْتِرَاس) against oversleeping (if he sank into deep sleep his head would drop and wake him).
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • عَرَّسَ— (of a traveller) to halt at night to rest and sleep (النِّهَايَة: نُزُولُ الْمُسَافِرِ آخِرَ اللَّيْلِ لِلنَّوْمِ وَالِاسْتِرَاحَة).
  • نَصَبَ ذِرَاعَهُ وَوَضَعَ رَأْسَهُ عَلَى كَفِّهِ— propped up his forearm and rested his head on his palm — a precaution so he would not sleep long and miss Fajr (لِئَلَّا يَنَامَ طَوِيلًا فَيَفُوتَهُ الصُّبْح).
Cross-ref: Sharḥ al-Sunnah (al-Baghawī). Verified in Mirqat (الفصل الثاني — Shamela 8176, page-id 6509, printed ٤٧١٦). Lamʿāt not yet checked.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ الْجُلُوسِ وَالنَّوْمِ وَالْمَشْيِ — الفصل الثاني
حديث ٤٧١٦
وَعَنْ بَعْضِ آلِ أُمِّ سَلَمَةَ قَالَ: كَانَ فِرَاشُ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ ﷺ نَحْوًا مِمَّا يُوضَعُ فِي قَبْرِهِ، وَكَانَ الْمَسْجِدُ عِنْدَ رَأْسِهِ. رَوَاهُ أَبُو دَاوُدَ.
Narrated by one of the family of Umm Salamah (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Abū Dāwūd
Translation
The bedding of the Messenger of Allah (S.A.W.) was close to what is placed [for a person] in his grave, and the مَسْجِد was at his head.
Class Notes
  • «الْمَسْجِد» here can refer to the actual مَسْجِد, or to his place of prayer (مُصَلَّى) in his house.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • فِرَاش— the bedding he spread to sleep on; it was close [in simplicity] to what is placed for a person in his grave.
  • الْمَسْجِد— the actual مَسْجِد, or his place of prayer (مُصَلَّى) at home.
Cross-ref: Abū Dāwūd. Verified in Mirqat (الفصل الثاني — Shamela 8176, page-id 6510, printed ٤٧١٧). Lamʿāt not yet checked.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ الْجُلُوسِ وَالنَّوْمِ وَالْمَشْيِ — الفصل الثاني
حديث ٤٧١٩
وَعَنْ عَلِيِّ بْنِ شَيْبَانَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ: «مَنْ بَاتَ عَلَى ظَهْرِ بَيْتٍ لَيْسَ عَلَيْهِ حِجَابٌ فَقَدْ بَرِئَتْ مِنْهُ الذِّمَّةُ». رَوَاهُ أَبُو دَاوُدَ.
Narrated by ʿAlī ibn Shaybān (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Abū Dāwūd
Translation
"Whoever spends the night on the roof of a house that has no barrier (حِجَاب) — the protection is lifted from him."
Class Notes
  • «حِجَاب» refers to a barrier (parapet) that would stop him from falling.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • حِجَاب— a barrier / parapet on the roof (variant readings: حِجَار / حِجًى [Khaṭṭābī in Maʿālim al-Sunan]) that prevents one from falling.
  • بَرِئَتْ مِنْهُ الذِّمَّة— the protective guarantee is lifted from him (if he falls, none but himself is to blame).
Cross-ref: Abū Dāwūd. Verified in Mirqat (الفصل الثاني — Shamela 8176, page-id 6513, printed ٤٧٢٠). Lamʿāt not yet checked.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ الْجُلُوسِ وَالنَّوْمِ وَالْمَشْيِ — الفصل الثاني
حديث ٤٧٢١
وَعَنْ حُذَيْفَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ قَالَ: مَلْعُونٌ عَلَى لِسَانِ مُحَمَّدٍ ﷺ مَنْ قَعَدَ وَسْطَ الْحَلْقَةِ. رَوَاهُ التِّرْمِذِيُّ وَأَبُو دَاوُدَ.
Narrated by Ḥudhayfah (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Tirmidhī, Abū Dāwūd
Translation
"Cursed on the tongue of Muḥammad (S.A.W.) is the one who sits in the middle of the circle (حَلْقَة)."
Class Notes
  • Khaṭṭābī interprets this two ways: (1) someone who comes late to a gathering, steps over the people's shoulders/necks (يَتَخَطَّى رِقَابَهُم), and sits in the middle instead of sitting where the gathering ends — so the كَرَاهَة is for hurting people (إِيذَاء); (2) sitting in the middle blocks the people from seeing one another (يَحُولُ بَيْنَ الْوُجُوه), which harms them (ضَرَر).
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • مَلْعُون— blameworthy / cursed (مَذْمُوم).
  • وَسْطَ الْحَلْقَةِ— the middle of the circle (of a seated gathering).
Cross-ref: Tirmidhī, Abū Dāwūd. Verified in Mirqat (الفصل الثاني — Shamela 8176, page-id 6516, printed ٤٧٢٢): the two تَأْوِيل of Khaṭṭābī (تَخَطِّي الرِّقَاب / حَجْب الْوُجُوه). Lamʿāt not yet checked.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ الْجُلُوسِ وَالنَّوْمِ وَالْمَشْيِ — الفصل الثاني
حديث ٤٧٢٤
وَعَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ ﷺ قَالَ: «إِذَا كَانَ أَحَدُكُمْ فِي الْفَيْءِ فَقَلَصَ عَنْهُ الظِّلُّ، فَصَارَ بَعْضُهُ فِي الشَّمْسِ وَبَعْضُهُ فِي الظِّلِّ، فَلْيَقُمْ». رَوَاهُ أَبُو دَاوُدَ.
Narrated by Abū Hurayrah (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Abū Dāwūd
Translation
"When one of you is in the shade and the shade shrinks away from him so that part of him is in the sun and part in the shade, let him get up (move)."
Class Notes
  • I.e. you should not sit in a place where part of your body is in the shade and part in the sun.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • الْفَيْء— the shade (that returns/lengthens after midday).
  • قَلَصَ عَنْهُ الظِّلُّ— the shade contracted / withdrew from him.
Cross-ref: Abū Dāwūd. Verified in Mirqat (الفصل الثاني — Shamela 8176, page-id 6520, printed ٤٧٢٥). Lamʿāt not yet checked.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ الْجُلُوسِ وَالنَّوْمِ وَالْمَشْيِ — الفصل الثاني
حديث ٤٧٢٨
وَعَنْ جَابِرِ بْنِ سَمُرَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا قَالَ: كُنَّا إِذَا أَتَيْنَا النَّبِيَّ ﷺ جَلَسَ أَحَدُنَا حَيْثُ يَنْتَهِي. رَوَاهُ أَبُو دَاوُدَ.
Narrated by Jābir ibn Samurah (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Abū Dāwūd
Translation
"When we came to the Prophet (S.A.W.), each of us would sit wherever [the gathering] ended [i.e. wherever he reached, without pushing to the front]."
Class Notes
  • They would sit down wherever the gathering ends (not stepping over people to reach the front).
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • حَيْثُ يَنْتَهِي— wherever [the gathering] ends — i.e. at its edge, wherever one reaches.
Cross-ref: Abū Dāwūd. Verified in Mirqat (الفصل الثاني — Shamela 8176, page-id 6525, printed ٤٧٢٩). Lamʿāt not yet checked.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ الْجُلُوسِ وَالنَّوْمِ وَالْمَشْيِ — الفصل الثالث
حديث ٤٧٢٩
وَعَنْ عَمْرِو بْنِ الشَّرِيدِ عَنْ أَبِيهِ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ قَالَ: مَرَّ بِي رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ وَأَنَا جَالِسٌ هَكَذَا، وَقَدْ وَضَعْتُ يَدِي الْيُسْرَى خَلْفَ ظَهْرِي وَاتَّكَأْتُ عَلَى أَلْيَةِ يَدِي، قَالَ: «أَتَقْعُدُ قِعْدَةَ الْمَغْضُوبِ عَلَيْهِمْ؟». رَوَاهُ أَبُو دَاوُدَ.
Narrated by ʿAmr ibn al-Sharīd, from his father al-Sharīd (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Abū Dāwūd
Translation
The Messenger of Allah (S.A.W.) passed by me while I was sitting like this — I had put my left hand behind my back and was leaning on the heel of my hand — and he said: "Do you sit like the sitting of those upon whom [Allah's] wrath has fallen (al-maghḍūb ʿalayhim)?"
Class Notes
  • Here «الْمَغْضُوب عَلَيْهِم» does not have to be restricted to the Yahūd; rather it includes all the كُفَّار and فُسَّاق whose arrogance (takabbur) can be understood from their manner of sitting.
  • The gist (خُلَاصَة) of the hadith: one should not sit in any manner that displays arrogance or resembles the arrogant ones.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • أَلْيَة يَدِي— the fleshy part at the base of the thumb (اللَّحْمَة الَّتِي فِي أَصْلِ الْإِبْهَام) — here, of the right hand.
  • الْمَغْضُوب عَلَيْهِم— those upon whom Allah's wrath fell; here understood generally — all كُفَّار / فُسَّاق known for arrogance.
Cross-ref: Abū Dāwūd. Verified in Mirqat (الفصل الثالث — Shamela 8176, page-id 6526, printed ٤٧٣٠). Lamʿāt not yet checked.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ الْعُطَاسِ وَالتَّثَاؤُبِ — الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٧٣١
وَعَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ عَنِ النَّبِيِّ ﷺ قَالَ: «إِنَّ اللَّهَ يُحِبُّ الْعُطَاسَ وَيَكْرَهُ التَّثَاؤُبَ، فَإِذَا عَطَسَ أَحَدُكُمْ وَحَمِدَ اللَّهَ كَانَ حَقًّا عَلَى كُلِّ مُسْلِمٍ سَمِعَهُ أَنْ يَقُولَ لَهُ: يَرْحَمُكَ اللَّهُ. فَأَمَّا التَّثَاؤُبُ فَإِنَّمَا هُوَ مِنَ الشَّيْطَانِ، فَإِذَا تَثَاءَبَ أَحَدُكُمْ فَلْيَرُدَّهُ مَا اسْتَطَاعَ، فَإِنَّ أَحَدَكُمْ إِذَا تَثَاءَبَ ضَحِكَ مِنْهُ الشَّيْطَانُ». رَوَاهُ الْبُخَارِيُّ.
Narrated by Abū Hurayrah (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Bukhārī
Translation
"Allah loves sneezing and dislikes yawning. So when one of you sneezes and praises Allah, it is a duty upon every Muslim who hears him to say to him: 'Yarḥamuka-llāh.' As for yawning, it is only from the Shayṭān — so when one of you yawns, let him restrain it as much as he can; for when one of you yawns, the Shayṭān laughs at him."
Class Notes
  • «يُحِبُّ الْعُطَاس» — the sneeze that is loved is the one which is not the result of sickness (it comes from lightness/briskness of the body).
  • «مِنَ الشَّيْطَان» (about yawning) — the Shayṭān is pleased when a person yawns; it does not [literally] mean that yawning is the action of the Shayṭān.
  • «ضَحِكَ مِنْهُ الشَّيْطَان» — i.e. he becomes happy, because yawning shows غَفْلَة (heedlessness) and gives him an opening to enter for waswasah.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • الْعُطَاس— a sneeze (from lightness/briskness of body; the disliked yawning is its opposite).
  • التَّثَاؤُب— yawning — a spell of drowsy heaviness (فَتْرَة مِنْ ثِقَلِ النُّعَاس) in which one opens the mouth; disliked because it prevents briskness in worship and brings غَفْلَة, so the Shayṭān rejoices — which is the meaning of his "laughing."
Cross-ref: Bukhārī. Verified in Mirqat (بَابُ الْعُطَاسِ وَالتَّثَاؤُبِ، الفصل الأول — Shamela 8176, page-id 6529, printed ٤٧٣٢). Lamʿāt not yet checked.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ الْعُطَاسِ وَالتَّثَاؤُبِ — الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٧٣٣
وَعَنْ أَنَسٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ قَالَ: عَطَسَ رَجُلَانِ عِنْدَ النَّبِيِّ ﷺ فَشَمَّتَ أَحَدَهُمَا وَلَمْ يُشَمِّتِ الْآخَرَ، فَقَالَ الرَّجُلُ: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ! شَمَّتَّ هَذَا وَلَمْ تُشَمِّتْنِي، قَالَ: «إِنَّ هَذَا حَمِدَ اللَّهَ وَلَمْ تَحْمَدِ اللَّهَ». مُتَّفَقٌ عَلَيْهِ.
Narrated by Anas (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Muttafaq ʿAlayh
Translation
Two men sneezed near the Prophet (S.A.W.). He responded to one of them (shammata) and not the other. The [other] man said, "O Messenger of Allah, you responded to this one and not to me!" He said, "This one praised Allah, and you did not praise Allah."
Class Notes
  • Gangohi: this shows that the تَشْمِيت of the sneezer (تَشْمِيتُ الْعَاطِس) is only وَاجِب if the sneezer (عَاطِس) says «الْحَمْدُ لِلَّهِ».
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • شَمَّتَ— to say «يَرْحَمُكَ اللَّهُ» to the sneezer (التَّشْمِيت).
Cross-ref: Muttafaq ʿAlayh. Verified in Mirqat (الفصل الأول — Shamela 8176, page-id 6532, printed ٤٧٣٤). Lamʿāt not yet checked.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ الْعُطَاسِ وَالتَّثَاؤُبِ — الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٧٣٤
وَعَنْ أَبِي مُوسَى رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ قَالَ: سَمِعْتُ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ ﷺ يَقُولُ: «إِذَا عَطَسَ أَحَدُكُمْ فَحَمِدَ اللَّهَ فَشَمِّتُوهُ، وَإِنْ لَمْ يَحْمَدِ اللَّهَ فَلَا تُشَمِّتُوهُ». رَوَاهُ مُسْلِمٌ.
Narrated by Abū Mūsā (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Muslim
Translation
"When one of you sneezes and praises Allah, respond to him («شَمِّتُوهُ»); but if he does not praise Allah, do not respond to him."
Class Notes
  • What is the ruling on the تَشْمِيت of the sneezer if he does not say «الْحَمْدُ لِلَّهِ»?
  • Ibn Ḥajar: the جُمْهُور hold that this نَهْي (not responding) is for تَنْزِيه (i.e. it is better left, not strictly forbidden).
  • Ibn ʿĀbidīn: the reason تَشْمِيت is only deserved by the عَاطِس who says «الْحَمْدُ لِلَّهِ» is that a sneeze is a نِعْمَة (blessing); so when a person commits كُفْرَان (ingratitude) of the نِعْمَة by not praising Allah, he does not deserve this دُعَاء.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • فَشَمِّتُوهُ— respond to him with «يَرْحَمُكَ اللَّهُ».
Cross-ref: Muslim. Verified in Mirqat (الفصل الأول — Shamela 8176, page-id 6533, printed ٤٧٣٥). Lamʿāt not yet checked.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ الْعُطَاسِ وَالتَّثَاؤُبِ — الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٧٣٥
وَعَنْ سَلَمَةَ بْنِ الْأَكْوَعِ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ أَنَّهُ سَمِعَ النَّبِيَّ ﷺ وَعَطَسَ رَجُلٌ عِنْدَهُ، فَقَالَ لَهُ: «يَرْحَمُكَ اللَّهُ»، ثُمَّ عَطَسَ أُخْرَى، فَقَالَ: «الرَّجُلُ مَزْكُومٌ». رَوَاهُ مُسْلِمٌ، وَفِي رِوَايَةٍ لِلتِّرْمِذِيِّ أَنَّهُ قَالَ لَهُ فِي الثَّالِثَةِ: «إِنَّهُ مَزْكُومٌ».
Narrated by Salamah ibn al-Akwaʿ (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Muslim (+ Tirmidhī variant)
Translation
He heard the Prophet (S.A.W.) — a man sneezed near him, so he said to him, «يَرْحَمُكَ اللَّهُ». Then the man sneezed again, so he said, "The man has a cold (مَزْكُوم)." In a narration of Tirmidhī, he said to him at the third sneeze: "He has a cold."
Class Notes
  • «الرَّجُلُ مَزْكُومٌ» — is there really no need to repeat the تَشْمِيت (response to a sneeze), given that when the عُطَاس is from sickness, isn't he more in need of دُعَاء [rather than less]?
  • We say: yes — but one should make دُعَاء for him with a دُعَاء suited to a sick person, not the دُعَاء said for an ordinary sneezer.
  • Gangohi: the real عِلَّة (governing reason) for whether تَشْمِيت is done at all is زُكَام (sickness) versus its absence — so if one knows from the very first sneeze that it is caused by sickness, تَشْمِيت would not be required from the start. But this specific point is not stated in any of the أَحَادِيث, nor mentioned by the other شُرُوح.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • مَزْكُومٌ— afflicted with زُكَام (a head-cold); per Tirmidhī's wording «أَنْتَ مَزْكُومٌ» — Nawawi: meaning you are not among those who deserve تَشْمِيت after this [third sneeze].
Cross-ref: Muslim; Tirmidhī variant («أَنْتَ مَزْكُومٌ» at the third sneeze). Verified in Mirqat (بَابُ الْعُطَاسِ وَالتَّثَاؤُبِ، الفصل الأول — Shamela 8176, page-id 6534, printed ٤٧٣٦). Lamʿāt not yet checked.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ الْعُطَاسِ وَالتَّثَاؤُبِ — الفصل الثاني
حديث ٤٧٣٧
عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ ﷺ كَانَ إِذَا عَطَسَ غَطَّى وَجْهَهُ بِيَدِهِ أَوْ ثَوْبِهِ، وَغَضَّ بِهَا صَوْتَهُ. رَوَاهُ التِّرْمِذِيُّ، وَأَبُو دَاوُدَ. وَقَالَ التِّرْمِذِيُّ: هَذَا حَدِيثٌ حَسَنٌ صَحِيحٌ.
Narrated by Abū Hurayrah (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Tirmidhī / Abū Dāwūd, حَسَن صَحِيح
Translation
The Prophet (S.A.W.), when he sneezed, would cover his face with his hand or his garment, and lower his voice with it.
Class Notes
  • Mirqat: the reason one should cover the mouth [face] when sneezing is so that nobody sees his disfigured face (تَشْوِيه), and so that a person's discharge doesn't land on anyone.
  • Ibn Ḥajar: when a person sneezes, he should not twist his neck to the left or right, lest he be harmed by that.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • غَطَّى وَجْهَهُ— he covered his face — so that no تَشْوِيه of the face nor discharge of the brain would be seen; Ṭūrbishtī: this is a form of أَدَب between companions, since the sneezer cannot guarantee avoiding what onlookers dislike.
  • غَضَّ بِهَا صَوْتَهُ— he lowered his voice with it, i.e. he did not raise it with a loud cry.
Cross-ref: Tirmidhī / Abū Dāwūd, حَسَن صَحِيح (al-Ḥākim also narrates it). Verified in Mirqat (بَابُ الْعُطَاسِ وَالتَّثَاؤُبِ، الفصل الثاني — Shamela 8176, page-id 6537, printed ٤٧٣٨). Lamʿāt not yet checked.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ الْعُطَاسِ وَالتَّثَاؤُبِ — الفصل الثاني
حديث ٤٧٣٩
وَعَنْ أَبِي مُوسَى رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ قَالَ: كَانَ الْيَهُودُ يَتَعَاطَسُونَ عِنْدَ النَّبِيِّ ﷺ يَرْجُونَ أَنْ يَقُولَ لَهُمْ: يَرْحَمُكُمُ اللَّهُ، فَيَقُولُ: «يَهْدِيكُمُ اللَّهُ وَيُصْلِحُ بَالَكُمْ». رَوَاهُ التِّرْمِذِيُّ، وَأَبُو دَاوُدَ.
Narrated by Abū Mūsā al-Ashʿarī (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Tirmidhī / Abū Dāwūd
Translation
The Jews used to sneeze deliberately in front of the Prophet (S.A.W.), hoping he would say to them, «يَرْحَمُكُمُ اللَّهُ». But he would say: «يَهْدِيكُمُ اللَّهُ وَيُصْلِحُ بَالَكُمْ» (May Allah guide you and set your condition right).
Class Notes
  • He (S.A.W.) would not say «يَرْحَمُكُمُ اللَّهُ» to them, because رَحْمَة is خَاصّ (exclusive) to believers; so instead he made a دُعَاء for them which is suitable for them.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • يَتَعَاطَسُونَ— they would deliberately induce sneezing from themselves, hoping for the Prophet's ﷺ دُعَاء of رَحْمَة.
  • يَهْدِيكُمُ اللَّهُ وَيُصْلِحُ بَالَكُمْ— "may Allah guide you and set your بَال (heart/condition) right" — he did not say «يَرْحَمُكُمُ اللَّهُ» to them because رَحْمَة is exclusive to the believers; rather he supplicated with what would rectify their state — هِدَايَة and تَوْفِيق to إِيمَان.
Cross-ref: Tirmidhī / Abū Dāwūd. Verified in Mirqat (بَابُ الْعُطَاسِ وَالتَّثَاؤُبِ، الفصل الثاني — Shamela 8176, page-id 6540, printed ٤٧٤٠). Lamʿāt not yet checked.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ الْعُطَاسِ وَالتَّثَاؤُبِ — الفصل الثاني
حديث ٤٧٤٠
وَعَنْ هِلَالِ بْنِ يَسَافٍ قَالَ: كُنَّا مَعَ سَالِمِ بْنِ عُبَيْدٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ، فَعَطَسَ رَجُلٌ مِنَ الْقَوْمِ فَقَالَ: السَّلَامُ عَلَيْكُمْ، فَقَالَ لَهُ سَالِمٌ: وَعَلَيْكَ وَعَلَى أُمِّكَ. فَكَأَنَّ الرَّجُلَ وَجَدَ فِي نَفْسِهِ، فَقَالَ: أَمَا إِنِّي لَمْ أَقُلْ إِلَّا مَا قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ، إِذْ عَطَسَ رَجُلٌ عِنْدَ النَّبِيِّ ﷺ فَقَالَ: السَّلَامُ عَلَيْكُمْ، فَقَالَ النَّبِيُّ ﷺ: «عَلَيْكَ وَعَلَى أُمِّكَ، إِذَا عَطَسَ أَحَدُكُمْ فَلْيَقُلِ: الْحَمْدُ لِلَّهِ رَبِّ الْعَالَمِينَ، وَلْيَقُلْ لَهُ مَنْ يَرُدُّ عَلَيْهِ: يَرْحَمُكَ اللَّهُ، وَلْيَقُلْ: يَغْفِرُ اللَّهُ لِي وَلَكُمْ». رَوَاهُ التِّرْمِذِيُّ، وَأَبُو دَاوُدَ.
Narrated by Sālim ibn ʿUbayd (R.A.) — via Hilāl ibn Yisāf  ·  Riwayah: Tirmidhī / Abū Dāwūd
Translation
We were with Sālim ibn ʿUbayd (R.A.) when a man among the people sneezed and said, «السَّلَامُ عَلَيْكُمْ». Sālim said to him, «وَعَلَيْكَ وَعَلَى أُمِّكَ» (and upon you and your mother). The man seemed to take offense at this, so Sālim said: "I said nothing but what the Messenger of Allah (S.A.W.) said — a man sneezed in front of the Prophet (S.A.W.) and said, «السَّلَامُ عَلَيْكُمْ», so the Prophet (S.A.W.) said: «عَلَيْكَ وَعَلَى أُمِّكَ» — when one of you sneezes, let him say: «الْحَمْدُ لِلَّهِ رَبِّ الْعَالَمِينَ»; and let the one who responds to him say: «يَرْحَمُكَ اللَّهُ»; and let him [the sneezer] say: «يَغْفِرُ اللَّهُ لِي وَلَكُمْ»."
Class Notes
  • Some عُلَمَاء prefer «يَغْفِرُ اللَّهُ لِي وَلَكُمْ», but the عَمَل of the سَلَف is to do «يَهْدِيكُمُ اللَّهُ وَيُصْلِحُ بَالَكُمْ» [al-Qārī himself notes the preferred view is to combine both].
  • Why does he (S.A.W.) say «عَلَيْكَ وَعَلَى أُمِّكَ»? Ibn al-Qayyim: to indicate that your سَلَام was not in its proper place.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • وَجَدَ فِي نَفْسِهِ— he felt [displeasure] within himself — either غَضَب (anger) or حُزْن (grief), concealed rather than shown.
  • عَلَيْكَ وَعَلَى أُمِّكَ— "and upon you and your mother" — Ṭūrbishtī: a reproach (تَنْبِيه) at the man's own foolishness and that of his mother, i.e. a rebuke for the misplaced greeting, not a literal return of سَلَام; al-Qārī: rather intended as زَجْر (a deterrent rebuke), since his سَلَام fell outside the correct place.
Cross-ref: Tirmidhī / Abū Dāwūd. Verified in Mirqat (بَابُ الْعُطَاسِ وَالتَّثَاؤُبِ، الفصل الثاني — Shamela 8176, page-id 6541–6542, printed ٤٧٤١). Ibn al-Qayyim's point (per class) parallels al-Qārī's own «قُلْت» comment in Mirqat almost verbatim — an independent Ibn al-Qayyim citation was not located this session. Lamʿāt not yet checked.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ الضَّحِكِ — الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٧٤٤
عَنْ عَائِشَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهَا قَالَتْ: مَا رَأَيْتُ النَّبِيَّ ﷺ مُسْتَجْمِعًا ضَاحِكًا حَتَّى أَرَى مِنْهُ لَهَوَاتِهِ، إِنَّمَا كَانَ يَبْتَسِمُ. رَوَاهُ الْبُخَارِيُّ.
Narrated by ʿĀʾishah (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Bukhārī
Translation
I never saw the Prophet (S.A.W.) laughing fully (مُسْتَجْمِعًا) to the point that I could see his لَهَوَات [uvula] — he would only smile.
Class Notes
  • I.e. usually he (S.A.W.) would smile; sometimes he would laugh; but his laughter would never reach this level.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • مُسْتَجْمِعًا ضَاحِكًا— laughing fully, wholly given over to it (not a partial or restrained laugh).
  • لَهَوَاتِهِ— his لَهَوَات (sing. لَهَاة) — the piece of flesh hanging at the back of the throat (uvula).
  • يَبْتَسِمُ— he would smile — a lighter degree of ضَحِك, without sound.
Cross-ref: Bukhārī. Verified in Mirqat (بَابُ الضَّحِكِ، الفصل الأول — Shamela 8176, page-id 6548, printed ٤٧٤٥). Lamʿāt not yet checked.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ الضَّحِكِ — الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٧٤٥
وَعَنْ جَرِيرٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ قَالَ: مَا حَجَبَنِي النَّبِيُّ ﷺ مُنْذُ أَسْلَمْتُ، وَلَا رَآنِي إِلَّا تَبَسَّمَ. مُتَّفَقٌ عَلَيْهِ.
Narrated by Jarīr ibn ʿAbdillāh al-Bajalī (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Muttafaq ʿAlayh
Translation
The Prophet (S.A.W.) never turned me away since I accepted Islam, and he never saw me except that he smiled.
Class Notes
  • He (Jarīr, R.A.) accepted Islam 40 days before Rasulullah (S.A.W.) passed away.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • حَجَبَنِي— he turned me away / withheld access from me — i.e. I never needed to seek إِذْن (permission) to see him.
  • تَبَسَّمَ— he smiled — ʿUmar (R.A.) said: "Jarīr is the Yūsuf of this أُمَّة" (on account of his handsomeness).
Cross-ref: Muttafaq ʿAlayh. Verified in Mirqat (بَابُ الضَّحِكِ، الفصل الأول — Shamela 8176, page-id 6549, printed ٤٧٤٦). Lamʿāt not yet checked.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ الْأَسَامِي — الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٧٥٠
وَعَنْ جَابِرٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ ﷺ قَالَ: «سَمُّوا بِاسْمِي وَلَا تَكْتَنُوا بِكُنْيَتِي، فَإِنِّي إِنَّمَا جُعِلْتُ قَاسِمًا أَقْسِمُ بَيْنَكُمْ». مُتَّفَقٌ عَلَيْهِ.
Narrated by Jābir ibn ʿAbdillāh (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Muttafaq ʿAlayh
Translation
"Name yourselves with my name, but do not take my كُنْيَة; for I have been made a قَاسِم (distributor) — I distribute among you."
Class Notes
  • Some state that this نَهْي (prohibition of the كُنْيَة «أَبُو الْقَاسِم») was only for the time of Rasulullah (S.A.W.), because it would lead to الْتِبَاس (confusion). As for after his death, others can be given the كُنْيَة of Rasulullah (S.A.W.). This is the opinion of Mālik; Qāḍī ʿIyāḍ states that the جُمْهُور of the سَلَف take this opinion.
  • Some say this نَهْي is عَامّ (general) for all times — this is the position of al-Shāfiʿī and the Ẓāhiriyyah.
  • Some say the نَهْي is only for one who already has the same name as Muhammad (S.A.W.). دَلِيل: hadith 4768 / hadith 4769.
  • Some say the نَهْي is تَنْزِيهِي, not تَحْرِيمِي — this is the مَذْهَب of Jarīr.
  • Ṭaḥāwī: النَّهْيُ فِي الِابْتِدَاءِ لِمَنْ سَمَّى بِاسْمِ مُحَمَّدٍ ثُمَّ صَارَ النَّهْيُ عَامًّا (the prohibition was at first for one named Muhammad, then it became general).
  • Ibn al-Qayyim: الصَّوَابُ أَنَّ التَّسْمِيَةَ بِاسْمِهِ جَائِزٌ وَالتَّكَنِّي بِكُنْيَتِهِ مَمْنُوعٌ وَهُوَ أَشَدُّ فِي مُدَّةِ حَيَاتِهِ (the correct view is that naming with his name is permissible, but taking his كُنْيَة is prohibited — and this is more severe during his lifetime).
  • The reason using his name is permissible while using his كُنْيَة isn't is explained by Mufti Taqi: Rasulullah (S.A.W.) was never [commonly] called by his name — the Muslims would call him "Rasulullah" while the كُفَّار would call him "Abū al-Qāsim" — so saying "Muhammad" would cause no confusion.
  • [Objection] This ḥadīth, ظَاهِرًا (apparently), is a proof against Mālik's opinion, because the عِلَّة (governing reason) mentioned here is not الْتِبَاس but something else — namely, his being قَاسِمٌ بِالْفِعْل (an actual distributor) — and this عِلَّة still applies even after his death. But Mufti Taqi responds: when one says «أَبُو الْقَاسِم», nobody thinks of the meaning قَاسِمٌ بِالْفِعْل.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • قَاسِمًا— a distributor: Allah made him a قَاسِم distributing knowledge, the spoils, and the like among the people; or the one distributing glad-tidings for the righteous and warning for the wicked.
  • لَا تَكْتَنُوا بِكُنْيَتِي— do not take my كُنْيَة — because the كُنْيَة is a matter of تَعْظِيم (honour) and تَوْقِير, unlike the bare name; so he prohibited it lest الْتِبَاس (confusion) occur when people are called out to.
Cross-ref: Muttafaq ʿAlayh. Mirqat (بَابُ الْأَسَامِي، الفصل الأول — Shamela 8176, page-id 6555–6556, printed ٤٧٥١) records six scholarly positions on the scope of this نهي (via al-Ṭībī, with al-Qārī's own «قُلْت» responses throughout); the Mālik/Qāḍī-ʿIyāḍ, Shāfiʿī/Ẓāhirī, and Jarīr (تَنْزِيهِي) positions above match it directly — the class's "Qadhi Khan" appears to be Qāḍī ʿIyāḍ per Mirqat's actual wording, corrected here. The Ṭaḥāwī quotation, Ibn al-Qayyim's ruling, and the Mufti Taqi قَاسِمٌ بِالْفِعْل exchange were not independently located in this Mirqat page — flagged for verification. Lamʿāt not yet checked.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ الْأَسَامِي — الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٧٥١
وَعَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ: «إِنَّ أَحَبَّ أَسْمَائِكُمْ إِلَى اللَّهِ: عَبْدُ اللَّهِ وَعَبْدُ الرَّحْمَنِ». رَوَاهُ مُسْلِمٌ.
Narrated by Ibn ʿUmar (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Muslim
Translation
"Indeed the most beloved of your names to Allah are ʿAbdullāh and ʿAbdur-Raḥmān."
Class Notes
  • Qurṭubī: other similar names will be attached to these two by قِيَاس (analogy) — like «عَبْدُ الرَّحِيم».
  • The reason he (S.A.W.) specified these two names [Allāh and al-Raḥmān] is that in the Qurʾān the word «عَبْد» (servant) was never attributed to any [divine name] besides these two.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • إِذَا سَمَّيْتُمْ فَعَبِّدُوا— "when you name, then attribute servitude [to a name of Allah]" — a مَرْفُوع narration (al-Ḥākim in al-Kunā, al-Ṭabarānī, from Abū Zuhayr al-Thaqafī) meaning: attach the عُبُودِيَّة to Allah's names, which includes «عَبْدُ الرَّحِيم», «عَبْدُ الْمَلِك», and others; but not permissible are names like «عَبْدُ الْحَارِث» or «عَبْدُ النَّبِيّ» — and no weight is given to what has become common among people in violation of this.
Cross-ref: Muslim. Verified in Mirqat (بَابُ الْأَسَامِي، الفصل الأول — Shamela 8176, page-id 6557, printed ٤٧٥٢): al-Qārī cites «إِذَا سَمَّيْتُمْ فَعَبِّدُوا» (al-Ḥākim/al-Ṭabarānī) as the basis for extending to names like «عَبْدُ الرَّحِيم» — matches the class's Qurṭubī note. The specific Qurṭubī citation that «عَبْد» is attributed only to these two divine names in the Qurʾān was not independently located in this Mirqat page — flagged. Lamʿāt not yet checked.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ الْأَسَامِي — الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٧٥٣
وَعَنْ جَابِرٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ قَالَ: أَرَادَ النَّبِيُّ ﷺ أَنْ يَنْهَى عَنْ أَنْ يُسَمَّى بِيَعْلَى وَبِبَرَكَةَ وَبِأَفْلَحَ وَبِيَسَارٍ وَبِنَافِعٍ وَبِنَحْوِ ذَلِكَ، ثُمَّ سَكَتَ بَعْدُ عَنْهَا، ثُمَّ قُبِضَ وَلَمْ يَنْهَ عَنْ ذَلِكَ. رَوَاهُ مُسْلِمٌ.
Narrated by Jābir ibn ʿAbdillāh (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Muslim
Translation
"The Prophet (S.A.W.) intended to prohibit naming with Yaʿlā, Barakah, Aflaḥ, Yasār, Nāfiʿ, and the like. Then afterward he remained silent about it, then he passed away without [explicitly] prohibiting that."
Class Notes
  • Some people use this ḥadīth to argue for the نَسْخ (abrogation) of the previous ḥadīth [Samurah's explicit prohibition of these names].
  • But the مُحَقِّقُون say that the previous ḥadīth is for تَنْزِيه, and the مُرَاد of the نَهْي in this ḥadīth [the one he intended but withheld] is تَحْرِيم — i.e. he wanted to also give a نَهْي تَحْرِيمِي, but he did not; he only gave a نَهْي تَنْزِيهِي.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • يَعْلَى— present-tense of عَلِيَ (to be elevated/exalted in honour) — i.e. "he will rise, be exalted".
  • سَكَتَ بَعْدُ عَنْهَا— he fell silent about them afterward — i.e. without stating either an explicit نَهْي or an explicit جَوَاز.
Cross-ref: Muslim. Verified in Mirqat (بَابُ الْأَسَامِي، الفصل الأول — Shamela 8176, page-id 6559, printed ٤٧٥٤). Al-Qārī's own «قُلْت» matches the class note in substance: «أَرَادَ أَنْ يَنْهَى نَهْيَ تَحْرِيمٍ، ثُمَّ سَكَتَ بَعْدَ ذَلِكَ رَحْمَةً عَلَى الْأُمَّةِ... فَالنَّهْيُ الْمَنْفِيُّ مَحْمُولٌ عَلَى التَّحْرِيمِ، وَالْمُثْبَتُ عَلَى التَّنْزِيهِ» (the withheld/intended prohibition is carried on تَحْرِيم, while the one actually established is carried on تَنْزِيه). "The previous ḥadīth" referenced in the notes is Samurah's «لَا تُسَمِّيَنَّ غُلَامَكَ يَسَارًا...» (Mirqat ٤٧٥٣, page-id 6558) — not yet built as its own entry. Lamʿāt not yet checked.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ الْأَسَامِي — الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٧٥٧
وَعَنِ ابْنِ عُمَرَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا أَنَّ بِنْتًا كَانَتْ لِعُمَرَ يُقَالُ لَهَا عَاصِيَةُ، فَسَمَّاهَا رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ جَمِيلَةً. رَوَاهُ مُسْلِمٌ.
Narrated by Ibn ʿUmar (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Muslim
Translation
ʿUmar had a daughter called ʿĀṣiyah (the disobedient one); the Messenger of Allah (S.A.W.) renamed her Jamīlah (the beautiful/good one).
Class Notes
  • Mufti Taqi: the summary of this بَاب is that there are three types of names which Rasulullah (S.A.W.) disliked: (1) names with a bad meaning, like «عَاصِيَة» [this ḥadīth]; (2) names carrying the chance of تِيَرَة (bad omen), like «يَسَار», even though تِيَرَة itself is حَرَام; (3) names carrying تَزْكِيَةُ النَّفْس (self-praise/self-purification), like «بَرَّة».
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • عَاصِيَة— Ṭūrbishtī: she was named this in the جَاهِلِيَّة, when they used to name with «الْعَاص»/«الْعَاصِيَة» meaning refusal to accept humiliation and unwillingness to accept being wronged — not necessarily from عِصْيَان (disobedience) itself; when Islam came, this [association] was disliked for her.
  • جَمِيلَة— al-Qārī: the apparent meaning here is "the good one" (الْحَسَنَة), not [only] "the one who has physical beauty" — since he did not rename her «مُطِيعَة» (the direct opposite of ʿĀṣiyah) out of fear of تَزْكِيَة (self-praise).
Cross-ref: Muslim. Verified in Mirqat (بَابُ الْأَسَامِي، الفصل الأول — Shamela 8176, page-id 6565, printed ٤٧٥٨): confirms Nawawī's point that this shows اسْتِحْبَاب of changing an ugly/disliked name to a good one. Mufti Taqi's 3-fold summary is a class synthesis of the whole بَاب (not itself in Mirqat) — the يسار example = Samurah's ḥadīth (Mirqat ٤٧٥٣, not yet built); the برة example belongs to a later ḥadīth in this بَاب (Zaynab bint Abī Salamah, Mirqat ٤٧٥٦) not yet built. Lamʿāt not yet checked.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ الْأَسَامِي — الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٧٥٨
وَعَنْ سَهْلِ بْنِ سَعْدٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ قَالَ: أُتِيَ بِالْمُنْذِرِ بْنِ أَبِي أُسَيْدٍ إِلَى النَّبِيِّ ﷺ حِينَ وُلِدَ، فَوَضَعَهُ عَلَى فَخِذِهِ، فَقَالَ: «مَا اسْمُهُ؟» قَالَ: فُلَانٌ. قَالَ: «لَا، لَكِنِ اسْمُهُ الْمُنْذِرُ». مُتَّفَقٌ عَلَيْهِ.
Narrated by Sahl ibn Saʿd (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Muttafaq ʿAlayh
Translation
"Al-Mundhir ibn Abī Usayd was brought to the Prophet (S.A.W.) when he was born; he placed him on his thigh and said, 'What is his name?' [The father] said, 'Fulān (so-and-so).' He said, 'No — rather his name is al-Mundhir.'"
Class Notes
  • Ṭībī: perhaps he (S.A.W.) did تَفَاؤُل (took a good omen) through this name, that he would become a فَقِيه, because of the آيَة: «لِيَتَفَقَّهُوا فِي الدِّينِ وَلِيُنْذِرُوا قَوْمَهُمْ» [al-Tawbah 9:122].
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • الْمُنْذِر— "the warner" — Ṭībī: perhaps he (S.A.W.) intended تَفَاؤُل with this name, hinting at the meaning of تَفَقُّه (deep understanding of the religion) in the آيَة «لِيَتَفَقَّهُوا فِي الدِّينِ وَلِيُنْذِرُوا قَوْمَهُمْ» — "that they may gain understanding in the religion and warn their people" (al-Tawbah 9:122).
Cross-ref: Muttafaq ʿAlayh. Verified in Mirqat (بَابُ الْأَسَامِي، الفصل الأول — Shamela 8176, page-id 6566, printed ٤٧٥٩): the Ṭībī / آيَة 9:122 تَفَاؤُل note is exactly as recorded in Mirqat. Lamʿāt not yet checked.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ الْأَسَامِي — الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٧٦٤
وَعَنْ عَائِشَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهَا قَالَتْ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ: «لَا يَقُولَنَّ أَحَدُكُمْ: خَبُثَتْ نَفْسِي، وَلَكِنْ لِيَقُلْ: لَقِسَتْ نَفْسِي». مُتَّفَقٌ عَلَيْهِ.
Narrated by ʿĀʾishah (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Muttafaq ʿAlayh (Bukhārī 6179/6180, Muslim 2250)
Translation
"None of you should say, 'My self has become foul (خَبُثَتْ)' — rather let him say, 'My self felt nauseous (لَقِسَتْ).'"
Class Notes
  • لَقَس in لُغَة (lexicon) is when a person is full [of food] and feels nauseous.
  • But in usage (اِسْتِعْمَال), لَقَس and خُبْث carry the same core meaning [nausea]; however خُبْث has a more عَامّ (general) meaning and is more قَبِيح (repugnant) than لَقَس, and it carries other قَبِيح meanings which this word [لَقَس] does not have.
  • So Rasulullah (S.A.W.) told them to say لَقَس as an encouragement to speak with طَيِّب (wholesome) speech.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • لَقِسَتْ نَفْسِي— "my self felt nauseous" — from اللَّقْس (nausea, غَثَيَان) per al-Nihāya; Ibn Ḥajar (quoting Ibn Abī Jamrah, Fatḥ al-Bārī): both خُبْث and لَقْس convey the intended meaning, but لَفْظ الْخُبْث is قَبِيح and gathers additional matters beyond what's intended, whereas اللَّقْس is specific to اِمْتِلَاءُ الْمَعِدَة (the stomach being full).
  • خَبُثَتْ— al-Rāghib al-Iṣfahānī: خُبْث is applied to الْبَاطِل (falsehood) in belief, الْكَذِب (lying) in speech, and الْقَبِيح in dealings/actions — a broader, uglier range of meaning than لَقَس.
Cross-ref: Muttafaq ʿAlayh (Bukhārī 6179/6180, Muslim 2250). Verified in Mirqat (بَابُ الْأَسَامِي، الفصل الأول — Shamela 8176, page-id 6573, printed ٤٧٦٥) and Lamʿāt (Shamela 145212, page-id 4534, hadith #16): both confirm لَقِسَتْ = غَثَيَان per al-Qāmūs/al-Nihāya, and that خُبْث was disliked for its قُبْح so a Muslim doesn't attribute a worse fault to himself. Fatḥ al-Bārī (كتاب الأدب، بَابُ لَا يَقُلْ خَبُثَتْ نَفْسِي — Shamela 1673, page-id 6324–6325) gives the fullest match for the class's exact point, quoting Ibn Abī Jamrah nearly verbatim (see meanings above) — the strongest cross-reference found for this hadith. Mirʾāt not accessible this session (Shamela book 8862 stops mid-Ḥajj at page 4545; Kitāb al-Ādāb isn't digitized in this edition). Badhl al-Majhūd/Kawkab al-Durrī not applicable (not Abū Dāwūd/Tirmidhī-sourced).
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ الْأَسَامِي — الفصل الثاني
حديث ٤٧٧٠
وَعَنْ عَائِشَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهَا أَنَّ امْرَأَةً قَالَتْ: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ! إِنِّي وَلَدْتُ غُلَامًا فَسَمَّيْتُهُ مُحَمَّدًا، وَكَنَّيْتُهُ أَبَا الْقَاسِمِ، فَذُكِرَ لِي أَنَّكَ تَكْرَهُ ذَلِكَ. فَقَالَ: «مَا الَّذِي أَحَلَّ اسْمِي وَحَرَّمَ كُنْيَتِي؟ أَوْ مَا الَّذِي حَرَّمَ كُنْيَتِي وَأَحَلَّ اسْمِي؟». رَوَاهُ أَبُو دَاوُدَ، وَقَالَ مُحْيِي السُّنَّةِ: غَرِيبٌ.
Narrated by ʿĀʾishah (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Abū Dāwūd (4967/4968), غَرِيب per Muḥyī al-Sunnah [al-Baghawī]
Translation
A woman said: "O Messenger of Allah, I gave birth to a boy — I named him Muhammad and gave him the كُنْيَة Abū al-Qāsim; I was told you dislike that." He said: "What is it that made my name permissible and my كُنْيَة prohibited? Or: what is it that made my كُنْيَة prohibited and my name permissible?"
Class Notes
  • This ḥadīth, ظَاهِرًا (apparently), allows جَمْع (combining) between his name and كُنْيَة.
  • If this ḥadīth is ثَابِت (established), it would show that the نَهْي from combining his name and كُنْيَة is for تَنْزِيه, not تَحْرِيم.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • أَحَلَّ / حَرَّمَ— "made permissible" / "made prohibited" — al-Qārī: this is an اِسْتِفْهَام إِنْكَارِيّ (a rhetorical question of rebuke), and it contains تَصْرِيح (an explicit statement) that the نَهْي about combining [name+كُنْيَة] is not for تَحْرِيم but for تَنْزِيه.
Cross-ref: Abū Dāwūd, graded غَرِيب by al-Baghawī. Verified in Mirqat (بَابُ الْأَسَامِي، الفصل الثاني — Shamela 8176, page-id 6581, printed ٤٧٧١): al-Qārī's own comment states verbatim «فِيهِ تَصْرِيحٌ عَلَى أَنَّ النَّهْيَ عَنِ الْجَمْعِ لَيْسَ لِلتَّحْرِيمِ بَلْ لِلتَّنْزِيهِ» — a direct match for the class note. Confirmed in Lamʿāt (Shamela 145212, page-id 4537, hadith #22), which gives the identical matn without additional discussion beyond confirming the context. Fatḥ al-Bārī not applicable (not Bukhārī-sourced); Mirʾāt not accessible (stops before Kitāb al-Ādāb); Badhl al-Majhūd (Abū Dāwūd شَرْح) not reached this session — flagged for a future session.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ الْأَسَامِي — الفصل الثاني
حديث ٤٧٧٦
وَعَنْ أَبِي مَسْعُودٍ الْأَنْصَارِيِّ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ قَالَ لِأَبِي عَبْدِ اللَّهِ — أَوْ قَالَ أَبُو عَبْدِ اللَّهِ لِأَبِي مَسْعُودٍ —: مَا سَمِعْتَ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ ﷺ يَقُولُ فِي «زَعَمُوا»؟ قَالَ: سَمِعْتُ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ ﷺ يَقُولُ: «بِئْسَ مَطِيَّةُ الرَّجُلِ». رَوَاهُ أَبُو دَاوُدَ، وَقَالَ: إِنَّ أَبَا عَبْدِ اللَّهِ حُذَيْفَةُ.
Narrated by Abū Masʿūd al-Anṣārī (R.A.) & Ḥudhayfah (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Abū Dāwūd
Translation
Abū Masʿūd al-Anṣārī said to Abū ʿAbdillāh — or Abū ʿAbdillāh said to Abū Masʿūd — "What did you hear the Messenger of Allah (S.A.W.) say about «زَعَمُوا» (they claim)?" He said: "I heard the Messenger of Allah (S.A.W.) say: «بِئْسَ مَطِيَّةُ الرَّجُلِ» (what a poor mount for a man)."
Class Notes
  • Some say that the مُنَاسَبَة (connection) of this ḥadīth to the chapter is that the chapter discusses تَغْيِيرُ الْأَسَامِي (changing of names), and this ḥadīth discusses تَغْيِيرُ الْكَلَام (changing/discouraging a disliked form of speech).
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • بِئْسَ مَطِيَّةُ الرَّجُلِ— "what a poor mount for a man" — i.e. the phrase «زَعَمُوا» is a poor vehicle a speaker leans on to convey unverified reports (الزَّعْم = claiming without تَحْقِيق or يَقِين); al-Qārī: it should either be verified and attributed to its actual sayer, or one should stay silent, as in «مَنْ كَانَ يُؤْمِنُ بِاللَّهِ وَالْيَوْمِ الْآخِرِ فَلْيَقُلْ خَيْرًا أَوْ لِيَصْمُتْ».
Cross-ref: Abū Dāwūd. Verified in Mirqat (بَابُ الْأَسَامِي، الفصل الثاني — Shamela 8176, page-id 6588–6589, printed ٤٧٧٧): al-Qārī's own comment states verbatim «وَلَعَلَّ وَجْهَ مُنَاسَبَةِ إِيرَادِ هَذَا الْحَدِيثِ لِلْبَابِ مُجَرَّدُ التَّغْيِيرِ لِلْأَمْرِ الْمَذْمُومِ أَعَمُّ مِنْ أَنْ يَكُونَ اسْمًا أَوْ غَيْرَهُ» — an exact match for the class's مُنَاسَبَة point. Lamʿāt (Shamela 145212, page-id 4541, hadith #28) confirms the matn and adds lexical detail (زَعَمَ per al-Nihāya/al-Ṣurāḥ/al-Qāmūs) but doesn't carry the مُنَاسَبَة point itself. Fatḥ al-Bārī (Shamela 1673, page-id 6312) shows Bukhārī himself created a bare, ḥadīth-less بَاب titled «مَا جَاءَ فِي زَعَمُوا» in the same spot — Ibn Ḥajar notes he was likely alluding to this very report without including its إِسْنَاد, confirming this theme's placement is a known cross-commentary pattern. Mirʾāt not accessible; Badhl al-Majhūd not reached this session — flagged.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ الْبَيَانِ وَالشِّعْرِ — الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٧٨٤
وَعَنِ ابْنِ مَسْعُودٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ: «هَلَكَ الْمُتَنَطِّعُونَ» قَالَهَا ثَلَاثًا. رَوَاهُ مُسْلِمٌ.
Narrated by Ibn Masʿūd (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Muslim
Translation
"Destroyed are الْمُتَنَطِّعُونَ (those who go to extremes/exaggerate in speech)" — he said it three times.
Class Notes
  • The difference between اِحْتِيَاط (caution) and غُلُوّ (extremism) is that refraining from شُبُهَات قَرِيبَة (doubtful matters that are near/likely) is اِحْتِيَاط, while being overly concerned with شُبُهَات بَعِيدَة (doubtful matters that are remote/unlikely) is غُلُوّ.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • الْمُتَنَطِّعُونَ— those who go to extremes/overreach — Ṭūrbishtī (per Mirqat) / al-Ṭībī (per Lamʿāt): meant by it are الْمُتَعَمِّقُونَ الْغَالُونَ (those who delve deep, going to extremes) in their preoccupation with speech that doesn't concern them; from النَّطْع, the roof of the mouth, since such a person speaks in an affected manner from the depths of his palate.
Cross-ref: Muslim. Verified in Mirqat (بَابُ الْبَيَانِ وَالشِّعْرِ، الفصل الأول — Shamela 8176, page-id 6600, printed ٤٧٨٥) and Lamʿāt (Shamela 145212, page-id 4548, hadith #3): both confirm الْمُتَنَطِّعُونَ = الْمُتَعَمِّقُونَ الْغَالُونَ (غُلُوّ), attributed to Ṭūrbishtī in Mirqat and to al-Ṭībī in Lamʿāt. The specific اِحْتِيَاط-vs-غُلُوّ / شُبُهَات قَرِيبَة-vs-بَعِيدَة distinction in the class note is a class-level elaboration building on this confirmed غُلُوّ concept — not itself found verbatim in Mirqat or Lamʿāt this session, flagged. Fatḥ al-Bārī/Badhl al-Majhūd/Kawkab al-Durrī not applicable (Muslim-sourced only; Takmila Fatḥ al-Mulhim is PDF-only, not checked this session). Mirʾāt not accessible.
