Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ الْبَيَانِ وَالشِّعْرِ — الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٧٨٥
وَعَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ: «أَصْدَقُ كَلِمَةٍ قَالَهَا الشَّاعِرُ كَلِمَةُ لَبِيدٍ: أَلَا كُلُّ شَيْءٍ مَا خَلَا اللَّهَ بَاطِلٌ». مُتَّفَقٌ عَلَيْهِ.
Narrated by Abū Hurayrah (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Muttafaq ʿAlayh (Bukhārī 6147, Muslim 2256)
Translation
"The most truthful word ever said by a poet is the word of Labīd: 'Indeed everything besides Allah is fleeting.'"
Class Notes
  • Labīd ibn Rabīʿah lived for over 100 years.
  • He died in Muʿāwiyah's time, and ʿUmar (R.A.) used to give him allowances.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • بَاطِلٌ— fleeting, perishing (الْفَانِي الْمُضْمَحِلّ) — Nawawī: in this ḥadīth is a مَنْقَبَة (virtue) for Labīd, a Ṣaḥābī; al-Ṭībī: it was "the most truthful" because it matches Allah's own statement «كُلُّ مَنْ عَلَيْهَا فَانٍ» [55:26].
  • لَبِيد— Labīd ibn Rabīʿah al-ʿĀmirī; noble in both الْجَاهِلِيَّة and Islam, settled in Kūfah and died there in 41 AH, having lived (per Mirqat) either 140 or 157 years. Once he accepted Islam he never composed poetry again, saying "the Qurʾān suffices me"; the rest of his own famous line continues (per Lamʿāt): «وَكُلُّ نَعِيمٍ لَا مَحَالَةَ زَائِلُ، سِوَى جَنَّةِ الْفِرْدَوْسِ إِنَّ نَعِيمَهَا سَيَبْقَى، وَإِنَّ الْمَوْتَ لَا بُدَّ نَازِلُ».
Cross-ref: Muttafaq ʿAlayh. Verified in Mirqat (بَابُ الْبَيَانِ وَالشِّعْرِ، الفصل الأول — Shamela 8176, page-id 6601, printed ٤٧٨٦): gives Labīd's biography (140 or 157 years, died 41 AH in Kūfah), matching the class's "over 100 years" note; ʿUmar's stipend to him was not located in this specific Mirqat passage — flagged. Confirmed in Lamʿāt (Shamela 145212, page-id 4549, hadith #4), which additionally preserves the continuation of Labīd's own line. Confirmed in Fatḥ al-Bārī (كتاب الأدب، بَابُ مَا يَجُوزُ مِنَ الشِّعْرِ — Shamela 1673, page-id 6298, Bukhārī 6147): Bukhārī's own wording combines this ḥadīth with the mention of Umayyah ibn Abī al-Ṣalt in a single narration, whereas Mishkāt/Mirqat present them as two separate entries — a textual-arrangement variance worth noting, not a discrepancy in content. Mirʾāt not accessible; Kawkab al-Durrī/Badhl al-Majhūd not applicable.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ الْبَيَانِ وَالشِّعْرِ — الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٧٨٦
وَعَنْ عَمْرِو بْنِ الشَّرِيدِ عَنْ أَبِيهِ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ قَالَ: رَدِفْتُ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ ﷺ يَوْمًا فَقَالَ: «هَلْ مَعَكَ مِنْ شِعْرِ أُمَيَّةَ بْنِ أَبِي الصَّلْتِ شَيْءٌ؟» قُلْتُ: نَعَمْ. قَالَ: «هِيهِ» فَأَنْشَدْتُهُ بَيْتًا، فَقَالَ: «هِيهِ»، ثُمَّ أَنْشَدْتُهُ بَيْتًا فَقَالَ: «هِيهِ»، حَتَّى أَنْشَدْتُهُ مِائَةَ بَيْتٍ. رَوَاهُ مُسْلِمٌ.
Narrated by ʿAmr ibn al-Sharīd, from his father al-Sharīd (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Muslim
Translation
"I rode behind the Messenger of Allah (S.A.W.) one day, and he said, 'Do you know any of the poetry of Umayyah ibn Abī al-Ṣalt?' I said, 'Yes.' He said, 'Hīh (go on).' So I recited a line of poetry to him, and he said, 'Hīh.' Then I recited another line and he said, 'Hīh' — until I had recited a hundred lines to him."
Class Notes
  • Umayyah [ibn Abī al-Ṣalt] was another جَاهِلِيّ poet, but he never accepted Islam.
  • He believed a prophet would come soon, but he thought that he himself was going to be the prophet. But because he believed in Allah, his أَشْعَار (poetry) contained good things, which is why Rasulullah (S.A.W.) liked his poetry.
  • These أَحَادِيث show that both إِنْشَاء (composing) and إِنْشَاد (reciting)/شِعْر are permissible. Rasulullah (S.A.W.) even designated a place for Ḥassān ibn Thābit (R.A.) in Masjid Nabawī for إِنْشَادُ الشِّعْر.
  • But other نُصُوص (texts) do ذَمّ (condemn) شِعْر. جَمْع (reconciliation) can be done based on the narration of ʿĀʾishah (R.A.) in al-Adab al-Mufrad that شِعْر is of 2 types — good and bad — so take the good and leave the bad. Ibn ʿUmar (R.A.) also stated that شِعْر is just like كَلَام: [some] good and [some] bad.
  • Examples of impermissible poems: content of شِرْك; فُحْش (obscenity); talking about a specific woman (not women in general); mocking a specific person without any حَقّ; mocking a tribe. These are impermissible to do إِنْشَاد as well as إِنْشَاء, except for اِسْتِشْهَاد (citing as a linguistic proof) in لُغَة.
  • Also, if أَشْعَار cause a person to become occupied and distracted from his religious responsibilities, it is not allowed even if the content is good. If the content of the شِعْر is حَسَن like تَوْحِيد, he will be rewarded «إِنْ شَاءَ اللَّهُ». If the content is مُبَاح, the شِعْر is also مُبَاح.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • أُمَيَّة بْنُ أَبِي الصَّلْت— a poet of Thaqīf who reached the beginnings of Islam and heard news of the mission but was not granted success to believe in the Messenger of Allah ﷺ; Mīrak: he was deeply immersed in [spiritual] meanings, incorporating realities into his poetry — for which the Prophet ﷺ said of him "he nearly (كَادَ) accepted Islam," and in another report: "his tongue believed but his heart disbelieved" (Mirqat). Nawawī (per Lamʿāt): he was a كَافِر, and the Prophet ﷺ still listened to his poetry which contained حِكْمَة; his father's [Abū al-Ṣalt's] name was ʿAbdullāh ibn Rabīʿah.
  • هِيهِ— "go on / say more" — with كَسْرَة on both هَاء, meaning هَاتِ (bring more); a اِسْمُ فِعْل in the meaning of a command.
Cross-ref: Muslim. Verified in Mirqat (بَابُ الْبَيَانِ وَالشِّعْرِ، الفصل الأول — Shamela 8176, page-id 6602, printed ٤٧٨٧): confirms Umayyah nearly accepted Islam and the "believed tongue, disbelieving heart" report. Confirmed in Lamʿāt (Shamela 145212, page-id 4549–4550, hadith #5), citing Nawawī that Umayyah was a كَافِر and preserving lines of his poetry plus a report on the origin of «بِاسْمِكَ اللَّهُمَّ». The broader poetry-permissibility discussion (إنشاء/إنشاد, ʿĀʾishah's al-Adab al-Mufrad two-types-of-شِعْر report, Ibn ʿUmar's comparison to كَلَام, the impermissible-content list, Ḥassān ibn Thābit's spot in the مَسْجِد) is the class's own synthesis across the whole بَاب, not tied to this single hadith's Mirqat/Lamʿāt commentary — presented here as the bāb-level notes per the class structure. Fatḥ al-Bārī (Shamela 1673, page-id 6298) shows Bukhārī's parallel report mentions Umayyah alongside Labīd's ḥadīth in a single narration, differently arranged than Mishkāt. Mirʾāt not accessible; Badhl al-Majhūd/Kawkab al-Durrī not applicable.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ الْبَيَانِ وَالشِّعْرِ — الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٧٨٧
وَعَنْ جُنْدُبٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ ﷺ كَانَ فِي بَعْضِ الْمَشَاهِدِ وَقَدْ دَمِيَتْ أُصْبُعُهُ فَقَالَ: «هَلْ أَنْتِ إِلَّا أُصْبُعٌ دَمِيتِ، وَفِي سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ مَا لَقِيتِ». مُتَّفَقٌ عَلَيْهِ.
Narrated by Jundub (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Muttafaq ʿAlayh
Translation
The Prophet (S.A.W.) was at one of the battle sites when his finger bled, so he said: "Are you but a finger that has bled, and in the way of Allah is what you have met."
Class Notes
  • Ṭūrbishtī quotes al-Khaṭṭābī that there are multiple answers explaining this statement of Rasulullah (S.A.W.); he mentioned 3 explanations:
  • (1) This is رَجَز, not شِعْر — because it is not from the famous أَعَارِيض (the poetic metres) which the شُعَرَاء (poets) use.
  • (2) A person is only a شَاعِر if he deliberately intends to compose poetry; here the rhyming occurred merely by اِتِّفَاق (coincidence), without any such intent.
  • (3) Just one بَيْت (line of verse) does not make a person a شَاعِر — the negation in «وَمَا عَلَّمْنَاهُ الشِّعْرَ» [Yā Sīn 36:69] is a refutation of the مُشْرِكِين who claimed he was a poet, and a single line does not earn that title.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • هَلْ أَنْتِ إِلَّا أُصْبُعٌ دَمِيتِ— rhetorical negation: "you are nothing but a finger that has bled" — addressing the finger as consolation, meaning: make it easy on yourself, you were not afflicted with destruction or severance, only bleeding, and that too فِي سَبِيلِ اللَّه (in Allah's way), not in vain.
Cross-ref: Muttafaq ʿAlayh. Verified in Mirqat (بَابُ الْبَيَانِ وَالشِّعْرِ، الفصل الأول — Shamela 8176, page-id 6603–6605, printed ٤٧٨٨): al-Qārī quotes al-Khaṭṭābī directly giving 3 explanations for how this statement (in رَجَز metre) came from the Prophet ﷺ despite {وَمَا عَلَّمْنَاهُ الشِّعْرَ}: (1) رَجَز is not شِعْر at all (not from the famous أَعَارِيض the شُعَرَاء use); (2) even matching poetic metre, it wasn't intentionally composed as poetry — a شَاعِر is one who intends to compose, so this rhyming was mere اِتِّفَاق (as coincidental metre also occurs in the Qurʾān); (3) the آيَة's negation refers to refuting the الْمُشْرِكِين's claim he was "a poet" — a single بَيْت doesn't earn that label. These are the 3 explanations in the class notes. Mirqat cites al-Khaṭṭābī directly for this 3-answer analysis, while the class routes it as al-Ṭūrbishtī quoting al-Khaṭṭābī — both name al-Khaṭṭābī as the source and give the same three. Confirmed in Lamʿāt (Shamela 145212, page-id 4552, hadith #6, Bukhārī 2802/Muslim 1796): gives a parallel discussion via al-Ṭabarī on whether the Prophet ﷺ said it مُنْشِئًا (composing it himself) or مُتَمَثِّلًا (reciting someone else's line — attributed to al-Walīd ibn al-Walīd or ʿAbdullāh ibn Rawāḥah), the same theme from a different angle. Confirmed in Fatḥ al-Bārī (Shamela 1673, page-id 6298, Bukhārī 6146) as part of the same بَابُ مَا يَجُوزُ مِنَ الشِّعْرِ. Mirʾāt not accessible; Badhl al-Majhūd/Kawkab al-Durrī not applicable.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ الْبَيَانِ وَالشِّعْرِ — الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٧٩٠
وَعَنْ عَائِشَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهَا قَالَتْ: سَمِعْتُ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ ﷺ يَقُولُ لِحَسَّانَ: «إِنَّ رُوحَ الْقُدُسِ لَا يَزَالُ يُؤَيِّدُكَ مَا نَافَحْتَ عَنِ اللَّهِ وَرَسُولِهِ». وَقَالَتْ: سَمِعْتُ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ ﷺ يَقُولُ: «هَجَاهُمْ حَسَّانُ فَشَفَى وَاشْتَفَى». رَوَاهُ مُسْلِمٌ.
Narrated by ʿĀʾishah (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Muslim
Translation
I heard the Messenger of Allah (S.A.W.) say to Ḥassān: "The Holy Spirit (Rūḥ al-Qudus) will not cease to support you as long as you defend Allah and His Messenger." And she said: I heard the Messenger of Allah (S.A.W.) say: "Ḥassān satirized them, so he healed and was healed."
Class Notes
  • The primary meaning: «فَشَفَى» = he healed/cured the الْمُسْلِمِين [by his satire against them], and «وَاشْتَفَى» = he himself found relief (اِشْتَفَى بِنَفْسِهِ).
  • Another explanation for شَفَى is that شَفَى and اِشْتَفَى (used together for تَأْكِيد / emphasis) both mean that he cured the غَيْظ (anger/rage) of the الْمُسْلِمِين, which was caused by the harsh words (هِجَاء) of the الْمُشْرِكِين.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • نَافَحْتَ— you defended and contended (دَافَعْتَ وَخَاصَمْتَ), striving in the defence of Allah and His Messenger; al-Nihāya: الْمُنَافَحَة = الْمُدَافَعَة (repelling/warding off), here meaning the satirizing of the الْمُشْرِكِين and countering them over their poetry.
  • رُوحُ الْقُدُسِ— the Holy Spirit, i.e. Jibrīl; al-Tūrbishtī: your poetry with which you defend Allah and His Messenger is one the angel inspires the way to — unlike what [other] poets say when they follow desire and "wander in every valley," whose words' source is the Shayṭān's promptings.
  • فَشَفَى وَاشْتَفَى— he healed [the الْمُسْلِمِين] and was himself relieved; al-Tūrbishtī: it may be that both words are for تَأْكِيد (emphasis), i.e. he cured the غَيْظ (rage) as much as he was able.
Cross-ref: Muslim (2490). Verified in Mirqat (بَابُ الْبَيَانِ وَالشِّعْرِ، الفصل الأول — Shamela 8176, page-id 6608, printed ٤٧٩١): gives «فَشَفَى» = الْمُسْلِمِين / «وَاشْتَفَى» = بِنَفْسِهِ, and al-Tūrbishtī's alternative that both words are for تَأْكِيد = شَفَى الْغَيْظَ (the class's "cured the anger" reading — directly matching the note). The «رُوحُ الْقُدُسِ»/«أَيِّدْهُ بِرُوحِ الْقُدُسِ» theme is also Muttafaq (the preceding class 4788, al-Barāʾ «اهْجُ الْمُشْرِكِينَ فَإِنَّ جِبْرِيلَ مَعَكَ», is in Bukhārī+Muslim), but this specific «هَجَاهُمْ حَسَّانُ فَشَفَى وَاشْتَفَى» wording is Muslim's — so Fatḥ al-Bārī / Badhl al-Majhūd / Kawkab al-Durrī are not applicable to this matn. Confirmed in Lamʿāt (Shamela 145212, page-id 4554, hadith #9): «فَشَفَى» = غَيْره (others — the الْمُسْلِمِين) / «وَاشْتَفَى» = بِنَفْسِهِ, and it explicitly grounds the غَيْظ reading in al-Qāmūs — «اشْتَفَى بِكَذَا: تَشَفَّى مِنْ غَيْظِهِ» (was relieved of his rage) — directly corroborating the note's "cured the anger" point; «نَافَحْتَ» = كَافَحَه وَخَاصَمَه. Mirʾāt not accessible (Kitāb al-Ādāb not digitized in the Shamela edition); Takmila Fatḥ al-Mulhim (Muslim sharḥ, PDF) not checked this session.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ الْبَيَانِ وَالشِّعْرِ — الفصل الثالث
حديث ٤٨٠٥
وَعَنْ أَنَسٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ قَالَ: كَانَ لِلنَّبِيِّ ﷺ حَادٍ يُقَالُ لَهُ أَنْجَشَةُ، وَكَانَ حَسَنَ الصَّوْتِ، فَقَالَ لَهُ النَّبِيُّ ﷺ: «رُوَيْدَكَ يَا أَنْجَشَةُ لَا تَكْسِرِ الْقَوَارِيرَ». قَالَ قَتَادَةُ: يَعْنِي ضَعْفَةَ النِّسَاءِ. مُتَّفَقٌ عَلَيْهِ.
Narrated by Anas (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Muttafaq ʿAlayh (Bukhārī 6211, Muslim 2323)
Translation
The Prophet (S.A.W.) had a camel-driver (ḥādī) named Anjashah, who had a beautiful voice. The Prophet (S.A.W.) said to him: "Gently, O Anjashah — do not break the قَوَارِير (glass vessels)." Qatādah said: he meant the delicate women.
Class Notes
  • الْحُدَاء = what the driver (السَّائِق) chants to urge the riding-animal (الدَّابَّة) to move along faster.
  • «رُوَيْدَكَ» has two possible meanings:
  • (1) Do the سَوْق (driving) gently, so the camel does not go too fast — because if it does, the woman who is riding may be harmed.
  • (2) Do the حُدَاء gently, because your voice is good, so the riding woman may become inclined toward you.
  • Ḥāshiyah quotes Lamaʿāt that the 2nd one is أَصَحّ; but other شُرَّاح state that the 1st one is أَصَحّ.
  • Women were compared to قَوَارِير (glass vessels) because they are more delicate physically, or because it is easier to make them incline to oneself — so they are delicate in this manner / from this perspective.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • حَادٍ— one who performs حُدَاء (urging and driving camels with chanting/song); the حُدَاء is مُبَاح with no disagreement (Lamʿāt, per al-Qāmūs).
  • رُوَيْدَكَ— "go gently / take your time" (أَمْهِلْ); from «أَمْهِلْهُمْ رُوَيْدًا» [al-Ṭāriq 86:17].
  • الْقَوَارِير— pl. of قَارُورَة, a glass vessel; used كِنَايَة for women for their رِقَّة (delicacy), لَطَافَة, and weakness of build — quick to be affected/incline, as glass is quick to break; Qatādah: he meant ضَعْفَة النِّسَاء.
Cross-ref: Muttafaq ʿAlayh (Bukhārī 6211, Muslim 2323). Verified in Mirqat (بَابُ الْبَيَانِ وَالشِّعْرِ، الفصل الثالث — Shamela 8176, page-id 6627–6628, printed ٤٨٠٦) and Lamʿāt (Shamela 145212, page-id 4566–4567, printed ٤٨٠٦). **The shurūḥ disagree on which reading of «رُوَيْدَكَ» is أَصَحّ:** Lamʿāt explicitly says «الْأَوَّلُ [the voice-affecting-hearts reading] أَصَحّ وَأَشْهَر», while Mirqat/al-Qārī holds the physical-harm/speed reading is أَظْهَر (arguing the fitna reading rests on a سُوء ظَنّ unbefitting prophethood) — exactly the class's "Lamaʿāt: the voice reading is aṣaḥḥ; other shurrāḥ: the physical reading is aṣaḥḥ." Both books gloss قَوَارِير = women via the glass/delicacy simile (Qatādah: ضَعْفَة النِّسَاء). This hadith is also in Bukhārī كتاب الأدب/النكاح (Fatḥ al-Bārī); Badhl/Kawkab N/A. Mirʾāt not accessible (Kitāb al-Ādāb not digitized in the Shamela edition).
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ الْبَيَانِ وَالشِّعْرِ — الفصل الثالث
حديث ٤٨٠٨
وَعَنْ أَبِي سَعِيدٍ الْخُدْرِيِّ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ قَالَ: بَيْنَا نَحْنُ نَسِيرُ مَعَ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ ﷺ بِالْعَرْجِ إِذْ عَرَضَ شَاعِرٌ يُنْشِدُ، فَقَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ: «خُذُوا الشَّيْطَانَ» أَوْ «أَمْسِكُوا الشَّيْطَانَ، لَأَنْ يَمْتَلِئَ جَوْفُ رَجُلٍ قَيْحًا خَيْرٌ لَهُ مِنْ أَنْ يَمْتَلِئَ شِعْرًا». رَوَاهُ مُسْلِمٌ.
Narrated by Abū Saʿīd al-Khudrī (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Muslim (2259)
Translation
While we were travelling with the Messenger of Allah (S.A.W.) at al-ʿArj, a poet appeared reciting poetry. The Messenger of Allah (S.A.W.) said: "Seize the Shayṭān" — or "Restrain the Shayṭān — for a man's belly to be filled with pus is better for him than to be filled with poetry."
Class Notes
  • Qāḍī ʿIyāḍ: this is the دَلِيل for those who prohibit شِعْر مُطْلَقًا (absolutely) — such as Masrūq and al-Ḥasan [al-Baṣrī].
  • But the جُمْهُور state that if the content is مُبَاح, then the شِعْر is allowed; and they say that the man in this hadith was reciting شِعْر مَذْمُوم (blameworthy poetry).
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • خُذُوا الشَّيْطَانَ— "seize/restrain the Shayṭān," i.e. stop him from reciting; al-Qārī: when the Prophet ﷺ saw him engrossed and shameless in reciting poetry, dominated by قَرْض الشِّعْر (composing verse) and stripped of حَيَاء and أَدَب, he applied the name "Shayṭān" to him.
  • يَمْتَلِئَ جَوْفُ رَجُلٍ قَيْحًا— for a man's belly to be filled with قَيْح (pus); Fatḥ al-Bārī (Ibn Ḥajar): the ذَمّ (blame) attaches to the اِمْتِلَاء — being wholly FILLED [with poetry to the exclusion of Qurʾān, dhikr and ʿilm] — which shows that شِعْر short of that (not dominating) is not blamed.
Cross-ref: Muslim (2259). Verified in Mirqat (بَابُ الْبَيَانِ وَالشِّعْرِ، الفصل الثالث — Shamela 8176, page-id 6631–6632, printed ٤٨٠٩): «خُذُوا الشَّيْطَانَ» = stop him reciting; the poet was so dominated by verse and stripped of حَيَاء/أَدَب that he was called "Shayṭān." Confirmed in Lamʿāt (Shamela 145212, page-id 4568, printed ٤٨٠٩): the man was likely reciting جَاهِلِيّ poetry containing فُحْش / هِجَاء / شِرْك — i.e. شِعْر مَذْمُوم (the جُمْهُور's reading in the note). The «يَمْتَلِئَ شِعْرًا» phrase: Fatḥ al-Bārī (Bukhārī 6154/6155, كتاب الأدب بَابُ مَا يُكْرَهُ أَنْ يَكُونَ الْغَالِبُ عَلَى الْإِنْسَانِ الشِّعْرُ — Shamela 1673, page-id 6309): Ibn Ḥajar — the ذَمّ attaches to being wholly filled with poetry to the exclusion of all else, so poetry short of that is not blamed (the basis of the جُمْهُور's "if content مُبَاح, allowed"). The specific attribution to Qāḍī ʿIyāḍ that Masrūq & al-Ḥasan prohibit poetry مُطْلَقًا is from Qāḍī ʿIyāḍ (Ikmāl al-Muʿlim, the Muslim sharḥ) / Nawawī's Sharḥ Muslim — not independently pulled this session, flagged. Mirʾāt not accessible; Badhl/Kawkab N/A.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ الْبَيَانِ وَالشِّعْرِ — الفصل الثالث
حديث ٤٨١٠
وَعَنْ نَافِعٍ قَالَ: كُنْتُ مَعَ ابْنِ عُمَرَ فِي طَرِيقٍ، فَسَمِعَ مِزْمَارًا، فَوَضَعَ أُصْبُعَيْهِ فِي أُذُنَيْهِ وَنَاءَ عَنِ الطَّرِيقِ إِلَى الْجَانِبِ الْآخَرِ، ثُمَّ قَالَ لِي بَعْدَ أَنْ بَعُدَ: يَا نَافِعُ! هَلْ تَسْمَعُ شَيْئًا؟ قُلْتُ: لَا، فَرَفَعَ أُصْبُعَيْهِ مِنْ أُذُنَيْهِ، قَالَ: كُنْتُ مَعَ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ ﷺ فَسَمِعَ صَوْتَ يَرَاعٍ، فَصَنَعَ مِثْلَ مَا صَنَعْتُ. قَالَ نَافِعٌ: فَكُنْتُ إِذْ ذَاكَ صَغِيرًا. رَوَاهُ أَحْمَدُ، وَأَبُو دَاوُدَ.
Narrated by Nāfiʿ, from Ibn ʿUmar (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Aḥmad & Abū Dāwūd (4924)
Translation
I was with Ibn ʿUmar on a road when he heard a مِزْمَار (flute). He put his fingers in his ears and moved off the road to the far side; then, after he had moved away, he said to me: "O Nāfiʿ, do you hear anything?" I said: No. So he removed his fingers from his ears and said: "I was with the Messenger of Allah (S.A.W.) when he heard the sound of a يَرَاع (reed-pipe) and did just as I did." Nāfiʿ said: And I was young at that time.
Class Notes
  • Abū Dāwūd says this hadith is مُنْكَر, but other مُحَدِّثُون say there is no cause for نَكَارَة.
  • Badhl al-Majhūd (al-Saharanpūrī) mentions 2 reasons why Ibn ʿUmar did not tell Nāfiʿ to cover his ears:
  • (1) Ibn ʿUmar refrained from hearing the يَرَاع not because it was مُحَرَّم, but only to follow Rasulullah ﷺ's action out of اِحْتِيَاط (caution) — because what is حَرَام is to intentionally listen (اِسْتِمَاع) to it, not what is heard by a person coincidentally and unintentionally (سَمَاع).
  • (2) Nāfiʿ was not بَالِغ.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • مِزْمَار / يَرَاع— a reed-pipe/flute (قَصَب); Nawawī: two views on the يَرَاع — al-Baghawī deemed it حَرَام, al-Ghazālī permissible; the أَصَحّ is the حُرْمَة of the يَرَاع (the pipe called الشَّبَّابَة).
  • نَاءَ— he moved far away (بَعُدَ) from the source of the sound.
  • فَكُنْتُ إِذْ ذَاكَ صَغِيرًا— "and I was young then" — Lamʿāt: this is the answer to the objection "why did Ibn ʿUmar not stop Nāfiʿ from hearing it" (Nāfiʿ, being young / not بَالِغ, was not obligated); Mirqat (al-Qārī): the finger-placing itself is from وَرَع and تَقْوَى and مُرَاعَاة الأَوْلَى — for a person is charged only with not INTENDING to listen (لَمْ يَقْصِدِ السَّمَاع), not with making himself not-hear.
Cross-ref: Aḥmad & Abū Dāwūd (4924). Verified in Mirqat (بَابُ الْبَيَانِ وَالشِّعْرِ، الفصل الثالث — Shamela 8176, page-id 6634, printed ٤٨١١): al-Qārī's تَحْقِيق — the finger-placing is وَرَع/تَقْوَى/مُرَاعَاة الأَوْلَى, not obligation; one is charged only with not intending the سَمَاع, not with not-hearing. Confirmed in Lamʿāt (Shamela 145212, page-id 4569, printed ٤٨١١): «فَكُنْتُ إِذْ ذَاكَ صَغِيرًا» is the express answer to "why did Ibn ʿUmar not stop Nāfiʿ from hearing it" (Nāfiʿ young); يَرَاع = قَصَب, with Nawawī's two views (Baghawī حُرْمَة / Ghazālī جَوَاز, the أَصَحّ = حُرْمَة). Confirmed in Badhl al-Majhūd (Abū Dāwūd sharḥ — Shamela 14601, بَابُ كَرَاهِيَةِ الْغِنَاءِ وَالزَّمْرِ, page-id 8357–8358, Abū Dāwūd 4924): carries the matn with an extensive treatment of the مَلَاهِي / غِنَاء rulings. The class's two "reasons Ibn ʿUmar didn't tell Nāfiʿ to cover his ears" are the synthesis of these — the "Nāfiʿ not bāligh" reason confirmed in Lamʿāt, the "intentional اِسْتِمَاع vs. incidental سَمَاع / اِحْتِيَاط not تَحْرِيم" reason confirmed in Mirqat. Abū Dāwūd's «مُنْكَر» grading (and the counter that there is no نَكَارَة) is the class's isnād note — not independently located in these shurūḥ this session. Mirʾāt not accessible; Kawkab N/A.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ حِفْظِ اللِّسَانِ وَالْغِيبَةِ — الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٨١٣
وَعَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ مَسْعُودٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ: «سِبَابُ الْمُسْلِمِ فُسُوقٌ، وَقِتَالُهُ كُفْرٌ». مُتَّفَقٌ عَلَيْهِ.
Narrated by ʿAbdullāh ibn Masʿūd (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Muttafaq ʿAlayh (Bukhārī 6044, Muslim 64)
Translation
The Messenger of Allah (S.A.W.) said: "Reviling a Muslim is فُسُوق (open disobedience), and fighting him is كُفْر."
Class Notes
  • It is فُسُوق because cursing/reviling (سَبّ) a Muslim without any حَقّ is completely حَرَام.
  • Another understanding of the last part is that arguing or fighting a Muslim without any حَقّ is كُفْرَان of the نِعْمَة of brotherhood (أُخُوَّة) through Islam.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • سِبَابُ الْمُسْلِمِ فُسُوقٌ— reviling (شَتْم) a Muslim is فُسُوق, because reviling him without حَقّ is حَرَام; فُسُوق linguistically = "going out," and in the Shariah = going out of obedience (الْخُرُوج عَنِ الطَّاعَة).
  • وَقِتَالُهُ كُفْرٌ— al-Qārī: the meaning is that disputing and fighting him بِالْبَاطِل is كُفْر in the sense of كُفْرَان (ingratitude) of the نِعْمَة and إِحْسَان of the brotherhood of Islam; or that it may lead to كُفْر; or that it is the act of the disbelievers; or it is meant as تَغْلِيظ / تَهْدِيد (emphatic threat) — like «مَنْ تَرَكَ صَلَاةً مُتَعَمِّدًا فَقَدْ كَفَرَ». Explicit كُفْر is only where one deems his killing lawful (اِسْتِحْلَال) without تَأْوِيل.
Cross-ref: Muttafaq ʿAlayh (Bukhārī 6044, Muslim 64). Verified in Mirqat (بَابُ حِفْظِ اللِّسَانِ، الفصل الأول — Shamela 8176, page-id 6639, printed ٤٨١٤): al-Qārī's «قِتَالُهُ كُفْرٌ = كُفْرَانُ النِّعْمَةِ وَالْإِحْسَانِ فِي أُخُوَّةِ الْإِسْلَامِ» is the exact "another understanding" in the note; Sharḥ al-Sunna adds that outright killing with اِسْتِحْلَال and no تَأْوِيل is رِدَّة/كُفْر. Confirmed in Lamʿāt (Shamela 145212, page-id 4572, printed ٤٨١٤). Confirmed in Fatḥ al-Bārī (Bukhārī 6044, كتاب الأدب بَابُ مَا يُنْهَى مِنَ السِّبَابِ وَاللَّعْنِ — Shamela 1673, page-id 6225). Mirʾāt not accessible (Kitāb al-Ādāb not digitized); Badhl/Kawkab N/A.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ حِفْظِ اللِّسَانِ وَالْغِيبَةِ — الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٨١٧
وَعَنْ أَنَسٍ وَأَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُمَا أَنَّ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ ﷺ قَالَ: «الْمُسْتَبَّانِ مَا قَالَا، فَعَلَى الْبَادِئِ مَا لَمْ يَعْتَدِ الْمَظْلُومُ». رَوَاهُ مُسْلِمٌ.
Narrated by Anas & Abū Hurayrah (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Muslim (2587)
Translation
The Messenger of Allah (S.A.W.) said: "The two who revile one another — whatever they say [its sin] is upon the one who began, so long as the wronged one does not exceed [the limit]."
Class Notes
  • [The sin is on the initiator] because the 2nd person's سَبّ (reviling back) was only retaliation and was not ظُلْم.
  • Nawawī: a مَسْبُوب (one reviled) may only curse back with the same amount that he was cursed with, and there must be no كَذِب (lying) nor any سَبّ against the أَسْلَاف (forefathers/ancestors).
  • Then, when the 2nd person takes his due by cursing back, the بَادِئ (initiator) is freed from the sin of that cursing and the 2nd person no longer has a حَقّ against him — but the sin of violating حَقُّ اللَّه remains upon the first person.
  • But some say that all the sin is removed, and the only thing remaining on the first person is لَوْم (blame).
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • الْمُسْتَبَّانِ— the two who revile each other (الْمُتَشَاتِمَانِ) — each has reviled the other, except that the "other" [second] intended to repel (رَدّ) the first, or mentioned some fault actually present in him.
  • فَعَلَى الْبَادِئِ مَا لَمْ يَعْتَدِ الْمَظْلُومُ— the إِثْم (sin) of what both said is on the بَادِئ (initiator) alone, because he was the cause of the quarrel — so long as the مَظْلُوم (wronged one) does not exceed the limit; if the wronged one over-reviles (اِعْتَدَى), the excess becomes his sin (some: he too becomes sinful, the rest staying on the initiator).
Cross-ref: Muslim (2587). Verified in Mirqat (بَابُ حِفْظِ اللِّسَانِ، الفصل الأول — Shamela 8176, page-id 6643–6644, printed ٤٨١٨–٤٨١٩) and Lamʿāt (Shamela 145212, page-id 4575, printed ٤٨١٨): both confirm the core — the whole إِثْم falls on the بَادِئ (as the cause) unless the مَظْلُوم exceeds, in which case the excess is the wronged one's. The detailed breakdown in the note (مَسْبُوب responds with an equal measure, no كَذِب, no سَبّ of the أَسْلَاف; the initiator freed of the responder's حَقّ but حَقُّ اللَّه remaining; the "all removed except لَوْم" view) is Nawawī's Sharḥ Muslim on this hadith — the class's stated source; not independently pulled this session, but its principle is confirmed by Mirqat/Lamʿāt above. Mirʾāt not accessible; Fatḥ al-Bārī N/A (Muslim-only); Takmila Fatḥ al-Mulhim (PDF) not checked.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ حِفْظِ اللِّسَانِ وَالْغِيبَةِ — الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٨١٩
وَعَنْ أَبِي الدَّرْدَاءِ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ قَالَ: سَمِعْتُ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ ﷺ يَقُولُ: «إِنَّ اللَّعَّانِينَ لَا يَكُونُونَ شُهَدَاءَ وَلَا شُفَعَاءَ يَوْمَ الْقِيَامَةِ». رَوَاهُ مُسْلِمٌ.
Narrated by Abū al-Dardāʾ (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Muslim (2599)
Translation
"Indeed the لَعَّانُون (habitual cursers) will not be witnesses (شُهَدَاء) nor intercessors (شُفَعَاء) on the Day of Judgement."
Class Notes
  • They will not be witnesses over the previous nations [testifying] that their prophets conveyed the message to them — so they will not attain this rank, which is exclusive to the أُمَّة of Muhammad (S.A.W.).
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • لَا يَكُونُونَ شُهَدَاءَ— i.e. witnesses over the people — the previous nations (الْأُمَم السَّالِفَة) — that their messengers conveyed the message to them; the لَعَّانُون are deprived of this noble rank exclusive to this أُمَّة, as «وَكَذَلِكَ جَعَلْنَاكُمْ أُمَّةً وَسَطًا لِتَكُونُوا شُهَدَاءَ عَلَى النَّاسِ» [al-Baqarah 2:143] — al-Ṭībī: الْوَسَط = الْعَدْل (justice), and the curse (لَعْنَة) strips away عَدَالَة.
  • وَلَا شُفَعَاءَ— nor will they have the rank of شَفَاعَة (intercession), because by cursing they forfeited that rank among the ranks of the prophets and martyrs.
Cross-ref: Muslim (2599). Verified in Mirqat (بَابُ حِفْظِ اللِّسَانِ، الفصل الأول — Shamela 8176, page-id 6646, printed ٤٨٢١): the class note is Mirqat verbatim — شُهَدَاء over the الْأُمَم السَّالِفَة that their messengers delivered the message, a rank مُخْتَصَّة بِهَذِهِ الْأُمَّة (Q 2:143), and لَعْن strips عَدَالَة (al-Ṭībī). Confirmed in Lamʿāt (Shamela 145212, page-id 4576, printed ٤٨٢٠): شُهَدَاء = for the obedient, شُفَعَاء = for the sinners. Mirʾāt not accessible; Fatḥ al-Bārī / Badhl / Kawkab N/A (Muslim-only). Note: class-numbered 4819 (Mishkāt standard ٤٨٢٠, class = std − 1); the label "4814" in the class notes was a slip — this hadith sits between entries 4817 and 4820.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ حِفْظِ اللِّسَانِ وَالْغِيبَةِ — الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٨٢٠
وَعَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ: «إِذَا قَالَ الرَّجُلُ: هَلَكَ النَّاسُ فَهُوَ أَهْلَكُهُمْ». رَوَاهُ مُسْلِمٌ.
Narrated by Abū Hurayrah (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Muslim (2623)
Translation
"When a man says: 'The people are ruined (هَلَكَ النَّاسُ),' he is the most ruined of them (أَهْلَكُهُمْ)."
Class Notes
  • I.e. he has pointed to their ruin because of the sin (إِثْم) that occurred through his saying this — and often such a saying leads him to عُجْب (self-conceit).
  • Māzirī: this [being blameworthy] is only if he says it out of اِحْتِقَار (contempt), عُجْب, and كِبْر.
  • But if he says it out of grief (حُزْن) for the passing away of the عُلَمَاء or the سَلَف or the صُلَحَاء, then it is permissible.
  • This is because the first shows تَكَبُّر, while the second shows حُبّ (love) for the pious.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • فَهُوَ أَهْلَكُهُمْ— read with ḍamma (أَهْلَكُهُم) = "the most ruined of them," because he busied himself with people's faults and self-conceit (عُجْب), seeing himself superior; or with fatḥa (أَهْلَكَهُم, past verb) = he is the one who cast them into ruin, since despairing them of Allah's mercy drove them to abandon obedience.
  • هَلَكَ النَّاسُ— Mālik (Sharḥ al-Sunna): if he says it out of عُجْب with himself and belittling the people, that is the disliked thing forbidden; but if he says it out of حُزْن or تَحْذِير for what he sees in people regarding their دِين, there is no harm in it — the same distinction the note attributes to Māzirī.
Cross-ref: Muslim (2623). Verified in Mirqat (بَابُ حِفْظِ اللِّسَانِ، الفصل الأول — Shamela 8176, page-id 6647–6648, printed ٤٨٢٢): the note's «عُجْب/كِبْر → blameworthy vs. حُزْن for the pious → permissible» distinction is given there via Mālik (Sharḥ al-Sunna) — «إِذَا قَالَ ذَلِكَ عَجَبًا بِنَفْسِهِ وَتَصَاغُرًا لِلنَّاسِ فَهُوَ الْمَكْرُوهُ... وَأَمَّا إِذَا قَالَ ذَلِكَ تَحَزُّنًا أَوْ تَحْذِيرًا... فَلَا أَرَى بِهِ بَأْسًا». The Māzirī attribution is from Nawawī's Sharḥ Muslim (which routinely cites al-Māzirī on Muslim) — same content. Confirmed in Lamʿāt (Shamela 145212, page-id 4576, printed ٤٨٢١): ḍamma = أَكْثَرُهُم هَلَاكًا (busied with faults + عُجْب), fatḥa = أَوْقَعَهُم فِي الْهَلَاك. Mirʾāt not accessible; Fatḥ al-Bārī / Badhl / Kawkab N/A (Muslim-only).
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ حِفْظِ اللِّسَانِ وَالْغِيبَةِ — الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٨٢٢
وَعَنْ حُذَيْفَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ قَالَ: سَمِعْتُ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ ﷺ يَقُولُ: «لَا يَدْخُلُ الْجَنَّةَ قَتَّاتٌ». مُتَّفَقٌ عَلَيْهِ، وَفِي رِوَايَةِ مُسْلِمٍ: «نَمَّامٌ».
Narrated by Ḥudhayfah (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Muttafaq ʿAlayh (Bukhārī 6056, Muslim 105)
Translation
"No قَتَّات will enter Paradise." In Muslim's narration: "No نَمَّام (talebearer)."
Class Notes
  • A قَتَّات is someone who intentionally eavesdrops [on people] and then spreads those statements to cause فَسَاد (corruption/discord).
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • قَتَّاتٌ— = نَمَّام (talebearer); النَّمِيمَة is conveying speech in a way that causes فَسَاد. al-Nihāya: the نَمَّام is one who is with a people and reports their talk; the قَتَّات is one who eavesdrops on people without their knowing, then carries the tale (يَنِمّ). Lamʿāt (al-Qāmūs): the قَتَّات eavesdrops without their knowledge, whether or not he then spreads it.
  • لَا يَدْخُلُ الْجَنَّةَ— i.e. [not] with the successful ones [at first]; a severe threat against tale-bearing. النَّمِيمَة is built on كَذِب, حَسَد, and نِفَاق (Abū Ḥāmid).
Cross-ref: Muttafaq ʿAlayh (Bukhārī 6056, Muslim 105). Verified in Mirqat (بَابُ حِفْظِ اللِّسَانِ، الفصل الأول — Shamela 8176, page-id 6650, printed ٤٨٢٤): قَتَّات = نَمَّام; al-Nihāya's distinction — the قَتَّات eavesdrops unseen then spreads — is exactly the note's definition. Confirmed in Lamʿāt (Shamela 145212, page-id 4577, printed ٤٨٢٣): al-Qāmūs — the قَتَّات eavesdrops without their knowledge (whether or not he passes it on). Confirmed in Fatḥ al-Bārī (Bukhārī 6056, كتاب الأدب بَابُ النَّمِيمَةِ مِنَ الْكَبَائِرِ — Shamela 1673, page-id 6233). Mirʾāt not accessible; Badhl / Kawkab N/A.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْآدَابِ بَابُ حِفْظِ اللِّسَانِ وَالْغِيبَةِ — الفصل الأول
حديث ٤٨٢٤
وَعَنْ أُمِّ كُلْثُومٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهَا قَالَتْ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ ﷺ: «لَيْسَ الْكَذَّابُ الَّذِي يُصْلِحُ بَيْنَ النَّاسِ وَيَقُولُ خَيْرًا وَيَنْمِي خَيْرًا». مُتَّفَقٌ عَلَيْهِ.
Narrated by Umm Kulthūm bint ʿUqbah (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Muttafaq ʿAlayh (Bukhārī 2692, Muslim 2605)
Translation
"He is not a liar who reconciles between people and conveys good (يَقُولُ خَيْرًا / يَنْمِي خَيْرًا)."
Class Notes
  • He is a person who tells one person [only] the good that the other said about him, without telling him the bad — and this is not كِذْب (lying), because he is not actually saying anything false.
  • The linguistic distinction: الْإِنْمَاء (نَمَى / أَنْمَى) = نَقْلُ الْكَلَام (conveying speech) عَلَى وَجْهِ الْإِصْلَاح; التَّنْمِيَة (نَمَّى) = نَقْلُ الْكَلَام عَلَى وَجْهِ الْفَسَاد. [The hadith uses «يَنْمِي» — the good/reconciling one.]
  • This hadith is a دَلِيل for those who allow explicit lying (كِذْب صَرِيح) in إِصْلَاح (reconciliation) and مُحَارَبَة (war).
  • But others state that what is actually allowed is تَعَارِيض (equivocation) — whose ظَاهِر (apparent meaning) is مُخَالِف لِلْوَاقِع (contrary to reality) but whose بَاطِن (inner meaning) is true, and it is that [inner meaning] which is مُرَاد (intended). E.g. you tell a person that so-and-so makes دُعَاء for him, when in reality he only makes دُعَاء for عَامَّة الْمُسْلِمِين (the general body of Muslims). — Mawlānā Anwar Shāh Kashmīrī.
  • كِذْب is جَائِز according to the Shāfiʿiyyah in some matters — the 3 mentioned in the [full] hadith: الْإِصْلَاح (reconciliation), الْحَرْب (war), and رِضَاء الزَّوْج (pleasing one's spouse).
  • As for the Aḥnāf, they do not allow explicit lying (كِذْب صَرِيح) anywhere, although they have leniency with مَعَارِيض (equivocation) in these matters.
  • Mufti Taqi: I have not found the جَوَاز of كِذْب صَرِيح in any of the قُدَمَاء (early classical) Aḥnāf except in حَالَة الِاضْطِرَار (a state of necessity). But Mufti Ẓafar Aḥmad quotes Mawlānā Thānwī that كِذْب صَرِيح is permissible in these 3 matters if تَعْرِيض is not possible.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • لَيْسَ الْكَذَّابُ الَّذِي يُصْلِحُ بَيْنَ النَّاسِ— he is not the blameworthy كَذَّاب (liar); Lamʿāt: conveying speech (and even a measure of untruth) to reconcile between people (إِصْلَاح ذَاتِ الْبَيْن) is permissible and is not from النَّمِيمَة or the blameworthy كَذِب — for النَّمِيمَة is conveying speech to spread it and cause فَسَاد.
  • يَنْمِي خَيْرًا— he relays good; al-Nihāya (in Mirqat): نَمَيْتُ الْحَدِيثَ / أَنْمَيْتُهُ (light) = you conveyed it عَلَى وَجْهِ الْإِصْلَاح وَطَلَبِ الْخَيْر, whereas نَمَّيْتُهُ (with tashdīd) = you conveyed it عَلَى وَجْهِ الْإِفْسَاد وَالنَّمِيمَة — the hadith's «يَنْمِي» is the former, relaying good, holding back the harmful.
Cross-ref: Muttafaq ʿAlayh (Bukhārī 2692, Muslim 2605). Verified in Mirqat (بَابُ حِفْظِ اللِّسَانِ، الفصل الأول — Shamela 8176, page-id 6653, printed ٤٨٢٦) and Lamʿāt (Shamela 145212, page-id 4578, printed ٤٨٢٥): both confirm that relaying speech / a measure of untruth to reconcile (إِصْلَاح ذَاتِ الْبَيْن) is permissible and is not النَّمِيمَة (which conveys speech to cause فَسَاد) — «يَنْمِي خَيْرًا» = relaying good, so he passes on the good and withholds the harmful, matching the note. **The الْإِنْمَاء (نَمَى, iṣlāḥ) vs. التَّنْمِيَة (نَمَّى, fasād) linguistic distinction in the note is confirmed verbatim in Mirqat (page-id 6654, via al-Nihāya / Abū ʿUbayd / Ibn Qutayba): «نَمَيْتُ الْحَدِيثَ وَأَنْمَيْتُهُ إِذَا بَلَّغْتَهُ عَلَى وَجْهِ الْإِصْلَاحِ وَطَلَبِ الْخَيْرِ... نَمَّيْتُهُ [بالتشديد] عَلَى وَجْهِ الْإِفْسَادِ وَالنَّمِيمَةِ».** The "3 matters" (الْحَرْب / الْإِصْلَاح / رِضَاء الزَّوْج) are the continuation of this same Umm Kulthūm hadith in the fuller Muslim wording (Muslim 2605: «...إِلَّا فِي ثَلَاثٍ: الْحَرْبِ، وَالْإِصْلَاحِ بَيْنَ النَّاسِ، وَحَدِيثِ الرَّجُلِ امْرَأَتَهُ») — Mishkāt's matn here is the abridged form. The كِذْب صَرِيح vs. تَعَارِيض debate and the Shāfiʿiyyah / Aḥnāf positions (Mawlānā Anwar Shāh Kashmīrī; Mufti Taqi — no جواز of كذب صريح in the قدماء Aḥnāf except حالة الاضطرار; Mufti Ẓafar Aḥmad via Iʿlāʾ al-Sunan quoting Mawlānā Thānwī) are the class's fiqh synthesis, from the Deobandi tradition (Fayḍ al-Bārī / Iʿlāʾ al-Sunan / Mufti Taqi's lessons) — not in the Mishkāt shurūḥ, flagged. This hadith is Bukhārī 2692 (كتاب الصلح, بَابُ لَيْسَ الْكَاذِبُ الَّذِي يُصْلِحُ بَيْنَ النَّاسِ) — Fatḥ al-Bārī there; not separately pulled this session. Mirʾāt not accessible; Badhl / Kawkab N/A.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْفِتَنِ الفصل الأول
حديث ٥٣٧٨
قَامَ فِينَا رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ مَقَامًا مَا تَرَكَ شَيْئًا يَكُونُ فِي مَقَامِهِ إِلَى قِيَامِ السَّاعَةِ إِلَّا حَدَّثَ بِهِ حَفِظَهُ مَنْ حَفِظَهُ وَنَسِيَهُ مَنْ نَسِيَهُ قَدْ عَلِمَهُ أَصْحَابِي هَؤُلَاءِ وَإِنَّهُ لَيَكُونُ مِنْهُ الشَّيْءُ قَدْ نَسِيتُهُ فَأَرَاهُ فَأَذْكُرُهُ كَمَا يَذْكُرُ الرَّجُلُ وَجْهَ الرَّجُلِ إِذَا غَابَ عَنْهُ ثُمَّ إِذَا رَآهُ عَرَفَهُ
Narrated by Hudhayfah ibn al-Yaman (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: al-Bukhari and Muslim (Muttafaq Alayh)  ·  Grade: Sahih
Class Notes
  • فِتْنَة has many different meanings; some scholars mention up to 12 meanings. It can mean إِمْتِحَان (test/trial) or ضَلَالَة (misguidance).
  • In كِتَابُ الْفِتَنِ there are أَحَادِيث regarding what Rasulullah (S.A.W.) predicted about the future.
  • Hudhayfah (R.A.) has narrated many أَحَادِيث regarding فِتَن.
  • Part of this kitab covers أَشْرَاطُ السَّاعَة (signs of the Hour).
  • This narration does not mention an exact amount of time.
  • قَامَ فِينَا means he stood among us and mentioned everything that will happen from that moment all the way until the final hour.
  • أَصْحَابِي هَؤُلَاءِ refers to the صَحَابَة (R.A.) who were present when Hudhayfah (R.A.) was narrating this hadith.
  • فَأَرَاهُ فَأَذْكُرُهُ — I cannot recall it at will, but when I see it happening, I remember that Rasulullah (S.A.W.) predicted it — just as a man recognizes the face of another after having forgotten it.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • قَامَ فِينَا مَقَامًا— he stood among us a standing, i.e., he delivered a sustained address; the مَصْدَر مَقَامًا emphasizes the duration and completeness of the speech.
  • حَفِظَهُ مَنْ حَفِظَهُ وَنَسِيَهُ مَنْ نَسِيَهُ— whoever retained it retained it, and whoever forgot it forgot it; indicates variation among the companions in what they preserved of this knowledge.
  • فَأَرَاهُ فَأَذْكُرُهُ— I see it (occur) and then I recall it (the prediction); the simile is to a man who forgets a face but instantly recognizes it upon seeing it again — knowledge present but not retrievable until the trigger appears.
Cross-ref: Hadith confirmed as Muttafaq Alayh; Mirqat commentary confirmed (Shamela page not yet pulled — flagged); cross-reference with Lam'at and remaining شُرُوحَات pending.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْفِتَنِ الفصل الأول
حديث ٥٣٧٩
تُعْرَضُ الْفِتَنُ عَلَى الْقُلُوبِ كَالْحَصِيرِ عُودًا عُودًا فَأَيُّ قَلْبٍ أُشْرِبَهَا نَكَتَتْ فِيهِ نُكْتَةً سَوْدَاءَ وَأَيُّ قَلْبٍ أَنْكَرَهَا نُكِتَتْ فِيهِ نُكْتَةٌ بَيْضَاءُ حَتَّى يَصِيرَ عَلَى قَلْبَيْنِ: أَبْيَضُ مِثْلِ الصَّفَا فَلَا تَضُرُّهُ فِتْنَةٌ مَا دَامَتِ السَّمَاوَاتُ وَالْأَرْضُ وَالْآخَرُ أَسْوَدُ مِرْبَادًّا كَالْكُوزِ مُجْخِيًّا لَا يَعْرِفُ مَعْرُوفًا وَلَا يُنْكِرُ مُنْكَرًا إِلَّا مَا أُشْرِبَ مِنْ هَوَاهُ
Narrated by Hudhayfah ibn al-Yaman (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Muslim  ·  Grade: Sahih
Class Notes
  • Mirqat: فِتَن can also refer to عَقَائِد فَاسِدَة (corrupt beliefs/doctrines).
  • عُودًا عُودًا — just as a حَصِير (mat) is crafted stick by stick, these فِتَن are presented to the hearts consecutively, one after the other.
  • Grammatical note: if يَسِيرُ (with ya'), the فَاعِل is إِنْسَان; if تَسِيرُ (with ta'), the فَاعِل is قُلُوب.
  • Why is the pure heart compared specifically to الصَّفَا? The whiteness (بَيَاض) signifies purity; being a stone signifies that such hearts will not be moved or affected by these فِتَن.
  • كَالْكُوزِ مُجْخِيًّا — his heart will be like an upside-down or inclining vessel; just as such a vessel holds nothing inside it, similarly these people's hearts do not retain anything of the حَقّ within them.
  • He will not distinguish between good and evil; rather, he will blindly follow his desires without first considering whether something is good or evil.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • عُودًا عُودًا— stick by stick, one after another; Mirqat: just as a mat is woven by laying each reed consecutively, the فِتَن are presented to the heart one by one in sequence.
  • أُشْرِبَهَا— was made to drink it / absorbed it; إِشْرَاب implies the فِتْنَة seeps into the heart the way a drink is absorbed into the body — leaving no trace it was rejected.
  • نَكَتَتْ / نُكِتَتْ— left a mark/dot; النُّكْتَة = a small point or dot. One black dot for every فِتْنَة absorbed; one white dot for every فِتْنَة rejected.
  • الصَّفَا— smooth white rock (with ص); chosen for its two qualities: بَيَاض (whiteness = purity) and صَلَابَة (hardness = imperviousness to fitan).
  • مِرْبَادًّا— dust-colored, darkened; مُرْبَدّ = something that has turned the color of رَبَد (ash/dusty black), indicating a heart blackened by accumulated فِتَن.
  • كَالْكُوزِ مُجْخِيًّا— like an overturned vessel; مُجْخِيًّا = flipped upside down, retaining nothing — such a heart no longer recognizes good or rejects evil.
Cross-ref: Hadith confirmed in Mirqat (عُودًا عُودًا and الصَّفَا meanings noted from Mirqat commentary; Shamela page not yet pulled — flagged); Muslim as primary source confirmed; cross-reference with Lam'at and remaining شُرُوحَات pending.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْفِتَنِ الفصل الثاني
حديث ٥٣٩٥
وَعَنْ حُذَيْفَةَ قَالَ: قُلْتُ: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ أَيَكُونُ بَعْدَ هَذَا الْخَيْرِ شَرٌّ كَمَا كَانَ قَبْلَهُ شَرٌّ؟ قَالَ: «نَعَمْ» قُلْتُ: فَمَا الْعِصْمَةُ؟ قَالَ: «السَّيْفُ» قُلْتُ: وَهَلْ بَعْدَ السَّيْفِ بَقِيَّةٌ؟ قَالَ: «نَعَمْ تَكُونُ إِمَارَةٌ عَلَى أَقْذَاءٍ وَهُدْنَةٌ عَلَى دَخَنٍ» . قُلْتُ: ثُمَّ مَاذَا؟ قَالَ: «ثُمَّ يَنْشَأُ دُعَاةُ الضَّلَالِ فَإِنْ كَانَ لِلَّهِ فِي الْأَرْضِ خَلِيفَةٌ جَلَدَ ظَهْرَكَ وَأَخَذَ مَالَكَ فَأَطِعْهُ وَإِلَّا فَمُتْ وَأَنْتَ عَاضٌّ عَلَى جَذْلِ شَجَرَةٍ» . قُلْتُ: ثُمَّ مَاذَا؟ قَالَ: «ثُمَّ يَخْرُجُ الدَّجَّالُ بَعْدَ ذَلِكَ مَعَهُ نَهْرٌ وَنَارٌ فَمَنْ وَقَعَ فِي نَارِهِ وَجَبَ أَجْرُهُ وَحُطَّ وِزْرُهُ وَمَنْ وَقَعَ فِي نَهْرِهِ وَجَبَ وِزْرُهُ وَحُطَّ أَجْرُهُ» . قَالَ: قُلْتُ: ثُمَّ مَاذَا؟ قَالَ: «ثُمَّ يُنْتَجُ الْمُهْرُ فَلَا يُرْكَبُ حَتَّى تَقُومَ السَّاعَةُ» وَفِي رِوَايَةٍ: «هُدْنَةٌ عَلَى دَخَنٍ وَجَمَاعَةٌ عَلَى أَقْذَاءٍ» . قُلْتُ: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ الْهُدْنَةُ عَلَى الدَّخَنِ مَا هِيَ؟ قَالَ: «لَا تَرْجِعُ قُلُوبُ أَقْوَامٍ كَمَا كَانَتْ عَلَيْهِ» . قُلْتُ: بَعْدَ هَذَا الْخَيْرِ شَرٌّ؟ قَالَ: «فِتْنَةٌ عَمْيَاءُ صَمَّاءُ عَلَيْهَا دُعَاةٌ عَلَى أَبْوَابِ النَّارِ فَإِنْ مُتَّ يَا حُذَيْفَةُ وَأَنْتَ عَاضٌّ عَلَى جَذْلٍ خَيْرٌ لَكَ مِنْ أَنْ تَتَّبِعَ أَحَدًا مِنْهُمْ»
Narrated by Hudhayfah ibn al-Yaman (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Abu Dawud
Class Notes
  • Obey the خَلِيفَة even if he beats your back and takes your wealth — so as not to stir up فِتْنَة.
  • عَاضٌّ عَلَى جَذْلِ شَجَرَةٍ (biting on a tree root) — used here as well to convey that isolation from people is so important that extreme hardship and difficulty are preferable to mixing with them.
  • يُنْتَجُ الْمُهْرُ فَلَا يُرْكَبُ (فَلَا يُرْكَبُ = it will not reach the age of being ridden): the time between the دَجَّال and يَوْمُ الْقِيَامَة will be so short that a horse's foal will not even grow to an age where it can be ridden.
  • هُدْنَةٌ عَلَى دَخَنٍ — there will be peace, but it will not restore the hearts to their former purity; animosity (حِقْد) will remain in the hearts.
  • فِتْنَةٌ عَمْيَاءُ صَمَّاءُ — it will blind the people from seeing الْحَقّ and deafen them from hearing الْحَقّ.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • الْعِصْمَة— Mirqat: طَرِيقُ النَّجَاةِ — the way of protection from falling into the شَرّ; answered with «السَّيْف» (Qatādah applied it to the ردة wars under Abū Bakr R.A.).
  • أَقْذَاء— Mirqat (al-Nihāya): plural of قَذًى (itself plural of قَذَاة) = the dust / straw / dirt that falls into the eye, water, or drink; al-Qāḍī: an إِمَارَة (rule) mixed with بِدَع and committing مَنَاهِي — the inner corruption likened to the قَذَى of the eye.
  • دَخَن— Mirqat: (two فَتْحَات) أَصْلُهُ الْكُدُورَة (turbidity) and a blackish hue; al-Qāḍī: مَعَ خِدَاعٍ وَنِفَاقٍ وَخِيَانَةٍ; al-Fāʾiq: outward صَلَاح over inner فَسَاد. The hadith itself glosses it: لَا تَرْجِعُ قُلُوبُ أَقْوَامٍ كَمَا كَانَتْ (hearts do not return to their former purity).
  • هُدْنَة— Mirqat: (ضَمَّة on the هَاء) = صُلْح — a truce / cessation of hostilities; here, an outward peace masking inner rancour.
  • عَاضٌّ عَلَى جَذْلِ شَجَرَةٍ— عَاضّ (شَدَّة on the ضَاد) = gripping firmly / biting; جَذْل (كَسْرَة or فَتْحَة on the جِيم) = أَصْلُهَا — the root / stump of the tree. al-Qāḍī: a كِنَايَة for taking to العُزْلَة (isolation) and enduring the hardships of the age — like the saying "so-and-so bites on stones from the severity of pain."
  • الْمُهْر— al-Tūrbishtī: (ضَمَّة, سُكُون on the هَاء) = وَلَدُ الْفَرَس (the foal); يُنْتَجُ = passive, يُولَد (is born) — born but not ridden before the Hour, so short is the time.
  • عَمْيَاءُ صَمَّاءُ— blind and deaf (feminine, agreeing with فِتْنَة): a فِتْنَة so overwhelming it blinds people from الْحَقّ and deafens them from it.
Cross-ref: Abū Dāwūd. Verified in Mirqat ٥٣٩٦ (كِتَابُ الْفِتَنِ, الفصل الثاني — Shamela 8176, page-ids 7431–7432): al-Qāḍī (دَخَن = خِدَاع/نِفَاق/كُدُورَة; إمارة مشوبة بالبدع), al-Tūrbishtī (الْمُهْر = وَلَدُ الْفَرَس), al-Ṭībī; Mirqat applies هُدْنَة على دَخَن to the صُلْح of al-Ḥasan (R.A.) with Muʿāwiyah (R.A.). Lamʿāt & Badhl al-Majhūd cross-ref pending.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْفِتَنِ الفصل الثاني
حديث ٥٣٩٦
وَعَنْ أَبِي ذَرٍّ قَالَ: كُنْتُ رَدِيفًا خَلْفَ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ يَوْمًا عَلَى حِمَارٍ فَلَمَّا جَاوَزْنَا بُيُوتَ الْمَدِينَةِ قَالَ: «كَيْفَ بِكَ يَا أَبَا ذَرٍّ إِذَا كَانَ بِالْمَدِينَةِ جُوعٌ تَقُومُ عَنْ فِرَاشِكَ وَلَا تَبْلُغُ مَسْجِدَكَ حَتَّى يُجْهِدَكَ الْجُوعُ؟» قَالَ: قُلْتُ: اللَّهُ وَرَسُولُهُ أَعْلَمُ. قَالَ: «تَعَفَّفْ يَا أَبَا ذَرٍّ» . قَالَ: «كَيْفَ بِكَ يَا أَبَا ذَرٍّ إِذَا كَانَ بِالْمَدِينَةِ مَوْتٌ يَبْلُغُ الْبَيْتَ الْعَبْدُ حَتَّى إِنَّهُ يُبَاعُ الْقَبْرُ بِالْعَبْدِ؟» قَالَ: قُلْتُ: اللَّهُ وَرَسُولُهُ أَعْلَمُ. قَالَ: «تَصْبِرُ يَا أَبَا ذَرٍّ» . قَالَ: «كَيْفَ بِكَ يَا أَبَا ذَرٍّ إِذَا كَانَ بِالْمَدِينَةِ قَتْلٌ تَغْمُرُ الدِّمَاءُ أَحْجَارَ الزَّيْتِ؟» قَالَ: قُلْتُ: اللَّهُ وَرَسُولُهُ أَعْلَمُ. قَالَ: «تَأْتِي مَنْ أَنْتَ مِنْهُ» . قَالَ: قُلْتُ: وَأَلْبَسُ السِّلَاحَ؟ قَالَ: «شَارَكْتَ الْقَوْمَ إِذًا» . قُلْتُ: فَكَيْفَ أَصْنَعُ يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ؟ قَالَ: «إِنْ خَشِيتَ أَنْ يَبْهَرَكَ شُعَاعُ السَّيْفِ فَأَلْقِ نَاحِيَةَ ثَوْبِكَ عَلَى وَجْهِكَ لِيَبُوءَ بِإِثْمِكَ وَإِثْمِهِ»
Narrated by Abu Dharr (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Abu Dawud
Class Notes
  • مَوْت here may refer to a famine or a plague — so severe that a grave is sold for the price of a slave.
  • The قَتْل that will make دِمَاء flood أَحْجَارَ الزَّيْتِ (a place in Madinah) occurred after the death of al-Husayn (R.A.): the people of Madinah refused to submit to Yazid, so he sent Muslim ibn Uqba who massacred the people of Madinah inside the city itself, despite it being a sanctified (حَرَام) city. He then proceeded to Makkah and killed people there as well.
  • تَأْتِي مَنْ أَنْتَ مِنْهُ: be with someone who is مُوَافِق to you in both دِين and way of life.
  • According to the حَاشِيَة's interpretation of تَأْتِي مَنْ أَنْتَ مِنْهُ: stay home and do not mix with the people at all.
  • إِنْ خَشِيتَ أَنْ يَبْهَرَكَ شُعَاعُ السَّيْفِ — if you fear the gleam of the sword will overcome you (i.e., that you too will begin fighting), cover your face with part of your garment: do not even go out to join the fighting; let them kill you rather than participate.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • رَدِيفًا— Mirqat: راكبًا خلف — riding pillion behind the Prophet ﷺ; a sign of his ﷺ تَوَاضُع and of Abū Dharr's closeness.
  • يُجْهِدَكَ الْجُوع— Mirqat: (ضَمَّة يَاء, كَسْرَة هَاء) brings you to مَشَقَّة and disables you from even walking from house to mosque.
  • تَعَفَّفْ— Mirqat: الْتَزِمِ الْعِفَّة — الصَّلَاح, الوَرَع, patience over the pain of hunger, التَّقْوَى, and abstaining from الحَرَام / الشُّبْهَة and from begging the creation.
  • يُبَاعُ الْقَبْرُ بِالْعَبْدِ— Mirqat (al-Nihāya): الْبَيْت here = الْقَبْر; grave-space grows so scarce that a single grave is bought for a slave (or its price); Sharḥ al-Sunna adds: none can be found to dig a grave except for a slave's price.
  • أَحْجَارُ الزَّيْتِ— Mirqat: a quarter / place in Madinah; al-Tūrbishtī (al-Muyassar): it is part of the الْحَرَّة where the Battle of al-Ḥarra occurred under Yazid — the commander Muslim ibn ʿUqba al-Murrī violated the sanctity of the Prophet's ﷺ حَرَم, killed its men, ran rampant 3 (or 5) days, then died between the two حَرَم.
  • تَغْمُرُ الدِّمَاءُ— Mirqat: (سُكُون ghayn, ضَمَّة مِيم) تَسْتُر وتَعْلُو — the blood covers over and rises above (so great is the slaughter).
  • تَأْتِي مَنْ أَنْتَ مِنْهُ— Mirqat: خَبَر بمعنى الأمر — come to one who agrees with you in your دِين and سِيرَة; al-Qāḍī: return to your family / clan; al-Ṭībī: rather, return to your imam.
  • شَارَكْتَ الْقَوْمَ إِذًا— Mirqat: i.e. you would share in their إِثْم by taking up the weapon — so do not bear arms; remain with the imam and the people of righteousness and do not fight.
  • يَبْهَرَكَ شُعَاعُ السَّيْفِ / لِيَبُوءَ— يَبْهَرَك = overwhelms/dazzles you (the gleam of the drawn sword sweeping you into the fighting); لِيَبُوءَ (from بَاءَ بِ = to return bearing a burden): so he returns bearing your sin (for slaying you unjustly) along with his own.
Cross-ref: Abū Dāwūd. Verified in Mirqat ٥٣٩٧ (كِتَابُ الْفِتَنِ, الفصل الثاني — Shamela 8176, page-ids 7434–7435): al-Tūrbishtī (al-Muyassar) explicitly identifies أَحْجَارَ الزَّيْتِ with the Battle of al-Ḥarra under Yazid and names Muslim ibn ʿUqba al-Murrī as its commander — confirming the class note; al-Qāḍī & al-Ṭībī on تأتي من أنت منه; al-Nihāya & Sharḥ al-Sunna on يُباع القبر بالعبد. Lamʿāt & Badhl al-Majhūd cross-ref pending.
Kitab كِتَابُ الْفِتَنِ الفصل الثاني
حديث ٥٤٠٦
وَعَنْ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ مَسْعُودٍ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ عَنِ النَّبِيِّ ﷺ قَالَ: «تَدُورُ رَحَى الْإِسْلَامِ لِخَمْسٍ وَثَلَاثِينَ أَوْ سِتٍّ وَثَلَاثِينَ أَوْ سَبْعٍ وَثَلَاثِينَ، فَإِنْ يَهْلِكُوا فَسَبِيلُ مَنْ هَلَكَ، وَإِنْ يَقُمْ لَهُمْ دِينُهُمْ يَقُمْ لَهُمْ سَبْعِينَ عَامًا». قُلْتُ: أَمِمَّا بَقِيَ أَوْ مِمَّا مَضَى؟ قَالَ: «مِمَّا مَضَى». رَوَاهُ أَبُو دَاوُدَ.
Narrated by ʿAbdullāh ibn Masʿūd (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Abū Dāwūd
Class Notes
  • «تَدُورُ رَحَى الْإِسْلَامِ» — meaning: the affair of Islam becomes established and carries on (يَسْتَقِرُّ وَيَسْتَمِرُّ أَمْرُ الْإِسْلَام).
  • These numbers refer to different incidents: 35 AH = the شَهَادَة of ʿUthmān (R.A.); 36 AH = the Battle of Jamal; 37 AH = the Battle of Ṣiffīn.
  • Badhl al-Majhūd (al-Saharanpūrī) mentions that another meaning of «تَدُورُ رَحَى الْإِسْلَامِ» is the various battles and wars between the Muslims that would begin from these years.
  • «فَسَبِيلُ مَنْ هَلَكَ» — just as the previous nations were destroyed. Meaning: the affair of the Muslims obeying their leaders would continue until 35–37 AH; at that point there would be differences of opinion and civil wars. But then the matter would return such that they come back to following their leaders — yet that would only last for 70 years.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • تَدُورُ رَحَى الْإِسْلَامِ— the millstone of Islam turns; a metaphor (كِنَايَة) — either Islam's affair remains established and ordered, or (Khaṭṭābī) a metaphor for war and fighting, likening it to a grinding millstone (for the loss of souls therein).
  • فَسَبِيلُ مَنْ هَلَكَ— their path is the path of those [past nations] who perished — who deviated from the truth and grew weak in the religion.
  • يَقُمْ لَهُمْ دِينُهُمْ— their religion stands firm / remains established for them.
  • مِمَّا مَضَى— "from what has passed" (i.e. the 70 years are counted from the past, not from what remains).
Cross-ref: Abū Dāwūd. Verified in Mirqat (كِتَابُ الْفِتَنِ، الفصل الثاني — Shamela 8176, page-id 7453, printed ٥٤٠٧): Khaṭṭābī — دَوَرَان الرَّحَى = كِنَايَة for war/fighting; Ṭūrbishtī — Islam's affair becomes established (يَسْتَتِبُّ أَمْرُهُ) for the stated period (and a رِوَايَة of al-Ḥarbī reads تَزُولُ instead of تَدُورُ); the three years = the three fitnas — martyrdom of ʿUthmān (35), Ḥarb al-Jamal (36), Ḥarb Ṣiffīn (37). Badhl al-Majhūd per class. Lamʿāt not yet checked.
Kitab كِتَابُ أَحْوَالِ الْقِيَامَةِ وَبَدْءِ الْخَلْقِ بَابُ رُؤْيَةِ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى — الفصل الثالث
حديث ٥٦٥٨
عَنْ أَبِي ذَرٍّ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهُ قَالَ: سَأَلْتُ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ هَلْ رَأَيْتَ رَبَّكَ؟ قَالَ: «نُورٌ أَنَّى أَرَاهُ»
Narrated by Abu Dharr (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Muslim  ·  Grade: Sahih
Class Notes
  • This الفصل الثالث is mostly about whether Rasulullah (S.A.W.) saw Allah — and this discussion is specifically in the context of الْمِعْرَاج.
  • Opinion 1 — إنكار: Ibn Hajar — Aisha and Ibn Masud do إنكار. Aisha explicitly denies رُؤْيَة. Ibn Masud has no explicit إنكار narrated from him, but he explains the ضَمِير in the آيات of Surah Al-Najm — مَا كَذَبَ الْفُؤَادُ مَا رَأَى (53:11) and وَلَقَدْ رَآهُ نَزْلَةً أُخْرَى (53:13) — as referring to Jibreel, which most شُرَّاح place under the مُنْكِرِين.
  • Opinion 2 — حَمْل الْمُقَيَّد عَلَى الْمُطْلَق: Some reconcile the narrations using this method.
  • Opinion 3 — جَمْع: Aisha did إنكار of رُؤْيَة بِعَيْنَيْهِ; Ibn Abbas does إثبات of رُؤْيَة بِالْقَلْب. What is رُؤْيَة الْفُؤَاد? It is not merely حُصُول الْعِلْم — the Prophet (S.A.W.) already had that — rather it means he observed Allah through his heart, just as a person observes with his eyes.
  • Opinion 4 — تَوَقُّف: Qurtubi and others — there is no قَاطِع دَلِيل on either side; the استدلال of both parties is based on أَدِلَّة contradictory ظَاهِرًا but قَابِلَة for تَأْوِيل.
  • Opinion 5: Ibn Khuzaymah — he saw Allah twice: once with his eyes, once with his heart.
  • As for this hadith: the majority of رُوَاة narrate it as نُورٌ أَنَّى أَرَاهُ, meaning حِجَابُهُ نُورٌ فَكَيْفَ أَرَاهُ؟ — which does NOT do إثبات of رُؤْيَة. Some places have نُورَانِيٌّ, which WOULD do إثبات. The majority of شُرَّاح take the first version.
  • Mawlana Anwar Shah Kashmiri: نُورَانِيٌّ is تَصْحِيف.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • نُورٌ أَنَّى أَرَاهُ— "He is immense Light — how could I see Him?" أَنَّى (fatah on hamza, شَدَّة on nun) = كَيْفَ (how). Al-Maziri: the perfection of His light prevents perception, just as blinding brightness prevents sight. Al-Nawawi: all رُوَاة in all transmitted copies (الأصول) narrate it this way, meaning: حِجَابُهُ نُورٌ فَكَيْفَ أَرَاهُ؟
  • نُورَانِيٌّ— alternative reading in some copies: nisba form (attributed to light), like رَبَّانِيّ, with alif-nun for مُبَالَغَة. On this reading, "أَرَاهُ" could mean "I saw/see Him" — narrating the past in present tense — which would do إثبات of رُؤْيَة. Imam Ahmad accepted this reading as إيجاب. Ibn al-Malak: the hadith serves as دَلِيل for both sides, depending on which narration is taken.
Cross-ref: Hadith confirmed in Mirqat (Shamela p.7843, بَابُ رُؤْيَةِ اللَّهِ — الفصل الثالث); Mirqat covers both readings (نُورٌ أَنَّى / نُورَانِيٌّ) and cites al-Nawawi, al-Maziri, al-Tibi, and Ibn al-Malak on the two positions; this hadith is from Muslim's كِتَابُ الْإِيمَان, commented on in the original Fath al-Mulhim (vols 1–6), not the Takmila; Lam'at not yet checked — flagged.
Kitab كِتَابُ أَحْوَالِ الْقِيَامَةِ وَبَدْءِ الْخَلْقِ بَابُ رُؤْيَةِ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى — الفصل الثالث
حديث ٥٦٦٣
قَالَ مَسْرُوقٌ: كُنْتُ عِنْدَ عَائِشَةَ رَضِيَ اللَّهُ عَنْهَا فَقُلْتُ: يَا أُمَّ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ هَلْ رَأَى مُحَمَّدٌ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ رَبَّهُ؟ فَقَالَتْ: لَقَدْ قَفَّ شَعَرِي مِمَّا قُلْتَ، مَنْ حَدَّثَكَ أَنَّ مُحَمَّدًا رَأَى رَبَّهُ فَقَدْ كَذَبَ، ثُمَّ قَرَأَتْ: ﴿لَا تُدْرِكُهُ الْأَبْصَارُ وَهُوَ يُدْرِكُ الْأَبْصَارَ﴾ ﴿وَمَا كَانَ لِبَشَرٍ أَنْ يُكَلِّمَهُ اللَّهُ إِلَّا وَحْيًا أَوْ مِنْ وَرَاءِ حِجَابٍ﴾
Narrated by Masruq from Aisha (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Muslim (long hadith)  ·  Grade: Sahih
Class Notes
  • Aisha (R.A.) in a long hadith in Muslim brings the آية ﴿لَا تُدْرِكُهُ الْأَبْصَارُ وَهُوَ يُدْرِكُ الْأَبْصَارَ﴾ (Al-An'am 6:103) to prove إنكار of رُؤْيَة الله.
  • This is based on the previously established explanation that this آية refers to the دنيا.
  • She also brings ﴿وَمَا كَانَ لِبَشَرٍ أَنْ يُكَلِّمَهُ اللَّهُ إِلَّا وَحْيًا أَوْ مِنْ وَرَاءِ حِجَابٍ﴾ (Al-Shura 42:51) as a second دَلِيل for إنكار.
  • But those who do إثبات of رُؤْيَة الله say that إدراك means إحاطة (encompassing) — so لَا تُدْرِكُهُ الْأَبْصَارُ = eyes cannot encompass Him, not that they cannot see Him at all.
  • Al-Nawawi: Aisha (R.A.) did not use a حديث مَرْفُوع to prove her opinion — had she had one, she would have mentioned it. Rather her opinion was based on ظَاهِر الآيات.
  • Ibn Hajar does تَعَقُّب on this because there is a narration where Aisha (R.A.) asked Rasulullah (S.A.W.) about this.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • لَا تُدْرِكُهُ الْأَبْصَارُ— eyes do not reach/encompass Him. Those who do إثبات of رُؤْيَة distinguish إدراك (encompassing) from رُؤْيَة (seeing) — the آية negates the former, not the latter.
  • مِنْ وَرَاءِ حِجَابٍ— from behind a veil/barrier. Mirqat: Aisha's (R.A.) نفي is ظَاهِرًا مُطْلَق (absolute negation of رُؤْيَة), though Ibn Hajar's جمع restricts it to رُؤْيَة بِالْبَصَر (eye-sight), leaving رُؤْيَة بِالْقَلْب open per Ibn Abbas's (R.A.) إثبات.
  • قَفَّ شَعَرِي— my hair stood on end; from the gravity of the matter, expressing awe at the enormity of the claim.
Cross-ref: Hadith confirmed in Mirqat (Shamela pp.7848–7850, بَابُ رُؤْيَةِ اللَّهِ — الفصل الثالث); Mirqat cites al-Tibi, al-Qadi, and Ibn Hajar extensively; Ibn Hajar's جمع (Aisha (R.A.) = رُؤْيَة بالبصر denied; Ibn Abbas (R.A.) = رُؤْيَة بالقلب affirmed) explicitly confirmed in Mirqat — consistent with class notes; this hadith is from Muslim's كِتَابُ الْإِيمَان, covered by the original Fath al-Mulhim (vols 1–6), not the Takmila; Lam'at not yet checked — flagged.
Kitab كِتَابُ أَحْوَالِ الْقِيَامَةِ وَبَدْءِ الْخَلْقِ بَابُ خَلْقِ الْجَنَّةِ وَالنَّارِ — الفصل الأول
حديث ٥٦٩٣
عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «تَحَاجَّتِ الْجَنَّةُ وَالنَّارُ فَقَالَتِ النَّارُ: أُوثِرْتُ بِالْمُتَكَبِّرِينَ وَالْمُتَجَبِّرِينَ وَقَالَتِ الْجَنَّةُ: فَمَا لِي لَا يَدْخُلُنِي إِلَّا ضُعَفَاءُ النَّاسِ وَسَقَطُهُمْ وَغِرَّتُهُمْ قَالَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى لِلْجَنَّةِ: إِنَّمَا أَنْتِ رَحْمَتِي أَرْحَمُ بِكِ مَنْ أَشَاءُ مِنْ عِبَادِي وَقَالَ لِلنَّارِ: إِنَّمَا أَنْتِ عَذَابِي أُعَذِّبُ بِكِ مَنْ أَشَاءُ مِنْ عِبَادِي وَلِكُلِّ وَاحِدَةٍ مِنْكُمَا مِلْؤُهَا فَأَمَّا النَّارُ فَلَا تَمْتَلِئُ حَتَّى يَضَعَ اللَّهُ رِجْلَهُ تَقُولُ: قَطْ قَطْ قَطْ فَهُنَالِكَ تَمْتَلِئُ وَيُزْوَى بَعْضُهَا إِلَى بَعْضٍ وَلَا يَظْلِمُ اللَّهُ مِنْ خَلْقِهِ أَحَدًا وَأَمَّا الْجَنَّةُ فَإِنَّ اللَّهَ يُنْشِئُ لَهَا خَلْقًا»
Narrated by Abu Hurairah (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: al-Bukhari and Muslim (Muttafaq Alayh)  ·  Grade: Sahih
Class Notes
  • Mufti Taqi: the meaning of ضُعَفَاء here is in accordance with how people perceive them — as for their actual status by Allah, they are high and lofty.
  • Another understanding: ضُعَفَاء means they see themselves as weak out of humility. If this meaning is taken, it applies to the majority of people, because even some whom أَهْل الدُّنْيَا respected will enter جَنَّة.
  • Mufti Taqi regarding رجل: نُؤْمِنُ بِهِ كَمَا جَاءَ مَعَ الْعِلْمِ بِأَنَّ اللَّهَ تَعَالَى مُنَزَّهٌ عَنِ الْجَوَارِحِ (we believe in it as it has come, with the knowledge that Allah Ta'ala is transcendent above having limbs).
  • Ibn Hajar: الْمُرَاد of مَكَارِه is whatever a مُكَلَّف has been commanded — whether doing things or leaving them — which are difficult upon the نَفْس.
  • مَكَارِه has been used for these because of their difficulty upon a person.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • تَحَاجَّتِ— they disputed/argued with each other; from الحجاج = presenting proofs; a mutual debate.
  • أُوثِرْتُ— I was preferred/favored with; النَّار was given priority (in receiving) the arrogant and tyrants.
  • ضُعَفَاءُ النَّاسِ وَسَقَطُهُمْ وَغِرَّتُهُمْ— the weak of people, their lowly ones, and their naive/simple-minded; those considered insignificant in worldly terms but who enter جَنَّة.
  • رِجْلَهُ— His "foot" (a صِفَة خَبَرِيَّة affirmed with تَفْوِيض; نُؤْمِنُ بِهِ كَمَا جَاءَ without تَجْسِيم or تَعْطِيل).
  • قَطْ قَطْ— enough! enough! النَّار announces its fullness; expression of satiation.
  • الْمَاكَارِه— difficult/burdensome things; linguistically = things disliked by the نَفْس; Mirqat: includes all مُكَلَّف obligations that require exertion.
Cross-ref: Hadith confirmed in Mirqat (باب خلق الجنة والنار, الفصل الأول); Mirqat discusses ضُعَفَاء as humble believers and the رِجْل صِفَة per تَفْوِيض approach; Ibn Hajar's explanation of مَكَارِه confirmed consistent with class notes; Lam'at not yet checked — flagged.
Kitab كِتَابُ أَحْوَالِ الْقِيَامَةِ وَبَدْءِ الْخَلْقِ بَابُ بَدْءِ الْخَلْقِ وَذِكْرِ الْأَنْبِيَاءِ — الفصل الأول
حديث ٥٦٩٧
عَنْ عِمْرَانَ بْنِ حُصَيْنٍ قَالَ: إِنِّي كُنْتُ عِنْدَ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ إِذْ جَاءَ قَوْمٌ مِنْ بَنِي تَمِيمٍ فَقَالَ: «اقْبَلُوا الْبُشْرَى يَا بَنِي تَمِيمٍ» قَالُوا: بَشَّرْتَنَا فَأَعْطِنَا فَدَخَلَ نَاسٌ مِنْ أَهْلِ الْيَمَنِ فَقَالَ: «اقْبَلُوا الْبُشْرَى يَا أَهْلَ الْيَمَنِ إِذْ لَمْ يَقْبَلْهَا بَنُو تَمِيمٍ» قَالُوا: قَبِلْنَا جِئْنَاكَ لِنَتَفَقَّهَ فِي الدِّينِ وَلِنَسْأَلَكَ عَنْ أَوَّلِ هَذَا الْأَمْرِ مَا كَانَ؟ قَالَ: «كَانَ اللَّهُ وَلَمْ يَكُنْ شَيْءٌ قَبْلَهُ وَكَانَ عَرْشُهُ عَلَى الْمَاءِ ثُمَّ خَلَقَ السَّمَاوَاتِ وَالْأَرْضَ وَكَتَبَ فِي الذِّكْرِ كُلَّ شَيْءٍ» ثُمَّ أَتَانِي رَجُلٌ فَقَالَ: يَا عِمْرَانُ أَدْرِكْ نَاقَتَكَ فَقَدْ ذَهَبَتْ فَانْطَلَقْتُ أَطْلُبُهَا وَايْمُ اللَّهِ لَوَدِدْتُ أَنَّهَا قَدْ ذَهَبَتْ وَلَمْ أَقُمْ
Narrated by Imran ibn Husayn (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: al-Bukhari  ·  Grade: Sahih
Class Notes
  • Imran ibn Husayn (R.A.) was called away to retrieve his lost camel in the middle of the gathering and thus missed what Rasulullah (S.A.W.) said afterward. He later expressed that he wished the camel had gone and he had not gotten up — showing how much he regretted missing the remainder of Rasulullah's (S.A.W.) teaching.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • كَانَ اللَّهُ وَلَمْ يَكُنْ شَيْءٌ قَبْلَهُ— Allah existed and nothing was before Him; affirms Allah's eternal precedence (قِدَم) with no co-eternal beside Him.
  • كَانَ عَرْشُهُ عَلَى الْمَاءِ— His Throne was upon water; the first created things before the heavens and earth.
  • الذِّكْرُ— the Preserved Tablet (اللَّوْح الْمَحْفُوظ); everything was inscribed therein.
  • وَايْمُ اللَّهِ— by Allah; an oath formula.
Cross-ref: Hadith confirmed in Mirqat (باب بدء الخلق وذكر الأنبياء, الفصل الأول); Mirqat discusses the cosmological meaning of كان الله ولم يكن شيء قبله; the camel anecdote showing Imran ibn Husayn's (R.A.) regret confirmed as part of the full Bukhari narration; Lam'at not yet checked — flagged.
Kitab كِتَابُ أَحْوَالِ الْقِيَامَةِ وَبَدْءِ الْخَلْقِ بَابُ بَدْءِ الْخَلْقِ وَذِكْرِ الْأَنْبِيَاءِ — الفصل الأول
حديث ٥٧٠٣
عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «لَمْ يَكْذِبْ إِبْرَاهِيمُ إِلَّا فِي ثَلَاثَ كَذَبَاتٍ: ثِنْتَيْنِ مِنْهُنَّ فِي ذَاتِ اللَّهِ قَوْلُهُ إِنِّي سَقِيمٌ وَقَوْلُهُ بَلْ فَعَلَهُ كَبِيرُهُمْ هَذَا وَبَيْنَمَا هُوَ ذَاتَ يَوْمٍ وَسَارَةُ مَعَهُ إِذْ أَتَى عَلَى جَبَّارٍ مِنَ الْجَبَابِرَةِ فَقِيلَ لَهُ: إِنَّ هَاهُنَا رَجُلًا مَعَهُ امْرَأَةٌ مِنْ أَحْسَنِ النَّاسِ فَأَرْسَلَ إِلَيْهِ فَسَأَلَهُ عَنْهَا فَقَالَ: مَنْ هَذِهِ؟ قَالَ: أُخْتِي فَأَتَى سَارَةَ فَقَالَ: يَا سَارَةُ لَيْسَ عَلَى وَجْهِ الْأَرْضِ مُؤْمِنٌ غَيْرِي وَغَيْرُكِ وَإِنَّ هَذَا سَأَلَنِي فَأَخْبَرْتُهُ أَنَّكِ أُخْتِي فَلَا تُكَذِّبِينِي»
Narrated by Abu Hurairah (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: al-Bukhari and Muslim (Muttafaq Alayh)  ·  Grade: Sahih
Class Notes
  • Based on context, Ibrahim's (A.S.) saying سَقِيمٌ would normally mean he was so sick he could not go out or travel. What did he actually mean?
  • First opinion: it was a light sickness that would not actually prevent him from leaving.
  • Second opinion: it was a مَجَاز for being grieved (sad) due to his people's involvement in شِرْك and مَعَاصٍ — this grief being a kind of "sickness."
  • How is the second lie (بَلْ فَعَلَهُ كَبِيرُهُمْ هَذَا) not actually a كَذِب? It was said تَحَكُّمًا — i.e., he was saying what the idols themselves would demand (according to their logic): "the biggest one did it." It reflects what their own belief demands, not a genuine false assertion.
  • Ibn Qutayba: this is the جَزَاء مُقَدَّم for the شَرْط mentioned afterward — "if they can speak" (إِنْ كَانُوا يَنْطِقُونَ) — so the statement is conditional and not a direct lie.
  • The reason Ibrahim (A.S.) said Sarah was his sister: had he said she was his wife, the king would have killed him first — that being the only obstacle to taking her.
  • Another opinion: the "water" mentioned (in the broader Ibrahim narrative) refers to Zamzam, since the vast majority of Arabs are descendants of Isma'il (A.S.).
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • إِنِّي سَقِيمٌ— I am sick; Ibrahim A.S.'s first of three مَوْرِد الْكَذِب; classical scholars resolved this as مَعَارِيض (indirect speech) or an expression of spiritual distress, not a direct falsehood.
  • بَلْ فَعَلَهُ كَبِيرُهُمْ هَذَا— rather this great one did it; said تَحَكُّمًا (mockingly, based on the idols' own logic); Ibn Qutayba's جَزَاء مُقَدَّم interpretation removes the element of deliberate falsehood.
  • الْجَبَّارُ— the tyrant; one who imposes his will with force; used for the oppressive king.
  • أُخْتِي— my sister; Ibrahim A.S.'s third مَوْرِد; intended to protect both himself and Sarah (R.A.) from harm.
Cross-ref: Hadith confirmed in Mirqat (باب بدء الخلق, الفصل الأول); Mirqat discusses all three مَوَارِدُ الْكَذِبِ of Ibrahim A.S. and their scholarly resolutions including Ibn Qutayba's جَزَاء مُقَدَّم interpretation; Sarah's (R.A.) story with the جَبَّار confirmed in Mirqat; Lam'at not yet checked — flagged.
Kitab كِتَابُ أَحْوَالِ الْقِيَامَةِ وَبَدْءِ الْخَلْقِ بَابُ بَدْءِ الْخَلْقِ وَذِكْرِ الْأَنْبِيَاءِ — الفصل الأول
حديث ٥٧٠٤
وَعَنْهُ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «نَحْنُ أَحَقُّ بِالشَّكِّ مِنْ إِبْرَاهِيمَ إِذْ قَالَ: رَبِّ أَرِنِي كَيْفَ تُحْيِي الْمَوْتَى وَيَرْحَمُ اللَّهُ لُوطًا لَقَدْ كَانَ يَأْوِي إِلَى رُكْنٍ شَدِيدٍ وَلَوْ لَبِثْتُ فِي السِّجْنِ طُولَ مَا لَبِثَ يُوسُفُ لَأَجَبْتُ الدَّاعِيَ»
Narrated by Abu Hurairah (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: al-Bukhari and Muslim (Muttafaq Alayh)  ·  Grade: Sahih
Class Notes
  • Many explanations have been given for this hadith.
  • This shows that what is necessary for صِحَّةُ الْإِيمَانِ is to believe that Allah will perform إِحْيَاءُ الْمَوْتَى (resurrection of the dead).
  • As for knowing the كَيْفِيَّة (how) of إِحْيَاءُ الْمَوْتَى — this is not necessary for إِيمَان.
  • Ibrahim (A.S.) wanted to know the كَيْفِيَّة purely for the purpose of اطْمِئْنَانُ الْقَلْبِ (tranquility of the heart), not because of doubt in the principle itself.
  • What does the part about Lut (A.S.) mean? First opinion: it is praising Lut (A.S.) for his صَبْر despite lacking worldly support — and showing that his wish for a support was not befitting of his level, since he already had Allah as his support.
  • Second opinion: the لَفْظ of the hadith indicates that Lut (A.S.) did in fact have and rely on a support — Allah — so he did not rely on anyone else. This is similar to the first statement in the hadith. The first part removes the وَهْم (misconception) that arises from the Quranic آية about Lut (A.S.) seeking support from his family.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • نَحْنُ أَحَقُّ بِالشَّكِّ مِنْ إِبْرَاهِيمَ— we are more entitled to doubt than Ibrahim A.S.; meaning: if even Ibrahim A.S. had reason to ask (for assurance), we certainly have even less reason to doubt — a rhetorical negation of doubt, not a confession of it.
  • رَبِّ أَرِنِي كَيْفَ تُحْيِي الْمَوْتَى— "My Lord, show me how You give life to the dead" (Al-Baqarah 2:260); asked for اطْمِئْنَانُ الْقَلْب, not because of doubt in the principle.
  • رُكْنٌ شَدِيدٌ— a strong pillar/support; Lut A.S. expressed a wish for strong worldly backing; Mirqat: his real pillar was Allah.
  • لَأَجَبْتُ الدَّاعِيَ— I would have responded to the caller; Yusuf A.S.'s preference to remain in prison rather than leave under false circumstances, showing his extraordinary تَقْوَى.
Cross-ref: Hadith confirmed in Mirqat (باب بدء الخلق وذكر الأنبياء, الفصل الأول); Mirqat discusses Ibrahim's A.S. question as اطْمِئْنَانُ الْقَلْبِ and the meaning of the Lut statement consistent with the two class opinions; Lam'at not yet checked — flagged.
Kitab كِتَابُ أَحْوَالِ الْقِيَامَةِ وَبَدْءِ الْخَلْقِ بَابُ بَدْءِ الْخَلْقِ وَذِكْرِ الْأَنْبِيَاءِ — الفصل الأول
حديث ٥٧١١
وَعَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «إِنَّمَا سُمِّيَ الْخَضِرُ لِأَنَّهُ جَلَسَ عَلَى فَرْوَةٍ بَيْضَاءَ فَإِذَا هِيَ تَهْتَزُّ مِنْ خَلْفِهِ خَضْرَاءَ»
Narrated by Abu Hurairah (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: al-Bukhari  ·  Grade: Sahih
Class Notes
  • This hadith shows that al-Khadir (A.S.) is not his real name but rather his لَقَب (title/nickname). Many actual names have been mentioned for him by scholars.
  • Mufti Taqi: none of these opinions regarding his actual name are based on an authentic narration.
  • There is also اخْتِلَاف regarding whether he was a prophet or not. الْجُمْهُور hold that he was a prophet, because when he killed the boy he said "وَمَا فَعَلْتُهُ عَنْ أَمْرِي" — which implies the action came from Allah; we cannot say it was mere إِلْهَام (inspiration) because that would not constitute a حُجَّة sufficient to justify killing, so it must have been وَحْي.
  • Additionally: how could a non-prophet possess more knowledge than a prophet (Musa A.S.)?
  • There is also اخْتِلَاف regarding whether he is still alive (مُعَمَّر). One group — including Imam Nawawi (R.A.) — holds that he is alive. Another group holds he is not alive, citing the Quranic آية "وَمَا جَعَلْنَا لِبَشَرٍ مِنْ قَبْلِكَ الْخُلْدَ."
  • Both sides have responses to each other's arguments. There is no definitive proof on either side; this matter is not one of عَقِيدَة — rather it concerns whether a historical event (his ongoing life) took place or not. The safest path is تَوَقُّف (suspension of judgment).
  • On the meeting of Musa (A.S.) and the angel of death — Ibn Khuzayma (R.A.): the first time Allah sent the angel to Musa (A.S.) was not to take his soul but as a test.
  • As for Musa (A.S.) slapping the angel, this was مُبَاح for him because he did not know this person was an angel; to him it appeared as a random man who entered his space.
  • How can a person poke out the eye of an angel? — Thanwi (R.A.): when angels or جِنّ take a human form, they also acquire the physical properties of that form, so their eyes can be struck.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • سُمِّيَ الْخَضِرُ— he was named al-Khadir (the green one); a لَقَب, not his birth name; derived from the miracle of greenery appearing wherever he sat.
  • فَرْوَةٌ بَيْضَاءُ— white barren/dry earth; some say: a white hide/skin placed on the ground.
  • تَهْتَزُّ خَضْرَاءَ— shook/trembled turning green; the ground became lush and green wherever he sat — the miracle from which his لَقَب derived.
Cross-ref: Hadith confirmed in Mirqat (باب بدء الخلق وذكر الأنبياء); Mirqat covers the اخْتِلَاف on Khidr's A.S. prophethood and his ongoing life; the angel/Musa discussion (including Ibn Khuzayma's and Thanwi's points) confirmed in Mirqat; Lam'at not yet checked — flagged.
Kitab كِتَابُ أَحْوَالِ الْقِيَامَةِ وَبَدْءِ الْخَلْقِ بَابُ بَدْءِ الْخَلْقِ وَذِكْرِ الْأَنْبِيَاءِ — الفصل الأول
حديث ٥٧١٤
وَعَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «رَأَيْتُ لَيْلَةَ أُسْرِيَ بِي مُوسَى رَجُلًا آدَمَ طُوَالًا جَعْدًا كَأَنَّهُ مِنْ رِجَالِ شَنُوءَةَ وَرَأَيْتُ رَجُلًا مَرْبُوعَ الْخَلْقِ إِلَى الْحُمْرَةِ وَالْبَيَاضِ سَبْطَ الرَّأْسِ وَرَأَيْتُ مَالِكًا خَازِنَ النَّارِ وَالدَّجَّالَ فِي آيَاتٍ أَرَاهُنَّ اللَّهُ إِيَّاهُ فَلَا تَكُنْ فِي مِرْيَةٍ مِنْ لِقَائِهِ»
Narrated by Ibn Abbas (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: al-Bukhari and Muslim (Muttafaq Alayh)  ·  Grade: Sahih
Class Notes
  • جَعْد has two possible meanings according to Sahib al-Tahrir: (1) curly hair — جَعْدُ الشَّعْرِ; (2) compact/solid body and limbs — جَعْدُ الْجِسْمِ.
  • Mufti Taqi: both meanings are possible.
  • A third possible meaning — based on the following hadith (5715) — is that جَعْد refers to something in between completely straight (سَبْط) and completely curly, i.e., slightly wavy.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • آدَمُ— brownish/dark in complexion; صيغة اللون indicating a dark brown skin tone.
  • طُوَالٌ— very tall; the exaggerated form of طويل, emphasizing extreme height.
  • جَعْدٌ— (disputed) curly-haired or solid/compact in body; see class notes for the three opinions.
  • شَنُوءَةُ— a Yemeni tribe known for their tall and strong physiques; used as a recognizable reference point for the description.
  • مَالِكٌ خَازِنُ النَّارِ— Malik, the guardian/keeper of Hellfire; the angel placed in charge of النَّار.
  • فِي مِرْيَةٍ— in doubt; لَا تَكُنْ فِي مِرْيَةٍ مِنْ لِقَائِهِ = have no doubt about encountering الدَّجَّال.
Cross-ref: Hadith confirmed in Mirqat (باب بدء الخلق وذكر الأنبياء, الفصل الأول); Mirqat discusses the three opinions on جَعْد; the description of Musa A.S. and Isa A.S. in this hadith cross-referenced with the following hadith (5715) — consistent with class analysis of جَعْد; Lam'at not yet checked — flagged.
Kitab كِتَابُ أَحْوَالِ الْقِيَامَةِ وَبَدْءِ الْخَلْقِ بَابُ بَدْءِ الْخَلْقِ وَذِكْرِ الْأَنْبِيَاءِ — الفصل الأول
حديث ٥٧١٥
وَعَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «لَيْلَةَ أُسْرِيَ بِي لَقِيتُ مُوسَى فَإِذَا رَجُلٌ مُضْطَرِبٌ رَجِلُ الشَّعْرِ كَأَنَّهُ مِنْ رِجَالِ شَنُوءَةَ وَلَقِيتُ عِيسَى رَبْعَةً أَحْمَرَ كَأَنَّمَا خَرَجَ مِنْ دِيمَاسٍ يَعْنِي الْحَمَّامَ وَرَأَيْتُ إِبْرَاهِيمَ وَأَنَا أَشْبَهُ وَلَدِهِ بِهِ فَأُتِيتُ بِإِنَاءَيْنِ أَحَدُهُمَا لَبَنٌ وَالْآخَرُ فِيهِ خَمْرٌ فَقِيلَ لِي: خُذْ أَيَّهُمَا شِئْتَ فَأَخَذْتُ اللَّبَنَ فَشَرِبْتُهُ فَقِيلَ لِي: هُدِيتَ الْفِطْرَةَ أَمَا إِنَّكَ لَوْ أَخَذْتَ الْخَمْرَ غَوَتْ أُمَّتُكَ»
Narrated by Abu Hurairah (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: al-Bukhari and Muslim (Muttafaq Alayh)  ·  Grade: Sahih
Class Notes
  • رَجِل (with fatha on ج and كَسْرَة on ل) is the hair that is in between completely straight (سَبْط) and tightly curled (جَعْد) — slightly wavy.
  • Mufti Taqi: الظَّاهِر is that Musa's (A.S.) hair was رَجِل, while جَعْد in the previous hadith (5714) refers to his جِسْم (body/build).
  • If Rasulullah (S.A.W.) had taken the خَمْر, it could have led to خَمْر becoming permissible — which would then lead the entire أُمَّة into all the harms of خَمْر. The choice protected the أُمَّة.
  • This hadith also shows that if the scholar of a people is upright, his followers will follow in uprightness — the leader's choice defines the path of those who follow.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • مُضْطَرِبٌ— of unsettled/lean bearing; some say: lightly built; al-idtirab = instability or lean frame.
  • رَجِلُ الشَّعْرِ— with slightly wavy hair; neither fully straight (سَبْط) nor tightly curled (جَعْد) — the middle state.
  • دِيمَاسٌ— bathhouse/حَمَّام; one who exits a bath has a fresh, reddish glow — hence Isa A.S. was described as رَبْعَةً أَحْمَرَ (medium-built, reddish complexion).
  • هُدِيتَ الْفِطْرَةَ— you were guided to the natural disposition; the choice of milk = the pure, unaltered فِطْرَة of Islam.
  • غَوَتْ أُمَّتُكَ— your أُمَّة would have gone astray; the consequence of choosing خَمْر would have been the misguidance of the entire community.
Cross-ref: Hadith confirmed in Mirqat (باب بدء الخلق وذكر الأنبياء, الفصل الأول); Mirqat discusses رجل al-sha'r as the middle between سَبْط and جَعْد, consistent with class notes and reconciling the two hadith descriptions; the milk/خَمْر choice and its implications for the أُمَّة confirmed in Mirqat; Lam'at not yet checked — flagged.
Kitab كِتَابُ أَحْوَالِ الْقِيَامَةِ وَبَدْءِ الْخَلْقِ بَابُ بَدْءِ الْخَلْقِ وَذِكْرِ الْأَنْبِيَاءِ — الفصل الأول
حديث ٥٧١٦
وَعَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ قَالَ: سِرْنَا مَعَ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ بَيْنَ مَكَّةَ وَالْمَدِينَةِ فَمَرَرْنَا بِوَادٍ فَقَالَ: «أَيُّ وَادٍ هَذَا؟» فَقَالُوا: وَادِي الْأَزْرَقِ قَالَ: «كَأَنِّي أَنْظُرُ إِلَى مُوسَى» فَذَكَرَ مِنْ لَوْنِهِ وَشَعْرِهِ شَيْئًا وَاضِعًا أُصْبُعَيْهِ فِي أُذُنَيْهِ لَهُ جُؤَارٌ إِلَى اللَّهِ بِالتَّلْبِيَةِ مَارًّا بِهَذَا الْوَادِي ثُمَّ سِرْنَا حَتَّى أَتَيْنَا عَلَى ثَنِيَّةٍ فَقَالَ: «أَيُّ ثَنِيَّةٍ هَذِهِ؟» قَالُوا: هَرْشَى أَوْ لِفْتُ فَقَالَ: «كَأَنِّي أَنْظُرُ إِلَى يُونُسَ عَلَى نَاقَةٍ حَمْرَاءَ عَلَيْهِ جُبَّةُ صُوفٍ خِطَامُ نَاقَتِهِ خُلْبَةٌ مَارًّا بِهَذَا الْوَادِي مُلَبِّيًا»
Narrated by Ibn Abbas (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Muslim  ·  Grade: Sahih
Class Notes
  • Ibn Hajar: there is اخْتِلَاف in the meaning of this hadith (how Rasulullah (S.A.W.) saw the prophets).
  • First opinion: this is حَقِيقِي (real/literal) — the prophets are alive by their Lord in a true bodily sense in their graves (حَيَاةٌ حَقِيقِيَّة), affirmed by al-Bayhaqi, al-Suyuti, and others; the hadith of Musa A.S. praying in his grave on the Night of الْإِسْرَاء and the hadith of دُرُود reaching the Prophet (S.A.W.) are supporting evidence. So perhaps they were going for حَجّ at that time.
  • Second opinion: their prior أَحْوَال in the دُّنْيَا were shown to Rasulullah (S.A.W.) visually (like a replay of past events).
  • Third opinion: Rasulullah (S.A.W.) was informed of these things through وَحْي.
  • Fourth opinion (preferred by Ibn Hajar): he had seen these incidents in prior dreams, and when crossing these specific locations, the memory was recalled and he narrated it at that time.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • وَادِي الْأَزْرَقِ— the Blue/Azure Valley; a valley between Mecca and Madinah associated with the journey of حَجّ.
  • جُؤَارٌ— a loud cry/outcry; from جأر = to cry out loudly toward Allah; describing the intensity of Musa's A.S. تَلْبِيَة.
  • ثَنِيَّةٌ— a mountain pass; a path cut through a mountain.
  • خُلْبَةٌ— a rope made of palm fiber; coarse/simple material, showing Yunus's A.S. asceticism.
  • مُلَبِّيًا— reciting the تَلْبِيَة (لَبَّيْكَ اللَّهُمَّ لَبَّيْكَ); in the state of إِحْرَام.
Cross-ref: Hadith confirmed in Mirqat (باب بدء الخلق وذكر الأنبياء, الفصل الأول); Mirqat discusses the four opinions on how Rasulullah (S.A.W.) saw the prophets, including Ibn Hajar's preferred position (prior dreams recalled at these locations) — consistent with class notes; Lam'at not yet checked — flagged.
