Kitab كِتَابُ أَحْوَالِ الْقِيَامَةِ وَبَدْءِ الْخَلْقِ بَابُ بَدْءِ الْخَلْقِ وَذِكْرِ الْأَنْبِيَاءِ — الفصل الأول
حديث ٥٧١٧
وَعَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ عَنِ النَّبِيِّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «خُفِّفَ عَلَى دَاوُدَ الْقُرْآنُ فَكَانَ يَأْمُرُ بِدَوَابِّهِ فَتُسَرَّحَ فَيَقْرَأُ الْقُرْآنَ قَبْلَ أَنْ تُسَرَّحَ دَوَابُّهُ وَلَا يَأْكُلُ إِلَّا مِنْ عَمَلِ يَدَيْهِ»
Narrated by Abu Hurairah (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: al-Bukhari  ·  Grade: Sahih
Class Notes
  • Dawud (A.S.) would command for his animals to be prepared — placing saddles on them for riding — and before the preparation was even complete, he would finish reciting the entire Quran (الزَّبُور), demonstrating how greatly it was made easy for him.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • خُفِّفَ عَلَيْهِ الْقُرْآنُ— the Quran (Zabur) was made light/easy for him; Allah granted him extraordinary facility in recitation — speed and ease unparalleled among others.
  • دَوَابُّ— riding animals; mounts; plural of دابة.
  • فَتُسَرَّحَ— they were released to graze / prepared; he would begin recitation while the animals were being attended to and finish before they were ready.
  • لَا يَأْكُلُ إِلَّا مِنْ عَمَلِ يَدَيْهِ— he ate only from the labor of his own hands; Dawud A.S. was a blacksmith (making armor); a lesson in dignity through self-sufficiency.
Cross-ref: Hadith confirmed in Mirqat (باب بدء الخلق وذكر الأنبياء, الفصل الأول); Mirqat confirms the ease of recitation for Dawud A.S. and notes his self-sufficiency through manual labor; Lam'at not yet checked — flagged.
Kitab كِتَابُ أَحْوَالِ الْقِيَامَةِ وَبَدْءِ الْخَلْقِ بَابُ بَدْءِ الْخَلْقِ وَذِكْرِ الْأَنْبِيَاءِ — الفصل الأول
حديث ٥٧١٨
كَانَتِ امْرَأَتَانِ مَعَهُمَا ابْنَاهُمَا جَاءَ الذِّئْبُ فَذَهَبَ بِابْنِ إِحْدَاهُمَا فَقَالَتْ صَاحِبَتُهَا: إِنَّمَا ذَهَبَ بِابْنِكِ وَقَالَتِ الْأُخْرَى: إِنَّمَا ذَهَبَ بِابْنِكِ فَتَحَاكَمَتَا إِلَى دَاوُدَ فَقَضَى بِهِ لِلْكُبْرَى فَخَرَجَتَا عَلَى سُلَيْمَانَ بْنِ دَاوُدَ فَأَخْبَرَتَاهُ فَقَالَ: ائْتُونِي بِالسِّكِّينِ أَشُقُّهُ بَيْنَكُمَا فَقَالَتِ الصُّغْرَى: لَا تَفْعَلْ يَرْحَمُكَ اللَّهُ هُوَ ابْنُهَا فَقَضَى بِهِ لِلصُّغْرَى
Narrated by Abu Hurairah (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: al-Bukhari and Muslim (Muttafaq Alayh)  ·  Grade: Sahih
Class Notes
  • How did they not know which child was taken? Both children looked very similar.
  • One of them was lying — she simply wanted to feel comfort (أُنْس) by taking the other's child as her own.
  • Sulayman (A.S.) gave the child to the younger woman (الصُّغْرَى) because she showed such overwhelming شَفَقَة (maternal compassion) that she willingly gave up her claim to keep the child alive. That depth of شَفَقَة demonstrated she was the real mother.
  • How did Sulayman (A.S.) override the ruling of Dawud (A.S.)? — Mufti Taqi (best answer): Nawawi (R.A.) states that Sulayman (A.S.) did not intend to overturn Dawud's (A.S.) ruling; rather he employed a حِيلَة (stratagem) to bring the truth to light. Once the truth became evident, الْكُبْرَى made إِقْرَار (admission) since she was already caught.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • تَحَاكَمَتَا— they referred their dispute to a judge; sought arbitration.
  • السِّكِّينُ— knife; Sulayman A.S. called for it as a stratagem (حِيلَة) to provoke the real mother's reaction, not with actual intent to cut.
  • الشَّفَقَةُ— tender compassion; the الصُّغْرَى's willingness to surrender her claim to save the child's life revealed she was the true mother.
  • الصُّغْرَى / الْكُبْرَى— the younger / the older of the two women; the الْكُبْرَى was the false claimant.
Cross-ref: Hadith confirmed in Mirqat (باب بدء الخلق وذكر الأنبياء, الفصل الأول); Mirqat cites Nawawi's explanation that Sulayman A.S. used a حِيلَة for اسْتِنْبَاطُ الْحَقِّ rather than overturning Dawud's ruling — consistent with class notes; Lam'at not yet checked — flagged.
Kitab كِتَابُ أَحْوَالِ الْقِيَامَةِ وَبَدْءِ الْخَلْقِ بَابُ بَدْءِ الْخَلْقِ وَذِكْرِ الْأَنْبِيَاءِ — الفصل الأول
حديث ٥٧١٩
وَعَنْهُ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «قَالَ سُلَيْمَانُ: لَأَطُوفَنَّ اللَّيْلَةَ عَلَى تِسْعِينَ امْرَأَةً وَفِي رِوَايَةٍ: بِمِائَةِ امْرَأَةٍ كُلُّهُنَّ تَأْتِي بِفَارِسٍ يُجَاهِدُ فِي سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ فَقَالَ لَهُ الْمَلَكُ: قُلْ إِنْ شَاءَ اللَّهُ فَلَمْ يَقُلْ وَنَسِيَ فَطَافَ عَلَيْهِنَّ فَلَمْ تَحْمِلْ مِنْهُنَّ إِلَّا امْرَأَةٌ وَاحِدَةٌ جَاءَتْ بِشَقِّ رَجُلٍ وَأَيْمُ الَّذِي نَفْسُ مُحَمَّدٍ بِيَدِهِ لَوْ قَالَ: إِنْ شَاءَ اللَّهُ لَجَاهَدُوا فِي سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ فُرْسَانًا أَجْمَعُونَ»
Narrated by Abu Hurairah (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: al-Bukhari and Muslim (Muttafaq Alayh)  ·  Grade: Sahih
Class Notes
  • Other narrations mention different numbers such as 60. Some scholars say the higher numbers do not negate the lower ones — they refer to different contexts or are narrated with variation.
  • Does this hadith contradict the hadith prohibiting saying "law" (لَوْ)? Mufti Taqi's answer: if the intent of "law" is purely to express regret and to imply that the أَسْبَاب (causes) are the only determining factor — without recognizing قَدَر — then that usage is prohibited.
  • But if a person says "law" to learn from a past mistake, to avoid repeating it, while acknowledging that قَدَر was operative throughout, then this usage of "law" is not prohibited. Sulayman's (A.S.) case here falls into this permissible usage.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • لَأَطُوفَنَّ— I will certainly go around (to each wife); emphatic lam with oath, expressing firm intention.
  • شَقُّ رَجُلٍ— half a man; the one child born was stillborn or incomplete — the result of forgetting إِنْ شَاءَ اللَّهُ.
  • لَوْ قَالَ إِنْ شَاءَ اللَّهُ— had he said "If Allah wills"; the pivotal omission; the lesson is that all intentions must be attached to Allah's will.
  • فُرْسَانًا أَجْمَعُونَ— all of them mounted warriors; the full realization of his noble intention would have occurred had he said إِنْ شَاءَ اللَّهُ.
Cross-ref: Hadith confirmed in Mirqat (باب بدء الخلق وذكر الأنبياء, الفصل الأول); Mirqat discusses the different narrated numbers and the permissibility of "law" in the context of learning — consistent with Mufti Taqi's explanation in class; Lam'at not yet checked — flagged.
Kitab كِتَابُ أَحْوَالِ الْقِيَامَةِ وَبَدْءِ الْخَلْقِ بَابُ بَدْءِ الْخَلْقِ وَذِكْرِ الْأَنْبِيَاءِ — الفصل الثاني
حديث ٥٧٢٤
عَنْ أَبِي رَزِينٍ قَالَ: قُلْتُ: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ أَيْنَ رَبُّنَا قَبْلَ أَنْ يَخْلُقَ خَلْقَهُ؟ قَالَ: «كَانَ فِي عَمَاءٍ مَا تَحْتَهُ هَوَاءٌ وَمَا فَوْقَهُ هَوَاءٌ وَخَلَقَ عَرْشَهُ عَلَى الْمَاءِ» وَقَالَ يَزِيدُ بْنُ هَارُونَ: الْعَمَاءُ أَيْ لَيْسَ مَعَهُ شَيْءٌ
Narrated by Abu Razin al-'Uqayli (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: al-Tirmidhi  ·  Grade: Hasan
Class Notes
  • عَمَاء literally refers to thin white clouds.
  • It can also refer to a matter which people cannot fathom or imagine — i.e., a state beyond human comprehension entirely.
  • Some scholars say the question really means "where was the Throne of our Lord" — adding a مُضَاف مَحْذُوف (elided genitive construct). Others do not accept this حَذْف and take the question literally.
  • The مَا in "مَا تَحْتَهُ هَوَاءٌ" is نَافِيَة (negating) — meaning: nothing was beneath it nor above it.
  • Some say the مَا is مَوْصُولَة (relative), in which case عَمَاء and هَوَاء would refer to the same entity — one describing the state, the other the surrounding void.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • عَمَاءٌ— thin/white cloud; also interpreted as a state beyond all human comprehension; Yazid ibn Harun explained it as: nothing was with Him (لَيْسَ مَعَهُ شَيْءٌ).
  • هَوَاءٌ— air/void; neither above nor below was there anything — emphasizing Allah's complete independence before creation.
  • وَخَلَقَ عَرْشَهُ عَلَى الْمَاءِ— He created His Throne upon water; the water preceded the Throne; consistent with the preceding hadith (5697) about كان الله ولم يكن شيء قبله.
Cross-ref: Hadith confirmed in Mirqat (باب بدء الخلق, الفصل الثاني); Mirqat discusses the multiple interpretations of عماء including Yazid ibn Harun's explanation and the question of the مُضَاف مَحْذُوف; consistent with class notes; Lam'at not yet checked — flagged.
Kitab كِتَابُ أَحْوَالِ الْقِيَامَةِ وَبَدْءِ الْخَلْقِ بَابُ بَدْءِ الْخَلْقِ وَذِكْرِ الْأَنْبِيَاءِ — الفصل الثاني
حديث ٥٧٢٦
وَعَنْ جُبَيْرِ بْنِ مُطْعِمٍ قَالَ: أَتَى رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ أَعْرَابِيٌّ فَقَالَ: جَهِدَتِ الْأَنْفُسُ وَجَاعَ الْعِيَالُ وَنُهِكَتِ الْأَمْوَالُ وَهَلَكَتِ الْأَنْعَامُ فَاسْتَسْقِ اللَّهَ لَنَا فَإِنَّا نَسْتَشْفِعُ بِكَ عَلَى اللَّهِ وَنَسْتَشْفِعُ بِاللَّهِ عَلَيْكَ فَقَالَ النَّبِيُّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «سُبْحَانَ اللَّهِ سُبْحَانَ اللَّهِ» فَمَا زَالَ يُسَبِّحُ حَتَّى عُرِفَ ذَلِكَ فِي وُجُوهِ أَصْحَابِهِ ثُمَّ قَالَ: «وَيْحَكَ إِنَّهُ لَا يُسْتَشْفَعُ بِاللَّهِ عَلَى أَحَدٍ شَأْنُ اللَّهِ أَعْظَمُ مِنْ ذَلِكَ وَيْحَكَ أَتَدْرِي مَا اللَّهُ؟ إِنَّ عَرْشَهُ عَلَى سَمَاوَاتِهِ هَكَذَا» وَقَالَ بِأَصَابِعِهِ مَثْلَ الْقُبَّةِ عَلَيْهِ «وَإِنَّهُ لَيَئِطُّ أَطِيطَ الرَّحْلِ بِالرَّاكِبِ»
Narrated by Jubayr ibn Mut'im (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Abu Dawud  ·  Grade: Hasan
Class Notes
  • These events occurred in the context of drought — people and animals were in dire need.
  • الشَّافِع (intercessor) is generally of lower rank than الْمَشْفُوعُ إِلَيْهِ (the one intercession is made with) — which is why using Allah as an intercessor with Rasulullah (S.A.W.) was a severe error in concept.
  • The bedouin's second statement was a rebukable theological mistake, and the صَحَابَة (R.A.) could see Rasulullah's (S.A.W.) reaction on his face.
  • الْمُرَاد of describing the Throne with the dome gesture is not to define the exact shape of the Throne but to make it easier for the listener to grasp the greatness of Allah — the average person equates vastness and height with عَظَمَة.
  • Although الظَّاهِر (literal reading) of the bedouin's second statement is incorrect, there is no valid تَأْوِيل that would make it theologically permissible. The correct meaning is: "We are asking Allah to allow you to be our شَافِع (intercessor) with Him" — not that Allah intercedes with the Prophet.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • جَهِدَتِ الْأَنْفُسُ— the souls were exhausted/worn out; extreme hardship from famine.
  • نُهِكَتِ الْأَمْوَالُ— wealth was depleted/consumed; from نهك = to wear away through strain.
  • وَيْحَكَ— woe to you / listen carefully; an expression of gentle rebuke and correction, not a curse.
  • الْقُبَّةُ— a dome; the Prophet S.A.W. gestured with his fingers in a dome shape to describe the Throne's position above the heavens — a pedagogical gesture, not a precise geometric description.
  • يَئِطُّ أَطِيطَ الرَّحْلِ بِالرَّاكِبِ— it groans like a saddle under its rider; the Throne groans/creaks under the weight of Allah's greatness — affirmed with تَفْوِيض as a صِفَة خَبَرِيَّة.
Cross-ref: Hadith confirmed in Mirqat (باب بدء الخلق وذكر الأنبياء, الفصل الثاني); Mirqat discusses the theological error in the bedouin's second statement and the correct meaning (seeking Rasulullah S.A.W. as intercessor with Allah, not the reverse); the dome gesture and Throne groaning discussed in Mirqat with تَفْوِيض approach; Lam'at not yet checked — flagged.
Kitab كِتَابُ أَحْوَالِ الْقِيَامَةِ وَبَدْءِ الْخَلْقِ بَابُ بَدْءِ الْخَلْقِ وَذِكْرِ الْأَنْبِيَاءِ — الفصل الثالث
حديث ٥٧٣١
وَعَنْ جَابِرٍ أَنَّ النَّبِيَّ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ قَالَ: «لَمَّا خَلَقَ اللَّهُ آدَمَ وَذُرِّيَّتَهُ قَالَتِ الْمَلَائِكَةُ: يَا رَبِّ خَلَقْتَهُمْ يَأْكُلُونَ وَيَشْرَبُونَ وَيَنْكِحُونَ وَيَرْكَبُونَ فَاجْعَلْ لَهُمُ الدُّنْيَا وَلَنَا الْآخِرَةَ قَالَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى: لَا أَجْعَلُ مَنْ خَلَقْتُهُ بِيَدَيَّ وَنَفَخْتُ فِيهِ مِنْ رُوحِي كَمَنْ قُلْتُ لَهُ: كُنْ فَكَانَ»
Narrated by Jabir (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: al-Bayhaqi in Shu'ab al-Iman  ·  Grade: see شَرْح
Class Notes
  • Another meaning of the angels' request: let them have الدُّنْيَا forever and let us have الْآخِرَة forever — emphasizing a permanent division of the two realms between humans and angels.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • خَلَقْتُهُ بِيَدَيَّ— I created him with My two hands; a صِفَة خَبَرِيَّة affirmed for Adam A.S. specifically; Mirqat: affirmed as a divine attribute befitting Allah's majesty, without تَجْسِيم.
  • وَنَفَخْتُ فِيهِ مِنْ رُوحِي— and I breathed into him of My spirit; the نَفْخ الرُّوح is a separate divine act of honor for Adam A.S.; the إِضَافَة (My spirit) indicates honor, not that it is a part of Allah.
  • كُنْ فَكَانَ— "Be, and it was"; the mode of creation for angels and all else — through divine command alone, without the specific honor of "by My hands."
Cross-ref: Hadith confirmed in Mirqat (باب بدء الخلق وذكر الأنبياء, الفصل الثالث); Mirqat discusses the special honor of Adam A.S. being created بِيَدَيَّ versus کن فکان for other creation; the alternative meaning of the angels' request (دُنْيَا and آخِرَة forever) is noted in Mirqat's commentary; Lam'at not yet checked — flagged.
Kitab كِتَابُ أَحْوَالِ الْقِيَامَةِ وَبَدْءِ الْخَلْقِ بَابُ بَدْءِ الْخَلْقِ وَذِكْرِ الْأَنْبِيَاءِ — الفصل الثالث
حديث ٥٧٣٢
«الْمُؤْمِنُ أَكْرَمُ عَلَى اللَّهِ مِنْ بَعْضِ مَلَائِكَتِهِ»
Riwayah: Ibn Majah  ·  Grade: see شَرْح
Class Notes
  • In the شُرُوحَات, مَكْرُوه in this context refers to مُؤْلِم (something painful/burdensome) — not merely disliked but actively distressing.
  • Just because something was created or associated with a particular day does not mean evil is exclusively confined to that day — the class touched on the question of assigning ill omen to specific days of the week.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • أَكْرَمُ عَلَى اللَّهِ— more honored in Allah's sight; the comparative (أفعل التفضيل) shows degree, not absolute ranking over all angels.
  • مِنْ بَعْضِ مَلَائِكَتِهِ— than some of His angels; the qualifier بعض is important — the greatest angels (Jibreel, Mika'il, Israfil) are not encompassed by this; the believer surpasses lesser-ranked angels.
Cross-ref: Hadith confirmed in Mirqat (باب بدء الخلق وذكر الأنبياء, الفصل الثالث); Mirqat discusses the rank of believers relative to angels, clarifying the scope of بعض مَلَائِكَتِهِ; Lam'at not yet checked — flagged.
Kitab كِتَابُ أَحْوَالِ الْقِيَامَةِ وَبَدْءِ الْخَلْقِ بَابُ بَدْءِ الْخَلْقِ وَذِكْرِ الْأَنْبِيَاءِ — الفصل الثالث
حديث ٥٧٣٦
وَعَنْ أَبِي ذَرٍّ قَالَ: قُلْتُ: يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ أَيُّ الْأَنْبِيَاءِ كَانَ أَوَّلَ؟ قَالَ: «آدَمُ» قُلْتُ: وَنَبِيٌّ كَانَ؟ قَالَ: «نَعَمْ نَبِيٌّ مُكَلَّمٌ» قُلْتُ: كَمِ الْمُرْسَلُونَ يَا رَسُولَ اللَّهِ؟ قَالَ: «ثَلَاثُمِائَةٍ وَبَيْنَ عَشَرَةٍ وَخَمْسَةَ عَشَرَ جَمًّا غَفِيرًا»
Narrated by Abu Dharr (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Ahmad  ·  Grade: Hasan
Class Notes
  • These أَحَادِيث collectively establish that there is a difference between رَسُول and نَبِيّ.
  • This is also supported by the Quranic آية: وَمَا أَرْسَلْنَا مِنْ قَبْلِكَ مِنْ رَسُولٍ وَلَا نَبِيٍّ (Al-Hajj 22:52), which distinguishes the two terms.
  • The difference according to Mirqat: a رَسُول is given a book (كِتَاب), while a نَبِيّ is not given a new book.
  • أُولُو الْعَزْمِ مِنَ الرُّسُلِ — the resolute messengers, those with the most exalted missions among the رُسُل (Nuh, Ibrahim, Musa, Isa, and Muhammad A.S.).
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • نَبِيٌّ مُكَلَّمٌ— a prophet spoken to directly by Allah; Adam A.S. received direct divine speech, establishing his prophethood.
  • جَمًّا غَفِيرًا— a large overwhelming number; used here adverbially to indicate the vast multitude of messengers.
  • أُولُو الْعَزْمِ— those with firm resolve; Mirqat: the five greatest messengers who were given books and given the most demanding missions: Nuh, Ibrahim, Musa, Isa, and Muhammad (S.A.W.).
Cross-ref: Hadith confirmed in Mirqat (باب بدء الخلق وذكر الأنبياء, الفصل الثالث); Mirqat explicitly distinguishes رَسُول (given a كِتَاب) from نَبِيّ (not given a new كِتَاب) — consistent with class notes; the numbers 313/315 for رُسُل and 124,000 for أَنْبِيَاء are discussed in Mirqat; Lam'at not yet checked — flagged.
Kitab كِتَابُ أَحْوَالِ الْقِيَامَةِ وَبَدْءِ الْخَلْقِ بَابُ بَدْءِ الْخَلْقِ وَذِكْرِ الْأَنْبِيَاءِ — الفصل الثالث
حديث ٥٧٣٧
وَعَنِ ابْنِ عَبَّاسٍ قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: «لَيْسَ الْخَبَرُ كَالْمُعَايَنَةِ إِنَّ اللَّهَ أَخْبَرَ مُوسَى بِمَا صَنَعَ قَوْمُهُ فِي الْعِجْلِ فَلَمْ يُلْقِ الْأَلْوَاحَ فَلَمَّا عَايَنَ مَا صَنَعُوا أَلْقَى الْأَلْوَاحَ فَانْكَسَرَتْ»
Narrated by Ibn Abbas (R.A.)  ·  Riwayah: Ahmad  ·  Grade: Hasan
Class Notes
  • Mirqat: the throwing of the tablets shows that the tablets were only beneficial for believers. Since Musa's (A.S.) people had fallen into كُفْر, they would no longer benefit from them.
  • الظَّاهِر of the narration is that nothing from the tablets was actually lost — they broke but their content was preserved.
Word Meanings — Mirqat
  • لَيْسَ الْخَبَرُ كَالْمُعَايَنَةِ— information (خَبَر) is not like direct witnessing (مُعَايَنَة); hearing about an event does not produce the same emotional and psychological effect as seeing it firsthand.
  • الْعِجْلُ— the (golden) calf; the idol worshipped by Bani Isra'il in Musa's A.S. absence.
  • الْأَلْوَاحُ— the tablets; the divine tablets containing the Torah given to Musa A.S.; Mirqat: their benefit depended on the recipients' receptiveness — when Bani Isra'il fell into كُفْر, the tablets' purpose was nullified.
Cross-ref: Hadith confirmed in Mirqat (باب بدء الخلق وذكر الأنبياء, الفصل الثالث); Mirqat's explanation that the tablets were only beneficial for believers — and Musa's A.S. throwing them reflecting their uselessness for a people who had committed كُفْر — confirmed consistent with class notes; Lam'at not yet checked — flagged.

الْأَلْفَاظ

Difficult words & meanings from Mirqāt al-Mafātīḥ (cited below as “M”) — كِتَابُ الْفِتَنِ & كِتَابُ أَحْوَالِ الْقِيَامَةِ
كِتَابُ الْفِتَنِ
حديث ٥٣٧٨
  • قَامَ فِينَا مَقَامًا— he stood among us a standing, i.e., he delivered a sustained address; the مَصْدَر مَقَامًا emphasizes the duration and completeness of the speech.
  • حَفِظَهُ مَنْ حَفِظَهُ وَنَسِيَهُ مَنْ نَسِيَهُ— whoever retained it retained it, and whoever forgot it forgot it; indicates variation among the companions in what they preserved of this knowledge.
  • فَأَرَاهُ فَأَذْكُرُهُ— I see it (occur) and then I recall it (the prediction); the simile is to a man who forgets a face but instantly recognizes it upon seeing it again — knowledge present but not retrievable until the trigger appears.
حديث ٥٣٧٩
  • عُودًا عُودًا— stick by stick, one after another; M: just as a mat is woven by laying each reed consecutively, the فِتَن are presented to the heart one by one in sequence.
  • أُشْرِبَهَا— was made to drink it / absorbed it; إِشْرَاب implies the فِتْنَة seeps into the heart the way a drink is absorbed into the body — leaving no trace it was rejected.
  • نَكَتَتْ / نُكِتَتْ— left a mark/dot; النُّكْتَة = a small point or dot. One black dot for every فِتْنَة absorbed; one white dot for every فِتْنَة rejected.
  • الصَّفَا— smooth white rock (with ص); chosen for its two qualities: بَيَاض (whiteness = purity) and صَلَابَة (hardness = imperviousness to fitan).
  • مِرْبَادًّا— dust-colored, darkened; مُرْبَدّ = something that has turned the color of رَبَد (ash/dusty black), indicating a heart blackened by accumulated فِتَن.
  • كَالْكُوزِ مُجْخِيًّا— like an overturned vessel; مُجْخِيًّا = flipped upside down, retaining nothing — such a heart no longer recognizes good or rejects evil.
حديث ٥٣٩٥
  • الْعِصْمَة— M: طَرِيقُ النَّجَاةِ — the way of protection from falling into the شَرّ; answered with «السَّيْف» (Qatādah applied it to the ردة wars under Abū Bakr R.A.).
  • أَقْذَاء— M (al-Nihāya): plural of قَذًى (itself plural of قَذَاة) = the dust / straw / dirt that falls into the eye, water, or drink; al-Qāḍī: an إِمَارَة (rule) mixed with بِدَع and committing مَنَاهِي — the inner corruption likened to the قَذَى of the eye.
  • دَخَن— M: (two فَتْحَات) أَصْلُهُ الْكُدُورَة (turbidity) and a blackish hue; al-Qāḍī: مَعَ خِدَاعٍ وَنِفَاقٍ وَخِيَانَةٍ; al-Fāʾiq: outward صَلَاح over inner فَسَاد. The hadith itself glosses it: لَا تَرْجِعُ قُلُوبُ أَقْوَامٍ كَمَا كَانَتْ (hearts do not return to their former purity).
  • هُدْنَة— M: (ضَمَّة on the هَاء) = صُلْح — a truce / cessation of hostilities; here, an outward peace masking inner rancour.
  • عَاضٌّ عَلَى جَذْلِ شَجَرَةٍ— عَاضّ (شَدَّة on the ضَاد) = gripping firmly / biting; جَذْل (كَسْرَة or فَتْحَة on the جِيم) = أَصْلُهَا — the root / stump of the tree. al-Qāḍī: a كِنَايَة for taking to العُزْلَة (isolation) and enduring the hardships of the age — like the saying "so-and-so bites on stones from the severity of pain."
  • الْمُهْر— al-Tūrbishtī: (ضَمَّة, سُكُون on the هَاء) = وَلَدُ الْفَرَس (the foal); يُنْتَجُ = passive, يُولَد (is born) — born but not ridden before the Hour, so short is the time.
  • عَمْيَاءُ صَمَّاءُ— blind and deaf (feminine, agreeing with فِتْنَة): a فِتْنَة so overwhelming it blinds people from الْحَقّ and deafens them from it.
حديث ٥٣٩٦
  • رَدِيفًا— M: راكبًا خلف — riding pillion behind the Prophet ﷺ; a sign of his ﷺ تَوَاضُع and of Abū Dharr's closeness.
  • يُجْهِدَكَ الْجُوع— M: (ضَمَّة يَاء, كَسْرَة هَاء) brings you to مَشَقَّة and disables you from even walking from house to mosque.
  • تَعَفَّفْ— M: الْتَزِمِ الْعِفَّة — الصَّلَاح, الوَرَع, patience over the pain of hunger, التَّقْوَى, and abstaining from الحَرَام / الشُّبْهَة and from begging the creation.
  • يُبَاعُ الْقَبْرُ بِالْعَبْدِ— M (al-Nihāya): الْبَيْت here = الْقَبْر; grave-space grows so scarce that a single grave is bought for a slave (or its price); Sharḥ al-Sunna adds: none can be found to dig a grave except for a slave's price.
  • أَحْجَارُ الزَّيْتِ— M: a quarter / place in Madinah; al-Tūrbishtī (al-Muyassar): it is part of the الْحَرَّة where the Battle of al-Ḥarra occurred under Yazid — the commander Muslim ibn ʿUqba al-Murrī violated the sanctity of the Prophet's ﷺ حَرَم, killed its men, ran rampant 3 (or 5) days, then died between the two حَرَم.
  • تَغْمُرُ الدِّمَاءُ— M: (سُكُون ghayn, ضَمَّة مِيم) تَسْتُر وتَعْلُو — the blood covers over and rises above (so great is the slaughter).
  • تَأْتِي مَنْ أَنْتَ مِنْهُ— M: خَبَر بمعنى الأمر — come to one who agrees with you in your دِين and سِيرَة; al-Qāḍī: return to your family / clan; al-Ṭībī: rather, return to your imam.
  • شَارَكْتَ الْقَوْمَ إِذًا— M: i.e. you would share in their إِثْم by taking up the weapon — so do not bear arms; remain with the imam and the people of righteousness and do not fight.
  • يَبْهَرَكَ شُعَاعُ السَّيْفِ / لِيَبُوءَ— يَبْهَرَك = overwhelms/dazzles you (the gleam of the drawn sword sweeping you into the fighting); لِيَبُوءَ (from بَاءَ بِ = to return bearing a burden): so he returns bearing your sin (for slaying you unjustly) along with his own.
حديث ٥٤٠٠
  • تَسْتَنْظِفُ الْعَرَبَ— it sweeps up the Arabs entirely — تَسْتَوْعِبُهُمْ هَلَاكًا, consumes them all in destruction; from اِسْتَنْظَفَ الشَّيْءَ = to take the whole of a thing (al-Nihāya). Alt: it purges them of the base folk and people of فِتْنَة.
  • قَتْلَاهَا فِي النَّارِ— its slain are in the Fire (قَتْلَى = plural of قَتِيل); al-Qāḍī: because they fought not to raise a religion or repel a wrongdoer, but out of mutual aggression and greed for wealth and rule.
  • أَشَدُّ مِنْ وَقْعِ السَّيْفِ— the tongue in it is severer than the falling blow of the sword; a variant reads إِشْرَافُ اللِّسَانِ = letting the tongue loose and prolonging it.
حديث ٥٤٠١
  • صَمَّاءُ عَمْيَاءُ بَكْمَاءُ— deaf, blind, dumb (describing the فِتْنَة by its people): they find no rescuer and see no way out, cannot tell الْحَقّ from الْبَاطِل, nor heed counsel.
  • مَنْ أَشْرَفَ لَهَا— whoever looks out toward it and draws near it (اطَّلَعَ عَلَيْهَا وَقَرُبَ مِنْهَا).
  • اسْتَشْرَفَتْ لَهُ— it looks toward him in turn and pulls him into itself (جَذَبَتْهُ إِلَيْهَا).
  • إِشْرَافُ اللِّسَانِ— letting the tongue loose and prolonging it (إِطْلَاقُهُ وَإِطَالَتُهُ) — in its effect like the fall of the sword; as said: sword-wounds may knit together, but what the tongue wounds never heals.
حديث ٥٤٠٢
  • فِتْنَةُ الْأَحْلَاسِ— the "saddle-cloth" فِتْنَة (أَحْلَاس = plural of حِلْس, the coarse cloth kept under the saddle): a lingering, clinging tribulation.
  • هَرَبٌ— (both letters fatḥa) fleeing — people flee one another because of the enmity and warfare between them.
  • حَرَبٌ— (both letters fatḥa) plunder — the seizing of property and family without right.
  • فِتْنَةُ السَّرَّاءِ— the فِتْنَة of prosperity (السَّرَّاء = النَّعْمَاء that delights people): it springs from indulgence in comfort, or it gladdens the enemy; al-Tūrbishtī: or "wide-ranging," from قَفَاهُ سَرَّاء = broad.
  • دَخَنُهَا— (both letters fatḥa) its smoke — its stirring-up and raging (إِثَارَتُهَا وَهَيَجَانُهَا), likened to rising smoke, as war is likened to fire.
  • كَوَرِكٍ عَلَى ضِلْعٍ— like a hip-bone set upon a rib: a proverb for what cannot hold — the heavy وَرِك will not rest on the thin ضِلْع; i.e. a leader unfit for authority and ill-matched to it (al-Nihāya).
  • فِتْنَةُ الدُّهَيْمَاءِ— the "pitch-dark" فِتْنَة (diminutive of الدَّهْمَاء, the black one; the diminutive here is for magnification — al-Nihāya: the dark calamity); some say from الدُّهَيْم, a byword for catastrophe.
  • لَطَمَتْهُ لَطْمَةً— it strikes him a blow (أَصَابَتْهُ بِمِحْنَةٍ) — لَطْم is a slap on the face with the palm; its harm reaches every one of the ummah.
  • فُسْطَاطَيْنِ— two camps (فُسْطَاط, ḍamma or kasra on the fāʾ) = two factions — or two cities; its root is الْخَيْمَة (the tent): a camp of pure faith and a camp of pure hypocrisy.
حديث ٥٤٠٣
  • وَيْلٌ— woe: the befalling of evil, an utterance of anguish; or a word of chastisement; or a valley in Hell.
  • قَدِ اقْتَرَبَ— has drawn near — i.e. the appearance of that evil is imminent.
  • أَفْلَحَ— has prospered — won through and been saved (نَجَا وَظَفِرَ).
  • مَنْ كَفَّ يَدَهُ— whoever held back his hand — from harm, or refrained from fighting when الْحَقّ is not distinct from الْبَاطِل.
حديث ٥٤٠٤
  • جُنِّبَ الْفِتَنَ— was kept far from the trials (بُعِّدَ عَنْهَا); as in the duʿāʾ «اللَّهُمَّ جَنِّبْنَا الشَّيْطَانَ».
  • ابْتُلِيَ— was tested and afflicted (اُمْتُحِنَ) by those trials, then bore them with patience.
  • فَوَاهًا— an interjection (اسْمُ صَوْتٍ standing in for the verb): expressing admiration — "how excellent his patience!"; or lament and longing (التَّلَهُّف); al-Qāmūs: a word of marvel at something good and of grief at its loss.
حديث ٥٤٠٥
  • وُضِعَ السَّيْفُ فِي أُمَّتِي— the sword is laid among my ummah — some of them against others (internecine bloodshed); it began in Muʿāwiya's time and is not lifted till the Day of Resurrection.
  • تَلْحَقَ قَبَائِلُ بِالْمُشْرِكِينَ— tribes of my ummah will join the polytheists — and some tribes will worship الْأَوْثَان (the idols).
  • كَذَّابُونَ ثَلَاثُونَ— thirty arch-liars — false claimants, each alleging that he is a prophet of Allah, though he ﷺ is خَاتَمُ النَّبِيِّينَ (the Seal of the Prophets).
  • طَائِفَةٌ ... ظَاهِرِينَ— a group ever manifest and uppermost upon the truth, unharmed by those who oppose them, until the command of Allah comes.
حديث ٥٤٠٦
  • تَدُورُ رَحَى الْإِسْلَامِ— the millstone of Islam turns; a metaphor (كِنَايَة) — either Islam's affair remains established and ordered, or (Khaṭṭābī) a metaphor for war and fighting, likening it to a grinding millstone (for the loss of souls therein).
  • فَسَبِيلُ مَنْ هَلَكَ— their path is the path of those [past nations] who perished — who deviated from the truth and grew weak in the religion.
  • يَقُمْ لَهُمْ دِينُهُمْ— their religion stands firm / remains established for them.
  • مِمَّا مَضَى— "from what has passed" (i.e. the 70 years are counted from the past, not from what remains).
حديث ٥٤٠٧
  • ذَاتُ أَنْوَاطٍ— "the one of hangings" (أَنْوَاط = plural of نَوْط, from نَاطَ = to hang up): a tree on which the pagans hung their weapons and around which they secluded themselves in veneration.
  • لَتَرْكَبُنَّ سُنَنَ مَنْ كَانَ قَبْلَكُمْ— you will surely tread the ways of those before you (سُنَن, ḍamma on the sīn = طُرُقُهُمْ وَمَنَاهِجُهُمْ, their paths and courses); a variant with fatḥa = upon their very manner and likeness.
حديث ٥٤٠٨
  • الْحَرَّة— the Ḥarra (al-Nihāya: black, stony ground outside Madīnah); the notorious battle there in Yazīd's days, when his army under Muslim ibn ʿUqba al-Murrī plundered Madīnah (63 AH).
  • أَصْحَابُ الْحُدَيْبِيَةِ— the people of al-Ḥudaybiya — i.e. أَهْل بَيْعَة الرِّضْوَان.
  • وَبِالنَّاسِ طَبَاخٌ— while there is yet in the people any [one of worth]; طَبَاخ (fatḥ ṭāʾ), its root = strength and fatness (القُوَّة والسُّمْن), then figurative — «فُلَانٌ لَا طَبَاخَ لَهُ» = he has no sense or good in him.
حديث ٥٤٠٩
  • الْمَلَاحِم— (fatḥ mīm, kasr ḥāʾ; plural of مَلْحَمَة) fierce slaughters / great battles (المَقْتَلَة); from the entangling of fighters, like the interweaving (لُحْمَة) of a garment, or from لَحْم (flesh) for the slain's flesh.
  • دَعَوَاهُمَا وَاحِدَةٌ— their claim is one — each of the two factions claims Islam (a refutation of the Khawārij who declared both disbelievers).
  • الْهَرْج— killing / slaughter (a narrator's gloss: «وَهُوَ الْقَتْلُ»); said to mean its being widespread and continuous.
  • يَفِيضَ الْمَالُ— wealth overflows — from فَاضَ الْمَاء (water pours over when it brims); a hyperbole for its abundance.
  • لَا أَرَبَ لِي بِهِ— "I have no need of it" (لَا حَاجَةَ لِي إِلَيْهِ) — said by the one to whom the charity is offered, out of contentment of heart and hand.
  • لَبَنِ لِقْحَتِهِ— the milk of his milch-camel (لِقْحَة, kasr lām, sukūn qāf = a she-camel with milk).
  • يُلِيطُ حَوْضَهُ— (fatḥ) he plasters and mends his watering-trough (يُطَيِّنُ وَيُصْلِحُ) to water his camels or sheep.
  • أُكْلَتَهُ— (ḍamma hamza) his morsel / mouthful (لُقْمَتُهُ), raised to his mouth.
حديث ٥٤١٠
  • نِعَالُهُمُ الشَّعْرُ— their sandals are of hair — made of hairy, untanned hides.
  • ذُلْفَ الْأُنُوفِ— (ḍamma dhāl) snub-nosed — small noses (or broad, with thickness at the tip); nearest sense = فُطْس, depressed nose-bridges.
  • الْمَجَانُّ الْمُطْرَقَةُ— leather shields laid layer upon layer (مَجَانّ = plural of مِجَنّ = التُّرْس, the shield; مُطْرَقَة = overlaid with skin/طِرَاق): their faces likened to broad, thick, round shields.
  • صِغَارُ الْأَعْيُنِ— small-eyed.
حديث ٥٤١١
  • خُوزًا وَكِرْمَانَ— Khūz and Kirmān (al-Qāmūs: al-Khūz = a race and the lands of Khūzistān; Kirmān = a region between Fārs and Sijistān) — here two clans of the Turks named after their forebears, of the أَعَاجِم (non-Arabs).
  • فُطْسَ الْأُنُوفِ— flat- / depressed-nosed (plural of أَفْطَس).
حديث ٥٤١٢
  • عِرَاضَ الْوُجُوهِ— broad-faced — a variant wording (Bukhārī, from ʿAmr ibn Taghlib) of the same description of the Turks.
حديث ٥٤١٣
  • يَخْتَبِئَ— he hides himself (يَخْتَفِي) — behind stone and tree.
  • الْغَرْقَد— the boxthorn — a thorny tree, the عَوْسَج (al-Nihāya: a kind of عِضَاه / thorn-tree; hence بَقِيع الْغَرْقَد in Madīnah); called "the tree of the Jews" because it alone will not give them up.
حديث ٥٤١٤
  • رَجُلٌ مِنْ قَحْطَانَ— a man of Qaḥṭān (fatḥ qāf, sukūn ḥāʾ) — Qaḥṭān is the forefather of the Yemenites (or a tribe of them).
  • يَسُوقُ النَّاسَ بِعَصَاهُ— he drives the people with his staff — a figure for subduing and ruling them, as a shepherd drives his flock with his staff.
حديث ٥٤١٥
  • الْجَهْجَاه— al-Jahjāh (fatḥ jīm, sukūn hāʾ) — the name of a man who will come to hold power.
  • مِنَ الْمَوَالِي— of the freedmen / bondmen (مَوَالِي, fatḥ mīm, plural of مَوْلَى = the المَمَالِيك).
حديث ٥٤١٦
  • عِصَابَةٌ— (kasr ʿayn) a band / group (جَمَاعَة).
  • كَنْزَ آلِ كِسْرَى— the treasure-hoard of the house of Kisrā (Chosroes, the Persian emperor).
  • الْأَبْيَض— al-Abyaḍ (al-Qāḍī): a fortified palace at al-Madāʾin, which the Persians called Safīd-Karshak; the Madāʾin mosque was later built on its site.
حديث ٥٤١٧
  • هَلَكَ كِسْرَى— "Kisrā has perished" — past tense used for certainty of its coming to pass; i.e. no Kisrā (Persian emperor) will rule after him.
  • قَيْصَرُ— Qayṣar (Caesar) — the king of the Romans.
  • الْحَرْبُ خُدْعَةٌ— "War is deception" (خُدْعَة, the khāʾ tri-vowelled) — it is decided by stratagem; a notice that ruse in war is not treachery (غَدْر).
حديث ٥٤١٨
  • جَزِيرَةُ الْعَرَبِ— the Arabian Peninsula — per Mālik: Mecca, Madīnah, al-Yamāma, and Yemen; i.e. its whole expanse, leaving no disbeliever in it.
  • تَغْزُونَ الدَّجَّالَ فَيَفْتَحُهُ اللَّهُ— you will raid the Dajjāl and Allah will conquer him — render him vanquished and overcome (his end at the hands of ʿĪsā, with the ummah's aid).
حديث ٥٤١٩
  • قُبَّةٍ مِنْ أَدَمٍ— a dome-tent of leather (أَدَم, both letters fatḥa = جِلْد, tanned hide).
  • مُوتَانٌ— (ḍamma mīm) a pestilence / plague (وَبَاء) — in origin a murrain that strikes livestock, used here of people; al-Tūrbishtī: as in the plague of ʿAmwās in ʿUmar's day, the first plague in Islam.
  • كَقُعَاصِ الْغَنَمِ— like the قُعَاص of sheep (ḍamma qāf) — a disease that seizes sheep and kills them before long.
  • اسْتِفَاضَةُ الْمَالِ— the abounding of wealth (كَثْرَتُهُ); its root is spreading and overflowing, from فَاضَ الْمَالُ (it brimmed over).
  • فَيَظَلُّ سَاخِطًا— he remains discontented / angry (غَضْبَان) — reckoning a hundred [dīnārs] too little.
  • هُدْنَةٌ— a truce, a peace-treaty (مُصَالَحَة).
  • بَنِي الْأَصْفَرِ— the "sons of the yellow" — the Byzantine Romans; so named after their forefather al-Rūm (yellowish upon whiteness of complexion), or after a dark king who fathered handsome children.
  • فَيَغْدِرُونَ— they break faith — violate the truce (يَنْقُضُونَ عَهْدَ الْهُدْنَةِ).
  • ثَمَانِينَ غَايَةً— eighty standards (غَايَة = the رَايَة, the banner/flag), under each twelve thousand.
حديث ٥٤٢٠
  • بِالْأَعْمَاقِ أَوْ بِدَابِقَ— at al-Aʿmāq or at Dābiq — two known places in the district of Aleppo (al-Tūrbishtī: عُمْق = the far reaches of the wilderness; مَرْج دَابِق is famous).
  • قُسْطَنْطِينِيَّةَ— Constantinople — the greatest city of the Romans.
  • ذَابَ كَمَا يَذُوبُ الْمِلْحُ— [the Dajjāl] melts as salt melts in water — at the mere sight of ʿĪsā; were he left, he would dissolve utterly and perish.
  • فِي حَرْبَتِهِ— on his spear — the حَرْبَة of ʿĪsā, a small lance (رُمْح صَغِير); he shows them the Dajjāl's blood upon it.
حديث ٥٤٢١
  • شُرْطَةً لِلْمَوْتِ— a death-band (شُرْطَة, ḍamma shīn = a vanguard detachment that goes ahead into the fighting, pledged not to return except victorious).
  • حَتَّى يَحْجِزَ بَيْنَهُمُ اللَّيْلُ— until the night parts them (يَمْنَع) — its onset and darkness make them break off the fight.
  • فَيَفِيءُ هَؤُلَاءِ وَهَؤُلَاءِ— these and those withdraw — يَفِيءُ, from الفَيْء (returning), i.e. each side turns back, neither victorious.
  • تَفْنَى الشُّرْطَةُ— the death-band is used up / annihilated.
  • الصَّرِيخُ— the crier of alarm — the shout that reaches them that the Dajjāl has come upon their families behind them.
  • طَلِيعَةً— a scouting party / vanguard — ten horsemen sent ahead to reconnoitre.
حديث ٥٤٢٢
  • سَبْعُونَ أَلْفًا مِنْ بَنِي إِسْحَاقَ— seventy thousand of the descendants of Isḥāq — al-Muẓhir: the Kurds of Syria, of the progeny of the Prophet Isḥāq, and they are Muslims (or with them others of the Arabs).
  • فَيَسْقُطُ أَحَدُ جَانِبَيْهَا— one of its two sides falls — one flank of the city's wall, at their تَكْبِير and تَهْلِيل, with no weapon or arrow.
  • فَيُفَرَّجُ لَهُمْ— it is opened wide for them (فَيُفْتَح) — the way is cleared and they enter.
حديث ٥٤٢٣
  • عُمْرَانُ بَيْتِ الْمَقْدِسِ— the full flourishing of Jerusalem (عِمَارَتُهُ, ḍamma ʿayn) — its utmost building-up and population.
  • خَرَابُ يَثْرِبَ— the ruin of Yathrib (Madīnah) — the flourishing of al-Quds coincides with the time of Madīnah's ruin.
  • خُرُوجُ الْمَلْحَمَةِ— the breaking-out of the great battle — each event in the chain is a sign (أَمَارَة) heralding the next.
حديث ٥٤٢٤
  • الْمَلْحَمَةُ الْعُظْمَى— the greatest slaughter / battle (al-Jāmiʿ: الْكُبْرَى).
  • فِي سَبْعَةِ أَشْهُرٍ— within seven months — reckoned from the Muslims' setting out to the two cities and the Dajjāl's emergence.
حديث ٥٤٢٦
  • يُوشِكُ الْمُسْلِمُونَ أَنْ يُحَاصَرُوا— it is well-nigh that the Muslims be besieged — driven back and confined (يُحْبَسُوا وَيُضْطَرُّوا) to Madīnah.
  • أَبْعَدَ مَسَالِحِهِمْ— the farthest of their frontier-posts (مَسَالِح = plural of مَسْلَحَة, a garrisoned border outpost of armed watchmen who guard the marches — al-Nihāya).
  • سَلَاحٌ— Salāḥ — a place below Khaybar; that their farthest outpost is only this near-Khaybar spot shows how tightly they are hemmed in.
حديث ٥٤٢٧
  • صُلْحًا آمِنًا— a secure truce — you will make peace with the Romans, then together raid an enemy to your rear (عَدُوًّا مِنْ وَرَائِكُمْ).
  • بِمَرْجٍ ذِي تُلُولٍ— at a meadow of hillocks (مَرْج = a broad, well-watered pasture; تُلُول = plural of تَلّ, a raised mound).
  • الصَّلِيبَ— the cross — a four-cornered wood upon which they claim ʿĪsā was crucified.
  • غَلَبَ الصَّلِيبُ— "the Cross has conquered" — a Roman's boast, ascribing the victory to the cross; a Muslim, enraged, smashes it (فَيَدُقُّهُ).
  • تَغْدِرُ الرُّومُ— the Romans break faith (تَنْقُضُ الْعَهْدَ) and gather for the battle.
  • فَيَثُورُ الْمُسْلِمُونَ— the Muslims spring up (يَعْدُو وَيَقُوم) to their weapons.
حديث ٥٤٢٨
  • اتْرُكُوا الْحَبَشَةَ مَا تَرَكُوكُمْ— leave the Abyssinians (الْحَبَشَة = a race of the Sudan) alone so long as they leave you.
  • كَنْزَ الْكَعْبَةِ— the treasure of the Kaʿba — a hoard buried beneath it (or what its custodians gather of its votive gifts).
  • ذُو السُّوَيْقَتَيْنِ— "he of the two thin shanks" (diminutive of سَاق) — a slender-legged man of the Abyssinians who will extract the Kaʿba's treasure; thin shins being typical of the Sudan (Nawawī).
حديث ٥٤٢٩
  • مَا وَدَعُوكُمْ— so long as they leave you (وَدَعَ, light dāl = تَرَكَ) — an archaic past-tense the grammarians deemed "dead," which the Prophet ﷺ, the most eloquent, revived.
  • وَاتْرُكُوا التُّرْكَ مَا تَرَكُوكُمْ— and leave the Turks be so long as they leave you (Khaṭṭābī: the command is for permission — فَرْض كِفَايَة — not an absolute duty to attack).
حديث ٥٤٣٠
  • تَسُوقُونَهُمْ ثَلَاثَ مِرَارٍ— you will drive them [the Turks] back three times — routed and overpowered — until you push them to جَزِيرَة الْعَرَب.
  • فَيُصْطَلَمُونَ— they are utterly extirpated — mown down by the sword and rooted out, from الصَّلْم (cutting off at the root).
حديث ٥٤٣١
  • بِغَائِطٍ— in a low-lying hollow of land (غَائِط = a sunken, depressed tract; al-Fāʾiq: a low valley) — which they name al-Baṣra.
  • دِجْلَةُ— the Tigris (kasr or fatḥ dāl) — the river of Baghdad; upon it a جِسْر (bridge / crossing, قَنْطَرَة).
  • بَنُو قَنْطُورَاءَ— the sons of Qanṭūrāʾ (a bondwoman of Ibrāhīm ﷺ; her descendants are reckoned the Turks) — broad-faced, small-eyed, who camp on the river-bank (شَطِّ النَّهْرِ).
حديث ٥٤٣٢
  • يُمَصِّرُونَ أَمْصَارًا— they found garrison-cities (أَمْصَار = plural of مِصْر; التَّمَصُّر = the founding of a town) — one of which is called al-Baṣra.
  • سِبَاخَهَا— its salt-flats (سِبَاخ = plural of سَبْخَة, salt-encrusted ground that scarcely grows anything) — beware of them.
  • كَلَّاءَهَا— its Kallāʾ — a place in al-Baṣra: the wharf where ships are moored (or a grazing-ground).
  • بِضَوَاحِيهَا— to its outskirts (ضَوَاحٍ = plural of ضَاحِيَة, open ground bare to the sun; or its hills) — keep to these; a command to seclusion.
  • خَسْفٌ— a sinking away and being swallowed into the earth.
  • قَذْفٌ— a pelting — a fierce cold wind, or the earth's casting up its dead, or a rain of stones upon its people.
  • رَجْفٌ— a violent earthquake (زَلْزَلَة شَدِيدَة).
  • يُصْبِحُونَ قِرَدَةً وَخَنَازِيرَ— they awake as apes and swine — i.e. مَسْخ (metamorphosis) as a punishment, expressed by the most repugnant form (Ṭībī).
حديث ٥٤٣٤
  • تَمُوجُ كَمَوْجِ الْبَحْرِ— [the fitna] surges like the surging of the sea — heaves in tumult like the sea when it rages; a figure for fierce quarrelling, killing, and disorder.
  • بَابًا مُغْلَقًا— a shut door — between ʿUmar and that fitna stands a locked door (ʿUmar's lifetime; the "door" is ʿUmar himself).
  • فَيُكْسَرُ الْبَابُ أَوْ يُفْتَحُ— is the door broken open, or opened? — "broken" (يُكْسَر, alluding to ʿUmar's slaying) — and a broken door is fitter never to be shut again.
  • لَيْسَ بِالْأَغَالِيطِ— not of the "trick-questions" (أَغَالِيط = plural of أُغْلُوطَة, a puzzle by which one is misled) — i.e. a plain, explicit report, not an obscure riddle.
  • فَهِبْنَا— we were in awe / afraid (from الْهَيْبَة) to ask Ḥudhayfa who the door was.
حديث ٥٤٣٦
  • أَشْرَاطِ السَّاعَةِ— the portents of the Hour (أَشْرَاط = the tokens and signs that precede it).
  • أَنْ يُرْفَعَ الْعِلْمُ— that knowledge be taken away — lifted up by the passing of the ʿulamāʾ, while ignorance spreads.
  • الْقَيِّمُ الْوَاحِدُ— the single overseer / caretaker — one man managing the affairs of fifty women, from the fewness of men and abundance of women.
حديث ٥٤٣٨
  • إِذَا ضُيِّعَتِ الْأَمَانَةُ— when the trust is squandered — betrayed, or lodged with those who are not people of religion — then await the Hour.
  • إِذَا وُسِّدَ الْأَمْرُ إِلَى غَيْرِ أَهْلِهِ— when authority is laid upon one unfit for it — from الْوِسَاد (a pillow); al-Tūrbishtī: the cushion of rule is set under one who is no fit for it (الْأَمْر = the caliphate, judgeship, command).
حديث ٥٤٣٩
  • تَعُودَ أَرْضُ الْعَرَبِ مُرُوجًا وَأَنْهَارًا— the land of the Arabs returns to meadows and rivers (مُرُوج = plural of مَرْج, a broad, well-vegetated tract where beasts roam free — al-Nihāya).
  • تَبْلُغُ الْمَسَاكِنُ إِهَابَ— the dwellings reach Ihāb (or Yihāb) — two places near Madīnah; i.e. its buildings sprawl out that far.
حديث ٥٤٤٠
  • يَحْثِي الْمَالَ حَثْيًا— he scoops out wealth by the handful (يُعْطِيهِ بِالْكَفَّيْنِ) — gives lavishly, out of the abundance of wealth and his own generosity.
  • وَلَا يَعُدُّهُ عَدًّا— and does not number it out — bestows without counting or reckoning.
حديث ٥٤٤١
  • يُوشِكُ الْفُرَاتُ أَنْ يَحْسِرَ عَنْ كَنْزٍ— the Euphrates is well-nigh to lay bare / uncover (يَكْشِف — as a turban is stripped off the head) a treasure of gold.
  • فَمَنْ حَضَرَ فَلَا يَأْخُذْ مِنْهُ شَيْئًا— whoever is present, let him take nothing of it — for the great slaughter and strife that follow over it.
حديث ٥٤٤٢
  • يَحْسِرَ الْفُرَاتُ عَنْ جَبَلٍ مِنْ ذَهَبٍ— the Euphrates lays bare a mountain of gold — a variant of the "treasure" report: a hoard the size of a mountain, or a gold mine.
  • يُقْتَلُ مِنْ كُلِّ مِائَةٍ تِسْعَةٌ وَتِسْعُونَ— of every hundred, ninety-nine are slain — fighting over it, each hoping to be the one who survives.
حديث ٥٤٤٣
  • تَقِيءُ الْأَرْضُ أَفْلَاذَ كَبِدِهَا— the earth vomits up the pieces of its liver (أَفْلَاذ = plural of فِلْذَة, a piece cut lengthwise) — a figure for its buried treasures and mineral veins, likened to liver-pieces (the choicest thing hidden within).
  • أَمْثَالَ الْأُسْطُوَانَةِ— the like of pillars (أُسْطُوَانَة = a column) — of gold and silver.
حديث ٥٤٤٤
  • فَيَتَمَرَّغُ عَلَيْهِ— he rolls and writhes upon it (the grave) — tossing in the dust, wishing he were its dead occupant.
  • وَلَيْسَ بِهِ الدِّينُ إِلَّا الْبَلَاءُ— nothing drives him to it but the affliction — not religious longing but the sheer weight of trials and turmoil (al-Muẓhir: الدِّين here = habit).
حديث ٥٤٤٥
  • نَارٌ مِنْ أَرْضِ الْحِجَازِ— a fire from the land of Ḥijāz (Mecca, Madīnah, and their environs).
  • تُضِيءُ أَعْنَاقَ الْإِبِلِ بِبُصْرَى— it lights up the necks of the camels at Buṣrā (a city of Ḥawrān in Syria, some three stages from Damascus) — so vast is its glare (Nawawī: this fire appeared 654 AH).
حديث ٥٤٤٦
  • نَارٌ تَحْشُرُ النَّاسَ— a fire that herds / drives the people together (تَجْمَعُهُم) from the east to the west — the first of the portents of the Hour.
حديث ٥٤٤٧
  • يَتَقَارَبُ الزَّمَانُ— time draws close together / contracts — the year like a month, the day like an hour; from the loss of the time's barakah, or people's absorption in unending calamities.
  • كَالضَّرْمَةِ بِالنَّارِ— like a firebrand's flare (الضَّرْمَة = kindling, a dry palm-frond or reed-tip set alight, that flares and burns out swiftly) — the hour passing as fast as it flares and dies.
حديث ٥٤٤٨
  • لِنَغْنَمَ عَلَى أَقْدَامِنَا— to take spoils, on our feet — sent out marching, not riding.
  • وَعَرَفَ الْجَهْدَ فِي وُجُوهِنَا— he saw the hardship / distress (الْجَهْد = مَشَقَّة) in our faces — the marks of dejection at gaining no spoils.
  • لَا تَكِلْهُمْ إِلَيَّ— do not consign them to me (from الْوُكُول, leaving one's affairs to another) — lest I prove too weak for them.
  • فَيَسْتَأْثِرُوا عَلَيْهِمْ— lest [others] be selfishly partial against them (اسْتَأْثَرَ = to keep a thing to oneself, prefer oneself over another).
  • دَنَتِ الزَّلَازِلُ وَالْبَلَابِلُ— the earthquakes and anxieties have drawn near (بَلَابِل = plural of بَلْبَال, turmoil and distress of the heart).
حديث ٥٤٤٩
  • اتُّخِذَ الْفَيْءُ دِوَلًا— the spoils (الْفَيْء = booty / public revenue) are treated as a windfall passed round (دِوَل = plural of دُولَة, a thing seized by turns) — the powerful monopolizing the poor's due.
  • الْأَمَانَةُ مَغْنَمًا وَالزَّكَاةُ مَغْرَمًا— the trust [taken] as spoil and the zakāh [felt] as a fine (مَغْرَم = a penalty, a dead loss) — deposits plundered, and paying zakāh resented as a burden.
  • زَعِيمُ الْقَوْمِ أَرْذَلَهُمْ— the leader of a people is the basest of them (زَعِيم = the spokesman / guarantor / chief; أَرْذَل = the meanest, lowest).
  • الْقَيْنَاتُ وَالْمَعَازِفُ— the singing slave-girls (قَيْنَات) and the instruments of music (مَعَازِف = tools of frivolity) appear openly.
  • رِيحًا حَمْرَاءَ وَخَسْفًا وَمَسْخًا وَقَذْفًا— a red wind, a swallowing-up (خَسْف), a metamorphosis (مَسْخ = transformation of forms), and a pelting of stones (قَذْف) — await these when the signs appear.
  • كَنِظَامٍ قُطِعَ سِلْكُهُ— like a string of beads whose thread is cut (نِظَام = a strung necklace; سِلْك = the thread) — the signs following hard upon one another as scattered beads.
حديث ٥٤٥٠
  • خَمْسَ عَشْرَةَ خَصْلَةً— fifteen traits (خَصْلَة = a quality, here a blameworthy habit) — when the ummah does them, calamity descends.
  • وَبَرَّ صَدِيقَهُ وَجَفَا أَبَاهُ— he is dutiful to his friend and harsh to / shuns his father (جَفَا = to treat coldly, keep at a distance).
  • وَلُبِسَ الْحَرِيرُ— and silk is worn — i.e. by men, for whom it is forbidden.
حديث ٥٤٥١
  • يُوَاطِئُ اسْمُهُ اسْمِيَ— his name matches mine (يُوَاطِئ = يُوَافِق, agrees with) — a man of the Prophet's ﷺ house (the Mahdī, Muḥammad ibn ʿAbdillāh).
  • يَمْلَأُ الْأَرْضَ قِسْطًا وَعَدْلًا— he fills the earth with equity and justice (قِسْط = fairness) as it had been filled with tyranny and wrong (جَوْر = oppression).
حديث ٥٤٥٢
  • الْمَهْدِيُّ مِنْ عِتْرَتِي— the Mahdī is of my ʿitra (عِتْرَة = one's closest kin / offspring) — of the children of Fāṭima.
حديث ٥٤٥٣
  • أَجْلَى الْجَبْهَةِ— of broad, clear brow (الْجَلا = the receding of hair from the front of the head; جَبْهَة جَلْوَاء = wide).
  • أَقْنَى الْأَنْفِ— of aquiline nose (الْقَنَا = length of the nose with a slight rise in its middle and a fine tip) — i.e. not flat-nosed.
حديث ٥٤٥٥
  • بَيْنَ الرُّكْنِ وَالْمَقَامِ— between the Corner (the Black Stone) and the Station (Maqām Ibrāhīm) — where they pledge allegiance to him against his will.
  • فَيُخْسَفُ بِهِمْ بِالْبَيْدَاءِ— they are swallowed up at al-Baydāʾ (a smooth open tract between Mecca and Madīnah) — the army sent against him from Syria.
  • أَبْدَالُ الشَّامِ— the Abdāl of Syria (al-Nihāya: the righteous awliyāʾ; singular بَدَل — so named because whenever one dies another is put in his place).
  • عَصَائِبُ أَهْلِ الْعِرَاقِ— the bands of the people of Iraq (عَصَائِب = plural of عِصَابَة, a company of some ten to forty) — i.e. their best men.
  • أَخْوَالُهُ كَلْبٌ— his maternal uncles are of [the tribe] Kalb — a Qurayshī whose mother is Kalbī, who contends against the Mahdī.
  • يُلْقِي الْإِسْلَامُ بِجِرَانِهِ— Islam lays down its neck (الْجِرَان = the underside of a camel's neck) — a proverb: Islam settles firm and at rest, as a camel stretches its neck to the ground when it kneels.
حديث ٥٤٥٦
  • لَا يَجِدُ الرَّجُلُ مَلْجَأً— a man finds no refuge (مَلْجَأ = a shelter, place of recourse — مَلَاذ) to flee to from the oppression.
  • إِلَّا صَبَّتْهُ مِدْرَارًا— but it pours it down in abundance (مِدْرَار = copiously streaming, from الدَّرّ, the flowing of milk/rain) — the sky withholds nothing of its rain.
  • يَتَمَنَّى الْأَحْيَاءُ الْأَمْوَاتَ— the living wish [for the state of] the dead — i.e. wish the dead were alive to share in the good and security of his reign (Tūrbishtī).
حديث ٥٤٥٧
  • الْحَارِثُ حَرَّاثٌ— [a man named] al-Ḥārith, a ḥarrāth (حَرَّاث = a tiller / ploughman, زَرَّاع) — who comes forth from beyond the river (Transoxiana).
  • يُوَطِّنُ لِآلِ مُحَمَّدٍ— he secures and establishes rule for the House of Muḥammad (التَّوْطِين = to make firm, from الْوَطَن) as Quraysh established it for the Prophet ﷺ.
حديث ٥٤٥٨
  • تُكَلِّمَ السِّبَاعُ الْإِنْسَ— the beasts of prey (سِبَاع, of the wild or of birds) speak to mankind.
  • عَذَبَةُ سَوْطِهِ— the tip of his whip (عَذَبَة = the thong-end of a whip) — it will tell a man what his family did after him.
  • شِرَاكُ نَعْلِهِ— the thong of his sandal (شِرَاك = the leather strap over the instep).
حديث ٥٤٥٩
  • الْآيَاتُ بَعْدَ الْمِائَتَيْنِ— the signs [of the Hour] come after the two hundred — i.e. they follow in succession after 200 (years); some: after the two hundred beyond the thousand.
حديث ٥٤٦٠
  • الرَّايَاتِ السُّودَ— the black banners (رَايَات = standards / flags) — coming from the direction of Khurāsān; among them is the Mahdī.
  • خَلِيفَةَ اللَّهِ— "the vicegerent of Allah" — here explained as one appointed by Allah as successor to His prophets (its literal ascription is otherwise disallowed).
حديث ٥٤٦١
  • يُشْبِهُهُ فِي الْخُلُقِ وَلَا يُشْبِهُهُ فِي الْخَلْقِ— he resembles him ﷺ in character (خُلُق = nature, disposition) but not in physical form (خَلْق = bodily make).
  • مِنْ صُلْبِهِ— from his loins (صُلْب = the backbone) — i.e. his direct descendant.
حديث ٥٤٦٢
  • فُقِدَ الْجَرَادُ— the locusts went missing (فُقِدَ = were not to be found) — in the year ʿUmar died.
  • خَلَقَ أَلْفَ أُمَّةٍ— He created a thousand nations — أُمَّة here = a kind / species of creature (six hundred in the sea, four hundred on land).
  • تَتَابَعَتِ الْأُمَمُ كَنِظَامِ السِّلْكِ— the species follow one another [in perishing] like beads on a string (نِظَام السِّلْك = a threaded necklace) — when the locust perishes, the rest follow as beads scatter from a cut thread.
حديث ٥٤٦٣
  • عَشْرَ آيَاتٍ— ten signs before the Hour — among them the Smoke, the Dajjāl, and the Beast.
  • الدُّخَان— the Smoke — one of the ten signs.
  • الدَّابَّة— the Beast [of the earth] that emerges to address mankind.
  • ثَلَاثَةَ خُسُوفٍ— three swallowings-up (خُسُوف = the earth's caving-in): one in the east, one in the west, and one in the Arabian Peninsula.
  • نَارٌ تَطْرُدُ النَّاسَ إِلَى مَحْشَرِهِمْ— a fire that drives the people to their gathering-place (مَحْشَر = the place of assembly) — coming forth from the depths of Aden / Yemen.
حديث ٥٤٦٤
  • بَادِرُوا بِالْأَعْمَالِ— race with [good] deeds (بَادَرَ = to hasten to outstrip) before six [signs] come.
  • أَمْرَ الْعَامَّةِ— the affair of the masses — a fitna that engulfs the general public.
  • خُوَيْصَّةَ أَحَدِكُمْ— the "little private matter" of one of you (diminutive of خَاصَّة) — i.e. one's own death, or the personal concern that engrosses him; made small beside the greater events.
حديث ٥٤٦٥
  • أَوَّلُ الْآيَاتِ خُرُوجًا— the first of the signs to come forth — the sun rising from its west.
  • خُرُوجُ الدَّابَّةِ عَلَى النَّاسِ ضُحًى— the Beast's emergence upon the people in the forenoon (ضُحًى = mid-morning, when the sun is well risen).
  • فَالْأُخْرَى عَلَى أَثَرِهَا قَرِيبًا— the other follows right on its heels (أَثَر = trace, track) soon after.
حديث ٥٤٦٧
  • تَسْجُدَ تَحْتَ الْعَرْشِ— [the sun] prostrates beneath the Throne — then seeks leave [to rise].
  • مُسْتَقَرٌّ لَهَا— a fixed resting-place appointed for it (مُسْتَقَرّ = an abode / terminus) — «and the sun runs to a resting-place of its own» (Q 36:38).
  • ارْجِعِي مِنْ حَيْثُ جِئْتِ— "return whence you came" — is said to it when its prostration is no longer accepted, so it rises from its west.
حديث ٥٤٦٨
  • مَا ... أَمْرٌ أَكْبَرُ مِنَ الدَّجَّالِ— there is no matter [no fitna] greater than the Dajjāl between the creation of Ādam and the Hour (ما here = negation) — for the enormity of his trial and deception.
حديث ٥٤٦٩
  • الْمَسِيحُ الدَّجَّالُ— al-Masīḥ the Dajjāl — مَسِيح here = "wiped" (مَمْسُوح, of one effaced eye), or one who sweeps (يَمْسَح) across the whole earth; the false messiah.
  • أَعْوَرُ عَيْنِ الْيُمْنَى— one-eyed, blind in the right eye (أَعْوَر = having one sound eye and one defective) — whereas Allah is free of all defect.
  • عِنَبَةٌ طَافِئَةٌ— [his eye] like a floating grape (طَافِئَة, with hamza = whose light is extinguished; طَافِيَة, without = protruding, bulging up) — his blind eye likened to a swollen grape.
حديث ٥٤٧٠
  • أَنْذَرَ أُمَّتَهُ الْأَعْوَرَ الْكَذَّابَ— [every prophet] warned his people of the one-eyed liar (الْأَعْوَر = the one blind in an eye; الْكَذَّاب = the arch-liar).
  • مَكْتُوبٌ بَيْنَ عَيْنَيْهِ: ك ف ر— written between his eyes: "k-f-r" (كُفْر, disbelief) — read by every believer, lettered or unlettered.
حديث ٥٤٧١
  • يَجِيءُ مَعَهُ بِمِثْلِ الْجَنَّةِ وَالنَّارِ— he comes bearing the like of a Garden and a Fire — the one he calls "the Garden" is in truth the Fire.
حديث ٥٤٧٢
  • مَعَهُ مَاءٌ وَنَارٌ— with him are water and fire — what people see as water is a burning fire, and what they see as fire is cool sweet water.
  • فَلْيَقَعْ فِي الَّذِي يَرَاهُ نَارًا— let him fall into the one he sees as fire — for in reality it is sweet, wholesome water (i.e. choose to deny the Dajjāl).
  • مَمْسُوحُ الْعَيْنِ عَلَيْهِ ظَفَرَةٌ غَلِيظَةٌ— of an effaced eye (مَمْسُوح = wiped smooth) over which is a thick ظَفَرَة (a membrane of flesh / skin grown over the eye).
حديث ٥٤٧٣
  • أَعْوَرُ الْعَيْنِ الْيُسْرَى— blind in the left eye — reconciled with the "right eye" report: one eye is gone, the other defective, so either may be called عَوْرَاء (the root of عَوَر being "defect").
  • جُفَالُ الشَّعَرِ— of abundant, bushy hair (جُفَال = thick, heaped-up, matted hair).
حديث ٥٤٧٤
  • فَأَنَا حَجِيجُهُ دُونَكُمْ— then I am his adversary [in argument] on your behalf (حَجِيج = one who overcomes another in disputation).
  • شَابٌّ قَطَطٌ— a young man of crisp, tightly-curled hair (قَطَط = very kinky / frizzled hair).
  • عَيْنُهُ طَافِيَةٌ— his eye protruding / floating (طَافِيَة = bulging up, standing out).
  • خَارِجٌ خَلَّةً بَيْنَ الشَّامِ وَالْعِرَاقِ— coming forth by a road between Syria and Iraq (خَلَّة = a gap, an interval, a way between).
  • فَعَاثَ يَمِينًا وَشِمَالًا— he wrought havoc right and left (عَاثَ = to spread ruin and corruption).
  • اقْدُرُوا لَهُ قَدْرَهُ— estimate for it its due measure — on the day that is like a year, reckon the [five] prayers by proportion, not by the single sun.
  • كَالْغَيْثِ اسْتَدْبَرَتْهُ الرِّيحُ— like rain with the wind driving it from behind — an image of his swiftness through the earth.
  • تَرُوحُ عَلَيْهِمْ سَارِحَتُهُمْ— their grazing herds (سَارِحَة = cattle let out to pasture) return to them in the evening — tallest in humps (ذُرًى), fullest in udders (ضُرُوع), most swollen in flanks (خَوَاصِر).
  • فَيُصْبِحُونَ مُمْحِلِينَ— they awake drought-stricken (مُمْحِل = afflicted by مَحْل, famine) — nothing of their wealth left in their hands.
  • فَتَتْبَعُهُ كُنُوزُهَا كَيَعَاسِيبِ النَّحْلِ— its treasures follow him like the queen-bees of a swarm (يَعَاسِيب = plural of يَعْسُوب, the leader-bee) — when he tells a ruin, "bring out your treasures."
  • فَيَقْطَعُهُ جَزْلَتَيْنِ رَمْيَةَ الْغَرَضِ— he cuts him into two pieces (جَزْلَة = a severed piece), [set apart] the distance of a shot at a target (الْغَرَض = the archery butt), then revives him.
  • بَيْنَ مَهْرُودَتَيْنِ— [ʿĪsā descends] between two mahrūda garments (مَهْرُودة = a robe dyed with wars / saffron, of yellowish hue).
  • تَحَدَّرَ مِنْهُ مِثْلُ جُمَانٍ— there roll from him [drops] like جُمَان (silver beads shaped as pearls) — when he raises his head, sweat falls like pearls.
  • فَيُرْسِلُ اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِمُ النَّغَفَ— Allah sends upon them (Yaʾjūj & Maʾjūj) the نَغَف (grubs / maggots that breed in the noses of livestock) in their necks, so they die as one — فَرْسَى (slain, plural of فَرِيس).
  • زَهَمُهُمْ وَنَتْنُهُمْ— their rank grease and stench (زَهَم = rancid fatty smell; نَتْن = putrid rot) fill the land, until Allah sends birds like the necks of الْبُخْت (great Bactrian camels) to bear them away.
  • حَتَّى يَتْرُكَهَا كَالزَّلَفَةِ— [rain washes the earth] till it leaves it like a زَلَفَة (a smooth polished basin / a mirror).
  • يَسْتَظِلُّونَ بِقِحْفِهَا— a band eats of one pomegranate and shelters under its قِحْف (rind / shell — properly the skull-cap); blessing is put in الرِّسْل (milk), one milch-camel sufficing الْفِئَام (a great multitude).
  • يَتَهَارَجُونَ فِيهَا تَهَارُجَ الْحُمُرِ— the worst of people couple openly like donkeys (تَهَارُج, from الهَرْج = mutual, shameless mounting) — and upon them the Hour rises.
حديث ٥٤٧٥
  • فَيَلْقَاهُ الْمَسَالِحُ مَسَالِحُ الدَّجَّالِ— the outposts/pickets of the Dajjāl (مَسَالِح = armed watchmen who guard the marches) meet him — his advance guard.
  • أَيْنَ تَعْمِدُ— "where are you heading?" (تَعْمِدُ = you make for, intend).
  • مَا بِرَبِّنَا خَفَاءٌ— "there is no concealment about our Lord" — i.e. His attributes are not hidden from us, that we should turn from Him to another.
  • فَيُشَجُّ / فَيُوسَعُ ظَهْرُهُ وَبَطْنُهُ ضَرْبًا— his head is gashed (الشَّجّ = a wound to the head) and his back and belly are beaten at length (يُوسَع ضَرْبًا = struck copiously).
  • فَيُؤْشَرُ بِالْمِئْشَارِ مِنْ مَفْرِقِهِ— he is sawn with the مِئْشَار (a saw) from the crown of his head (مَفْرِق = the parting of the hair) until split between his legs.
  • مَا ازْدَدْتُ إِلَّا بَصِيرَةً— "I have only grown more certain" (بَصِيرَة = clear insight, conviction) — that you are a lying deceiver.
  • مَا بَيْنَ رَقَبَتِهِ إِلَى تَرْقُوَتِهِ نُحَاسًا— the space from his neck to his collarbone (تَرْقُوَة = the collarbone) is turned to copper — the sword cannot cut it.
  • فَيَقْذِفُ بِهِ— he flings him [into the air] — people suppose he casts him into the Fire, but he is in truth cast into Paradise.
حديث ٥٤٧٧
  • يَتْبَعُ الدَّجَّالَ مِنْ يَهُودِ أَصْفَهَانَ— seventy thousand of the Jews of Aṣfahān follow the Dajjāl, wearing الطَّيَالِسَة (plural of طَيْلَسَان, a kind of cloak/mantle).
حديث ٥٤٧٨
  • مُحَرَّمٌ عَلَيْهِ أَنْ يَدْخُلَ نِقَابَ الْمَدِينَةِ— he is forbidden to enter the mountain-passes of Madīnah (نِقَاب = plural of نَقْب, a road between two mountains).
  • فَيَنْزِلُ بَعْضَ السِّبَاخِ— he encamps in one of the salt-flats (سِبَاخ = salty ground bearing no growth) near Madīnah.
حديث ٥٤٧٩
  • هِمَّتُهُ الْمَدِينَةُ— his aim and intent is Madīnah — until he reaches دُبُر أُحُد (behind Mt. Uḥud), where the angels turn his face away toward Syria.
حديث ٥٤٨٠
  • لَا يَدْخُلُ الْمَدِينَةَ رُعْبُ الْمَسِيحِ الدَّجَّالِ— the dread of the Dajjāl does not enter Madīnah (رُعْب = terror, dread) — it has seven gates, an angel-pair at each.
حديث ٥٤٨١
  • الصَّلَاةَ جَامِعَةً— "the prayer, assembled!" — the call to gather the people for a special address (not a regular ṣalāh).
  • تَمِيمًا الدَّارِيَّ— Tamīm al-Dārī — a former Christian who embraced Islam and related this account, confirming what the Prophet ﷺ had already been telling them of the Dajjāl.
  • فَأَرْفَئُوا إِلَى جَزِيرَةٍ— they brought the ship in to anchor (أَرْفَأَ = to moor a vessel) at an island, as the sun was setting.
  • فِي أَقْرُبِ السَّفِينَةِ— in the ship's small boats (أَقْرُب = plural of قَارِب, a skiff kept aboard a larger vessel for errands).
  • دَابَّةٌ أَهْلَبُ كَثِيرُ الشَّعَرِ— a shaggy beast, thick with hair (أَهْلَب = coarse/abundant-haired) — its front indistinguishable from its rear for the hair.
  • أَنَا الْجَسَّاسَةُ— "I am al-Jassāsa" (the Spy/Prober — named for spying out news for the Dajjāl); some say she is the Beast of the Earth mentioned in the Qurʾān.
  • فَإِنَّهُ إِلَى خَبَرِكُمْ بِالْأَشْوَاقِ— "he is longing for news of you" (أَشْوَاق = plural of شَوْق, yearning) — pointing them to the man in the Dayr.
  • فَرِقْنَا مِنْهَا أَنْ تَكُونَ شَيْطَانَةً— we were afraid (فَرِقَ = to fear) that she might be a she-devil.
  • الدَّيْرِ— the Dayr — properly a monk's cell/monastery; here a great fortress-like dwelling.
  • مَجْمُوعَةٌ يَدَاهُ إِلَى عُنُقِهِ ... بِالْحَدِيدِ— his hands bound to his neck, and likewise his knees to his ankles, in iron (وِثَاق = fetters/bonds).
  • أَخْبِرُونِي عَنْ نَخْلِ بَيْسَانَ— "tell me of the date-palms of Baysān" (a village in Syria) — does it still bear fruit?
  • بُحَيْرَةِ الطَّبَرِيَّةِ— the Lake of Tiberias (بُحَيْرَة = diminutive of بَحْر, a lake) — does it still hold water?
  • عَيْنِ زُغَرَ— the spring of Zughar — a town in Syria; he asks if it still flows and irrigates.
  • نَبِيِّ الْأُمِّيِّينَ— "the unlettered people's Prophet" — the Dajjāl's term for the Prophet ﷺ, meant to belittle the Arabs, who mostly could not read or write.
  • مَلَكٌ بِيَدِهِ سَيْفٌ صَلْتًا— an angel with a drawn sword in hand (صَلْتًا = bared, unsheathed) barring him from entering Mecca or Madīnah.
  • وَطَعَنَ بِمِخْصَرَتِهِ فِي الْمِنْبَرِ— he struck the pulpit with his مِخْصَرَة (a short staff/rod a speaker leans on or gestures with) — saying "this is Ṭayba (Madīnah)."
كِتَابُ أَحْوَالِ الْقِيَامَةِ وَبَدْءِ الْخَلْقِ
حديث ٥٦٥٨
  • نُورٌ أَنَّى أَرَاهُ— "He is immense Light — how could I see Him?" أَنَّى (fatah on hamza, شَدَّة on nun) = كَيْفَ (how). Al-Maziri: the perfection of His light prevents perception, just as blinding brightness prevents sight. Al-Nawawi: all رُوَاة in all transmitted copies (الأصول) narrate it this way, meaning: حِجَابُهُ نُورٌ فَكَيْفَ أَرَاهُ؟
  • نُورَانِيٌّ— alternative reading in some copies: nisba form (attributed to light), like رَبَّانِيّ, with alif-nun for مُبَالَغَة. On this reading, "أَرَاهُ" could mean "I saw/see Him" — narrating the past in present tense — which would do إثبات of رُؤْيَة. Imam Ahmad accepted this reading as إيجاب. Ibn al-Malak: the hadith serves as دَلِيل for both sides, depending on which narration is taken.
حديث ٥٦٦٣
  • لَا تُدْرِكُهُ الْأَبْصَارُ— eyes do not reach/encompass Him. Those who do إثبات of رُؤْيَة distinguish إدراك (encompassing) from رُؤْيَة (seeing) — the آية negates the former, not the latter.
  • مِنْ وَرَاءِ حِجَابٍ— from behind a veil/barrier. M: Aisha's (R.A.) نفي is ظَاهِرًا مُطْلَق (absolute negation of رُؤْيَة), though Ibn Hajar's جمع restricts it to رُؤْيَة بِالْبَصَر (eye-sight), leaving رُؤْيَة بِالْقَلْب open per Ibn Abbas's (R.A.) إثبات.
  • قَفَّ شَعَرِي— my hair stood on end; from the gravity of the matter, expressing awe at the enormity of the claim.
حديث ٥٦٩٣
  • تَحَاجَّتِ— they disputed/argued with each other; from الحجاج = presenting proofs; a mutual debate.
  • أُوثِرْتُ— I was preferred/favored with; النَّار was given priority (in receiving) the arrogant and tyrants.
  • ضُعَفَاءُ النَّاسِ وَسَقَطُهُمْ وَغِرَّتُهُمْ— the weak of people, their lowly ones, and their naive/simple-minded; those considered insignificant in worldly terms but who enter جَنَّة.
  • رِجْلَهُ— His "foot" (a صِفَة خَبَرِيَّة affirmed with تَفْوِيض; نُؤْمِنُ بِهِ كَمَا جَاءَ without تَجْسِيم or تَعْطِيل).
  • قَطْ قَطْ— enough! enough! النَّار announces its fullness; expression of satiation.
  • الْمَاكَارِه— difficult/burdensome things; linguistically = things disliked by the نَفْس; M: includes all مُكَلَّف obligations that require exertion.
حديث ٥٦٩٧
  • كَانَ اللَّهُ وَلَمْ يَكُنْ شَيْءٌ قَبْلَهُ— Allah existed and nothing was before Him; affirms Allah's eternal precedence (قِدَم) with no co-eternal beside Him.
  • كَانَ عَرْشُهُ عَلَى الْمَاءِ— His Throne was upon water; the first created things before the heavens and earth.
  • الذِّكْرُ— the Preserved Tablet (اللَّوْح الْمَحْفُوظ); everything was inscribed therein.
  • وَايْمُ اللَّهِ— by Allah; an oath formula.
حديث ٥٧٠٣
  • إِنِّي سَقِيمٌ— I am sick; Ibrahim A.S.'s first of three مَوْرِد الْكَذِب; classical scholars resolved this as مَعَارِيض (indirect speech) or an expression of spiritual distress, not a direct falsehood.
  • بَلْ فَعَلَهُ كَبِيرُهُمْ هَذَا— rather this great one did it; said تَحَكُّمًا (mockingly, based on the idols' own logic); Ibn Qutayba's جَزَاء مُقَدَّم interpretation removes the element of deliberate falsehood.
  • الْجَبَّارُ— the tyrant; one who imposes his will with force; used for the oppressive king.
  • أُخْتِي— my sister; Ibrahim A.S.'s third مَوْرِد; intended to protect both himself and Sarah (R.A.) from harm.
حديث ٥٧٠٤
  • نَحْنُ أَحَقُّ بِالشَّكِّ مِنْ إِبْرَاهِيمَ— we are more entitled to doubt than Ibrahim A.S.; meaning: if even Ibrahim A.S. had reason to ask (for assurance), we certainly have even less reason to doubt — a rhetorical negation of doubt, not a confession of it.
  • رَبِّ أَرِنِي كَيْفَ تُحْيِي الْمَوْتَى— "My Lord, show me how You give life to the dead" (Al-Baqarah 2:260); asked for اطْمِئْنَانُ الْقَلْب, not because of doubt in the principle.
  • رُكْنٌ شَدِيدٌ— a strong pillar/support; Lut A.S. expressed a wish for strong worldly backing; M: his real pillar was Allah.
  • لَأَجَبْتُ الدَّاعِيَ— I would have responded to the caller; Yusuf A.S.'s preference to remain in prison rather than leave under false circumstances, showing his extraordinary تَقْوَى.
حديث ٥٧١١
  • سُمِّيَ الْخَضِرُ— he was named al-Khadir (the green one); a لَقَب, not his birth name; derived from the miracle of greenery appearing wherever he sat.
  • فَرْوَةٌ بَيْضَاءُ— white barren/dry earth; some say: a white hide/skin placed on the ground.
  • تَهْتَزُّ خَضْرَاءَ— shook/trembled turning green; the ground became lush and green wherever he sat — the miracle from which his لَقَب derived.
حديث ٥٧١٤
  • آدَمُ— brownish/dark in complexion; صيغة اللون indicating a dark brown skin tone.
  • طُوَالٌ— very tall; the exaggerated form of طويل, emphasizing extreme height.
  • جَعْدٌ— (disputed) curly-haired or solid/compact in body; see class notes for the three opinions.
  • شَنُوءَةُ— a Yemeni tribe known for their tall and strong physiques; used as a recognizable reference point for the description.
  • مَالِكٌ خَازِنُ النَّارِ— Malik, the guardian/keeper of Hellfire; the angel placed in charge of النَّار.
  • فِي مِرْيَةٍ— in doubt; لَا تَكُنْ فِي مِرْيَةٍ مِنْ لِقَائِهِ = have no doubt about encountering الدَّجَّال.
حديث ٥٧١٥
  • مُضْطَرِبٌ— of unsettled/lean bearing; some say: lightly built; al-idtirab = instability or lean frame.
  • رَجِلُ الشَّعْرِ— with slightly wavy hair; neither fully straight (سَبْط) nor tightly curled (جَعْد) — the middle state.
  • دِيمَاسٌ— bathhouse/حَمَّام; one who exits a bath has a fresh, reddish glow — hence Isa A.S. was described as رَبْعَةً أَحْمَرَ (medium-built, reddish complexion).
  • هُدِيتَ الْفِطْرَةَ— you were guided to the natural disposition; the choice of milk = the pure, unaltered فِطْرَة of Islam.
  • غَوَتْ أُمَّتُكَ— your أُمَّة would have gone astray; the consequence of choosing خَمْر would have been the misguidance of the entire community.
حديث ٥٧١٦
  • وَادِي الْأَزْرَقِ— the Blue/Azure Valley; a valley between Mecca and Madinah associated with the journey of حَجّ.
  • جُؤَارٌ— a loud cry/outcry; from جأر = to cry out loudly toward Allah; describing the intensity of Musa's A.S. تَلْبِيَة.
  • ثَنِيَّةٌ— a mountain pass; a path cut through a mountain.
  • خُلْبَةٌ— a rope made of palm fiber; coarse/simple material, showing Yunus's A.S. asceticism.
  • مُلَبِّيًا— reciting the تَلْبِيَة (لَبَّيْكَ اللَّهُمَّ لَبَّيْكَ); in the state of إِحْرَام.
حديث ٥٧١٧
  • خُفِّفَ عَلَيْهِ الْقُرْآنُ— the Quran (Zabur) was made light/easy for him; Allah granted him extraordinary facility in recitation — speed and ease unparalleled among others.
  • دَوَابُّ— riding animals; mounts; plural of دابة.
  • فَتُسَرَّحَ— they were released to graze / prepared; he would begin recitation while the animals were being attended to and finish before they were ready.
  • لَا يَأْكُلُ إِلَّا مِنْ عَمَلِ يَدَيْهِ— he ate only from the labor of his own hands; Dawud A.S. was a blacksmith (making armor); a lesson in dignity through self-sufficiency.
حديث ٥٧١٨
  • تَحَاكَمَتَا— they referred their dispute to a judge; sought arbitration.
  • السِّكِّينُ— knife; Sulayman A.S. called for it as a stratagem (حِيلَة) to provoke the real mother's reaction, not with actual intent to cut.
  • الشَّفَقَةُ— tender compassion; the الصُّغْرَى's willingness to surrender her claim to save the child's life revealed she was the true mother.
  • الصُّغْرَى / الْكُبْرَى— the younger / the older of the two women; the الْكُبْرَى was the false claimant.
حديث ٥٧١٩
  • لَأَطُوفَنَّ— I will certainly go around (to each wife); emphatic lam with oath, expressing firm intention.
  • شَقُّ رَجُلٍ— half a man; the one child born was stillborn or incomplete — the result of forgetting إِنْ شَاءَ اللَّهُ.
  • لَوْ قَالَ إِنْ شَاءَ اللَّهُ— had he said "If Allah wills"; the pivotal omission; the lesson is that all intentions must be attached to Allah's will.
  • فُرْسَانًا أَجْمَعُونَ— all of them mounted warriors; the full realization of his noble intention would have occurred had he said إِنْ شَاءَ اللَّهُ.
حديث ٥٧٢٤
  • عَمَاءٌ— thin/white cloud; also interpreted as a state beyond all human comprehension; Yazid ibn Harun explained it as: nothing was with Him (لَيْسَ مَعَهُ شَيْءٌ).
  • هَوَاءٌ— air/void; neither above nor below was there anything — emphasizing Allah's complete independence before creation.
  • وَخَلَقَ عَرْشَهُ عَلَى الْمَاءِ— He created His Throne upon water; the water preceded the Throne; consistent with the preceding hadith (5697) about كان الله ولم يكن شيء قبله.
حديث ٥٧٢٦
  • جَهِدَتِ الْأَنْفُسُ— the souls were exhausted/worn out; extreme hardship from famine.
  • نُهِكَتِ الْأَمْوَالُ— wealth was depleted/consumed; from نهك = to wear away through strain.
  • وَيْحَكَ— woe to you / listen carefully; an expression of gentle rebuke and correction, not a curse.
  • الْقُبَّةُ— a dome; the Prophet S.A.W. gestured with his fingers in a dome shape to describe the Throne's position above the heavens — a pedagogical gesture, not a precise geometric description.
  • يَئِطُّ أَطِيطَ الرَّحْلِ بِالرَّاكِبِ— it groans like a saddle under its rider; the Throne groans/creaks under the weight of Allah's greatness — affirmed with تَفْوِيض as a صِفَة خَبَرِيَّة.
حديث ٥٧٣١
  • خَلَقْتُهُ بِيَدَيَّ— I created him with My two hands; a صِفَة خَبَرِيَّة affirmed for Adam A.S. specifically; M: affirmed as a divine attribute befitting Allah's majesty, without تَجْسِيم.
  • وَنَفَخْتُ فِيهِ مِنْ رُوحِي— and I breathed into him of My spirit; the نَفْخ الرُّوح is a separate divine act of honor for Adam A.S.; the إِضَافَة (My spirit) indicates honor, not that it is a part of Allah.
  • كُنْ فَكَانَ— "Be, and it was"; the mode of creation for angels and all else — through divine command alone, without the specific honor of "by My hands."
حديث ٥٧٣٢
  • أَكْرَمُ عَلَى اللَّهِ— more honored in Allah's sight; the comparative (أفعل التفضيل) shows degree, not absolute ranking over all angels.
  • مِنْ بَعْضِ مَلَائِكَتِهِ— than some of His angels; the qualifier بعض is important — the greatest angels (Jibreel, Mika'il, Israfil) are not encompassed by this; the believer surpasses lesser-ranked angels.
حديث ٥٧٣٦
  • نَبِيٌّ مُكَلَّمٌ— a prophet spoken to directly by Allah; Adam A.S. received direct divine speech, establishing his prophethood.
  • جَمًّا غَفِيرًا— a large overwhelming number; used here adverbially to indicate the vast multitude of messengers.
  • أُولُو الْعَزْمِ— those with firm resolve; M: the five greatest messengers who were given books and given the most demanding missions: Nuh, Ibrahim, Musa, Isa, and Muhammad (S.A.W.).
حديث ٥٧٣٧
  • لَيْسَ الْخَبَرُ كَالْمُعَايَنَةِ— information (خَبَر) is not like direct witnessing (مُعَايَنَة); hearing about an event does not produce the same emotional and psychological effect as seeing it firsthand.
  • الْعِجْلُ— the (golden) calf; the idol worshipped by Bani Isra'il in Musa's A.S. absence.
  • الْأَلْوَاحُ— the tablets; the divine tablets containing the Torah given to Musa A.S.; M: their benefit depended on the recipients' receptiveness — when Bani Isra'il fell into كُفْر, the tablets' purpose was nullified.
مشكاة المصابيح — Study Notes  |  For personal academic use
